

 ### Chapter 751: The Great Craftsman's Heir

Chen Pingan discussed the matter of overcoming obstacles with the sword cultivators of the Hidden Officials lineage. The sword cultivators understood the principle well, but Chen Pingan provided an example that even the sorrowful Miao Sword Immortal found enlightening.

In the realm of Qingming, the Grand Master of Baiyu City, Lu Chen, once visited the hometown of the young Hidden Official. Disguised, he set up a fortune-telling stall in the Liuzhu Cave Heaven, where he stayed for over a decade.

Under the suppression of the Great Dao from the Haoran world, he had remained at the Ascended Realm for a long time.

Wang Xinshui felt a bit resentful towards the Hidden Official. Why hadn’t such astonishing tales been mentioned earlier? If he had known sooner, his admiration for the Hidden Official would have elevated him to the Ascended Realm long ago, rather than being stuck at the bottleneck of the Nascent Soul Realm.

Among the latest group of six who were closely aligned with the young Hidden Official on a small mountain peak, Guo Zhujiu held the highest cultivation level, making her the standard by which others were measured in terms of comprehension and achievement. Even Guke Long’s fair comments surprised Guo Zhujiu, indicating that her cultivation was not low, reaching the Immortal Realm, second only to her.

Xuan Can, due to his experience with chess, gained a powerful technique akin to a supreme secret manual that allowed him to advance to the Jade Purity Realm, with the Great Dao within reach. Cao Gun, who had come to the mountain to learn this path, started too late and lacked diligence, remaining at the Golden Core Realm. Wang Xinshui was at the Nascent Soul bottleneck, while Mi Yu, the Sword Immortal, displayed poor talent and lack of sincerity, not even qualifying as an Earth Immortal.

Today, Chen Pingan went out for a stroll again. Guo Zhujiu finished her tasks and adjusted the position of a small snowman on the table, patting its head before hoisting her small bamboo box and dashing out.

With her gaze and encouragement, dubbed “from little Guo Zhujiu,” the snowman looked at her, filled with care and motivation. The bamboo branch in its hand pointed assertively. Who dared to slack off? The bamboo branch would act like a flying sword, and one had to be careful about their head.

Her master was still walking slowly today, and Guo Zhujiu caught up with him after just a few steps.

“Master, why are you walking so slowly lately? Are you in meditation?” Guo Zhujiu asked.

Chen Pingan smiled, “Yes, I’m cultivating my heart.”

The little girl spun around, always facing her master. “This grand knowledge of heaven and earth, I don’t need to learn it, right? Even if I wanted to, I couldn't learn it?”

Chen Pingan replied, “Anyone can learn it, but there’s no need to.”

The little girl felt both happy and troubled.

In a secluded courtyard, Chen Pingan pulled out one horizontal river water talisman and one earth-absorbing soil talisman. “Master will draw you a map of the Haoran world.”

On the ground, each continent he mentioned was accompanied by stories about its customs and cultures, some witnessed firsthand, others noted in books or heard through discussions.

There was the Southeast Tongye Continent, the Eastern Baoping Continent from his master’s hometown, the Northern Julu Continent where most sword cultivators traveled along the Sword Qi Great Wall, the Aihai Continent, the origin of the Snowflake Coins, the flourishing Buddhist Northwest Liuxia Continent, the ancient battlefield remnants of the Western Golden Armor Continent, the currently chaotic Southwestern Fuyiao Continent, and the Southern Posha Continent where the Chen family, known for their scholarly pursuits, resided.

Lin Junbi's hometown was the Central Land Divine Continent.

Guo Zhujiu squatted in the corridor, gazing at the map, exclaiming, “The heavens are round and the earth is flat. If this isn’t round heaven and flat earth, then it’s easier for you to travel from your hometown, Baoping Continent, to the Golden Armor Continent without taking such a long detour.”

Chen Pingan chuckled, “Because all the worlds and all the blessed lands are a fragmented new map. If they were all found, combined with the newly discovered fifth world by the Confucian saints, perhaps it would resemble a grand round heaven and small earth, much like circles within circles, or moons within moons.”

During their journey to the Daxu Mountain Academy, Little Baoping had once posed this question, answered at the time by the seemingly omniscient Cui Dongshan.

Cui Dongshan had taken out a water bowl, a freshly plucked green branch, and a random stone, asking everyone what they felt about heaven and earth.

Unfortunately, at that moment, the rice was cooked, and the fish was fragrant, so no one paid him any mind.

Cui Dongshan tossed the stone, inserted the branch into the back of his collar, poured water into the bowl, and requested a bowl of rice from Chen Pingan.

Chen Pingan mentioned he needed to find the dazed Pang Yuanji, and Guo Zhujiu immediately sprang up, calling out that she understood and hurried away.

Guo Zhujiu returned to the main hall, where the atmosphere remained somewhat heavy and tense.

It was bearable when her master was present.

However, when he was absent, it became even more suffocating.

Guo Zhujiu set down her bamboo box at her feet.

After the incident, Lin Junbi questioned the Hidden Official whether the tale of the Ascended Realm great demon being slain outside the Inverted Mountain could be shared with all the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Otherwise, over time, with people's hearts fluctuating like the tides, if it were to burst like a dam, it could easily affect the overall situation.

But Chen Pingan merely stated it was unnecessary and that they could wait a little longer.

The rampant discussions targeted only him, the Hidden Official, not the sword cultivators of the entire lineage, which made it less significant for the time being.

Pang Yuanji sat on a railing in a corridor, lost in thought, heavy-hearted, with nothing to say.

Hearing footsteps, he turned his head, nodded as a greeting.

However, Pang Yuanji waited for a long time before the fellow finally sat beside him.

It seemed lately, every time Chen Pingan left the main hall, it was just for a stroll, moving at the same slow pace.

Chen Pingan sat next to him, handing over a jug of wine. “This is the fairy wine brewed at Chunfan Studio, quite expensive, and its taste rivals that of the bamboo sea cave wine.”

Pang Yuanji shook his head, “No thanks, I haven’t drunk in a long time.”

Chen Pingan looked at this scruffy-faced fellow and said, “You should speak some words that ease your heart; there’s no need to hold back. I know you have grievances against me, but if you feel it’s unreasonable, you can just endure it. However, that’s not necessary. Can you brew fine wine by storing up sorrow like a wine barrel?”

Pang Yuanji replied, “You should have explored the corners of both the Summer Palace and Winter Palace, right?”

Chen Pingan nodded, “Of course, but unfortunately, there weren’t any hidden mechanisms to uncover unexpected treasures.”

Pang Yuanji spoke softly, “But you would never feel what I feel. It's not just now that I feel this way; I realized it shortly after entering the old Hidden Official lineage.”

“What feeling? Tell me about it.”

Chen Pingan unsealed the jar of wine mud, took a sip, and said, “I’ll just drink and listen to your complaints. No need to reason; sometimes, venting emotions itself is a form of reasoning.”

Pang Yuanji’s expression turned dazed as he muttered, “In two houses, is there anything superfluous? Any trivial decorative items? There’s nothing. When my master left the Sword Qi Great Wall, the ‘Hidden Official’ jade token was left behind, all the secret records remained, and I was left here alone. I only feel like my master never came to this Summer Palace in her life. Recently, I’ve been thinking about what my master thinks or does when she’s alone. Does she also feel sad and disappointed but can’t speak to anyone? Everyone thinks my master must always be powerful and invincible, slaying demons time and again, but I never felt that way.”

At this point, Pang Yuanji glanced at the city wall, recalling his master, Xiao Xian, and unconsciously thought of the old Sword Immortal.

The two Hidden Official palaces were so desolate; how much more so for the old Sword Immortal living in a thatched cottage?

It seemed hardly anyone on the Sword Qi Great Wall had thought deeply about what the old Sword Immortal might think or feel.

Chen Pingan looked around and nodded, “Hearing you say this, I realize the house is indeed empty, which indicates your master, Xiao Xian, is incredible. Only someone with a powerful and self-sufficient heart would be indifferent to external possessions. You can’t do it, and of course, I can’t either.”

In fact, Chen Pingan was more sensitive to the feelings of a stranger in an unfamiliar environment than to a particular stranger.

But such conversations couldn’t be pursued.

Pang Yuanji’s eyes reddened as he raised his head, taking a deep breath, and forced a smile. “I thought you would scold my master, at least berate me severely.”

After all, Pang Yuanji’s master had nearly killed this young Hidden Official’s brother in battle.

And she had attacked in the most dishonorable way.

Self-mockery at one’s most sorrowful moment serves as a form of subconscious self-protection.

Chen Pingan shook his head, sipping the wine, “If I were to speak lofty principles, I wouldn’t have enough baskets to hold all the words. How can I criticize you two as master and disciple? It’s pointless. One must be tolerant of others’ selfishness; otherwise, in the end, it’s oneself who grows weary. Why bother?”

Chen Pingan continued, “Without discussing Xiao Xian’s eventual betrayal, you know well the many things she did for the Sword Qi Great Wall, as do I. As for why she betrayed, I might understand it better than you because I’m an observer. It’s just that presently and in the future, many sword immortals and cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall choose to forget, some intentionally, some unwittingly, and very few understand yet don’t accept it. So I guess this is your most frustrating part?”

Pang Yuanji remained silent.

Chen Pingan took a large gulp of wine and smiled, “Indeed, even with those selfish thoughts, Pang Yuanji, you still do the work of the new Hidden Official lineage’s sword cultivators, not falling behind anyone else. In terms of affairs, you owe the Sword Qi Great Wall nothing; in terms of feelings, you have not wronged the master-disciple bond. What else can you expect from Pang Yuanji to be seen as doing well?”

Thus, Chen Pingan did not think that Pang Yuanji’s path of cultivation had reached a dead end due to an unstable sword heart.

Pang Yuanji forced a smile and said, “Even if you say that, my heart doesn’t feel any better.”

Chen Pingan said, “I’ll ask you one last question; you don’t have to answer.”

Pang Yuanji didn’t want to hear this question, which would certainly be troubling.

Chen Pingan asked, “If after Xiao Xian threw that punch, hypothetically, you could kill her right away, what would Pang Yuanji do?”

Pang Yuanji instinctively crossed his arms, shoulders slumped, and remained silent.

Chen Pingan chuckled, “Since it’s all painful anyway, might as well make you feel a bit worse.”

Pang Yuanji wanted to say that the Hidden Official could continue being busy with his own matters.

To his surprise, the man continued, “How about I ask you another question?”

Pang Yuanji asked, “If I don’t provide an answer, will you keep asking?”

Chen Pingan drank his wine, oblivious, and asked, “I heard that Lin Junbi’s senior brother at the border is actually an Ascended Realm great demon. Deep down, does it make you feel a little better? Or would you feel even worse realizing this because you are friends with Lin Junbi?”

Pang Yuanji’s face was filled with bitterness.

Chen Pingan patted Pang Yuanji’s shoulder, “You just have to endure; there’s no escaping. You can close the door and avoid people, but how can your true self not meet?”

Who hasn’t got a few principles on their lips? It’s easiest to deceive oneself in this world.

Chen Pingan didn’t push further, taking another large sip of wine, ready to let Pang Yuanji enjoy his solitude.

Pang Yuanji turned and asked, “Chen Pingan, why do I feel like you’re relishing my misfortune?”

Chen Pingan was surprised, “You can tell? I’m not particularly skilled at many things, but hiding my true feelings is something I excel at. Brother Pang, you have good insight.”

Pang Yuanji asked, “Is it true?”

Chen Pingan retorted, “What’s true or false? In this matter, we are both in the same boat. Otherwise, why do you think I’m here drinking with you, making you feel uncomfortable so that I can feel good?”

Pang Yuanji sighed, feeling weak, “I ask you to just go away.”

Chen Pingan jumped off the railing, laughing, “Talking to the Hidden Official like this is a one-time thing, a rare exception. It’s not good to bully honest folks.”

Pang Yuanji suddenly said, “Chen Pingan, I’m not going to kill demons on the city walls.”

In the corridor, Chen Pingan turned around and chuckled, “As long as you’re not afraid of the scorn and gossip from outside, then you don’t need to worry about anything from me. The new Hidden Official lineage doesn’t mandate that sword cultivators must leave the city to slay demons.”

Pang Yuanji’s expression was miserable as he replied, “Truly, we are kindred spirits.”

Chen Pingan smiled, “When can you learn from Lin Junbi, endure on your own, and find joy in hardship? That would be a sign of successful heart cultivation.”

Pang Yuanji remained lost in thought.

The questions between the Barbarian World and the Sword Qi Great Wall continued.

However, during this time, the Barbarian World did something apart from asking swords. The peak great demon, Yangzhi, the crowned woman in a dragon robe, returned to the battlefield, hovering high in the air, holding a half-dead man, a sword immortal who had blocked a large army’s northward advance in the heart of the Barbarian World. Both Yangzhi and her peer Huang Luan achieved their own victories, but the two sword immortals Huang Luan killed had turned to dust, their souls scattered, while Yangzhi had captured one alive.

On that day in battle, Yangzhi gripped the dying sword immortal’s head with her five fingers, standing not far from two torrents of sword energy, revealing the sword immortal’s background and what actions he had carried out in the Barbarian World. Then, under everyone’s gaze, Yangzhi slowly stripped the flesh from that sword immortal, the process painstakingly slow, starting with the flesh, followed by shattering bones, then extracting a golden core, piece by piece, grinding it away until the Nascent Soul was finally strangled, and ultimately, she extracted and shattered the sword immortal’s soul.

After Yangzhi appeared, the Hidden Official lineage’s flying swords sent messages to all parts of the Sword Qi Great Wall, and it was the flying sword inscribed with “Hidden Official.”

No sword immortal or cultivator was permitted to question Yangzhi without authorization.

Later, several great sword immortals privately sent flying swords to the Summer Palace, inquiring if the sword formation could still be used, but they were permitted to work together to interrupt Yangzhi’s actions.

The reply from the Hidden Official lineage’s flying sword was still that great sword immortals were not allowed to act without permission, warning that peak great demons, including Huang Luan, were lying in wait, and this more obvious ambush could be even deadlier than the previous concealment of great demons within the Five Mountains. The position where Yangzhi stood was extremely crucial; even a slight shift could cost the lives of one or two great sword immortals from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Once the battle escalated, with both sides’ top combatants entering the fray, regardless of how both sides suffered losses, it would quickly advance the progression of this war.

Nalan Shaowei, Yue Qing, and Yao Lianyun, among others, managed to hold back from drawing their swords, but everyone felt pent-up frustration.

Even Yue Qing cursed under his breath.

Yao Lianyun’s face was particularly grim.

Before this, the head of the Yao family had been spirited, slicing through every battle with vigor, a sight to behold.

The biggest issue was that the sword immortals were following the commands of the Hidden Official lineage.

However, a group of young sword cultivators, filled with indignation, instead took the initiative to strike first, launching dozens of flying swords to question the great demon Yangzhi.

If it weren’t for several great sword immortals quickly intervening, it’s likely that over a hundred life swords would have rushed at that great demon. If that happened, even more flying swords would have followed suit, and the entire sword formation would have likely seen a division.

Yangzhi’s response was filled with surprises; seeing that several great sword immortals had blocked the subsequent questioning, she not only did not destroy any of the approaching flying swords but casually maneuvered those uncontrolled swords belonging to cultivators on the city walls to approach the sword immortal facing a grim fate, as if deliberately allowing this dying sword immortal to meet those young sword cultivators. Finally, she returned all thirty-nine flying swords to the city walls, letting them return safely to the sword formation.

In the end, Yangzhi shattered the remaining soul of the sword immortal in her grasp, laughing, “What a Sword Qi Great Wall! What a sword immortal with heavenly killing power! Everyone sees death and refuses to save; yet a group of mere young sword cultivators struggles to offer their lives to save. I understand the former’s desire to live, and I respect the latter’s stupidity!”

Afterward, the hearts of the people within the Sword Qi Great Wall became even more intricate than when the previous Hidden Official Xiao Xian betrayed the Sword Qi Great Wall, injuring others.

The command and dispatch that had been increasingly smooth within the Hidden Official lineage started to show slight stagnation here and there.

Among those on the Sword Qi Great Wall, a heartfelt, furious sentiment arose.

“Why should the Hidden Official take risks and die? Why not save us?! We sword cultivators are willing to die; why won’t they?”

Afterward, more discussions evolved.

“Today, that sword immortal risked his life for the Great Dao, intending to slay enemies in the heart of the Barbarian World, and still received no help. In the future, if the Barbarian World’s ants swarm to attack, if there’s even a chance it’s a trap, which sword cultivator will the Hidden Official save?”

“Even that great demon respects those who willingly draw their swords to face death; yet it turns out our own people are so cold-blooded, calculating every detail. Such a Hidden Official, is it really beneficial to the Sword Qi Great Wall? Can it truly compare to what the previous Hidden Official did? At least the latter dared to plunge into the fray, slaying countless demon beasts in battle before betraying us!”

With these emerging sentiments, it was clear that more thoughts and ideas lay buried deep in the hearts of many.

Chen Pingan walked back out of the main hall just as Song Gaoyuan, Cao Gun, and Xuan Can were returning from the city walls with their swords. Next, it would be the turn of Luo Zhenyi, Xu Ning, and Chang Taiqing, three local sword cultivators, to head to the city walls to slay demons.

Song Gaoyuan and Cao Gun wore gloomy expressions.

Among them, Xuan Can, the youngest, was surprisingly the most open-minded of the sword cultivators, even showing a hint of a smile as he said, “Hidden Official, I advise Luo Zhenyi and the others not to go to the city walls for now. First, they will be isolated; often, they will be snatched away by other sword cultivators for the battlefield. Our efforts in slaying demons would be nearly fruitless. Furthermore, although they don’t speak ill of us, mentioning the Hidden Official, there are no good words and not a hint of caution.”

The first two batches of sword cultivators from the Hidden Official lineage who went to the city walls to slay demons mostly returned injured, while this time Xuan Can and the others returned unscathed.

Luo Zhenyi and the others stood by the door, looking to the young Hidden Official for guidance.

Whether to go or not depended on the Hidden Official’s word.

Chen Pingan turned and said, “We still have to go.”

Luo Zhenyi nodded, and along with the other two sword cultivators, they left on their swords.

Chen Pingan smiled, “Thank you for your hard work.”

Cao Gun looked dispirited, “We aren’t working hard at all.”

Chen Pingan comforted him, “Now that’s true hard work.”

Cao Gun forced a smile, wanting to say something but held back.

They all returned to the main hall and took their seats.

Lin Junbi sighed, “We can’t just openly discuss with everyone that the ferry between the Eight Continents of the Haoran world and our dealings have changed significantly. We have hope to prolong this battle, enough to exhaust more of the Barbarian World’s resources, even those peak great demons must feel the pinch. We’ve worked so long for this, finally seeing a glimpse of victory; how can we let Yangzhi’s little tricks ruin it?”

Xuan Can gloomily added, “It’s often said, ‘The one who kills the killers kills on behalf of the great craftsman.’”

Cao Gun nodded in agreement. “Indeed, ‘The one who kills on behalf of the great craftsman rarely escapes unscathed.’”

Lin Junbi chuckled, “You’re misusing the sage’s words; moreover, they’re hardly comforting.”

Chen Pingan laughed, “Not talking about the sage’s true meaning, just using it here brings a different flavor.”

The usually quiet Miao Sword Immortal even shared some insights, “What is true is true, but in the end, it’s not the same as reality. This makes it hardest to reason.”

Many heated arguments don’t arise from one extreme being unreasonable and the other being entirely logical, but from each side having its own reasoning, with varying degrees of right and wrong.

Lin Junbi asked, “Is there a way to resolve this situation?”

Chen Pingan nodded, “Of course.”

“How?”

“First, acknowledge that it’s unsolvable.”

Everyone fell silent, with only Lin Junbi seeming to grasp something.

When Pang Yuanji returned and took his seat, Chen Pingan spoke with his heart to the three of them: Miao Sword Immortal, Lin Junbi, and Pang Yuanji.

The Miao Sword Immortal rejected outright.

Pang Yuanji was frustrated and didn’t want to say another word.

Lin Junbi asked, “Hidden Official, clearly you uncovered that Ascended Realm great demon. Why would you want to share this monumental achievement with us three?”

Chen Pingan smiled, “To break the deadlock. If the credit belongs solely to me, who would believe it now? Even if they did, what difference would it make? By the way, when the young sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall reach their lowest point, gathering in groups to shout outside the Summer Palace, the highest-ranked Miao Sword Immortal will be responsible for climbing the city walls and presenting that great demon’s head, paying respects to the Barbarian World.”

Pang Yuanji said, “I should have agreed to drink before and gotten drunk outside instead.”

Guo Zhujiu was unaware of what her master was whispering about.

It must have been some discussion.

Guo Zhujiu finally looked down at the two treasured items she was to keep safe on the table, both gifts from the Fuyiao Continent’s mountains and waters.

One was an ancient inkstone, a square piece adorned with the patterns of a Kuilong, with an engraved seal: “Clouds Hang Low, Waters Stand Tall, Words Flow Deep.”

As for the other, a fan shimmering with treasure light, the inscription was also pretty elegant: “Golden Ripples, Jade Circles. The old fool dreams of the Moon Palace, carving away at the osmanthus tree. People say, on this night most complete, lights illuminate countless homes.”

Master had secretly told her that once she accumulated some military achievements, they would keep these two treasures for themselves.

Dong Budu suddenly raised her head and said, “Green Duan, that fan is one I’ve had my eyes on for a long time.”

Guo Zhujiu asked, “If it was once tucked away by Chen Sanqiu, would you still want it, Sister Dong?”

Dong Budu coldly laughed, “If Chen Sanqiu wants to see this fan, you’ll have to smash through the walls of the Summer Palace first to clear the way.”

Guo Zhujiu slapped her forehead, proudly declaring, “My Iron Head skill is extraordinary; even Master cannot compare!”

Chen Pingan laughed, “It’s not about competing in this; remember, this isn’t a secret skill of our sect, but something you’ve comprehended yourself.”

Guo Zhujiu nodded, “With my big sister’s mad sword technique combined with my unique skill, we can promote it greatly in the future!”

Chen Pingan waved his hand, continuing to gaze at the map on the ground.

Guo Zhujiu patted the little snowman’s head, which was getting smaller and smaller.

Chen Pingan suddenly asked, “Isn’t Lu Zhi about to return to the Inverted Mountain soon?”

Lin Junbi nodded, “Barring any accidents, she should return with Shao Yunyan today.”

Chen Pingan stood up, “Miao, accompany me to the Inverted Mountain.”

At Chunfan Studio.

Mi Yu was meticulous and focused on checking the accounts.

This wasn’t actually Mi Yu’s forte; to put it bluntly, if Yan Ming and Nalan Caihuan wanted to misappropriate funds while going through the ledger, the only way Mi Yu could find a flaw would be if the young Hidden Official had reviewed it and then sent Mi Yu over to relay the message verbatim. Therefore, Nalan Caihuan and Yan Ming were both cooperating and keeping each other in check, with Mi Yu merely being a pawn placed by the young Hidden Official at Chunfan Studio, doing it for show. Nalan Caihuan viewed Mi Yu as a second-rate sword immortal who happened to drink the bamboo sea cave wine and had connections with the young Hidden Official, holding little goodwill toward him.

However, Mi Yu often encountered difficult issues and would consult Yan Ming for key insights.

Yan Ming had a very poor impression of Mi Yu, only stating things as they were, never showing a good face.

Anyone with even a bit of ambition at the Sword Qi Great Wall, regardless of their cultivation level, held a poor impression of the wine-loving Mi Sword Immortal.

Mi Yu surprisingly asked three times and appeared willing to ask thirty more in the future.

This made Nalan Caihuan feel increasingly strange about Mi Yu.

Nalan Caihuan didn’t bother to hide anything from Mi Yu and straightforwardly asked, “Mi Yu, have you lost your mind?”

Mi Yu replied, “Have I ever been normal?”

Nalan Caihuan didn’t bother with polite words, “Mi Yu, you’re really not suited for accounting. Don’t waste the head of the Yan family’s time with trivial matters. When it comes to handling affairs, don’t say that Shao Yunyan isn’t at the Inverted Mountain now; even if he were at Chunfan Studio, he is ultimately an outsider sword immortal. If no one from our side shows up beforehand, he’s just a sword immortal at Chunfan Studio, which isn’t appropriate. The unpleasant words you casually mentioned before actually carry some truth.”

Mi Yu asked curiously, “Which words?”

Yan Ming said, “Thunder begins with lightning; one must first establish authority before launching an expedition.”

Mi Yu burst out laughing, “So that’s it.”

This phrase was derived from a fan’s inscription at Yan’s shop, and the reason it was in Mi Yu’s mouth was incidental; the main point was the other side of the folding fan, which read, “The beauty hasn’t arrived but the fragrance has, before she rises, my heart is already stirred.” This captivated Mi Yu at first glance. The fan’s one side had serious wording while the other was articulate, making Mi Yu feel it was tailor-made for him. Unfortunately, he didn’t know which young lady had gotten there first. Fortunately, the Yan family’s shop also sold inscribed fan covers, and the prices were not low.

In the room, there was also an outsider who was observant and quiet.

The direct disciple of Shao Yunyan at Chunfan Studio, Wei Wenlong, was a genius in divination.

Compared to the three outsiders in the room, Wei Wenlong was incredibly reserved.

He sat alone, quietly working through the seemingly dull ledgers that bored the others, as if he was swimming in water.

In essence, Wei Wenlong was not good at dealing with people; he was destined to have only numbers and divine money as his lifelong friends.

Finances and accounting had always been viewed as lowly professions; officials from the Ministry of Revenue were even mocked as “murky officials.” This was true both on and off the mountain; those managing the ferries between the eight continents were often pitiful people, with no hope of achieving the Great Dao, unable to break their respective bottlenecks.

Additionally, Wei Wenlong was merely at the Golden Core level, facing two long-established Nascent Soul sword immortal family heads and a Mi Sword Immortal who sounded as though he had just reached the fifth realm.

He indeed didn’t dare to breathe too loudly.

The local Qi Cultivators born from the Inverted Mountain were not unfamiliar with the Sword Qi Great Wall but were not intimate either.

In fact, they were less so than the outsiders who intentionally traveled to the Inverted Mountain, as those often aimed for the Sword Qi Great Wall.

There were many people like Wei Wenlong, a native of the Inverted Mountain, who had never visited the Sword Qi Great Wall in their entire lives.

What Wei Wenlong feared most was that renowned sword immortal, Mi Yu.

The charming rogue was the most fickle.

Moreover, he was a sword immortal.

Mi Yu felt Nalan Caihuan was right and humbly accepted the advice, getting up to leave the room.

Before Mi Yu left, he wore a friendly expression and spoke sincerely to Wei Wenlong, “Wenlong, you are a talent that our Hidden Official values greatly. Don’t belittle yourself; do your work well, and the Great Dao will be within reach. From now on, we’ll be friends.”

Wei Wenlong hurriedly stood up, but he was too reserved, too timid, and didn’t manage to utter a word. Mi Yu found this lad increasingly likable and urged him to sit and work without being so polite.

Mi Yu walked to the empty main hall, glancing at the seats previously occupied by several female cultivator shipowners.

Finally, he sat in his chair, taking out a jade token he prepared to gift. This was a bit peculiar.

The jade token, engraved with the number ninety-nine, was a matter that the Hidden Official had specifically instructed him to give to the Fan family’s ferry at Guihua Island before leaving.

Not to mention the shipowner of the Aihai Continent, Jiang Gaotai, even the sword immortal Shao’s face had not been spared.

However, the little manager of the Ding family’s ferry was trembling as he privately approached the Hidden Official, offering a “fair” price that even Mi Yu found unexpected.

But the Ding family genuinely hoped that future transactions would trouble the Hidden Official, to avoid the Ding family’s ferry becoming a target of resentment.

The young Hidden Official agreed with a smile, saying Chunfan Studio would undoubtedly return the favor.

Later, when Mi Yu inquired about this matter, the Hidden Official merely said that every family has its burdens to bear, and that the Ding family had no choice.

Without the female shipowner, Mi Yu didn’t bother thinking too hard on it.

However, regarding the Fan family’s cross-continent ferry, Mi Yu knew quite a bit. There was no helping it; there was a remarkable lady named Lady Guihua on Guihua Island, not in terms of appearance.

Mi Yu was not superficial, well aware that a woman’s beauty comes in many forms.

Only those who focused solely on facial features and figures were missing the myriad facets of female allure, rendering them unworthy of being considered Mi Yu’s peers.

The Fan family of Old Dragon City was inconspicuous among the families engaged in cross-continent ferry trading.

In fact, aside from the Fu family having a slight reputation, the other major surnames’ ferries were hardly worth mentioning when docked at the Inverted Mountain.

Just like the Ding family shipowner who earlier held discussions in the Chunfan Studio main hall, he did not measure up to the “Nishang” shipowner, Liu Shen.

As long as it involved enchanting women, Mi Yu would inevitably feel touched, never letting a beauty go to waste.

Mi Yu soon remembered that it seemed a young lady named Jin Su lived on Guihua Island, and she was quite beautiful too.

Of course, Mi Yu had never seen her.

He wouldn’t go out of his way to see Jin Su, not in the past, and certainly not now.

During that time at Chunfan Studio, gathering so many ferries in one night involved significant intrigue.

Wu Qiao and Bai Xi, those old foxes, along with the Rain Dragon Sect, which had a private residence called the Water Crystal Palace at the Inverted Mountain, and the Mei Flower Garden, all contributed greatly.

But the Hidden Official had never mentioned this matter, nor did he intend to settle scores afterward.

After all, it was merely a small matter.

This time, only twelve shipowners received invitations to visit Chunfan Studio for discussions.

Many shipowners who had docked at the Inverted Mountain early chose to linger for a while, neither in a hurry to unload their cargo nor to leave, waiting for invitations from Chunfan Studio.

Except for the closest Southern Posha Continent, it seemed the earlier ferries had yet to return to their respective continents and were still on their way back.

Apart from the Fan family’s Guihua Island, there was also the Hou family’s ferry, the “Yanzhi.”

They must have received flying sword messages from the Fu or Ding families; these two cross-continent ferries arrived at the Inverted Mountain one after the other within just two days.

The various ferries from the Eight Continents, along with the Yan family, Nalan family, or the widely connected Sun Juyuan, all had varying degrees of personal relationships. The reasoning was simple: on the Sword Qi Great Wall, sword immortals or their descendants from influential families often had numerous strange requests. Not to mention the exorbitant prices for rare treasures, they also sought nearly a hundred types of mountain delicacies at inflated prices.

The Hou family ferry, “Yanzhi,” catered specifically to provide exquisite fragrances, weaving sixteen types of fragrant sachets for the fixed buyers on the Sword Qi Great Wall.

On this matter, the Hidden Official lineage had seen considerable disputes. Lin Junbi and Miao Sword Immortal rarely stood on the same front, proposing to cut off all such supply channels and cease receiving any useless items for the Sword Qi Great Wall.

However, in the end, they chose a compromise plan to reduce such business dealings, but did not completely sever the connections.

Guihua Island, still docked at the Zhuofang Pavilion, received the Chunfan Studio invitation. After the Hou family ferry manager arrived, they exchanged information.

Currently, the manager position of Guihua Island had fallen to the Fan family’s offering, Ma Zhi.

A Golden Core sword cultivator, his life sword was “Liang Yin.”

The small courtyard on Guihua Island was recorded in the name of an outsider and had not opened to the public for years.

Ma Zhi had previously guided an outsider youth in swordsmanship there.

In Lady Guihua’s elegant courtyard, her disciple Jin Su was responsible for brewing tea for guests.

Ma Zhi and the Hou family shipowner were discussing how to present gifts, as they heard previously that Lingzhi Studio had lost over a hundred pieces of fairy treasures overnight. The remaining items were either too lightweight for meaningful sentiment or were excessively expensive, intimidating buyers.

Shipowner Hou Peng was quite worried about this; although the Hou family conducted thriving business in the expansive area north of Old Dragon City and south of Guanhu Academy, the actual profits outside the books were quite limited. If the Hou family ferry “Yanzhi” had heard of this matter before leaving Old Dragon City, they would need to visit Chunfan Studio and prepare a hefty gift before entering, which would not be too troublesome. This amount of profit was still manageable. However, as Hou Peng and Guihua Island received their flying sword messages halfway through, he would have to cover the expenses himself, which was troublesome. If the gifts were insufficient in weight, the Chunfan Studio would snub them, and later, the Fan family’s ancestral hall would likely criticize him; if he spent too much, after passing through Chunfan Studio, his family would have more gossip to deal with.

People who genuinely do things often encounter mistakes, while those who enjoy comfort at home chatter endlessly throughout the year.

Ma Zhi was not much better off; the Fan family was in a troublesome period, and the old sword cultivator, precisely because of being close to the future family head Fan Er, was dragged into it as well.

Now, every one of his actions was closely monitored by the old men of the Fan family’s ancestral hall.

The eldest Miss Fan Junmiao had not shown herself for a long time; the Fan family claimed she had gone on a long journey alone.

Ma Zhi had some speculations but didn’t dare to discuss it with anyone.

The young Fan Er, having transformed from a boy into a young man, was gradually beginning to participate in family business affairs. Naturally, Ma Zhi belonged to the faction of Fan Er; otherwise, he couldn’t have become the manager of the ferry, even if Lady Guihua had put forward the recommendation.

Although Guihua Island was already under Fan Er’s ownership, the Fan family had substantial doubts about this inexperienced young master. After all, he had borrowed a large sum of money from the Gu Yu family to assist the down-and-out Longquan of the Great Li dynasty. The discussions held in the ancestral hall had been heated, with many old-timers believing that Fan Er was still too naive and impulsive. Even the future family head should not completely manage Guihua Island’s ferry business; a more seasoned elder from the Fan family should assist with management for a while before trusting Fan Er with it.

If it weren’t for the Sun family also chipping in, along with Fan Er using a significant amount of his own private funds already recorded in his name, this would not have been possible.

Lady Guihua merely drank tea, her demeanor calm, without a word.

Both sides roughly agreed on how to prepare gifts and conduct themselves once inside Chunfan Studio, generally learning from the previously discussed matters with the Fu and Ding families: say little, watch more, and speak less is no mistake.

Hou Peng set down his teacup, a strange expression crossing his face.

After Ma Zhi finished discussing the issues, he no longer drank the tea and instead helped himself to a pot of Guihua’s brew.

Hou Peng asked softly, “The new Hidden Official is Chen Pingan, right?”

Ma Zhi’s face stiffened, but he couldn’t help but burst into laughter, “Brother Hou, what are you thinking?!”

Jin Su was bewildered.

Lady Guihua chuckled softly, teasing, “A rare guest, a noble guest.”

After Chen Pingan sat down, he apologized, “Lady Guihua, don’t think too much; I just came here to ask for a pot of Guihua brew.”

Lady Guihua brought out a jug of Guihua brew, handing it to the young man, asking with a smile, “Since you say that, does it mean the Hidden Official has begun paying attention to the Mei Flower Garden?”

Chen Pingan remained silent.

Lady Guihua then asked, “You’re not worried about me and that rosy-faced lady being in cahoots?”

Chen Pingan shook his head, “Of course not.”

Lady Guihua no longer asked about the fate of the Mei Flower Garden.

Chen Pingan said he came here to drink but didn’t actually drink much of the Guihua brew; instead, he smiled and asked, “Miss Jin Su, do you still like Sun Jianshu and not Fan Er?”

Lady Guihua nodded.

Then Chen Pingan only sat for a while, and Lady Guihua merely chatted about Fan Er’s recent situation.

Both seemed to have little more to say aside from the subject of Fan Er.

After such a long separation, their words were few, unlike the instant connection they had during their first meeting, the sword-bearing youth and Lady Guihua.

Lady Guihua, of course, could also see that the young Hidden Official, despite his youth, was burdened with worries. It was evident that his current situation was not easy.

After Chen Pingan had a small jug of Guihua brew, he prepared to return to the Inverted Mountain’s Chunfan Studio, but he wouldn’t be appearing there.

This trip was, besides for leisure, more importantly to request that Guihua Island relay a letter to Cui Dongshan and the royal prince Song Jixin.

Lady Guihua accepted the two sealed letters.

After Chen Pingan thanked her and was about to take his leave, a familiar figure ran from the courtyard entrance.

It was the young lady from the Guihua small courtyard, Jin Su.

Chen Pingan stood up to greet her, smiling as he called out, “Miss Jin Su.”

Jin Su paused for a moment, halting her steps, clearly not expecting this fellow to sneakily come to Guihua Island. She smiled back, “Chen Pingan, why are you here?”

Then Jin Su quickly corrected herself, “Young Master Chen.”

Chen Pingan helplessly said, “Just call my name.”

Jin Su nodded, sitting beside Lady Guihua and softly asking, “Aren’t you practicing punches at the Sword Qi Great Wall? Why do you have time to run over here for wine? I heard that both gates of the Inverted Mountain are strictly guarded, like preventing thieves.”

Jin Su hesitated for a moment before gently asking, “Is it because you accidentally share the same name as that Hidden Official, making you feel some frustration and thus came here to drink away your sorrows?”

Chen Pingan stifled a laugh and nodded, “That’s right.”

Lady Guihua also smiled knowingly.

Jin Su lamented, “I had hoped that you were the legendary Hidden Official, the great sword immortal of the Sword Qi Great Wall.”

Chen Pingan said, “If I were really that Hidden Official, I think Miss Jin Su would also feel frustrated enough to want to drink.”

Jin Su broke into a bright smile and turned to Lady Guihua, saying, “Master, Young Master Chen speaks much more refined now than before.”

Lady Guihua asked with a smile, “What brings you back?”

Jin Su softly replied, “I still want to stroll around the Deer Horn Cliff.”

Lady Guihua looked at Chen Pingan.

The young man gave a significant glance.

Lady Guihua nodded but said, “Just right, you and Young Master Chen can go together towards the Zhuofang Pavilion.”

Jin Su hurriedly said, “No, no, I know the Inverted Mountain better than Young Master Chen.”

She liked Sun Jianshu and disliked Fan Er, while Chen Pingan was good friends with Fan Er and business partners with Sun Jianshu.

Thus, she felt it best not to get involved with Chen Pingan at all.

Lady Guihua didn’t press further, letting Jin Su leave alone, and her smile widened.

After a brief wait, Chen Pingan then stood up to bid farewell to Lady Guihua.

As Lady Guihua escorted him to the door, she suddenly said, “Be cautious of the most adept at hiding their clumsiness, Zhengyang Mountain.”

Chen Pingan casually glanced in the direction of Baoping Continent, nodding, “I will.”

Internally, he silently muttered that in the future, Zhengyang Mountain should kneel and beg him to be less cautious.

Lady Guihua asked, “Is it finally that sword cultivator?”

Chen Pingan replied with his heart, “Two life swords; once I reveal my identity as a sword cultivator, I’ll declare one as ‘Chopping Firewood’ and the other as ‘Accounts.’”

Lady Guihua remained silent for a moment before insincerely saying, “Nice names.”

As for what Chen Pingan’s true names for the two flying swords were, Lady Guihua had completely lost her curiosity.

Chen Pingan scratched his head, saying, “As for the real names of the flying swords, one is ‘Caged Sparrow.’ I originally planned to name it ‘Mid-Autumn,’ but it seems to conflict with ‘Flying Sword Fifteen.’ The other one, I’m still torn between ‘Moon in the Sky’ or ‘Moon in the Well.’”

When it comes to naming things, being too skilled is not necessarily a good thing.

Lady Guihua laughed, “At last, they have names befitting flying swords.”

Chen Pingan quietly left Guihua Island, meeting Miao Sword Immortal at the Zhuofang Pavilion.

The two then headed towards the Mei Flower Garden.

They sought to meet that rosy-faced lady, who was at home yet longing for a distant land. 

In addition to the Miao Sword Immortal, there was also Lu Zhi, who had just returned from her journey to the Fuyiao Continent’s mountains and waters.

When it came to reasoning with ladies, it must be the ladies themselves who spoke. 

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 752: Whispers Among the Mountains

The Plum Blossom Garden was the most intricate of the four private residences on Hanging Mountain, renowned for its winding corridors. However, it was best known for the plum trees, which grew naturally without the twisted forms of sickly or stunted trees. Their arrangement was haphazard yet pleasing, a testament to nature's artistry. Despite this, the garden was celebrated far and wide due to its substantial investment in importing numerous celestial plum trees from the Eight Continents, which were then transplanted into the garden.

The best spot for viewing in the Plum Blossom Garden was the pavilion with the plaque inscribed with "Not Contending for Spring."

The charming Madam Rouyan knelt on a bamboo mat made from the green bamboo of Qing Shen Mountain, her hands folded neatly on her knees, exuding grace and a warm smile. 

She turned her gaze towards the three sword cultivators slowly ascending the steps of the pavilion and said with a smile, "Since the matter has come to light, I am willing to accept my punishment. I just hope that the Great Sword Immortal Lu Zhi will be swift with her sword."

Chen Ping'an sat on the ground opposite Madam Rouyan and asked, "Will you not attempt to remedy this? The cultivation of plant spirits at the Fifth Realm is no easy task."

In the entire history of Baoping Continent, there had yet to be a single plant spirit at the Fifth Realm.

Madam Rouyan shook her head, saying, "If I could find my way past the border and kill it, it would only mean that I am destined not to survive. There's no need for pretenses."

Chen Ping'an pressed on, "Then the true form of that ascended great demon is buried beneath the Plum Blossom Garden? Otherwise, how would you know the border is dead?"

Madam Rouyan smiled but did not respond. Instead, she extended a hand towards the tall, slender woman, "It has been said that among the women of the Sword Qi Great Wall, the one resembling Sword Immortal Lu Zhi is the most beautiful, capable of toppling nations. The harmony between person and sword is truly fitting; seeing her today, it is indeed true."

Lu Zhi frowned slightly.

Sword Immortal Chou Miao sighed, knowing well who had spoken such words.

Chen Ping'an then queried, "So I will ask you one thing: you were born in the realm of Hao Ran, so why do you long for the wild and untamed world?"

Madam Rouyan chuckled, "The rules set by the Sage of Rituals are good, but unfortunately, the later generations of cultivators have not upheld them well. Once they ascend the mountain and attain the Dao, there are countless immortals and divine figures, yet how many regard us fortunate plant spirits as people? I have suffered greatly and do not wish to speak of it. After barely escaping the sea of suffering, I look around, and throughout the centuries, the human world has shown little difference. Therefore, I have harbored resentment for a long time."

She turned her gaze towards a large door nearby the Plum Blossom Garden before withdrawing it and smiling, "It's not that I truly like the wild world, where uncivilized beasts hold power; such a distant land, compared to Hao Ran, can it really be any better? I merely wish to see the realm of Hao Ran with my own eyes. On the mountains and in the valleys, all are dead, and among the cultivators, those of the Dao will perish first. Only the plants remain, thriving in their cycles of life and death, flourishing through the years. Is that reason enough for you, Sir Hidden Official?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "If you say it is enough, then it is."

Chou Miao felt that this visit to the Plum Blossom Garden had unexpectedly gone quite smoothly.

Suddenly, Lu Zhi spoke up, "I will exchange the military achievements I have accumulated to spare her life. From now on, I will take her under my wing. Sir Hidden Official, what do you think?"

Chou Miao was taken aback.

Madam Rouyan was even more astonished. Just moments ago, she had truly resigned herself to death.

After countless calculations, she had deemed her fate either to die or to live a fate worse than death. If that were the case, her luck was not the worst; at least among the sword immortals, there was a woman, fortunate enough not to be surrounded by those filthy men—what could be simpler?

Madam Rouyan never expected Lu Zhi would say such words.

Lu Zhi addressed Madam Rouyan, "From now on, you will follow me in your cultivation; you need not be a servant or a maid."

Lu Zhi then turned to Chen Ping'an, seeking his agreement.

After a moment of thought, Chen Ping'an nodded, "That works."

Madam Rouyan collapsed to the ground, on the verge of tears.

All around the Plum Blossom Garden, the plum trees bloomed abundantly, reflecting the connection between Madam Rouyan and this small world, bringing forth a spectacle of nature.

Lu Zhi frowned, "Rouyan, I have only one request of you: in the future, when faced with life and death, if there are men before you, do not behave in such a manner. Of course, it won't be easy for others to want you dead."

Madam Rouyan bowed deeply to Lu Zhi, saying, "Thank you, Daoist friend Lu Zhi!"

She stood up gracefully and approached Lu Zhi's side.

Even Chou Miao had to admit that Madam Rouyan was an innate beauty.

Meanwhile, the young Hidden Official had squatted down to roll up the valuable bamboo mat from Qing Shen Mountain.

It was undeniably more genuine than his own bamboo sea cave wine.

Chou Miao pretended not to notice anything.

Madam Rouyan hesitated for a moment, looking at the young man who was moving the bamboo mat, and couldn't help but inquire with her heart, "What is this?"

Lu Zhi smiled, "Our Hidden Official is too shy to scavenge for land over at Spring Fan Pavilion, so this unclaimed Plum Blossom Garden is going to face a disaster."

Chou Miao became even more puzzled.

From Lu Zhi's tone, it seemed that her impression of this Hidden Official was not entirely negative?

Chen Ping'an finished rolling up the mat, tucking it under his arm, and stood up. "Lu Zhi, let me say this first: the reason the Plum Blossom Garden can take root on Hanging Mountain is not solely due to Madam Rouyan's cultivation but also because of cunning and strategy—something you are not particularly good at."

Lu Zhi shot a glance at Madam Rouyan, "It doesn't matter. As long as one is willing to risk their life, whether they are cultivators or plant spirits, it's all a matter of a single sword strike."

Continuing, Lu Zhi added, "Chen Ping'an, you are skilled in all sorts of convoluted calculations, so help me keep an eye on her in the future."

Lu Zhi then said to Madam Rouyan, "To be frank, I do not yet trust you. However, I can guarantee that after a thousand years, you will regain your freedom. If my path were to falter and I die within that thousand years, the matter of you will be left to Chen Ping'an. If you think a thousand years is too long, we can negotiate, but I won't agree to it."

Madam Rouyan smiled enchantingly, bowed deeply to Lu Zhi, her elegance captivating.

At Lu Zhi's level as a sword cultivator, her sword heart was exceptionally clear, and given Lu Zhi's many rumors and stories, Madam Rouyan was indeed willing to trust her.

Chou Miao gave a thumbs-up to the Hidden Official.

Indeed, women discussing matters among themselves was more appropriate.

Chen Ping'an put the bamboo mat away and asked Lu Zhi and Chou Miao to leave for a moment, saying he wanted to ask Madam Rouyan some matters.

The two sword immortals left the pavilion.

Madam Rouyan exclaimed softly, looking around, "Sir Hidden Official, you are truly deep and unassuming. After not seeing you for years, you’ve become a sword cultivator? The innate magical powers of this flying sword are so rare."

Chen Ping'an was not the least bit surprised and asked, "When Jiang Heng of Yuguizong visited Hanging Mountain and stayed at the Plum Blossom Garden, what did this Jiang family heir seek?"

Madam Rouyan countered, "Why not directly inquire about the matters of Guihua Island in Old Dragon City? Is it that you cannot bear to ask, yet feel compelled, or are you unwilling to ask because you fear the answer?"

Chen Ping'an frowned, "This matter does not require further inquiry."

Madam Rouyan laughed, "May I ask, Sir Hidden Official, if you were to go to Guihua Island now, would you call her Aunt Gui or Madam Gui?"

Chen Ping'an answered vaguely, "In the future, you should consider Lu Zhi more when you are by her side. The sword immortal's heart is too pure; however, without this sword heart, Lu Zhi would not be the Lu Zhi of today. But in the future, when she reaches the realm of Hao Ran, she may not find everything to her liking."

Madam Rouyan's eyes lit up. "I won’t have to stay at the Sword Qi Great Wall forever?"

Chen Ping'an nodded, "In the future, you will accompany Lu Zhi to South Posa Continent."

Madam Rouyan smiled, "Since I can not only live but also have no worries, I will answer all your questions fully and truthfully. First, Jiang Heng is truly ambitious yet incompetent, vastly inferior to the border. Initially, Jiang Heng set his sights on the Guihua Island of the Fan family, but Madam Gui did not agree. He then foolishly tried to persuade me, in the Plum Blossom Garden, to assist Yuguizong in opening a new trade route, a transit point for Qi practitioners engaged in pearl harvesting on Luhua Island."

Chen Ping'an inquired, "Why not Rain Dragon Sect?"

Madam Rouyan shot him a sidelong glance, "Sir Hidden Official, are you truly unaware or just pretending to be ignorant?"

Chen Ping'an said, "Please tell me."

Madam Rouyan chuckled, "The Rain Dragon Sect has a female ancestor who, in her early years, traveled to Tongye Continent and was so smitten by Jiang Shangzhen that she nearly shattered her heart; she directly returned, a fine embryonic immortal, only barely entering the Jade Pure Realm after hundreds of years. As Jiang Heng's son, does he dare to go to Rain Dragon Sect seeking death? But times have changed; now, if Jiang Heng were to visit Rain Dragon Sect again, it would indeed be seeking death, but it would be difficult to achieve."

Chen Ping'an sat on a bench, rubbing his forehead.

Once Jiang Shangzhen was involved, everything turned into those bewildering surprises.

How many people would take the initiative to donate money to the mountain’s expenses?

But the biggest surprise was that Jiang Shangzhen had now actually become the leader of Yuguizong!

Xun Yuan was truly formidable.

In Chen Ping'an's mind, Jiang Shangzhen's current success owed much to Xun Yuan's influence.

Setting aside personal grievances, Chen Ping'an believed that the position of sect leader was one that Xun Yuan rightly deserved.

Xun Yuan's schemes against Chen Ping'an back then still left him feeling uneasy.

Madam Rouyan performed a hand sign, and a figure that resembled an old man appeared in the pavilion, which Chen Ping'an stowed away.

The ensuing questions and answers in the pavilion were succinct and to the point.

In the end, the group left the Plum Blossom Garden.

According to Madam Rouyan's prior revelations, the Plum Blossom Garden would indeed be able to relocate, but where it could escape to now was uncertain, especially since Madam Rouyan was now following Lu Zhi.

Lu Zhi took her directly to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Lu Zhi had a private residence south of the city, where Madam Rouyan would temporarily reside.

Chen Ping'an, along with Chou Miao, headed to Spring Fan Pavilion, where Madam Rouyan promised to catalog all the treasures of the Plum Blossom Garden. The volume should be quite thick and would later be sent to the Summer Resort Palace.

The nominal owner of the Plum Blossom Garden was merely a puppet that Madam Rouyan had raised.

The intricate and convoluted stories within, if Madam Rouyan were willing to share, and if the young Hidden Official had the leisure to document them, could likely fill a fantastical novel of twists and turns.

Upon arriving at Spring Fan Pavilion, Mi Yu and the others were in the main hall discussing business, and Shao Yunyan had yet to return from Hanging Mountain, arriving later than Lu Zhi.

It was not that Shao the Sword Immortal did not wish to return with Lu Zhi; it was simply that his flying sword could not catch up with hers.

To save time, he chose not to take a ferry, instead opting to fly his sword from Fuyou Continent all the way to Hanging Mountain, which was no small feat.

Tonight, twelve ferry managers were arriving at Spring Fan Pavilion, and not everyone could take a jade token home; however, as long as the relationships were not too close, these boatmen, seasoned by the dangers of the Jianghu, would not easily disclose to others who had received a token. Those who failed to get one would likely wish for others to believe they had secured one.

Chen Ping'an did not head to the main hall but found Wei Wenlong in the account room.

Chou Miao had no intention of dealing with a pile of account books; during her time at the Summer Resort Palace, she had also flipped through many books and accounts. As Cao Jun said, once she left the Summer Resort Palace, she never wanted to see another page of a book again in her life.

However, Chen Ping'an insisted on having Chou Miao sit down with him.

When Wei Wenlong saw the young Hidden Official and Sword Immortal Chou Miao, he became even more flustered.

Wei Wenlong had brought some miscellaneous books to this side. Chen Ping'an picked one up, opened it, and was pleasantly surprised; a true expert could discern quality at a glance. If this Wei Wenlong were merely a façade, Chen Ping'an felt he could consume that book in his hands.

For this "miscellaneous book," was actually a secret document from the Ministry of Revenue of the old Lu Dynasty in Baoping Continent, likely a result of Old Dragon City's intercontinental ferry service.

Wei Wenlong, feeling somewhat anxious, forced himself to speak softly, "Sir Hidden Official, as long as I have free time, there’s no need to settle accounts. I just read these Ministry of Revenue records on the overthrown dynasties of various continents. They were not expensive, bought by the sack, and compared to those rare items, they cost but a few snowflake coins. Moreover, thanks to my master’s connections, the six ferries in Old Dragon City have been quite generous, selling them at half price."

Chen Ping'an patted Wei Wenlong's shoulder, a bright smile on his face, "You've encountered a great person!"

Wei Wenlong stumbled back, more shocked than anything.

His smile was strained; it was no wonder that the Great Sword Immortal, the Hidden Official, had such terrifying strength.

Chen Ping'an moved a chair closer to Wei Wenlong and began asking about the annual tax situation of the Dali Dynasty.

Wei Wenlong answered fluently, also mentioning some minor tricks played by earlier Ministry officials. However, he indicated that the financial records of the Dali Dynasty had become increasingly obscured over the past century. Moreover, for such a large dynasty, the numbers on the accounts were all fabricated; the key lay in the secret treasury’s records. Otherwise, there was no need to discuss the imitation white jade capital of the Great Dali; the mountain and river ferries built by the Mo family alone would require a significant amount of divine money. Wei Wenlong speculated that aside from the Mo family, merchants must be behind the scenes propping up the Dali’s financial operations; otherwise, the funds should have collapsed long ago, rotting into nothingness.

Wei Wenlong was clearly determined to truly master the intricacies of fiscal matters, so he needed to delve deeply into a series of relevant rules.

Chen Ping'an mostly posed small, incisive questions that allowed Wei Wenlong to speak freely.

Once the topic turned to finances, Wei Wenlong transformed into a different person.

He articulated clearly and was adept with the rules, skilled in calculations.

Chen Ping'an listened intently.

This knowledge was truly valuable.

It was the first time Chou Miao had seen the young Hidden Official so animated.

Chen Ping'an suddenly said, "Complete the task, no interest in currency."

Wei Wenlong paused for a moment before softly asking, "What is the principle of governing a country?"

Chen Ping'an smiled, "All farming should be beneficial, and all goods should flow freely; the marketplace should be abundant."

Wei Wenlong inquired, "What is the aim?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "To ensure wealth and currency flow like water!"

Wei Wenlong broke into a grin, unable to contain his excitement, his hands pressed down on the desk, jubilant, "Friend, you are truly a friend!"

Then, Wei Wenlong felt incredibly awkward, quickly pulling back his hands, trying to maintain a respectful demeanor as he softly said, "Sir Hidden Official, I have greatly offended you."

Chen Ping'an laughed, "We are fellow travelers; no need to mind that. From now on, call me Chen Daoist! You can also call me a good man brother."

Chou Miao couldn't help but ask, "Are you discussing merchant knowledge?"

Chen Ping'an waved his hand, "There is a large connection, but they must not be conflated."

Wei Wenlong shot a glance at the sword immortal Chou Miao, who was sitting there like a wooden statue, nearly rolling his eyes. It was obvious he was a novice, utterly clueless about the subject, yet he was still a sword immortal.

No wonder he couldn't become the Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Chen Ping'an glanced out the window at the evening sky, leaving a jar of osmanthus wine on the table. He stood up, smiling, "You are always welcome to visit our Summer Resort Palace in the future. If you wish to stay longer, even better! I can directly clear out a residence for you. But it won't be until the trade route of the Eight Continents is properly established; otherwise, it would delay serious matters. No need to rush, no need to rush. Once I return to the Summer Resort Palace, I will help you clear out a unique residence."

Wei Wenlong hurriedly stood up, flustered, "Sir Hidden Official, this is too much, too much."

Chen Ping'an waved his hand, "It’s settled."

After leaving the room, at the end of winter, Chen Ping'an habitually rubbed his hands together for warmth.

Sword Immortal Chou Miao smiled, "In a good mood?"

Chen Ping'an grinned, "Great mood."

If given the chance, he would certainly want to recruit Wei Wenlong to Ruining Mountain in the future.

He could easily let Wei Wenlong practice on that Lotus Root Blessed Land.

Chou Miao looked at the young Hidden Official, who was grinning like a fool, and asked, "Is this Wei Wenlong truly that impressive?"

Chen Ping'an nodded, "I wouldn’t trade a Spring Fan Pavilion for him, not even a bit."

Chou Miao inquired, "What if we added a Plum Blossom Garden?"

Chen Ping'an complained, "Sword Immortal Chou Miao, this kind of banter is no fun at all."

Chou Miao suddenly spoke in thought, "The Hidden Official’s schemes have yielded results; they can delay matters for another six months. If the trade routes of the Eight Continents go smoothly without major setbacks, we might gain another year. So, we are still short a year and a half."

Chou Miao was certainly regarded as the best candidate for the next Hidden Official, and it wasn’t without reason.

Chen Ping'an cursed under his breath.

Chou Miao chuckled, "Who are you cursing?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "Definitely not the Great Sword Immortal."

Chou Miao smiled, "I advise you not to mistake me for Sword Immortal Mi Yu."

Chen Ping'an said, "This will not happen again; everything can be forgiven up to three times."

Chou Miao remarked, "That last look Wei Wenlong gave me seemed a bit off."

Chen Ping'an said, "Impossible; when Wei Wenlong looks at you, his eyes are full of admiration, almost mistaking you for a stunning woman."

Chou Miao laughed, "Sir Hidden Official, do you wish to return to the Summer Resort Palace with a bruised face, or do you want Wei Wenlong to be half-dead from my sword?"

Chen Ping'an chuckled, "Only up to three times."

Before becoming the new Hidden Official.

At the thatched cottage, Chen Ping'an had a conversation with the Great Sword Immortal.

"Do you think this Hidden Official can merely delay matters for the Sword Qi Great Wall by three years?"

"Just three?"

"Or should I let you delay for thirty years? If you think you can pull that off, promise me now, and I will help you propose to Ning Fu and the Yao family right away."

"Deal, no problem."

"Get lost."

After saying goodbye to Sister Bei at the Mountain Cliff Academy, Pei Qian and Cui Dongshan left the Great Sui Capital together.

They trekked through mountains and rivers, approaching the border of the former vassal Huang Ting Kingdom, which Pei Qian described as "easy and leisurely, accompanied by the Great Dao."

Along the way, holding a mountain staff and carrying a small bamboo box, Pei Qian diligently copied texts every day without fail, practicing that crazy demonic sword technique against Cui Dongshan, and had yet to lose a match.

Otherwise, she would be staring blankly at a cluster of golden threads—the essence of sword intent gifted to her by the swinging sword immortal from the Sword Qi Great Wall, Zhou Cheng.

Pei Qian asked the big white goose multiple times whether it was truly inedible. In the romantic novels that Sister Bei and Li Huai enjoyed, they often described treasures gifted by elders that could enhance one's inner strength when consumed.

Cui Dongshan insisted it was definitely not edible; if she did, she would be in for a disaster, with intestines spilling everywhere, not even able to hold it with both hands. Wouldn't that be disgusting if she tried to put it in her small book box?

Today, the two were by the river; Cui Dongshan was fishing while Pei Qian squatted nearby, using the small bamboo box as a makeshift writing desk.

Cui Dongshan had crafted the small bamboo writing box himself, which Pei Qian reluctantly accepted. Though she found its color unappealing, she didn’t directly say it, only asking if he knew what "vibrantly green" meant.

Cui Dongshan pretended not to hear her countless hints.

As he fished, Cui Dongshan rambled on about things that Pei Qian only half-listened to. 

He spoke of practicing writing, the method of imitating the ancients, like a ghost enjoying sacrifices, absorbing its essence but not consuming its substance. To honor the ancient, one must meet the divine encounter, passing a threshold.

"The novice must focus on the structure, ensuring clarity in strokes and markings; avoid lofty claims of profundity. Remember, it is not about quantity but continuity."

And then there were instructions on writing small script, advocating clarity and richness.

As Pei Qian copied her texts, she focused intently and ignored the big white goose’s chatter.

"Your writing, can it compare to Master’s? Look at how many convoluted sayings he has. You’re just showing off, trying to bully me because I’m copying less, aren’t you?"

Cui Dongshan turned his head and glanced at the serious Pei Qian, chuckling.

"Is my writing good? How it measures up can be gauged by the price of a few palm-sized pieces of calligraphy, and how much grain they can fetch."

Unfortunately, he couldn’t say this out loud; otherwise, Pei Qian might immediately rush up the mountain, chop out seven or eight large bamboo boxes, and insist he fill them up or not be allowed to leave.

Furthermore, not every stroke written could be deemed worthy of being a piece of calligraphy.

Once she finished copying, Pei Qian leaned against the small bamboo box, patiently waiting for a fish to bite; she had truly inherited her master's teachings on cooking fish.

Suddenly, Cui Dongshan asked if Pei Qian wanted to wander the Jianghu alone, to slowly return home to Ruining Mountain.

Pei Qian certainly dared not. Was the big white goose's head not quite right from being hit with a mountain staff? That question was such a wet blanket.

Pei Qian quickly said, "No, no, I must have Master’s consent to descend the mountain alone as his first disciple, plus I would need that little donkey for companionship to travel the rivers and mountains."

Cui Dongshan then mentioned that further ahead, the Yu River of Huang Ting Kingdom was where Chen Lingjun had made his fortune. There was also the Cao family’s Zhilian Pavilion, which was practically the hometown of the warm tree girl. Wouldn’t she want to go take a look?

Pei Qian adjusted the strap of her bamboo box, standing up and beginning to stroll beside Cui Dongshan, one hand holding the bamboo box and the other gripping her mountain staff. "You’re talking too much; wandering is trivial, but returning home is paramount. If I'm not there keeping an eye, wouldn’t the old chef’s great cooking skills go to waste? Besides, if I’m not watching the New Year shop, what if Sister Shi Rou secretly buys that rouge and powder, misusing funds?"

Cui Dongshan laughed, "Sister Shi Rou buys that rouge and powder? Why? To put it on her face? First scare the living, then frighten the ghosts?"

Pei Qian frowned, "Big White Goose, you mustn't speak ill of Sister Shi Rou. If she has to sneakily buy rouge and powder, she needs to keep it hidden well so I won't see, fearing I might laugh at her..."

Cui Dongshan chuckled, "So did you laugh at her?"

Pei Qian maintained a straight face, stifling laughter.

Cui Dongshan said, "Since the master is not around..."

Pei Qian burst out laughing. "When I was younger, I was even smaller and more clueless! I almost laughed myself to death back then, my stomach hurt so much I nearly put holes in the counter."

She quickly added, "But I only laughed; I didn’t say a single word of nonsense! I swear on my life!"

Cui Dongshan smiled, "Just too busy laughing to speak, huh?"

Pei Qian playfully slapped Cui Dongshan's head, her brows brightening, "Still, my little senior brother understands me! Look at you being so clever, let’s catch a big fish and cook it up! We have to eat well and drink well before we continue our journey!"

Then Pei Qian grew a little sad, "Sister Shi Rou is quite pitiful; you shouldn’t bully her anymore. It’s about reasoning, after all. Learn from Master, and speak well to her. Sister Shi Rou isn't dumb, she can understand. However, I’m just saying this casually…"

Pei Qian softly added, "Both my little senior brother and Master are people who think a lot before doing things. I don’t want to overthink things; I can’t even copy fast enough."

Cui Dongshan gazed at the water’s surface, rubbing his brow, "When Master was younger than you, he dared to leave the Great Sui alone to return home."

Pei Qian questioned, "Is it so surprising that a disciple can't match his master?"

Cui Dongshan replied, "Disciples need not be inferior to their masters; that is what the ancient sages taught in black and white."

Pei Qian pouted, "I only listen to Master."

Cui Dongshan sighed, "I truly have urgent matters and must head to the Great Dali Capital immediately. Even the ferry seems too slow. If I delay, the next time I meet my senior sister, it might be quite difficult—who knows when that will be."

Pei Qian thought for a moment and nodded, "Fine, if you had begged me earlier, it would have been done. I can walk back to Ruining Mountain alone—it's just a small matter!"

She pulled out a yellow paper talisman from her sleeve, not immediately sticking it to her forehead, but carefully tucking it back into her sleeve.

She had traveled through countless mountains and rivers with her master, so this talisman had also accompanied her for quite some time.

With it, she feared nothing.

Cui Dongshan smiled and asked, "So I’m really leaving now?"

Pei Qian impatiently replied, "Stop talking so much! You think my crazy demonic sword technique is just for show?"

Cui Dongshan sighed, "Fine, fine, then I’ll stay with you a bit longer. Otherwise, Master will blame me later."

Standing next to Cui Dongshan, Pei Qian said, "Go on, go on, don’t mind me! I’m not afraid of all the sword qi immortals at the Sword Qi Great Wall, why would I fear a Huang Ting Kingdom?"

Cui Dongshan put away his fishing rod.

"I’ll walk you a little way; see that stone cliff over there? I’ll take you to that point."

As they walked along the riverbank, Pei Qian softly said, "Big White Goose, can I speak my mind?"

"Sure."

"Actually, Master worries that I won’t know better in the future, and I get that. But Master also worries that I’ll end up like him, which I just can't comprehend. What’s wrong with being like Master?"

"Why not just tell Master directly?"

"Master already worries; if I say this, he’ll probably worry even more. The more he worries, the more worried I become. The master I love most is this first disciple of his, and then I worry more and more..."

Cui Dongshan looked towards the distant green mountains and smiled, "With a calm heart, let the white clouds deal with trivial matters; wait for the rain to come when you leave the mountain."

Pei Qian frowned, "Are you making fun of me?"

"I’m praising you."

"By the heavens?"

"By the heavens!"

In the end, Pei Qian stopped and said solemnly, "Little Senior Brother, take care on your journey!"

Cui Dongshan nodded with a smile, "If I hadn’t met Master, I wouldn’t have such a wonderful senior sister like you."

With that, Cui Dongshan leaped into the air, like a wisp of white cloud returning home.

However, he didn’t leave just yet. Using an illusion technique, he surveyed the riverside.

He saw Pei Qian standing in place for a long while before finally mustering the courage to move, shaking her hands as she tried to take large strides, albeit slowly. At this rate, it would take her a century to reach Qidun Mountain.

Cui Dongshan rubbed his brow, feeling exasperated.

He watched for a long time until Pei Qian seemed to have found her resolve. She took a deep breath, stomped her foot down heavily, and dashed forward in an instant, disappearing like a flash of lightning.

Cui Dongshan felt even more worried.

With Pei Qian's minute courage, if she encountered any mountain spirits or ghosts, wouldn’t they just scare each other to death?

Cui Dongshan glanced around, riding the wind in a flash, yet silently, he headed towards a larger river. Stomping his foot, he shook the river god awake, grabbing its head and twisting its wrist so that its face turned towards the petite figure carrying a bamboo box. "Did you see that? My senior sister, you will be escorted to Hongzhu Town without any appearance. You cannot reveal yourself or leave any traces; after that, you can head home, and it will count as a contribution for you. Later, you can obtain a no-incident talisman from Dali; the Ministry of Rites will see to it, just wait at home. But if anything goes wrong, I’ll shatter your golden body."

As he spoke, Cui Dongshan exerted more force with his fingers, causing the water god’s golden body to explode like firecrackers, bursting with numerous cracks. After he withdrew his hand, "I feel like you’re not reliable at all; I’m worried you won’t take this seriously, so I shattered half of your golden body. After the task is completed, you can seek out the water god Yang Hua of the Iron Talisman River to help repair your golden body and claim that no-incident talisman."

The water god nearly collapsed on the spot, aghast at the audacity of this young man who was both powerful and brazen.

From start to finish, the little god had not uttered a word or completed a single task.

Cui Dongshan loosened his grip, gently patting the water god's head, and the numerous cracks in its golden body instantly closed, returning to normal.

Cui Dongshan shook his sleeves, watching the bewildered water god, and asked, "What are you dawdling for? Did the experience of having your golden body shattered feel so good that you want it again?"

The water god gulped, ready to ride the wind to pursue the so-called "senior sister."

But he was met with a slap from the white-clad youth, sending him splashing into the river, causing waves to erupt. "Is that how you're going? I told you not to leave a trace!"

Cui Dongshan smacked his forehead, "I should have asked the mountain god instead—my bad. I’m sorry, just go back where you came from."

Unexpectedly, the water god was not too foolish. He held back the pain from his golden body’s damage and knelt in the water, bowing, "Little god pays respects to the immortal master."

Cui Dongshan smiled, "No wonder you were once a little river lord, daring to wield a spear and declare, 'In Liu Gong's realm, no one dares to offend.' Get up and speak; I see you’re quite clever. I believe that even if you are a water god, you won’t fall too far behind once you enter the mountains. But to be safe, I’ll give you a Water God Mountain Crossing Talisman."

Cui Dongshan brought two fingers together, conjuring a golden talisman out of thin air, which he gently tossed down for the water god to catch.

When the water god looked up again, the white-clad youth’s figure had vanished.

With the Water God Mountain Crossing Talisman in hand, the water god found that by slightly channeling his spiritual energy, it merged seamlessly with his golden body.

After cautiously reaching the shore, he found himself moving even more freely than in the waters he ruled.

The water god felt as if he were dreaming.

He immediately concealed his aura and began to chase after that young girl.

Just as the water god relaxed, a ripple surged through his heart lake, akin to a raging storm. He had to stop in his tracks to resist it, and then he heard the white-clad youth’s voice again, “Remember, don’t approach my senior sister within a hundred yards. Otherwise, even with the talisman, you will still be detected; the consequences are yours to weigh. At that point, whether this talisman serves as a lifeline or a death knell, who can say?"

The water god immediately bowed and clasped his fists in acknowledgment.

After that, he followed the small girl from a distance.

The water god couldn’t help but feel amused. This little girl, despite her young age, could really run fast.
