If she got hungry, she would run while pulling out dry rations from her bamboo box, hastily eating while continuing to run.

At first, the water god thought she was hiding from something.

But no matter how the water god searched, he found no signs.

Yet the water god grew increasingly puzzled; this little girl didn’t seem to be a practitioner of the Dao—how did she become such a formidable martial artist?

Throughout her journey, the little girl would bypass caves that offered shelter from the wind and rain, neglected and dilapidated temples, and even places rich in spiritual energy.

When she finally became tired and wanted to rest, she consciously chose to do so during the day, drawing a large circle with her staff and muttering to herself, then briefly resting, only to rise quickly and resume her journey.

Eventually, when the little girl leaped onto a high branch and caught sight of a city’s outline, her face scrunched up as if she were about to cry.

The water god was just feeling pity for the little girl when she landed heavily on the ground, swaggering along as if nothing were wrong, swinging her staff and humming about how delicious stinky tofu was.

The water god, of course, had no idea.

From a high branch, the white-clad youth quietly stood watching, his expression gentle, gazing at Pei Qian from a distance.

Only Cui Dongshan understood why things were this way.

When Master wasn’t around her, or she wasn’t at Master’s side, every place she passed alone mirrored the Lotus Root Blessed Land of her childhood.

Everyone she met along the way would resemble those familiar faces from the streets and alleys of the Lotus Root Blessed Land, nothing much different.

Cui Dongshan looked around, the green mountains stretching endlessly.

A single person murmured, and the mountains echoed back.

One could only hope so.

Cui Dongshan sighed.

Finally, he was willing to leave.

He still had to meet a significant figure on behalf of that old bastard. 

In a flash of white clothing, he soared into the air, crashing through the entire sea of clouds, with thunder rumbling like a farewell in the heavens. 

Meanwhile, Pei Qian, walking through the mountains and forests, originally joyfully chanting her way through, suddenly paused, quickly turning around, raising her head, and bouncing as she waved goodbye with all her might.

The water god realized that even when the little girl reached the county town, she never stayed at an inn.

The most she did was buy some snacks, keeping some in her pocket and more in her small bamboo box.

Moreover, she would visit various water shrines and temples to pay her respects, and if she encountered Daoist temples, she would light incense.

Aside from that, she rarely spoke to anyone, merely walking through the mountains and rivers at a much slower pace, without the need to rush.

The only time she lingered for a long while was when she squatted on a low earthen wall, gazing longingly at a group of horseback Jianghu heroes. The little girl appeared somewhat envious.

But it wasn’t the impressive-looking Jianghu figures that caught her eye; it was their mounts.

On the side of the Yu River in Huang Ting Kingdom, the little girl merely glanced before bolting away. Near the Cao family’s Zhilian Pavilion, she did the same, sneaking a couple of peeks before running off.

Finally, she reached the borders of Hongzhu Town.

The water god felt a sense of relief while also finding it somewhat laughable. With the little girl being so cautious, did she really need his protection all the way?

Was it truly so fortunate to have obtained a rare talisman? Would she really get that no-incident talisman from Dali?

The water god couldn’t believe it, but it didn’t matter; he followed the white-clad youth’s instructions and stopped there, ready to return home!

As the water god turned to leave, he noticed the little girl sprinting toward him from a distance. She stopped a short distance away, planted her mountain staff firmly into the ground, and then clasped her fists with a smile, bowing to him.

Once the water god returned the gesture, she grinned widely, "My master is the lord of Ruining Mountain, and you are always welcome to visit our home!"

The water god froze for a moment before nodding.

Had this little girl forgotten to introduce herself?

But the little girl had already pulled up her staff, turned around, and skipped away, shaking the small bamboo box on her back.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 753: The One Who Wishes to Support Heaven, Please Rise

In the desolate mountains, evening clouds hinted at snow.

Zhu Lian had a lot on his mind.

Today, while Zhu Lian and Zheng Dafu played chess, they exchanged complaints. Zhu Lian grumbled that his brother Dafu's earnest gaze had scared off the celestial maiden, Huang Ting, while Zheng Dafu blamed the old cook for his lackluster culinary skills, which failed to retain the maiden. They lamented that Lupo Mountain had unjustly lost a registered supporter who was a Yuan Ying sword cultivator, a grave offense indeed. To atone, they felt compelled to hand over several treasured texts from the immortals to Zheng Dafu for safekeeping.

Wei Ban sat nearby, puzzled as to why, even after all this time, the two continued their quarrel. Then he realized: Was it that beautiful maiden, Huang Ting, captivating enough to warrant such fuss?

Zhu Lian turned to Wei Ban and asked with a smile, “I’ve heard you’re heading to the capital soon to pay respects to the Emperor. Perhaps you can score some dragon energy to bring back for our blessed land. That’s what I call purposeful travel!”

Zheng Dafu chimed in, “Indeed, the Mountain Lord can’t just lounge around watching chess without contributing!”

Wei Ban felt helpless; the title of North Peak Mountain Lord had even reached the ears of North Julu Continent. No passing wild chicken could lay an egg without permission.

However, their efforts had not been in vain. The latest lotus root blessed land had recently transitioned into a medium blessed land after investing several thousand Gu Yu coins. It was now brimming with new landscapes, spirits, and the nascent forms of heroic deities, flourishing like bamboo shoots after rain. Yet, overall numbers were still capped by a bottleneck.

But as long as enough divine coins were invested, the skies would widen and the fortunes would thicken, naturally breaking through any prior limitations.

What intrigued Zheng Dafu most was a popular romantic novel from the Southern Garden Kingdom, where a woman, gifted with ethereal charm, manifested in the mortal realm. She was born from collective human sentiment, yet her spiritual awareness was still not fully realized, leaving her somewhat dazed, drifting among books and paintings while quietly observing the unfamiliar world.

Her appearance was a rarity in the grand scheme of things.

She was quite different from the young girl, Chen Nuanshu.

This woman, who had never possessed a true form, was a manifestation of countless sentiments from all eras and corners, a rather unconventional “manifestation of the Dao.” 

Yet, even if unconventional, it was still a remarkable manifestation of the Dao, and merely touching upon the concept of the Dao was no small matter.

If discovered in other blessed lands, she would certainly be captured, with no shortage of buyers willing to pay exorbitant prices.

Fortunately, she was born in the Lotus Root blessed land, under the governance of such a principled young mountain lord, ensuring her future luck would be quite favorable.

Zheng Dafu wiped his mouth. “A remarkable talent and spirit of the land, worth a visit! A timid yet delicate young lady and a gallant hero—both are indispensable, lest we fall victim to the clutches of those lonely spirits and malevolent ghosts.”

Zhu Lian, however, stated, “I think keeping her on the mountain would be just fine.”

Deep down, Zhu Lian harbored a significant concern; the Lotus Flower blessed land of yesteryears, now the Lotus Root blessed land, left him with a lingering sense that the old temple master’s schemes were far-reaching.

Once someone entered a blessed land, regardless of who they were, it wouldn’t be an easy journey.

Wei Ban added, “If we’ve chosen a leisurely life, we might as well enjoy it to the fullest until we grow old.”

Zheng Dafu laughed, “What are you thinking? Our Lupo Mountain is brimming with talented individuals. It’s not that I need to exert myself; it’s truly just for a stroll and to clear our minds.”

In truth, Zheng Dafu was stronger in chess than both Zhu Lian and Wei Ban, so playing was quite easy for him. As Zhu Lian pondered deeply over his next move, Zheng Dafu lifted a folding fan from the table, fanning himself in the winter chill. It seemed absurd. He only needed to pretend; after a quick flick of the wrist, he tucked it away. Such a refined item in the hands of a handsome man like him was simply extraordinary; any woman with eyes wouldn’t dislike it. If someone claimed to dislike it, they were likely pretending.

At that moment on Lupo Mountain, aside from Pei Qian still wandering outside, the old scholar had taken Cao Qinglang to the Southern Posa Continent for a trip. The atmosphere was quite lively, as Yuan Lai had recently chosen to remain on the mountain for cultivation. Zheng Dafu genuinely wished to guide the young girl Yuan Bao in her boxing techniques, but unfortunately, she was too shy and timid, preferring to learn from an old man. Young Yuan Lai wanted to learn from Zheng Dafu, but Zheng Dafu was hesitant, only sharing some miscellaneous knowledge from books. Yuan Lai had been advised by her sister many times on this.

Moreover, there were now three unnamed disciples residing at the Sword Offering Platform of Lupo Mountain.

These three were genuine outsiders from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Jindan sword cultivator Cui Wei.

And two shop assistants from a certain store, Zhang Jiazhen and Jiang Qu.

The three hadn’t arrived via the ferry from the old dragon city to North Julu Continent, but had instead taken a short ferry northward, then traversed what was said to be an underground river carved by a true dragon, carrying three travel documents and a peace talisman from the Great Li dynasty. They traveled northward, passing through Hongzhu Town and Qidun Mountain, finally entering the territory of Lupo Mountain.

Ultimately, under Zhu Lian’s arrangement, they settled at the Sword Offering Platform in silence.

Since the three were only considered registered disciples of Lupo Mountain for the time being, they didn’t need to offer incense or hang their portraits.

With the lavish spending of the veneration Zhou Fei, all the subordinate mountain residences of Lupo Mountain were undergoing grand construction. As Zhou Fei put it, “Whatever is expensive, bring it! Don’t save money for me. Where does the mountain’s celestial energy come from? It’s all built up from the heaviest copper stench of divine coins, one by one!”

Cui Wei especially concealed his identity; given his recent journey, he had a rough understanding of the value of a Jindan cultivator in the vast world. An ordinary Jindan Qi cultivator could hold a peak ceremony, which would be immensely valued by the celestial sects of the vast realm, let alone a sword cultivator destined to become Yuan Ying.

However, Cui Wei was even more reserved than Zhang Jiazhen and Jiang Qu, almost timid.

Cui Wei left the Sword Qi Great Wall with little more than his own life-protecting flying sword, a robe from a clothing store, and a long sword from the sword workshop.

Zhang Jiazhen had received a handwritten calligraphy piece from Mr. Chen, titled “Rain for the Day, Sun for the Night,” stamped with two seals.

Jiang Qu received a stack of talismans gifted by Mr. Chen, among which was a golden talisman.

Zheng Dafu asked, “Old cook, are we just leaving those two young ones at the Sword Offering Platform? I think that’s not right. We should send them to the New Year shop to pick up some energy from the crowd.”

Wei Ban laughed and replied, “You can’t say that, Zhang Jiazhen and Jiang Qu are both from urban backgrounds; they’re not lacking in this regard.”

Zheng Dafu chuckled, “I just thought that Zhang Jiazhen looks quite decent and wanted to match him up with Xiao Jiu’er. We’ve been freezing in bed every night—how comfortable is that? Do we really want these younger ones to follow in our footsteps? I don’t think so; absolutely not.”

The New Year shop housed three registered disciples: the blind old Daoist Jia Cheng, the limping young man Zhao Denggao, and the young girl Tian Jiu’er.

Zhu Lian smiled, “Those two outsiders at the Sword Offering Platform should have a bright future, though they may take longer to mature. We need to be patient.”

Wei Ban added, “Even if they want to be unambitious, they need to consider Zhou Fei’s divine coins. Will the gods agree?”

Zhu Lian and Zheng Dafu nodded in unison, “That makes sense.”

Zheng Dafu said, “Let’s have Nuanshu write this down. Next time we gather at the Ancestor Hall, we’ll pull it out and show it to Brother Zhou Fei.”

After finishing her tasks, Chen Nuanshu came over to watch the chess game.

Chen Lingjun yawned as he entered the courtyard, spotting Chen Nuanshu, and grinned, “Little silly girl, haven’t you refined that Dragon King’s lantern yet?”

Years ago, before Chen Pingan left Lupo Mountain, he had given the pair of Dragon King lanterns from the ruins of the North Julu Continent to both Chen Nuanshu and Chen Lingjun for them to refine, as a means to safeguard the Huang Lake Mountain of Lupo Mountain. Chen Lingjun had already successfully refined his, but Chen Nuanshu was progressing slowly. However, this slowness was only relative to Chen Lingjun. A fellow who almost got taken by Lu Chen to cultivate in the Qingming realm wouldn’t have poor aptitude.

Chen Nuanshu’s expression dimmed as she fell silent, her small hands gripping her sleeves tightly.

Wei Ban reached out and gently patted Chen Lingjun’s head, bending down with a smile to ask, “What’s wrong?”

Chen Lingjun blinked and replied earnestly, “Nuanshu, in cultivation, diligence is enough. Don’t rush; being hasty can lead to mistakes. We should learn from our lord, taking things slow so that our punches come out fast.”

Wei Ban patted Chen Lingjun’s head again, “If you keep talking without a filter like this, once Pei Qian returns to Lupo Mountain, you’ll have to deal with it yourself.”

Chen Lingjun nearly kneeled before Wei Ban, quickly standing on his toes, placing his hands on Wei Ban’s shoulders, smiling ingratiatingly, urging the seated Wei Ban to sit down so he could help massage the Mountain Lord’s shoulders.

The North Julu Continent’s Taihui Sword Sect was a top-tier sect! The sword immortal Qi Jinglong’s direct disciple Bai Shou—how impressive!

Yet, with one kick from Pei Qian, he was left lying on the ground, twitching.

The most terrifying thing was that Pei Qian held grudges.

Cen Yuanshi, Yuan Bao, and Yuan Lai, during their training breaks, also came to the courtyard to unwind. 

As soon as they arrived, they noticed Chen Lingjun, helping Wei Ban massage his shoulders while praising Brother Dafu’s elegant demeanor. If that fan were to gain sentience, it would surely be grateful to shed tears, thanking its previous life for accumulating virtues, allowing it to end up in Brother Dafu’s hands in this life.

Chen Nuanshu made room, but Cen Yuanshi and young Yuan Lai didn’t sit down. Yuan Bao expressed his gratitude and took a seat.

Chen Lingjun rolled his eyes.

This little girl picked up by Lu Baixiang had no sense whatsoever.

Look at all the exceptional talents my lord brought in; how could anyone not be outstanding?

Just think about that little girl, right now still squatting by Qidun Mountain, eagerly waiting for Pei Qian, clutching a large bag of seeds. The little girl's conscience was bigger than a bowl.

Yuan Bao was merely lucky; he arrived at Lupo Mountain late, and all the extraordinary individuals had been dealt with by the venerable Chen himself, who had fought for the path of vitality. Otherwise, with Yuan Bao’s temperament, he would have been smacked down long ago during his walks.

Zhu Lian smiled and asked, “Yuan Bao, do you have something to say?”

Yuan Bao nodded, “I can wait until Mr. Zhu finishes his chess game.”

Although the girl was sharp-tongued, she was still polite.

Moreover, Yuan Bao had a good impression of the elder Zhu Lian. The one he disliked was Zheng Dafu, and the one he felt indifferent about was the Mountain Lord who frequently visited Lupo Mountain for no reason.

Previously, when Mr. Zhu had traveled to the Lotus Root blessed land, he had only brought back a scroll hidden in a secret place, an exquisite work from a master painter from his hometown.

Prosperous, bustling, a scene of great vitality.

At that time, Pei Qian had sharp eyes and noticed that there were fewer horses and more yellow cattle and donkeys in the painting, leading him to exclaim, “So many little donkeys, if I grit my teeth and take out a snowflake coin, could I buy a hundred of them?”

Yuan Bao and Yuan Lai were also present, with Yuan Lai searching for the bookstore in the painting, while Yuan Bao glanced at the painting and sneered, declaring it a display of decline.

Zhu Lian nodded; this perspective made sense.

In fact, the painting depicted the very capital where Zhu Lian resided. Within less than sixty years, all the beauty and prosperity had been trampled into dust by horse hooves.

Even though Zhu Lian had exerted every effort, he still couldn’t turn the tide. Eventually, he left the political arena and returned to the rivers and lakes, transforming from a noble heir into a cultured general, ultimately becoming a martial madman.

In that lifetime, Zhu Lian had three proud moments.

Writing books. Zhu Lian’s small script was something even Cui Dongshan admired greatly.

He pioneered double-entry bookkeeping.

He casually wrote a martial arts manual with a low threshold for entry, allowing for quick breakthroughs, yet reaching the pinnacle was incredibly difficult. He wrote ninety-nine volumes, giving them away freely, sparking a scramble among those in the martial world.

Scholars, common folk, the rivers and lakes.

Looking back on his life, whether as the noble Zhu Lian or the martial madman Zhu Lian, he had found closure.

Zhu Lian placed the white piece he was about to drop back into the box and smiled, “Yuan Bao, the chess game is currently too close to call. Let’s finish this game first; you can speak your mind.”

Zheng Dafu continued to crack sunflower seeds.

Wei Ban remained quiet. In a chess match, as long as Zhu Lian didn’t deliberately take a long time to think, Zheng Dafu would wrap up the game within a few moves.

Yuan Bao began, “I have some thoughts regarding the Lotus Root blessed land. I’ll speak freely; if I’m wrong, please forgive me, Mr. Zhu.”

Zhu Lian chuckled, “Feel free to speak. Whether right or wrong isn’t solely up to me; we can discuss it, argue, and reason with each other.”

Yuan Bao appreciated the elder’s open-mindedness and straightforwardness, allowing him to interact without restraint.

In a serious tone, Yuan Bao said, “We should directly publish some simple celestial techniques into books and have the emperors of the four nations issue edicts mandating that everyone must study them. We could promote martial arts manuals in the same way; with no entry barriers, even those with poor aptitude who can’t cultivate celestial techniques can still walk the path of martial arts. Whether they succeed or not, they will at least have had the opportunity. Otherwise, after we’ve invested so many Gu Yu coins, are we just here for the spectacle? We must at least see some profit, right?”

Yuan Lai whispered, “If we’re causing chaos with martial arts, it will be troublesome for the imperial government. The entire Lotus Root blessed land will become hard to control. If we’re not careful, the government will become merely decorative. If the government and the imperial court lose their authority, it will create significant issues for the entire landscape system. Cao Qinglang once said, ‘No matter how small a realm is, it requires stability.’”

Yuan Bao scoffed, “If those old emperors and officials won’t do their jobs or can’t do them well, then simply replace them with a batch of obedient puppets. Those who dare to kill can keep the mountain cultivators in check and deal with the masters of the rivers and lakes. If we really fear that place is small, we can always take the good seedlings directly from the blessed land and raise them at Lupo Mountain. With so many peaks and celestial residences, they’ll just sit empty. For instance, those who have hopes of advancing to the cave realm and are already at the sixth stage of martial arts can become our unnamed disciples at Lupo Mountain. Once they’ve accumulated enough merit, they can earn positions and learn better boxing techniques and higher celestial techniques.”

Yuan Lai’s voice grew even softer, “But what about human feelings? It’s not that simple. Sister, just on our master’s side, there are so many complicated relationships.”

Yuan Bao glared at his bookish younger brother, feeling utterly exasperated! No wonder he got along so well with Cao Qinglang.

Zhu Lian remained silent.

The girl’s words couldn’t be said to be entirely right or entirely wrong. However, some things are intricately connected, not merely a matter of adding or subtracting techniques, but more like constructing a building; if one beam is askew, over time, the whole structure may collapse.

Nonetheless, it’s beneficial to think and speak more, so Zhu Lian did not rush to refute or endorse anything and simply smiled at the girl, encouraging her to be bold and share her thoughts.

Yuan Bao crossed his arms and squinted, “The reason our master is constrained is due to the chaotic situation. The Lotus Root blessed land is different; here, we at Lupo Mountain are the gods of this blessed land! As a person, who wouldn’t fear death and cherish their life! Our vast world possesses profound techniques and magical powers. In this grand scheme, who cares about human emotions? Perhaps those seeking to affiliate with us at Lupo Mountain will be the last thing on their minds.”

Zheng Dafu chuckled, “In childhood, I feared the difficulty of studying; in youth, I thought it was easy to be human.”

Young Yuan Lai silently took this to heart. Uncle Zheng's knowledge was indeed vast.

Zhu Lian scratched his head and sighed, “Yesterday’s child rode a bamboo horse, and tonight, how is it that he has become a white-haired elder?”

Wei Ban asked with a smile, “Yuan Bao, I have a question. Once these people arrive in the vast world and are nurtured at Lupo Mountain, what will they do?”

Yuan Bao had long prepared an answer and said without hesitation, “They will continue cultivating or encourage them to practice martial arts. As long as the Qi cultivators become Dragon Gate realm cultivators or seventh-stage martial arts masters, they can be sold to various powers in the Baopin Continent, establishing good connections and earning substantial wealth. Those with high aspirations who refuse to be treated as goods can sign contracts with us at Lupo Mountain. After they leave, they can agree on a period of ten, twenty, or even a hundred years, allowing them to buy their freedom with money!”

Wei Ban inquired further, “If among these people, someone commits evil or causes chaos, who takes responsibility for this muddled account?”

Yuan Bao frowned, “What does that matter? In the rivers and lakes, life and death are their own responsibility. If they suffer misfortune, it’s their own fault. Those who lack the ability will be trampled by others. The world has always been this way! Why should we take the blame at Lupo Mountain?”

Zhu Lian remained unperturbed.

Zheng Dafu rolled his eyes.

Wei Ban twirled the golden earring between his fingers, feeling somewhat troubled.

Lu Baixiang’s teaching of disciples was truly worry-free.

Yuan Bao clenched his fists, speaking solemnly, “In the Lotus Root blessed land, we are the gods, overseeing them. Those who follow will thrive, while those who oppose will perish! Once they leave Lupo Mountain, they will have no more connection with us, only business dealings. This world was built by our thousands of Gu Yu coins, creating a thriving environment! We must continue to invest, pouring in even more Gu Yu coins—on what grounds?”

Yuan Bao was somewhat agitated, “The formation of those heavenly treasures is far too slow, and the gathering of spiritual energy into a cultivation treasure land will take ages! Are we to suffer losses indefinitely? My master’s earning is not easy; it’s challenging! Unlike some people, who sit atop the mountain, basking in the sun, playing chess, and enjoying the snow.”

Zhu Lian smiled and waved his hand, “Yuan Bao, at Lupo Mountain, not to mention our current discussion, even in future arguments, we must keep in mind ‘discuss matters as they are.’ Otherwise, being right will mean nothing.”

Yuan Bao nodded, “I’ll heed Mr. Zhu’s words.”

Zheng Dafu, cracking sunflower seeds, found himself feeling a bit guilty after the girl’s words.

Yuan Bao took a deep breath, his gaze resolute, glancing at Zheng Dafu and Wei Ban, “If either of you finds them displeasing, I’ll take responsibility for dealing with them, as though raising a useless waste of space.”

Cen Yuanshi hoped her good sister would say less, so she had been signaling for quite a while, but her eyelids were growing heavier by the second.

At this moment, Cen Yuanshi started to rub her eyes.

Yuan Bao gently squeezed Cen Yuanshi’s arm, signaling that he understood her feelings.

Among all of Lupo Mountain, only Cen Yuanshi was the most pleasing to him; she was a friend. The rest were either useless or deceitful, or they simply acted frivolously and lacked a sense of purpose. Well, Nuanshu was an exception; she was diligent and peaceful, which made her quite endearing.

Zhu Lian said, “Yuan Bao, I have a rough understanding of your thoughts, and I’ve made a note of them. Don’t worry; I won’t let this just sit idly. Perhaps at the next Ancestor Hall meeting, your ideas will be discussed individually. The Ancestor Hall’s discussions are not a joke; every word is recorded, so it’s best for you to consider them carefully in the near future to avoid any loopholes being pointed out later. I have a suggestion; do you want to hear it?”

Yuan Bao smiled, “Please, Mr. Zhu!”

Zhu Lian glanced at the timid young Yuan Lai and said, “Since Yuan Lai has some objections, you should set aside your sister’s airs and try to be more calm. If you can convince Yuan Lai, do you think you’ll truly have the confidence to bring this matter to the Ancestor Hall? Is that reasonable?”

Yuan Bao thought for a moment and nodded, “Alright!”

Zhu Lian continued, “Outside of the Ancestor Hall, all paths of cultivation may proceed as they wish, but once seated in the Ancestor Hall, everyone’s words must be carefully considered. This isn’t me acting like an elder or targeting you, Yuan Bao, or thinking the girl’s brilliance is too bright and needs dimming. We at Lupo Mountain have no such chaotic rules now, nor will we in the future.”

Yuan Bao smiled, “Mr. Zhu has always been open-minded; I won’t overthink it.”

Zheng Dafu sighed deeply.

Whatever the old cook says, the girl seems to take it all in stride.

So many celestial texts, all of which the old cook has bought and hidden in the mountains—why is it only I who am a carefree wastrel?

People are more alive than the living.

Yuan Bao, along with his friends Cen Yuanshi and the dense younger brother, left the courtyard in high spirits.

Chen Lingjun muttered, “That little girl is so domineering.”

Zhu Lian smiled, “Lupo Mountain should have such thoughts. The more we prepare for battles and competitions, the better. So I’ll make it clear with you all beforehand: no matter the final outcome of the Ancestor Hall discussions, we must not hurt the girl’s feelings.”

Wei Ban shook his head, “This move may not be without merit; in fact, many blessed lands in the vast world operate on this principle. Following this approach, it may even be more direct than Yuan Bao’s proposal. On one hand, it’s somewhat mercantile and carries a poor reputation, making it incredibly difficult to become a candidate for the sect, let alone ascend to a proper sect. On the other hand, as Yuan Lai worries, Yuan Bao still underestimates human sentiment. The more seeds of the Dao or martial talents one has, not to say all, but most will rebel and turn against Lupo Mountain. Ultimately, it’s easy to overreach and fish in a dry pond.”

Zheng Dafu remarked, “The little girl is still at an early stage of martial arts. For her to have such vision is quite impressive.”

Wei Ban suddenly grew somber.

Zheng Dafu asked, “Did something happen to the little girl?”

Earlier, Wei Ban had merely sensed a subtle feeling, but now he activated his divine sense to observe the mountains and rivers.

He hadn’t anticipated that Chen Lingjun had already taken to the winds, soaring from Lupo Mountain like a green rainbow.

Wei Ban chuckled, “Pei Qian is already protecting that little girl.”

Zhu Lian’s expression remained indifferent. “Wei Ban, you don’t need to meddle; let Lupo Mountain handle it.”

Wei Ban didn’t take it to heart, nodding, “I’ll intervene; otherwise, it would be harder to manage. Just as I need to go to the capital for discussions, I’ll leave first. You all continue as you wish.”

Zhu Lian suddenly became fidgety, “That would be too rude, quite embarrassing.”

Wei Ban asked with a smile, “Then should I leave later?”

Zhu Lian had already risen, “Mountain Lord matters are pressing. The sooner you leave, the sooner you return. It’s best to bring back some windfall.”

Wei Ban’s figure shimmered and vanished in an instant, appearing thousands of miles away.

Zheng Dafu gestured for Nuanshu not to be nervous, nor to follow Chen Lingjun to the confluence of the three rivers at Hongzhu Town.

Zheng Dafu continued to crack sunflower seeds.

Could Lupo Mountain allow people to bully them on their own territory? What a joke.

Then Zheng Dafu rubbed his chin, grateful that the young mountain lord wasn’t on the mountain. Otherwise, based on Chen Pingan’s temperament now, he would likely throw a punch first and find a quiet place to break a river, and then reason things out.

The Emperor’s study in the Great Li dynasty wasn’t particularly large.

However, to enter and sit down for a discussion, one had to have a sufficiently large official hat or a high enough cultivation level.

The young Emperor Song He was meditating with his eyes closed. Today, he had made an exception and canceled the morning court session in preparation for the upcoming discussions.

Furthermore, the situation was special, with mostly cultivators present and only a few officials from the Great Li dynasty—just the Minister of Rites and two deputies.

Song He opened his eyes, realizing he still had about a stick of incense’s worth of time. The young Emperor glanced at the desk, where there lay a landscape painting by Li Yingqiu, which had been placed there by the former emperor. After inheriting the throne, Song He had not removed anything from the room but had added a few items, only to feel it was becoming cluttered and secretly removed some.

The container for Li Yingqiu’s landscape painting was a green porcelain pen holder made from the Longyao kiln in Lihuzhou, which was rather obtrusive.

Li Yingqiu wasn’t a mountain dweller; the arts from the lower realms had never caught the attention of the celestial families, but there were exceptions. Li Yingqiu was an unavoidable figure in the history of painting of the Great Sui dynasty, not only favored by the Great Li Song family but also appreciated by many celestial families on Baopin Continent.

Besides Li Yingqiu’s meticulous green landscape, there were also wild flower-and-bird paintings.

Song He glanced at the scrolls in the pen holder, wanting to apologize to Li Yingqiu, feeling sorry for the elder’s landscape painting being placed next to this person’s flower-and-bird painting.

Song He had a very poor impression of Bian Ye, both in terms of his paintings and character, finding him unworthy of regard. He was a down-and-out painter from the previous Lu dynasty, who had wandered to the vassal state of Great Li, becoming one of the few outsiders to settle here. Thus, he was highly valued by that generation’s Great Li Emperor. All his paintings bore the seals of the consecutive Great Li emperors. Bian Ye probably never expected that within a century of his death, he would inexplicably become a revered figure in the painting world of Baopin Continent, hailed as “most adept at the beauty of wildflowers and birds, with exquisite colors so lifelike,” and “exceptionally skillful, a standard of ancient and modern.” Countless praises surged forth.

When Song He was younger, he attended lessons here with some princes. Some shared his views, saying Bian Ye’s paintings were indeed overly extravagant; the former emperor didn’t provide any evaluations of the paintings, simply stating that no matter who became the owner of this room, they must keep Bian Ye’s works, regardless of preference.

However, among the pen holder was a calligraphy piece that was an actual treasure, titled “Returning Home Is Better Than Never Returning.”

It could even be regarded as the first treasure of this Great Li study.

It was a piece written by Song He’s teacher, the national master of the Great Li dynasty, Cui Zhan. Of course, it was a genuine work.

Cui Zhan’s calligraphy, especially in running and cursive scripts, was renowned and considered worth its weight in gold across the vast world.

Once the first disciple of the Confucian Sage lineage, Embroidered Tiger Cui Zhan, deserved that title, just as Chen Chun’an of Posa Continent deserved his title of “refined Confucian.”

Cui Zhan had four pieces from the flower collection, four from the cloud collection, four from the spring collection, and four from the mountain collection, totaling sixteen pieces of calligraphy that have survived. 

These sixteen scrolls scattered across the nine continents, all falling into the hands of renowned collectors, including one notable mountain cultivator from the central continent who deeply connected with Cui Zhan, expending massive resources to purchase two pieces, the “Beggar Seeking Rice” and the “Seat Contention,” publicly destroying them, which was considered a great feat, pleasing the masses.

Only a century later did the truth come to light: this self-proclaimed “the best in the world at despising Cui Zhan” old cultivator was revealed by his descendants, exposing that this old scoundrel merely destroyed two counterfeits while secretly hoarding the genuine pieces for his family.

Additionally, it was said that the Liu family from Aiyai Continent, the Bai Emperor City, the Yushi family from the central continent, and Jiang Shangzhen from Yuguizong all had one in their collections.

Cui Zhan stepped in and bowed, “Your Majesty, we may begin our discussion.”

This was a rite of courtesy between sovereign and subject.

The young emperor immediately rose and returned the gesture, a courtesy between teacher and student.

In truth, this was unnecessary; Song He had never deviated from this, even in front of the senior ministers of the small court assembly.

Not long after Cui Zhan took his seat, the three of them from the Ministry of Rites stood to pay their respects and then took their seats.

Then came the various mountain dwellers from the Baopin Continent.

The head of the Shengaosong sect, a Daoist immortal, the Great Heavenly Lord Qi Zhen.

The chief veneration of Great Li, the sect master of Longquan Sword Sect, Ruan Qiong.

The founder of the Wind and Snow Temple, an immortal looking like a youth; the last time he appeared in the realm was during the three competitions at Fenglei Garden and Zhengyang Mountain.

From Zhenwu Mountain, a man who had just been promoted to the head of the Ancestor Hall, with a sword on his back.

In the eyes of outsiders, Zhenwu Mountain only needed a Ma Kuxuan to ensure a bright future.

In fact, Wind and Snow Temple was not lacking either, having a deity named Wei Jin, with the only shortcoming being that Wei Jin had little concern for Wind and Snow Temple due to his master’s influence, keeping a distance from it. Now he had gone to the Sword Qi Great Wall. Otherwise, today could have seen the presence of Sword Immortal Wei Jin.

The chief veneration of Zhenjing Sect, Liu Lao Cheng, who was of the wild cultivator lineage from Shujian Lake.

A great gentleman from Guanh Lake Academy.

The mountain master of Piyun Mountain’s Deer Academy.

The lord of Old Dragon City, Fu Qi.

The founder of the Great Sui dynasty, the ancestor of the Ge Yang Gao family.

Only four of the new Five Peaks mountain lords arrived today, including North Peak Wei Ban and Central Peak Jin Qing.

Only South Peak Fan Junmao was absent.

The master of the Mohist School.

A wandering Mohist ranger, Xu Ruo, behind the sword.

An elder from the Jiang family of Yunlin.

Two water deities from the central region of Baopin Continent.

It was rumored that they were gathering the waters from six rivers and twelve streams, ultimately merging them to flow into the sea as a great deluge!

It seems this shocking rumor was no mere empty talk.

The clan head of the Xu family from Qingfeng City, after acquiring a piece of leprosy armor, became significantly more powerful, with enormous killing power.

A young woman from Zhengyang Mountain, said to be a recently appointed elder in charge of financial dealings, was relatively unknown compared to the older sword cultivators from Zhengyang Mountain.

Today, she found herself in the last seat.

In comparison to the leaders of several older powers from Great Li, she was seated even further back.

Logically, Zhengyang Mountain and Qingfeng City’s Xu family were deeply allied, but the Xu family head had been waiting elsewhere for a summons. Upon seeing the Zhengyang woman next to him, he merely nodded in acknowledgment, too lazy to engage in any pleasantries.

In contrast, she took the initiative to bow and then took her seat.

A total of thirty-six cultivators and deities gathered, most engaged in mutual conversation. For example, the Jiang family and the Fu family of Old Dragon City were in-laws, while the Xu family of Qingfeng City were in-laws with the Yuan family. The Minister of Rites’ right deputy was also somewhat related, and the Minister of Rites sat beside Ruan Qiong, engaging in friendly dialogue. Wei Ban and Jin Qing, the two mountain lords, were exchanging barbs. The other two new mountain lords seemed to be on good terms as they discussed important matters. Qi Zhen and the Mohist giant were in deep conversation. Even the ancestor of the Ge Yang Gao family had been hiding away in Piyun Mountain for years, and with the great gentleman from Guanh Lake Academy, they could chat about academic matters.

Sadly, this Zhengyang woman found herself without anyone she could converse with.

Cui Zhan stood up and spoke straightforwardly, “Today, I have summoned everyone here to discuss ten matters.”

Within the room and outside, it felt like two separate worlds.

Everyone held their breath, focused, without any signs of laxity.

Aside from the discussions today being related to everyone present, the Great Li National Master’s enigmatic realm was also critical.

As for the three key figures from the Ministry of Rites, they appeared as students listening to their teacher’s teachings.

Cui Zhan continued, “The first matter is that the court will soon issue the next mountain lord to assist the heirs of the Five Peaks.”

The four mountain lords listened attentively; this was a fundamental issue of the Dao.

In fact, this matter was not only about the affairs of the Five Peaks but also about the personal interests of everyone present.

The Minister of Rites stood up, opened a book, and began to call names.

After he finished the last word, he looked at Cui Zhan, who had been standing, and once Cui Zhan nodded, the old Minister of Rites sat down.

Cui Zhan said, “The second matter is to select several candidate sects that are widely supported.”

The head of the Xu family from Qingfeng City straightened his back and sat upright.

The Zhengyang woman hurriedly composed herself.

Women often find it especially difficult to meet the gaze of Ruan Qiong, the sect master of Longquan Sword Sect.

Even when waiting for the emperor’s summons, she hadn’t glanced at Ruan Qiong.

The reason was simple: Zhengyang Mountain wished to become a sect, which required them to absorb the sword Dao’s fortunes of the entire Zhu Ying Dynasty, needing to establish an immortal sect residence there to recruit and gather all the sword Dao talents.

In the end, the four candidate mountain sects, including the Xu family of Qingfeng City and Zhengyang Mountain, had hopes of entering the sect ranks; in the future, the Great Li court would naturally tilt its financial resources toward them.

The third matter is to discuss the excavation of the great flood leading into the sea and to nominate the various celestial masters responsible for assisting this task.

The two water deities of the great river, currently of equal rank with the Tiefu River’s Yang Hua, couldn’t hide their excitement. 

Although today’s discussions wouldn’t decide who would take the position of the great flood water deity, being invited to participate in today’s discussions was already a significant honor.

In addition, the Great Li court had designated three individuals: the scholar Liu Qingfeng, the martial general Guan Yiran, and Liu Xunmei.

Other assisted candidates were all mountain cultivators from the nearby peaks of the future great flood, each offering their suggestions.

Moreover, the elder from the Jiang family felt this trip wasn’t in vain, as the mouth of the great flood was extremely close to the Jiang family’s territory. Thus, he also proposed a Jiang family disciple, Jiang Yun, to participate.

Liu Lao Cheng, the veneration from Zhenjing Sect, smiled knowingly.

The fourth matter is to filter through the shrines and temples of various mountains and waters, upgrading them to orthodox temples, with the court issuing corresponding decrees. The cultivators of various mountains will assist in adding incense. If any are deemed lewd shrines, they will be immediately prohibited and destroyed, with the various mountain heads responsible for suppressing them.

The two deputies from the Ministry of Rites read through their respective content.

The fifth matter is to relocate the Great Li capital, which is modeled after the White Jade Capital, to the former Zhu Ying Dynasty’s Central Peak territory.

The Mohist giant stood up and briefly mentioned some points of caution.

Those below the thirteenth realm can all be killed. The one responsible for guarding the White Jade Capital is a long-time acquaintance of the Central Peak’s mountain lord, Jin Qing, the Mohist ranger Xu Ruo.

The sixth matter is to discuss the tax that all celestial forces in Baopin Continent must pay to the Great Li court.

Immediately, the study fell silent.

Cui Zhan spoke, “This matter is complex, and wanting to cover all bases cannot be settled in a day or two. Today, I only need to know whether you agree or disagree. If you agree, someone will work out the details later. If you disagree, we’ll set it aside for now. The Great Li court will not deliberately target anyone in the near future. Regardless of whether you agree or disagree, you will receive a book upon leaving, detailing everything. There will be slight differences for the various mountains, but they won’t be significant. You all need not rush to express your opinions today; this is merely to inform you, with a maximum buffer period of one year.”

The seventh matter is regarding the Great Li dynasty borrowing people and money from the various mountain heads, as well as how to repay this debt. Furthermore, each mountain head needs to send cultivators down the mountain to gain experience, “appeasing” the remnants of the fallen dynasties and the old royal families, inviting them to temporarily stay in the Great Li capital. If they enjoy the local customs, they are welcome to dwell for a long time.

The eighth matter is to discuss the revival of Buddhist teachings in Baopin Continent and the construction of temples. A certain eminent monk will serve as the main official.

Hearing this, the Great Heavenly Lord Qi Zhen frowned.

The ninth matter is that the Great Sui Mountain Cliff Academy must return to the ranks of the Confucian seventy-two academies, and if possible, Lin Deer Academy should also strive to compete.

The ancestor of the Ge Yang Gao family felt immensely satisfied.

One by one, the matters and agendas were rapidly advanced under Cui Zhan’s leadership.

The young emperor, Song He, merely sat behind the desk, showing no signs of anger at the national master’s encroachment. Instead, he appeared invigorated.

Cui Zhan stated, “The previous nine matters were all in preparation for the final tenth matter, which is crucial for everyone present, including His Majesty the Emperor.”

With a sweep of his sleeve, a map of the entire continent’s mountains and rivers unfolded before everyone’s eyes.

All the critical peaks and sects appeared like lights igniting on the canvas.

Cui Zhan continued, “We need to discuss how to arrange defensive lines for Baopin Continent in light of the Sword Qi Great Wall being breached, leading to the collapse of the entire Tongye Continent against the advancing demonic army.”

The five sacred peaks of the continent commanded the mountain ranges, while the central great flood gathered the continent’s waterways.

The Guanh Lake Academy, Mountain Cliff Academy, and Lin Deer Academy were the centers of literature and culture in the continent.

The Shengaosong sect, Longquan Sword Sect, Wind and Snow Temple, Zhenwu Mountain, Old Dragon City, Yunlin Jiang family, Shujian Lake Zhenjing sect, Zhengyang Mountain, and the Xu family of Qingfeng City were all key defensive strongholds.

Moreover, the various vassal forces and scattered mountain ranges across the land were all rooted and immovable pieces on the board.

Cui Zhan asserted, “Simply having a series of coastal defenses, like Old Dragon City and the Yunlin Jiang family, will be far from sufficient. We also need sufficient strategic depth and mutual support between the mountains.”

“Using points to form lines, then to form areas, is still not enough; it’s too rigid.”

“We also require a vast number of offensive sword ships and more mountain ferries, with countless divine coins poured in.”

“Additionally, many of the strategies and plans are not related to you. There’s no need to elaborate; you will all learn about them in due course.”

In the Great Li emperor’s study, silence reigned.

Cui Zhan pointed to the southern and western ends of the Baopin Continent map, one being Tongye Continent and the other the central divine continent.

Cui Zhan’s expression turned cold, “In a vast world, it is laughable that the smallest Baopin Continent must step in to help delay the demonic army. I wish to see the seven continents of the vast world die laughing.”

Finally, Cui Zhan spoke solemnly, “If the great Tongye Continent cannot withstand the demonic army, leading to its imminent downfall, then let our little Baopin Continent take it upon itself to make this happen. Everyone, the tides of fortune are shifting; those wishing to resist the heavens, please rise.”

The young emperor was the first to stand.

Everyone present rose to their feet.

At this moment, a figure entered the study, looking somewhat out of place as a cultivator, smiling, “I’m surnamed Fan, though I’m not from the Fan family of Old Dragon City. I hail from the central divine continent, with a little wealth to spare, and I am willing to use divine coins as a pillar to offer my humble assistance to Baopin Continent.”

Outside the study, a strange-looking old eunuch in a bright red robe stood in the corridor, casting a sidelong glance at the white-clad youth squatting against the wall.

The white-clad youth yelled, “I’ve been hustling and bustling all this way, working myself to the bone. After standing here for half a day, I can’t even take a break? Am I here to urinate or defecate? Who are you to care if I squat or stand? You wanna try me? I’ll give you a taste of the Monkey Picking Peaches, fishing for the moon in the sea, trust me, do you fear it?”

Heaven and earth were separated, and no one outside knew of the words exchanged. Inside, Cui Zhan still lightly admonished, “Cui Dongshan!”

The white-clad youth with a mole on his forehead swayed his sleeves, not striding into the emperor’s study but merely walking in, leaving behind a sentence: “I have good news—the Sword Qi Great Wall can hold out an extra two to three years than expected.”

Cui Dongshan ascended the imitation White Jade Capital, climbing to the rooftop.

On the rooftop, Cui Dongshan gazed at the sky through the windows, feeling nostalgic for the times he spent locked away in the attic, reading books as a child.

Never would he have thought that now, still a youthful lad, he was also a white-haired elder.

To hell with the carefree youth who knows not the taste of sorrow, and to hell with the old crane’s call, all clangor and no substance.

A sprout that does not bloom is a cause for mourning since ancient times.

One continent like this, and several continents like this; the mountain dwellers and the world at large were all like this.

Cui Dongshan slapped his face. “At this time and place, I should cry.”

Rubbing his cheeks, he opened his mouth wide and howled, “I can be fierce!”

Leaving the Great Li capital, along the official road, passersby cast curious glances.

A thin, pitiful child was carrying a white-clad youth on his back, stuttering along the way, while the youth was grinning ear to ear.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 754: Zhu Lian Has Questions to Ask (Part 1)

Pei Qian arrived at Red Candle Town and was somewhat puzzled. How dare that little rice grain not show up? Instead, she was up in the mountains, snacking away like she had no conscience at all! Upon reaching Lupo Mountain, Pei Qian was determined to take Zhou Mi Li to the Patriarch Hall for a punishment stand. After that, they would clean the courtyard together.

However, it didn’t take long for Pei Qian to sense that something was amiss. In the distance, there was a commotion in the streets, with people discussing something animatedly. With her keen ears, she rushed over. Upon hearing the gossip, she tightened her grip on her walking stick.

Still stubbornly holding back, she didn’t rush off immediately, instead listening for a while longer. Finally, she sprang lightly onto the rooftops, looking around. Following the general direction indicated by passersby, she darted across the rooftops, fleeting as a dragonfly skimming the water.

On the outskirts of Red Candle Town, there was a crescent-shaped bay where delicate pleasure boats drifted, exuding an overwhelming scent of perfume. It was home to several unfortunate boat girls.

Pei Qian had stepped onto a pleasure boat about four or five times. Each time, the boat would dip slightly before suddenly rising again, but it didn’t rock too much.

As she crossed the bay, she pressed onward, spotting a little girl in black who had left the water’s edge and was heading up the mountain alone.

At this point, she didn’t care about whether she might attract the attention of any cultivators or mountain spirits. She needed to see the little rice grain first to feel at ease.

The carefree little girl in black swayed as she hummed a tune while walking through the forest.

Pei Qian landed lightly on a branch and didn’t reveal herself right away. She scanned her surroundings, frowned slightly, and pretended to be unaware of the situation. After gauging the area, she concluded that there shouldn’t be too much trouble. After all, the little spirit hiding over eighty feet away was far less capable than the water deity of the river.

Pei Qian was initially anxious and angry, but when she noticed that Zhou Mi Li was happily wandering around, casually grabbing a handful of green leaves and stuffing them into her mouth, she felt her irritation grow. Before chewing the leaves, the little girl glanced around to make sure no one was watching, and then took a big bite.

Pei Qian’s initial worry dissipated, but she became even more annoyed.

From the previous discussions she had overheard, the situation was indeed serious. According to passersby, Mi Li had been wandering around the vicinity of Red Candle Town for quite some time, and today, while lying by the riverbank, she was spotted by some spirit servants of the Water Goddess of the Jade Liquid River. Mistaking her for a little spirit not registered in their records, they attempted to recruit her to work in the river’s service. When Zhou Mi Li refused, things escalated into a conflict, and the water deity’s side seemed to have invoked some laws from the Da Li Mountain, causing quite a stir. Zhou Mi Li was frightened and ended up getting beaten.

Pei Qian had more insight into the matter. According to Mountain Lord Wei Ban, Mi Li hailed from the Mute Lake in the North Ju Lu Continent, and her roots were tied to a different water spirit identity. This made her somewhat incompatible with the waters of Da Li’s Three Rivers. Thankfully, she had now obtained the status of a devotee of Lupo Mountain, which mitigated the effect. With more exposure to the various water spirits, she could integrate better into local customs. That was why Pei Qian often took Mi Li out from Lupo Mountain to play around Red Candle Town and Qi Dune Mountain, without getting too close to the Three Rivers. She felt that if they took it slow, and if Mi Li came alone to the banks of the Dan, Embroidery, and Jade Liquid Rivers in the future, it would be fine.

Pei Qian adjusted the small bamboo box on her back, sighed, and called out, “Zhou Mi Li!”

The little girl in black turned around, saw Pei Qian falling from the tree, and broke into a wide smile. She scratched her cheek, then tilted her head slightly to show Pei Qian her unbruised side.

Pei Qian had sharp eyes and immediately noticed the bruise on the other cheek. Well, it seemed that walking home so slowly and munching on leaves was actually a cover-up for the fact that she had been beaten up!

Pei Qian stayed silent.

Zhou Mi Li blinked her eyes.

The little girl tightly clenched her fists, then began to scratch her head.

Her faintly yellowed eyebrows furrowed delicately, and she didn’t dare to frown too hard, fearing Pei Qian might think she was greatly wronged.

Back when they were wandering around in the North Ju Lu Continent, someone had once said that every little worry from childhood was like a small rice grain. When one grew old and looked back, it would amount to a big bowl full!

Pei Qian asked, “What happened?”

Zhou Mi Li thought for a moment, “I was playing by the river, poking my head underwater to see if there were any fish or shrimp. I didn’t dare to eat anything, just wanted a peek. Then I encountered a high-ranking official from the Jade Liquid River’s Water Goddess palace. I explained for quite a while before they believed I lived in a small town in Huai Huang County. I didn’t mention Lupo Mountain or Mud Bottle Alley, just made up some random name for a nearby alley where I raised chickens and ducks. That official believed me and let me go home…”

Pei Qian exclaimed angrily, “Zhou Mi Li! Why didn’t you report my master’s name when they bullied you? Your home is Lupo Mountain; you are the Right Protector of Lupo Mountain!”

The little girl in black timidly replied, “I was afraid of causing trouble. It wasn’t a big deal, just a little rice grain.”

Now that Pei Qian had grown a bit taller, Mi Li felt a little shorter in comparison.

Zhou Mi Li opened her hand, revealing just a handful of sunflower seeds. Earlier, she had brought a large bag, and now only this much remained. The little girl said softly, “Pei Qian, shall we go home? We can eat seeds while we hurry back.”

Pei Qian shot her a glare.

Zhou Mi Li frowned, looking like she was about to cry.

Pei Qian had been away from home for so long that it was hard to finally return, only to be reprimanded right away. This made the little girl feel genuinely wronged.

She had wandered around Qi Dune Mountain and Red Candle Town so many times just to wait for Pei Qian to come home, hoping to see her first and have some sunflower seeds to munch on.

Pei Qian gently ruffled the top of Mi Li’s head and said softly, “Don’t cry, don’t cry.”

Then Pei Qian urged Zhou Mi Li to recount the events in more detail.

The little girl, who usually had a carefree demeanor, finally managed to piece the story together.

Pei Qian then commanded, “Zhou Mi Li, listen up!”

Zhou Mi Li immediately straightened her back and stood on her tiptoes.

Pei Qian waved her hand, “You go home first, hurry up, no dawdling, and don’t wander around. Once home, if the old chef is there and if Wei Mountain Lord is on our mountain, you privately tell the old chef that I’m in Red Candle Town buying some things before returning home. With the New Year coming, I need to prepare some goods. If I come back late, it’ll be because I have too much stuff. You tell the old chef to lend a hand.”

Zhou Mi Li squatted down, “I’m not stupid; I’m not following orders today. I want to go back together.”

Pei Qian said, “On Lupo Mountain, who has a higher rank? Who recommended you to be the Right Protector? Zhou Mi Li!”

The little girl in black squatted on the ground, pretending to be foolish, poking at the dirt and dead leaves.

Pei Qian crouched down and asked, “I have my master’s orders; what is there to be afraid of?”

Zhou Mi Li looked up, “What?”

Pei Qian pulled out a bundle of golden silk thread from her sleeve, “See this?”

Zhou Mi Li gaped, covering her mouth with both hands, mumbling, “Looks impressive and valuable.”

Pei Qian stood up, “Hurry back to Lupo Mountain and tell the old chef what happened. This is called relaying military orders; it’s a heavy responsibility. Can you handle it? Do you have that sense of duty?”

Zhou Mi Li immediately stood up, shouting, “Right Protector is ordered! I will leave immediately!”

Pei Qian tucked the golden sword intent away, then took out a treasured talisman she had kept for many years and slapped it onto Zhou Mi Li’s forehead, “With this talisman, demons and monsters will steer clear. Go!”

Zhou Mi Li dashed off, not forgetting to stretch out her hands as she left.

Pei Qian laughed in exasperation, “You can munch on them on your own way back.”

Pei Qian turned around, tightened her grip on her walking stick, took a deep breath, and headed straight for the distant Water Goddess Palace of the Jade Liquid River.

In the world of rivers and lakes, one must uphold righteousness!

Having become a deity of mountains and waters, she should protect the local land and waters.

What kind of ability was it to bully a little rice grain?

The Water Goddess temple was on the opposite bank. After Pei Qian dashed down the mountain, she leaped high, striking the river with a punch, propelling herself upward before leaping across the vast river in one bound.

A young man dressed in black, running a bookstore in Red Candle Town, sat on the roof. Upon witnessing this scene, the young shopkeeper chuckled, “Now, that’s entertaining.”

He was currently the water deity of the Chong Dan River, a colleague of the Embroidery River and Jade Liquid River.

The attributes of the three rivers varied; the Embroidery River was wide and gentle, the Chong Dan River was swift and fierce, while the Jade Liquid River had the shortest course but was unstable, with spiritual energy distributed irregularly. The water palace of the Jade Liquid River was the most vibrant, and the water goddess was famously adept at "human relations," maintaining good connections with various parties.

The shrine of the Water Goddess was bustling with activity.

Before Pei Qian could enter and reason things out, an elderly priestess and a middle-aged official from the water palace, who had clumsily attempted to conceal their presence, stepped out.

The old priestess had just received news from a diligent spirit who had been tracking the little girl. In a panic, she rushed back to inform of an extremely troubling revelation. The little girl in black was actually a spirit from Lupo Mountain and seemed to be a protective devotee.

The old priestess didn’t take it seriously; a protective devotee? Not to mention that mysterious Lupo Mountain, even their own water deity’s devotees had to start at the Golden Core level! How could a mountain as prestigious as Lupo Mountain, blessed by Wei Dajun’s guardianship, have such low-level beings?

In the old Li Zhu Cave realm, Lupo Mountain was an enigmatic presence shrouded in fog. The young mountain lord, Chen Ping An, was said to have once been a poor orphan from Mud Bottle Alley, but his fortunes changed drastically. He first met the beloved daughter of the saint Ruan Qiong and later encountered Wei Ban during a time of hardship. With these two great benefactors, he eventually came to possess several important feng shui sites.

However, that little girl indeed seemed to possess the registry from Lupo Mountain.

Outsiders only hazily knew that Lupo Mountain appeared to not be too concerned about the classification of spirits, warriors, or cultivators.

With Wei Dajun protecting Lupo Mountain, who would dare be foolish enough to investigate? There were only five mountain lords across the continent, and Wei Ban was the sole upper-level deity of the Baoping Continent!

The emperor himself was quite close to him, and not only was Da Li’s Song clan the land of dragon rise, but the entire old Da Li territory also fell under the jurisdiction of the northern mountain area!

The official from the water palace clasped his hands and bowed, saying, “I misjudged that little girl earlier, mistaking her for a mountain spirit that had wandered into the streets. Considering my duties, I questioned her, and a dispute arose. It was indeed my rudeness, and I wish to apologize to Lupo Mountain.”

The old priestess smiled and replied, “Simply apologizing won’t suffice. We at the Jade Liquid River Water Shrine will make further amends; I’ll personally bring gifts when I visit.”

Pei Qian gripped her walking stick tightly, remaining silent.

What to do?

Something felt off, but she couldn’t pinpoint what it was.

If only her master were around.

Even if her master wasn’t here, having her junior brother would be enough.

The old priestess maintained a calm smile, while the official subtly tugged at his mouth. He knew he’d face some punishment, and would have to buy gifts afterward. However, did they really think this little girl would come demanding retribution? Did they think the Jade Liquid River Water Shrine was of such little consequence? What they truly feared was that incredibly lucky young mountain lord, and the power behind him, Ruan Xiu, Wei Ban. Who did this little martial artist think he was? Did he really intend to rely on brute strength, a walking stick, to smash their shrine? It would be amusing to let him do so, but eventually, who would be left to apologize and make amends? 

Pei Qian, with her sharp gaze, noticed something.

Fuming, she took a deep breath.

Her walking stick trembled slightly, and a subtle ripple emerged from her sleeve. Since it wasn’t the kind of spiritual energy that a cultivator would use, even the elderly priestess didn’t notice.

“Apologize to your mother!” 

A figure clad in green, radiating an imposing aura, landed directly in front of the Water Goddess Shrine, standing beside Pei Qian.

It was none other than Chen Lingjun, who had fully refined a Dragon King’s basket.

Without a word, Chen Lingjun raised the Dragon King’s basket, which had been meticulously repaired by the true dragon of the North Ju Lu Continent, and it suddenly grew large as a mountain, enveloping the entire Water Goddess Shrine.

In the world, the Dragon King’s basket could capture even the most unruly of dragons. Chen Lingjun’s presence alone put immense pressure on the old priestess and the official from the water palace, both of whom were of water spirit heritage. The old priestess could still manage to hold her ground, but the official found his knees buckling, nearly collapsing to the ground, only prevented from losing face by the old priestess grabbing him by the shoulder.

Chen Lingjun spoke, “So, you want to apologize, huh? I’ll do you one better: I’ll beat you first, then apologize!”

The old priestess smiled and replied, “If we harm the little girl, that’s a thousand mistakes. But once a mistake is made, to apologize is also not wrong. This immortal master isn’t trying to bully anyone, are you planning to suppress the Water Goddess Shrine today with that magical artifact?”

Chen Lingjun’s expression darkened as he nodded, “Yes, after I smash this dilapidated Water Goddess Shrine, I’ll head straight back to North Ju Lu Continent. Even if my lord wants to scold me, he won’t be able to.”

Pei Qian suddenly interjected, “Chen Lingjun, I’m used to being scolded by my master; let me handle this.”

Chen Lingjun was taken aback.

His lord would never dare to scold this little girl.

Chen Lingjun chuckled, “Pei Qian, your current realm…”

Before he could finish his sentence, Pei Qian brought her walking stick down heavily onto the ground. The golden silk thread, which even Pei Qian couldn’t suppress, instantly unfurled like a waterfall, wrapping around her walking stick.

It resembled a golden longsword.

Pei Qian thrust the stick into the ground.

In that instant, the aura of the sword filled the air.

Even Chen Lingjun, with his extremely resilient physique, couldn’t help but take a few steps back.

The old ancestor of the sword cultivators, Zhou Cheng, had once said that when one felt deep discontent, one must draw the sword.

The old priestess was thrown into a panic, unable to maintain her calm demeanor, realizing how trivial the situation was. The girl with the bamboo box was evidently a sword cultivator.

She might even be the legendary sword genius!

The old priestess had already lost track of the official from the water palace and hurriedly activated her water spirit’s innate divine ability, sending ripples of thought to notify the Water Goddess in the great river’s palace.

However, there was no response.

Because above the water palace, an old man with a hunched back, floating in the air, was looking down into the water with his hands behind his back, smiling as he said, “You’ll die.”

Pei Qian brandished the walking stick entwined with golden sword intent, her eyes shining brightly.

She declared, “I remember what my master said! Apologies must be sincere, not just about the quantity of gifts. This matter is wrong, and the order is wrong. What is sincerity? You’re not merely apologizing to Lupo Mountain; you must apologize to Zhou Mi Li.”

The water deity of the Chong Dan River retracted his hand, looking helpless. They couldn’t just let the Jade Liquid River Water Shrine go down this path, so he rushed over. After a while of enjoying the fun, being overly relaxed could lead to trouble. Eventually, someone would cause a commotion.

Just as he was about to approach the water palace, the old man said, “Bias and twisted reasoning will lead to death as well.”

The black-clad water deity had to land on the surface of the Jade Liquid River.

A gracefully dressed woman emerged from the water, sneering, “Lupo Mountain seeks trouble with the Jade Liquid River; I’ll be reporting you all to the Grand Li Department of Rites.”

Zhu Lian pulled out a Great Li Peace and No Trouble token, the first-class token, and placed it at his waist, nodding and smiling, “Alright. I’ll give you this opportunity. I don’t want your Chong Dan River colleague thinking you’re just posturing.”

Upon seeing the unmistakable first-class token, the water goddess’s expression changed dramatically. Hesitating, she bit her lip, ready to bow her head first before making a decision...

But before she could act, a punch landed squarely on her.

She was directly knocked down to the depths of the Jade Liquid River.

Her golden body trembled, and golden blood flowed from her seven orifices, revealing her identity as a deity of the waters.

The hunchbacked old man, exuding an immense aura of martial intent, found himself landing not far from the water’s bottom, as if using the divine power of a celestial to split the waters.

The old man laughed, “Since Lupo Mountain is in charge, Zhu Lian is here today to ask questions of the Jade Liquid River Water Palace. I have offended greatly.”

As the old man took a step back, he gently stepped out, his hunched frame bending even lower, calmly saying, “I will strike, and only life or death shall decide. No reasoning involved.”

On the distant river surface of the battlefield below, the deity of the Chong Dan River frowned, his expression grave.

That martial arts master below the water was not merely at the distant travel realm.

The old man’s martial intent was so immense that it suddenly pressed down on the current of the Jade Liquid River.

It was an unfathomable sense of superiority!

With one punch, the river shattered.

The old man reached out and grabbed the neck of the palace-dressed woman, who was now bleeding golden blood and sinking into the rushing waters.

The old man glanced at the Chong Dan River deity, who stood up and clasped his fists, saying, “Senior, please feel free to head to the Jade Liquid River Water Shrine.”

The old man laughed, “I’ve had a long-standing relationship with the Water Goddess regarding purchasing and selling books; Lupo Mountain remembers it well. Earlier, I was merely posturing. Water Goddess, please don’t hold a grudge.”

The Chong Dan River deity could only smile bitterly and nod.

At the shrine, the priestess caught a glimpse of the scene from afar, witnessing the old man soaring through the air, holding their severely injured water goddess.

The old priestess’s soul seemed to fly away, and she hurriedly activated her meager divine abilities, casting illusions to conceal the scene and quickly shut the doors of the shrine to prevent the faithful from seeing what had transpired.

Earlier, the Water Goddess Shrine had already been in an uproar; after all, no one was blind. Everyone could see the suspended Dragon King’s basket. The old priestess had intentionally left the door open, merely preventing the devotees from going out, allowing them to crowd at the entrance to watch the commotion.

After Zhu Lian landed, he casually tossed the injured water goddess at the feet of the old priestess, then walked between Pei Qian and Chen Lingjun, extending his hands to pat their heads, smiling, “Very good.”

Pei Qian slapped the old chef’s hand away.

Chen Lingjun tucked away the massive Dragon King’s basket that overshadowed everything.

Zhu Lian stepped forward, placing a foot on the barely conscious water goddess’s head, looking towards the entrance, and smiled at the old priestess, “You, old hag, with a bad heart and an ugly face, why don’t you continue to drag the common folk to share the danger? Are you still hoping to tarnish our Lupo Mountain’s reputation? Useless.”

Zhu Lian pressed down harder, causing the water goddess’s head to sink into the ground.

“Alright, let’s leave it at that. Remember to apologize. Whether you survive or not doesn’t matter; it’ll save a few cups of tea money. However, the deity’s money from the Jade Liquid River must be collected. Our Lupo Mountain is but a small hill, too poor to even scrape by.”

Zhu Lian turned to ask, “Do you prefer it easier, or do you want to leave a way out for future meetings?”

Pei Qian shook her walking stick, puzzled, “What do you mean?”

Zhu Lian smiled, “You’ll understand when your sister Xiu returns.”

Pei Qian responded, “Then we’ll just apologize and be done with it.”

Zhu Lian looked down at the half-dead but still pretending to be dead water goddess and, channeling his voice with intent, smiled at her, “You’re just lucky to run into us at Lupo Mountain. Just enjoy it quietly; otherwise, not just this shrine, but your Jade Liquid River’s existence will be uncertain in the future. The method of salvation has already been imparted to you; think for yourself.”

Zhu Lian then left with Pei Qian and Chen Lingjun, strolling leisurely along the riverbank.

Zhu Lian rubbed his wrist, sighing, “In the end, it wasn’t satisfying enough. If all mountain and water deities had such a disposition, then the methods of Yuan Bao would be the way to go. Luckily, it’s not all like this.”

Pei Qian complained, “Fighting and killing—what’s the propriety in that? Old chef, what did that dim-witted Yuan Bao say? She’s quite tall; why is her mind always muddled?”

Zhu Lian chuckled, “We’ll talk about it when we get home.”

Pei Qian struck Chen Lingjun’s head with her stick, and even though it was just a trace of sword intent left behind, it nearly knocked him to the ground, causing him to tremble.

Chen Lingjun, swaying like a pendulum, finally hugged his head and shouted, “Pei Qian, what’s that for?”

Pei Qian paused, quickly apologizing, saying her walking stick had been acting weird today. Seeing that Chen Lingjun wasn’t angry, she felt relieved! Pei Qian then laughed heartily, “Chen Lingjun, you did a great job today. I’ll erase all seventy-two accounts of you stealing sunflower seeds from my little ledger!”

Seventy-two entries… just for munching on sunflower seeds.

Chen Lingjun grinned through the pain, “Thank you.”

Pei Qian bounced up, “Let’s go find Mi Li and munch on seeds!”

Zhu Lian reminded, “Pei Qian, don’t forget.”

Pei Qian brandished the insane sword technique, occasionally scaring Chen Lingjun, “Don’t worry; I’ll remind Mi Li.”

Chen Lingjun said, “Old chef, I plan to go to North Ju Lu Continent.”

Zhu Lian nodded, “The sooner you go and return, the better.”

Ruan Qiong had returned to the Longquan Sword Sect from the Da Li capital, still focused on sword forging.

The discussions held in the Imperial Study had all been sworn into a pact; anyone who leaked the details would face retribution, and the Da Li court would punish their entire family.

Ruan Qiong was indifferent to these matters, for he and the Da Li court were allies.

Affairs of the Longquan Sword Sect were entirely left to disciples like Dong Gu and Xu Xiaoqiao, who were the trusted ones. Ruan Xiu had spent several years cultivating at Dragon Spine Mountain and had quietly descended the mountain to travel north to the new territory of the Longquan Sword Sect. Fortunately, there were no conflicts, and she managed to negotiate peacefully with the old Middle Mount deity, which greatly relieved Ruan Qiong.

With the territory established but no one managing it, this was the most awkward aspect of the Longquan Sword Sect.

For a sect of its stature, the number of direct disciples in the Patriarch Hall was too few.

Even though they had gradually accepted three groups of disciples, each group was small, making it seem as if the sect’s vitality was waning.

Thus, the Da Li Song clan handed over the old Zhu Ying dynasty territory to Zhengyang Mountain. Ruan Qiong didn’t feel any resentment; if one’s ability was insufficient to hold onto the meat, it would naturally fall into someone else’s bowl. Therefore, he had to content himself with the pickled vegetables in his own bowl.

Moreover, the Da Li court had previously allocated a large chunk of territory to the Longquan Sword Sect, laying the groundwork.

The proximity to the capital was a gesture from the young emperor to prevent court officials from suspecting that the Longquan Sword Sect had fallen to the sidelines, and that Zhengyang Mountain would become the future first sect of the Baoping Continent.

Of course, it also diminished the suspicion of crossing the river and tearing down the bridge.

The Da Li court had treated Ruan Qiong very well since the previous emperor and the current one, from the time Ruan Qiong was stationed at Li Zhu Cave until now.

It was mainly Ruan Qiong’s unwillingness to accept disciples indiscriminately; those lacking in temperament, no matter how talented they were as innate sword seedlings, had other places to go, and it didn’t matter if they went to Zhengyang Mountain, which was likely to become the next sword sect.

Of the twelve named disciples, half had left, including one innate sword seedling, who had now gone to Zhengyang Mountain and was already a direct disciple of that sect’s Patriarch.

Of course, Ruan Qiong’s good relationships had truly opened the eyes of the young emperor, Song He.

Before the discussions in the Imperial Study, various mountain lords, including Qi Zhen of the Divine Decree Sect, the old ancestor of the Wind and Snow Temple, the Law Sword cultivator of Zhenwu Mountain, and Liu Lao Cheng of Zhenjing Sect, along with Wei Ban and Jin Qing, had all engaged in friendly conversation with Ruan Qiong. They had all taken the initiative to approach him, at least greeting him properly and treating him with the utmost courtesy.

No one else compared.

Though Ruan Qiong was not a good speaker, the nature of a cultivator’s character was difficult to conceal over time.

Those who knew Ruan Qiong found no flaws in him and preferred to foster friendships. Those who didn’t know him, if they casually mentioned Ruan Qiong, whether it was the past Ruan Qiong of the Wind and Snow Temple or the current sect master, would still speak highly of the number one swordsmith of the Baoping Continent.

Today, Ruan Qiong rarely made an appearance and called all his first-generation disciples to dine together.

The first disciple listed in the genealogy of the Longquan Sword Sect, Dong Gu, had long since entered the Golden Core level and had opened his peak. However, the most awkward part for Dong Gu was that he was not a sword cultivator, and his background was difficult to speak of. Now, whispers had begun to circulate among the Da Li court and various celestial mountain sects.

Xu Xiaoqiao was once a sword cultivator of the Wind and Snow Temple, but after committing a grave mistake and being expelled from the sect, he found Ruan Qiong. He cut off the thumb of his right hand, which wielded the sword, to become Ruan Qiong’s direct disciple.

Xie Ling had already nurtured a flying sword of his own. Besides that, the celestial weapon gifted by Lu Chen, the old ancestor Xie Shi, had also been gifted to this descendant of Taoye Alley, along with two treasured items: one was a relic of a Baoping Continent sword cultivator named “Peach Leaf,” which Xie Ling refined into one of his vital treasures, and another was a high-ranking nurturing sword gourd named “Full Moon.”

The four master and disciple sat on separate benches.

Ruan Xiu was still in the old Middle Mount territory, so Ruan Qiong had no chance to serve food to anyone.

Even though his daughter wasn’t present, just the thought of that scoundrel not being in Lupo Mountain made Ruan Qiong feel somewhat better.
