Ruan Qiong said, “Dong Gu, you mentioned before that you aim to reach the Nascent Soul stage within a hundred years?”

Dong Gu quickly put down his utensils and wiped his mouth, solemnly saying, “Yes, Master.”

Ruan Qiong instructed, “Then don’t let others’ progress affect your state of mind, forcing yourself to advance to the Nascent Soul stage ahead of time. Cultivation and understanding the Dao are solely dependent on your efforts. Being in the Longquan Sword Sect, so what if you’re not a sword cultivator? So what if outsiders gossip and laugh? Even if you are eventually surpassed by Xu Xiaoqiao and Xie Ling in realm, so what? You will still be the founding disciple of the Longquan Sword Sect! When did the Longquan Sword Sect ever need to rely on fists to determine seniority? Have I not taught you this? Or have you forgotten?”

Ruan Qiong glanced at Dong Gu, “Continue eating.”

Dong Gu immediately picked up his chopsticks.

Ruan Qiong then turned to Xu Xiaoqiao and Xie Ling, “After you finish your meal, go to the old Middle Mount territory. If Xiu Xiu doesn’t want to come back, there’s no use in trying to persuade her.”

Xu Xiaoqiao nodded.

Ruan Qiong suddenly said, “Remember to stop by the Qilong Alley New Year’s shop and buy some pastries.”

Xu Xiaoqiao, usually quiet, rarely showed a smile.

Xie Ling was even more unable to hide his happiness, finally getting to see Sister Xiu.

The two direct sword cultivators of the Longquan Sword Sect took to their swords and headed toward the new territory of the Longquan Sword Sect.

Above the sea of clouds, Xie Ling asked with a smile, “Second Sister, I heard that Sister Xiu has a little spirit companion with her?”

Xu Xiaoqiao responded with an “Mm.”

Xie Ling didn’t ask more.

In the thick snow-covered mountain fields, as the two were descending the mountain, a little girl holding an oil-paper umbrella suddenly pounced out, rolling around in the snow, completely covered in white, tumbling down the slope.

The young woman followed slowly behind.

Once the little girl got up, she wielded the oil-paper umbrella like a hammer, chanting, “Old Lord swings his hammer, the comet adds charcoal dust, oh no, oh no! The Rain Master and Wind Lord are helping, and the Thunder Lord and Lightning Mother are coming to assist, bang bang bang!”

The young woman remarked, “The sword forging chant isn’t recited like that.”

The little girl paused her hammering motion, looked up at the distant mountains, and asked in a lowered voice, “Sister Xiu, is that the mountain deity? The former mountain lord of our Da Li Dynasty! Even a fart sounds like thunder and could blow me away. Why is it still so polite to you? It doesn’t seem polite; it’s more like fear of Sister Xiu.”

Ruan Xiu said, “You’re so clever, knowing the answer, why ask? Talking more makes you hungry.”

The little girl’s eyes twinkled, “Sister Xiu, doesn’t that mean you’re even smarter than me?”

Ruan Xiu shook her head, “I don’t like to think; I’m rather dull.”

The little girl pretended to be scared, “Sister Xiu, if you get too hungry and eat me, I’ll be in trouble!”

Ruan Xiu nodded, “I will.”

The little girl scampered over to Ruan Xiu’s side, genuinely frightened now, tugging at her sleeve, whispering, “Sister Xiu, don’t eat me.”

Ruan Xiu wasn’t very inclined to talk.

The little girl held her beloved umbrella, “Sister Xiu, be careful, or I’ll tell on you…”

In response, the little girl received a gentle slap from Ruan Xiu, spinning her around several times before landing heavily in the thick snow, rolling away and breaking countless dry branches.

However, the little girl quickly dashed back to Ruan Xiu’s side as if nothing had happened, clearly used to it.

As they approached the foot of the mountain, the little girl quickly hid behind Ruan Xiu.

Xu Xiaoqiao and Xie Ling gracefully landed, sheathing their swords. The way they sheathed their swords was distinctly different—one was neat and efficient, while the other was flowing and artistic.

One respectfully called out “Elder Sister,” while the other playfully called “Sister Xiu.”

Ruan Xiu nodded slightly, simply saying, “You’re here.”

The little girl peeked out from behind Ruan Xiu, puzzled. How strange! Two sword immortals had arrived; they didn’t look like a pair of divine lovers. That boy with an awkward expression was clearly infatuated with Sister Xiu.

Didn’t he just call her Sister Xiu?

Tsk tsk tsk.

The little girl thought this young sword immortal was quite pathetic.

She really wanted to knock that boy out, drag him back to her cave as her future husband, and raise him properly. As for the so-called cave, it would only be hers.

Ruan Xiu cautiously took out a piece of peach blossom cake and placed it in her mouth, instantly beaming with joy.

She then pinched a piece and offered it to the little girl. The little girl swallowed it in one bite, the taste unknown.

Ruan Xiu asked, “Did you pay?”

Xu Xiaoqiao replied, “I already did.”

Ruan Xiu nodded but said, “I don’t need to pay when I go there.”

Xu Xiaoqiao fell silent.

Xie Ling felt a complex mix of emotions.

(End of Chapter)

 **Chapter 755: Zhu Lian Has Questions to Ask (Part 2)**

Xu Xiaoqiao said, “Master asked me to ask Senior Sister whether we should head back.” 

Ruan Xiu replied, “Of course we should go back! I want to hear Xiaomi Li tell stories. It’s been so long since we last met, and I’m sure Xiaomi Li can come up with plenty of new tales.” 

Xu Xiaoqiao thought that Ruan Xiu’s reasoning was entirely justified.

In a small bookshop located in an old city of a vassal state from the Zhurong Dynasty, the shopkeeper was a young woman named He Jia. Although she was of average beauty, her figure was exquisite enough to attract many roguish youths who often lingered around the shop. However, none of them managed to take advantage of her; at most, they would engage in some flirtatious banter, to which the young woman paid little mind. There were also well-off but not particularly notable young scholars who visited to buy books, their intentions not solely aimed at literature.

This evening, He Jia sat behind the counter, flipping through a book. As she glanced at the darkening sky, she decided to close the shop and head back to her residence, which was only two alleys away.

Just as she set down her book, she noticed a young man standing outside the shop with a sword on his back. Though he appeared somewhat disheveled, his handsome features were hard to ignore—like a jade tree standing in the wind, his beauty shone brightly.

“Excuse me, young sir,” she said softly, “I’m sorry, but the shop is about to close.”

He remained on the threshold, seemingly hesitant to step inside. His lips trembled slightly as he tried to calm his voice, “I just happened to pass by and wanted to buy a few books. I didn’t mean to seek you out.”

He Jia sighed inwardly. Such a clumsy excuse—did he think anyone would believe it?

However, she chose not to press further. Sitting back down, she picked up her book and said gently, “If you truly want to buy books, feel free to choose for yourself. I can keep the shop open a little longer.”

The young man still didn’t step over the threshold.

He Jia continued to read, the fading sunlight casting a warm glow over her. Although her current circumstances were far from glorious, she was not an ordinary person and didn’t feel particularly troubled.

Gathering his courage, he spoke with a shaky voice, “Will you come with me to Fenglei Garden? Please, Su Jia?”

Even without any tricks to disguise herself, even if she had transformed into someone entirely different, Liu Baqiao would still recognize her at a glance. No matter how time flowed, whether she became a young girl or an old woman with white hair, he would never miss her in a crowd.

But how could he voice these thoughts? On what grounds could he say such things?

He Jia lifted her head, frowning slightly. “Although I’m no longer a direct disciple of the Patriarch Hall, my name is still clearly listed on the outer sect roster of Zhengyang Mountain. Why would you say such things, Liu Gongzi?”

She paused for a moment before continuing, “But now, I consider this a journey of experience. So please, don’t call me Su Jia anymore.”

Liu Baqiao felt a tightening in his chest. Even as a promising sword cultivator at the Golden Elixir stage, he felt breathless at this moment, as if he wanted to bend over to catch his breath.

“What do you go by now?” he asked.

He Jia responded with a hint of annoyance, “Liu Gongzi, does it have anything to do with you?!”

Liu Baqiao lowered his head and muttered softly, “I like you. I’ve been looking for you for many years.”

The bookshop’s proprietress, He Jia—or rather, Su Jia of Zhengyang Mountain—stood up and said, “Liu Gongzi, I ask you to leave me a little peace, will you? I’ve invested my last bit of savings to settle here and start a new life. It hasn’t been easy. Liu Gongzi, I am different from you now. I never liked you, and you should reflect on that. How many times have we met? How many words have we exchanged?”

Liu Baqiao looked up, offering a sad smile. “We never spoke before. Today is the first time.”

Su Jia softened her tone. “Liu Gongzi, you should know that I don’t have feelings for you, right?”

Liu Baqiao nodded.

Su Jia chuckled helplessly, “You like Su Jia, the talented sword cultivator of Fenglei Garden, so should Su Jia be grateful to you?”

Liu Baqiao shook his head. “That’s not how it works. It’s right that you don’t like me.”

Su Jia closed the book and gently placed it on the table. “If you feel guilty because my senior brother bested me in a duel years ago, let me sincerely tell you that there’s no need for that. I bear no grudge against your senior brother Huang He. On the contrary, I understand that he far surpasses me in both swordsmanship and cultivation. Losing is just losing. Furthermore, if you think I resent Zhengyang Mountain for being expelled after my defeat, then you have misunderstood me even more.”

Su Jia’s eyes were clear. “I have been cultivating on the mountain since childhood and have no memories of the world below. So from the moment I could remember, I have regarded Zhengyang Mountain as my only home.”

Liu Baqiao spoke softly, “As long as Su Jia continues to run this shop, I will leave, and I promise to never disturb you again.”

Su Jia was both frustrated and amused. “I’ve already told you, opening this bookstore and buying a small house have exhausted my savings. Even if I wanted to move, where could I go? I just hope you keep your promise.”

Liu Baqiao nodded. “I will.”

In the end, Liu Baqiao still didn’t step across the threshold, only asking, “May I sit here for a while? Just a little while.”

Su Jia had no choice but to agree.

And so, Liu Baqiao sat right there on the threshold.

As the sunset cast longer shadows across the street, Liu Baqiao finally stood up and left.

He Zhi Xiu was indeed Su Jia, and many admired such a woman.

What was wrong with liking her?

Inside the bookshop, Su Jia shook her head, wishing this strange situation would come to an end. The fact that Liu Baqiao liked her had long been an open secret between Zhengyang Mountain and Fenglei Garden, but Su Jia genuinely didn’t return his feelings.

She locked up the shop and headed to her small residence.

After that duel years ago, Su Jia lost everything—a sword peak, her status as a direct disciple of the Patriarch Hall, and the treasured sword nurturing gourd gifted by her master.

Now, she was left with nothing but mud on her feet, forced to hide in the common streets.

Before this, she had faced hardships, but she had managed to cope with all the troubles, and now she was moving forward.

As for Zhengyang Mountain, as she had said, she held no resentment—only an unshakeable guilt.

What was difficult to let go were certain people and certain words.

But regarding Huang He, the door disciple of Li Tun Jing and now the master of Fenglei Garden, Su Jia felt an indescribable fear that often jolted her awake from nightmares.

She couldn’t comprehend it, nor could she let it go.

Back then, on the snowy temple’s divine platform where the three sword duels were held, the man with the sword case, filled with small swords but not his own flying sword, distractedly wielding them, was beyond reason.

One sword pierced the hand that wielded her sword, another severed the red cord that connected the nourishing sword gourd at her waist, and finally, two flying swords pinned her wrists.

After Su Jia fainted, the last scene she saw before closing her eyes was Huang He stepping on her nourishing sword gourd, twisting it gently.

That mountain-like man, seemingly powerful and invincible, was cold and merciless in every regard.

Even today, upon seeing Liu Baqiao, Su Jia trembled at the thought of Huang He and that nightmare, the true source of her anguish.

Walking through the secluded alley, Su Jia wrapped her arms around her shoulders, as if seeking warmth.

As she walked, her face turned pale. Leaning against the wall, she raised a hand to rub her temples.

After a long time, Su Jia wiped the sweat from her forehead and made her way to her small house.

When she reached the end of an alley and opened the door, she froze in place, tears streaming down her face.

The woman before her resembled her, but just as Liu Baqiao recognized Su Jia in an instant, Su Jia recognized the woman standing in front of her.

It was her master, the one who had taken her up the mountain to cultivate.

However, for some reason, the records of the Patriarch Hall did not reflect this; Su Jia had long ago joined the ranks of an elder of Zhengyang Mountain and subsequently became a direct disciple of the Patriarch Hall.

Yet her master remained unrecorded, despite her high status—she had simply never made a name for herself on Zhengyang Mountain.

Every time the Patriarch Hall convened, her master almost never appeared, and the chair at the back, which she occupied, always sat empty. She preferred to wander the world, often gone for decades at a time.

The woman revealed her true form, the Zhengyang Mountain female cultivator who had attended meetings at the Great Li Imperial Study, sitting in a position where no one bothered to acknowledge her.

Young in appearance, she was not particularly beautiful.

She walked to Su Jia, who was teary-eyed, and reached out to gently touch her head, smiling softly, “Silly disciple. Master merely left Zhengyang Mountain for a few years to travel. Why have you become such a timid girl? Did you forget how to walk in the dark? I should have known not to send you to Yuhu Peak back then.”

Su Jia smiled, her eyes sparkling like autumn water, as if with her master by her side, she could truly fear nothing, returning to the carefree girl she once was.

The woman withdrew her hand, noticing the red string tied around her wrist.

After a brief moment, she stood up to leave.

She didn’t mention bringing Su Jia back to Zhengyang Mountain or restoring her status as a direct disciple of the Patriarch Hall, nor did she bring up the future of the nourishing sword gourd.

Yet Su Jia felt that her current, simple life was not as hard as she had imagined. Although there were many regrets in her heart, simply guarding the bookshop and earning a bit of silver and copper coins brought her peace of mind, except for that haunting nightmare.

After the woman left, she transformed back into an ordinary woman dressed plainly.

Not long after she departed, there was a knock on the door.

Su Jia rushed to open it, mistakenly believing it was her master returning, only to stumble back, swaying unsteadily.

With her sword heart destroyed and her cultivation fallen to the lower ranks, Su Jia felt less than an ordinary woman at this moment.

The man standing outside had a cold expression as he spoke slowly, “Su Jia, you should know that Liu Baqiao will definitely sneak over to see you later, just so you won't notice. Now you have two choices: either crawl back to Zhengyang Mountain and cling to life, or find a man to marry and settle down. If Liu Baqiao still harbors feelings for you, causing delays in your sword training, I will ensure he gives up entirely.”

Su Jia bit her lip, blood seeping from it, unable to utter a word.

The speaker was none other than Huang He, the master of Fenglei Garden, who had broken through at an unknown time.

If it weren’t for the sword immortal Wei Jin from the Snow Temple, Huang He would undoubtedly be regarded as the number one sword genius in Baoping Continent today.

After saying this, Huang He took flight on his sword and departed.

If Liu Baqiao weren’t someone highly valued by her master, Huang He wouldn’t even bother with such trivial matters of love.

If Fenglei Garden didn’t require someone to bear the burden in case of his unexpected absence, Huang He wouldn’t have felt the need to concern himself with Liu Baqiao at all.

Both were sword cultivators, yet the gap between their paths was vast.

After successfully exiting his latest closed-door retreat, Huang He awaited a duel with a certain elder sword cultivator from Zhengyang Mountain.

Following Liu Baqiao to this place, Huang He had resisted the urge to strike several times, almost wanting to knock Liu Baqiao unconscious and drag him back to Fenglei Garden, forcing the talent-wasting young man to spend a hundred years in seclusion.

Su Jia, lost in thought, shut the door behind her, leaning against it and collapsing to the ground in tears.

What would she do about Huang He, whose shadow lingered on?

Her master, that woman, had just stepped outside the city gate, looking up at the sky before continuing her journey—not towards Zhengyang Mountain, but in search of her next disciple.

As for Fenglei Garden, it would stagnate for hundreds of years from now on.

Brotherhood had turned into deadly enmity.

Whether it was Huang He remaining or Liu Baqiao, all that was left was the next Li Tun Jing.

What made this interesting was not that Su Jia didn’t like Liu Baqiao—she wouldn’t like him in the future either—but that she herself didn’t realize that she had already developed feelings for Huang He.

If both Liu Baqiao and Huang He were to end up half-dead, that would be even better.

As for the Zhengyang Mountain woman killed by Li Tun Jing hundreds of years ago, she was, in fact, a disciple of the woman who had just walked away, similarly unrecorded.

There were also several women who were not disciples, yet had some connection to her.

Or perhaps she had engaged in some trivial matters unrelated to being a master or disciple.

For instance, how she met and fell for He Xiaolian at the Snow Temple.

In the early years of the Zhurong Dynasty, there were also some old stories of trivial matters.

Unknowingly, the sword path’s fate over the past thousand years had been manipulated by her, though she wouldn’t dare claim it all—at least half of it was indeed in her hands.

Beyond that, she had once been to Tongye Continent, leaving behind a prophecy at the Fuyi Sect.

She shook her sleeves, slightly raised her wrist, looked down with a smile, retracted her gaze, and walked forward slowly.

Many so-called wise men at the mountain tops excel at weaving intricate plots, but such plots are ultimately fragile and easily broken.

Yet there is one thread in the world, once it is made, even sword immortals find it hard to sever. Even if it appears to be cut, it remains a connection that can entangle for a lifetime.

Unless there is someone truly skilled in deep calculations and adept at unraveling intricacies, there might be hope to confront this deadlock and feel a bit better.

Once the thread is pulled, it’s not that sword immortals cannot kill, but often it leads to a fate worse than death, and then death itself seems like a relief.

She never underestimated her enemies.

Thus, for those she cared about, she had to bury more threads.

The world is filled with infatuated souls, fond of sorrowful tales, finding joy in suffering, reveling in it. How could one be considered infatuated without heartache?

Her thoughts wandered.

It was a pity she hadn’t seen her senior brother in so many years.

The last time was actually very close, as if they had brushed past each other. But as long as her senior brother wanted to avoid her, she thought she would be blind even if they were close enough to touch.

She had heard that he was last seen near the Daoist temple in Tongye Continent.

Her senior brother had one flaw—he liked to borrow the red thread from her wrist but never returned it.

Suddenly, the woman scoffed at herself, “Could it be that I’ve already been noticed?”

Shaking her head, she smiled, “Absolutely not. I’m still quite young. Why should I care about a little Zhengyang Mountain?”

A scruffy young man, hunched and wearing ragged clothes, first went to the tavern in the small town for a drink and some banter, then wandered over to the street where Yang’s shop was located.

He was both a shop assistant and a disciple of the old man Yang, sitting behind the counter with a sleepy expression, lost in thought.

Today, the diligent Su Dian wasn’t practicing her peculiar boxing technique; instead, she was sitting at the door soaking up the sun when she noticed her senior brother Zheng Dafu approaching. Su Dian stood up, and Zheng Dafu waved, “Su girl, you look even prettier than before. If you keep getting more charming, it’ll make me anxious thinking about how you’ll eventually marry off.”

As he got closer to Su Dian, Zheng Dafu slapped his chest dramatically, feigning heartbreak.

Su Dian asked, “Are you looking for Master?”

Zheng Dafu sighed, “Not looking for Master. It’s just so cold on the mountain that no matter how many blankets I use, I can’t get warm. I thought I’d come down and stretch my legs. Su girl, you’re just a few steps away from me. Don’t you ever think of visiting your senior brother? I live in such a big house, and yet I’m here all alone, like a thin willow.”

Su Dian shook her head, “I don’t dare stay there overnight. I’m afraid there might be mice scurrying around the walls.”

Zheng Dafu said earnestly, “Su girl, it’s not that your senior brother is using his status to scold you. As a martial artist, you should have the courage of a hero. How can you be so timid? Come on, let’s go stay at my place tonight and toughen your spirit.”

Su Dian said helplessly, “Senior brother, if there’s something to discuss, please just say it.”

If she hadn’t known this reckless senior brother would only talk and not take action, Su Dian would have fallen out with him long ago.

Zheng Dafu, hands behind his back, spotted a small stool, wanting to sit down, thinking it would be warmer.

But Su Dian kicked it aside, lifting it into her hands.

Zheng Dafu crossed the threshold, saw Shi Ling Shan, and shook his head. “They say the ones closest to the water have the first chance. But you, boy, can’t even keep an eye on your own senior sister. Just wait, soon you’ll be the one to suffer. Which novel doesn’t write about senior sisters or younger sisters walking the world only to be deceived by handsome, wealthy young heroes? Shi Ling Shan, wake up! Your senior sister is getting married!”

Shi Ling Shan was so furious he nearly exploded, glaring at Zheng Dafu. “Zheng Dafu, stop stirring the pot and spreading rumors!”

Zheng Dafu rolled his eyes. “You can’t even curse properly. What good are you?”

Shi Ling Shan was about to retort when his senior sister spoke up, “Senior brother, you said before that if I wanted to break through the fourth realm or reach the fifth realm, I should choose an ancient battlefield as a site. Do you have any suggestions? I want to go out for a while.”

Shi Ling Shan was taken aback.

Zheng Dafu, glancing at him, remarked, “Your senior brother didn’t eat enough before coming down. If he doesn’t go to relieve himself, he won’t get anything.”

Feeling both heartbroken and furious, Shi Ling Shan was almost pushed to spar with Zheng Dafu. But when he saw the other’s hunchbacked figure, he felt a pang of sympathy and decided against it.

Zheng Dafu chuckled and turned to Su Dian, saying, “There are indeed places in mind, but for such important matters, Master has his own plans, so it’s not for me to worry about.”

Su Dian asked, “Do you think I can leave home alone now?”

Zheng Dafu shook his head. “You should take a sidekick with you for safety. You both are still inexperienced, and the world outside is dangerous—not just in terms of cultivation levels but in human hearts. Shi Ling Shan is alright. He’s soft-hearted but can be ruthless when it counts. But you, you’re hard-hearted most of the time, which can lead to trouble. Su girl, when you both go on a journey, you can say Shi Ling Shan is your son. This way, those shameless suitors won’t bother you. Just thinking about it keeps me up at night.”

Su Dian didn’t know how to respond.

Shi Ling Shan was also infuriated, feeling as if a thunderbolt had struck him.

Zheng Dafu glanced toward the bamboo curtain and then turned to leave Yang’s shop.

Zheng Dafu went to the dilapidated archway where the four plaques had lost their mystique. He wandered around, and though the plaques remained, their significance was lost.

He then went to the iron-locked well, which had become a private forbidden area atop a certain mountain. It had been bought for a hefty price years ago, yet yielded no benefits. How foolish could one be?

Remembering the Jiang family from Yunlin, Zheng Dafu gritted his teeth, checked his surroundings, and discreetly adjusted his pants. “I’m sorry, big brother. You’ve worked hard studying, learning all those skills, only to realize you have no thieves to catch.”

Zheng Dafu left the small town and headed toward the Immortal Graveyard, now devoid of that name. The Great Li had deliberately downplayed this old saying; even the dilapidated divine statues were being propped back up, restored to their former glory. 

The Great Li court had put in effort to rejuvenate the place, but as for the large new martial temple, he didn’t bother visiting—it was pointless, a waste of time.

He took a detour to the waterfall where the Iron Talismans River met the Dragon Whisker River, squatting there to toss stones.

What a sight, as Yang Ru plunged into the water like a duckweed.

Zheng Dafu shifted to a deeper, gentler area, staring at the water’s surface, muttering to himself, “Is there truly such a handsome man in the world? The more I look, the more I want to punch him.”

Finally, Zheng Dafu passed by Ruan Qiong’s earliest sword forge. 

He arrived at the stone arch bridge, where the corridor bridge had long been dismantled, revealing the true form of the old stone bridge.

Alone, Zheng Dafu sat on the stone bridge.

He turned his gaze to the north of the small town, where the Old Porcelain Mountain and many nearby dragon kilns stood.

He withdrew his gaze.

Thirty centuries ago, that swiftly rising, swiftly disappearing sword immortal had made a mistake, suddenly gaining fame only to seek to kill dragons, causing chaos and aiming to become the first sword cultivator to break the ascension realm.

The most accomplished scholar from Central Continent, after all, was not a sword cultivator but merely a scholar. Otherwise, the entire structure of the Vast World might have changed.

Yet regarding this secret matter, the old man who surely knew the answer never provided one. Zheng Dafu had once tried to subtly ask Li Er, hoping his senior brother would inquire, but Li Er agreed only to leave it at that.

There was no other way. Thankfully, he could still endure a few curses. In the past, if the old man was willing to speak to him, just ten words would make Zheng Dafu feel like it was the New Year.

So, he only knew that the world’s last true dragon had not attempted to seek those ancient underwater forbidden areas but had instead emerged from the Old Dragon City, breaking through an underground dragon path and eventually falling within the territory of the Great Li.

In search of protection, it sought to have some ancient existence reopen the ascension platform, retreating into those unknown places that sages found hard to reach.

But that old man chose to stand by and watch, ultimately leading to the creation of one of the thirty-six small caves, the Lih Zhu Cave.

The three teachings united, four sages set rules, crafting the archway that would be humorously referred to as the Crab Square by the locals of Lih Zhu Cave in later generations.

The Great Li’s Song family, on the original arch bridge, built another corridor bridge to ensure the longevity and flourishing of the Great Li’s national power, striving for supremacy.

Before leaving, Song Changjing specifically instructed Prince Song Jixin to offer incense at the steps of the corridor bridge.

Those who worshipped were all the tragic and unjustly slain descendants of the Great Li’s Song family.

Old Supervisor Song Yuzhang personally took charge of this matter, effectively overseeing the bloody internal strife within the Great Li’s Song family.

Ultimately, under the order of the influential lady who prioritized giving birth to sons above all else, the attendant of the fallen general Lu had his head severed and placed in a box, sent to the capital of Great Li.

After his death, Song Yuzhang, as a spirit, became the mountain god of the Fallen Mountain, a matter that could be seen as compensation from the Great Li emperor to this significant figure or a form of punishment. After all, Song Yuzhang had offended the old emperor’s bottom line by daring to develop a father-son bond with Song Jixin. 

And Song Jixin, indeed, held a complex mix of resentment and admiration toward Song Yuzhang. As the illegitimate son of the supervisor, living comfortably in Mud Bottle Alley, Song Jixin viewed Song Yuzhang as his biological father during those leisurely days, feeling both anger and admiration.

Unintentionally, he recalled the dusty medicine shop in Old Dragon City.

In truth, Zheng Dafu felt a sense of nostalgia.

People rarely think fondly of good times; what’s done is done. Instead, it's the bittersweet memories that linger.

Zheng Dafu leaned back, using his hands as a pillow, closing his eyes and murmuring, “Is it so hard not to consider oneself superior while treating others as fools? The world is strange.”

Ruan Xiu returned to Longquan Sword Sect.

She arranged to meet Pei Qian and Zhou Mili at the New Year's shop in Qilong Alley.

Today, the three sat together in front of the shop, basking in the sun.

Ruan Xiu noticed that Xiaomi Li seemed to be avoiding her; even the stories of the mountains and waters in Northern Julu were less smooth than before. Looking closely, Ruan Xiu quickly grasped the situation.

In any case, it was related to the Jade Liquid River Water Deity’s estate. The specifics didn’t pique her curiosity, and she didn’t feel the need to press a young girl for details.

Ruan Xiu simply enjoyed her peach blossom cake, which cost her nothing.

In truth, she was among the earliest shopkeepers of both shops.

Pei Qian said, “Sister Xiu, I’ve traveled far and wide on this trip.”

Ruan Xiu smiled, “That’s impressive!”

Pei Qian nodded vigorously, “Very impressive! I’m starting to admire myself!”

Pei Qian hesitated for a moment before softly asking, “Sister Xiu, have you traveled far as well?”

Ruan Xiu thought for a moment and casually replied, “From the heavens to the earth, across the five lakes and four seas, through ancient mountains and deep abysses, I have traveled everywhere. Wherever the sun shines, there are my footprints. Wherever the light of fire spreads, that is my territory.”

Zhou Mili hurriedly raised both hands, though she didn’t clap, “Wow, Sister Xiu, you’re the best! Sister Xiu, you must have changed your shoes many times, right?”

Ruan Xiu smiled, “Not too many.”

Zhou Mili finished her story with great effort and then went next door to chat with Jiu Er.

Pei Qian had told her not to mention anything about the matters in Hongzhu Town. Although Zhou Mili had initially forgotten, after Pei Qian brought it up, she kept thinking about it even in her sleep, causing her to lose her appetite for meals and snacks. So, seeing Sister Xiu today, she felt extremely uncomfortable.

Ruan Xiu stood up, “Let’s go have some fun.”

Pei Qian followed suit, “Sister Xiu, let’s not go to the Jade Liquid River.”

Ruan Xiu smiled with narrowed eyes, ruffling the little girl’s hair, “Liking you and Xiaomi Li’s stories is one thing; how I conduct myself is my own decision.”

Just then, Pei Qian began to stamp her feet anxiously, scratching her head in a fluster, not knowing what to do.

Fortunately, Zhu Lian arrived and said to Pei Qian, “It’s alright.”

Pei Qian beamed, “Old chef, are you addicted to appearing and disappearing mysteriously?”

Zhu Lian stepped into the New Year’s shop.

Pei Qian followed behind, grinning, “Family discount, 20% off.”

Zhu Lian laughed, “Actually, I know a bit about making pastries myself. The golden date paste cake is quite famous; I came up with the recipe myself.”

Pei Qian looked skeptical. “Isn’t that the expensive date cake from the capital of Nanyuan?”

Zhu Lian clasped his hands behind his back, surveying the various pastries in the shop, and nodded, “You didn’t expect that, did you?”

Pei Qian praised, “Old chef, you truly have the heart of a cook. It’s a pity your looks aren’t great; otherwise, even at your age, you wouldn’t be single!”

Zhu Lian simply grunted.

Shi Rou had a strange expression.

Ruan Xiu, riding the wind, hesitated for a moment and reluctantly used her illusion technique.

Upon entering the Jade Liquid River, the water instantly boiled, as if the sun had plunged beneath the surface, igniting a blazing furnace.

The heavens roared with might.

Ruan Xiu walked into the grand hall of the water deity’s estate. The water goddess, who had been leaning against the waterworks to repair her golden form, was now kneeling on the ground, trembling, not even knowing why she felt compelled to beg for death upon seeing this woman. 

Ruan Xiu crossed the steps, turned, and sat on the main seat of the hall, her posture slightly slanted as she propped her chin on one hand, gazing into the distance.

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 756: A Blank Sheet from Cui Dongshan (Part 1)

Zhu Lian arrived at the New Year's shop, dissatisfied that it hadn’t been opened in a while. The kitchen had become more of a display than a functional space, so he sent Pei Qian to buy some groceries, saying they should prepare a meal to liven things up.

Pei Qian was worried about her sister Xiu who was headed to Yu Ye River and was reluctant to leave, suggesting they wait for Xiu to return. Instead, she proposed they go next door to the nearby grass-roots shop, which was bustling with activity every day. "We could just eat there; Miss Jiu'er’s cooking is quite good, and the smell of her dishes wafts all the way through Qilong Alley." 

Zhu Lian disagreed, saying that every shop had its own unique atmosphere. While they could mooch off the food, they couldn’t bring back the vibe. "Where does the energy come from? It’s all about daily life—having smoke from cooking fires, bedding aired out, and the sound of reading. Just the sound of an abacus clicking won’t do; it’s tough to hold onto wealth in this world without a bit of warmth to gather people at home."

Pei Qian was at a loss. Old Chef was indeed particular about his rules, and even if she couldn't argue with him, she decided to take her little guardian, Xiaomi, and head to a nearby street shop to buy some wild game and vegetables. Meanwhile, Shi Rou, feeling guilty and scared, thought that Zhu Lian was subtly criticizing her. After all, she hadn’t been able to help with the shop’s finances or maintain its good fortune. She secretly took out some of her own money and slipped it to Pei Qian. Pei Qian initially protested, saying it would be more appropriate to charge it to the shop's account, but before Shi Rou could take the money back, Pei Qian stuffed a bag of coins into her sleeve, stomped her foot, and complained, "Shi Rou, you’re really being too formal. Let this be the last time!" Then she whisked Xiaomi away, calling out cheerfully as they disappeared in an instant.

The town had now become the county seat of Huaihuang County, with bustling streets and numerous shops. Many began selling antiques, most of which were looked down upon by the Bull Horn Mountain’s Baozi Zhai, but if they sold even one, it could fetch several pieces of heavenly currency, enough to buy a house in the new county. In truth, the grass-roots shop in Qilong Alley was quite famous now; the items on display were expensive but genuine, so not many people bought them, although plenty came to look.

Countless scholars from the Great Li dynasty visited the town, paying respects at the Old Porcelain Mountain and the Immortal Tomb at the Literary and Martial Temple, exploring the many peaks where immortals were said to reside, visiting the Piyun Mountain and the Lin Deer Academy. Those who rode the immortal ferries down from Bull Horn Mountain were often students traveling to learn, flipping their sightseeing routes: the peach trees in Tao Ye Alley, the iron chain well near Xinghua Alley, the New Year’s shop selling pastries and dried fruits, the grass-roots shop that seemed to sell miscellaneous goods yet had its roots in the immortal realm, and the new academy established by the Chen family at Longwei Creek. These places were often must-visit spots for outsiders.

The little town bustled with activity, full of people coming and going.

Zhu Lian went to the kitchen, but found the water tank empty. He grabbed a carrying pole and balanced two buckets on his shoulders. Nowadays, fetching water from the iron chain well was no longer possible as it had been sealed off. The Great Li court had drilled several new wells in the town to prevent the common folk from having trouble getting water. However, the older locals often lamented that the taste was off, saying it couldn’t compare to the sweet water from the locked Dragon Well. Life had to go on, and while they didn’t mind complaining, the old folks missed the shade of the old locust tree, which had once provided respite from the sun. Yet, the children of the new generation, with their snotty faces and split trousers, seemed to be living carefree and joyful lives.

With the New Year’s shop momentarily empty, Shi Rou sat alone behind the counter, feeling a bit out of place. She pondered what groceries Pei Qian would bring back and imagined Zhu Lian later tying on an apron, wielding a spatula in the kitchen, which made her chuckle. Glancing out at the evening glow, it felt as if the day was slowly returning home after a long day’s work.

Next door, the grass-roots shop under the auspices of Falling Fortune Mountain was doing much better than her own shop, which seemed more cluttered and complicated despite the appearance of thicker account books. Selling even one item there equaled years of profit for the New Year’s shop. The blind old Daoist, Jia Sheng, had become less visible lately, having hit a bottleneck in his cultivation. He entrusted the shop's business to his two disciples: the taciturn, limping Zhao Denggao and the clever, sprightly Tian Jiu'er.

Jia Sheng spent more than half the year cultivating at the newly acquired Huanghu Mountain, a dependency of Falling Fortune Mountain, and paid little attention to worldly affairs.

Most Daoists were like this.

Ordinary people spent half their lives in bed, while Qi practitioners spent the majority of their lives in meditation, away from the world and severing ties with mundane matters. What they called "descending the mountain for experience" was merely a chance to test their resolve and cultivate their Dao heart. As Zhu Lian once casually mentioned to Pei Qian, cultivating on the mountain was fundamentally about probing the heavenly heart with one’s own heart, merely sitting in stillness. While it could yield some results, it was exceedingly difficult to achieve great success, which is why there was the saying, “In stillness, one thinks of action,” prompting some to actively engage with the world.

These immortals, having distanced themselves from human affairs, were accustomed to the mountain winds and the falling pine nuts. According to Zhu Lian, what of their hearts? Not much. It was merely a fist-sized matter, with varying realms, and as for the journey of the heart, it was long. Time on the mountain, spanning hundreds of years, was unlikely to surpass the short lives of ordinary folk down below in terms of distance traveled. The length of the heart’s journey depended on interactions with people. After all, there were fewer people on the mountain.

Shi Rou thought there was some merit in this line of reasoning, even if it seemed a bit off.

As for their young mountain lord, he was quite the outlier, never idle. He left such a large family business unattended, spending more time wandering outside than enjoying a life of luxury and cultivation on his own mountain.

It was said that the reason why that well-watered mountain could be acquired was due to Chen Lingjun’s significant contributions. The deal between Falling Fortune Mountain and Huanghu Mountain was made with mutual agreement, with the Dragon Prefecture’s governor’s office, along with the Ministry of Rites and the Ministry of Revenue, recording it all. Huanghu Mountain quietly became an asset under the young mountain lord’s name. Shi Rou felt distant from the old Daoist Jia, who was so consumed with ambitions of acquiring the mountain, thinking he was too much of a money-grubber. 

The geomancy of Huanghu Mountain was no simple matter; was it something that Jia Sheng could just covet?

After they became nominal deities of Falling Fortune Mountain, Jia Sheng had transformed into two different people. Previously, he was overly polite to Shi Rou, making small talk even when there was nothing to discuss, and would linger around for a long time to subtly get close. However, ever since the three of them were recognized as nominal deities, he hadn’t once visited the New Year’s shop. Shi Rou understood; he was putting on airs, and though she thought about going to the next door to say a few encouraging words, she stubbornly refused.

In the past, preoccupied with fear and worry, she hadn’t given much thought to the past few years of peace, but now she was starting to reflect on it.

The young mountain lord’s ability to purchase mountain land was truly astute, always managing to profit significantly, and he never flaunted his wealth. A poor youth from Mud Bottle Alley, who had never attended school, had never shown any desire to boast after becoming successful, which was indeed rare. However, to say he was stingy was far from the truth; even Shi Rou, who contributed little, found him to be quite generous. The mountain heads he acquired were all at extremely low prices. Moreover, Huanghu Mountain had several ready-made immortal residences, all handed over to the ancestral hall of Falling Fortune Mountain. The same went for Zhu Sha Mountain, and Bull Horn Mountain even had a ready-made ferry landing, alongside the shops built with a significant amount of heavenly currency from Baozi Zhai, all falling into the hands of Falling Fortune Mountain.

As Zhu Lian returned from drawing water, Pei Qian and Xiaomi, each carrying a bamboo basket, arrived right behind him.

Xiaomi helped start the fire, puffing her cheeks as she handled the bellows, while Pei Qian selected vegetables and teased Xiaomi to be careful not to blow the whole stove away. Xiaomi laughed, inhaling a mouthful of ashes, and Pei Qian laughed heartily, while Xiaomi giggled, saying she almost ate enough to be full. The old chef tied on his apron, carefully washed the cutting board with well water, and sharpened the cleaver, ready to show off his skills.

Shi Rou wanted to help but found herself unable to contribute, so she stood at the kitchen door, feeling somewhat unnecessary yet unwilling to leave, so she just remained there like a guardian.

In truth, Shi Rou didn’t feel embarrassed; she had always been like this. Watching the lively atmosphere in the kitchen, it felt as if the festive spirit of the New Year had already arrived, even if the holiday wasn’t quite here yet.

Zhu Lian sliced the vegetables with a knife, his movements fluid and graceful, pleasing to the eye. 

Pei Qian, standing nearby, praised, "What great knife skills! Old chef, why don’t you use your knife in a duel?"

Without raising his head, Zhu Lian chuckled, “A kitchen knife? If one must carry a weapon, wouldn’t it be more impressive to wield a sword on a journey?”

Pei Qian replied helplessly, “I find it strange; you certainly weren’t handsome when you were young, so where do all these fancy ideas come from?”

Zhu Lian remarked, “Exactly because I wasn’t handsome, I had to fuss about it; otherwise, what's the point? If I didn’t care, I’d be just another broken pot, and who would want to marry me then?”

Pei Qian inquired, “So, have you found someone or not? With our status in the martial world so far apart, and your reputation not being that great, I haven’t heard much about your exploits.”

Zhu Lian casually mentioned, “The Golden Cake with Jujube Paste, you’ve certainly heard about it in the capital of the South Garden Kingdom, right?”

Pei Qian’s eyes widened as she whispered, “Walls have ears! You’re such an old hand at this! How can you be so careless? I regret bringing up the matter of that kingdom and capital; you had already made a mistake, and now you’re making it worse."

Zhu Lian nodded with a smile, “You’re right; I’ll be more careful in the future.”

Pei Qian asked, “Do you know if Master Shizi and Cao Muto will dare to return this year?”

Zhu Lian shook his head, “Doubtful. Scholars who reach that Bosa Continent act like women visiting the Upside-Down Mountain; they just go for a stroll.”

Pei Qian then asked, “So who will write the Spring Festival couplets this year? Master’s ancestral home, Falling Fortune Mountain, the Ancestral Hall at Jisi Peak, the Bamboo Pavilion, and all those other mountain peaks—it seems like there’s a lot to write!”

Zhu Lian laughed, “If you can’t manage it, both I and Brother Dafu can help.”

Pei Qian frowned, “If you help, old chef, I might consider it, but what about Zheng Dafu’s calligraphy? Can anyone even read it? I'm worried his characters are so ominous that they’ll scare off the spirits and demons, but I don’t want our good fortune to be scared away too.”

Zhu Lian assured her, “Brother Dafu is quite talented at heart; aside from chess, his writing and knowledge are both commendable.”

Then Zhu Lian suddenly said, “Forget it; let’s not have Brother Dafu help after all.”

Pei Qian laughed.

Sitting on the little stool by the stove, Xiaomi had been holding the bamboo bellows, her face full of confusion. Pei Qian, sitting beside her, explained softly, “Complimenting someone’s talents is actually a way of calling them ugly.”

Xiaomi glanced at the old chef, then at Shi Rou, thought about Zheng Dafu’s appearance, and grinned widely. In Falling Fortune Mountain’s household, it seemed only Wei Shanjun's looks were somewhat fitting for the mountain scenery.

Zhu Lian suggested that Shi Rou should sauté a couple of simple dishes as well.

Shi Rou was hesitant but didn’t dare refuse, so Zhu Lian adjusted his apron and settled at the kitchen door.

After finishing her sunflower seeds, Pei Qian started counting with her fingers, “My master, Wei Shanjun, the big white goose, and the reverend Zhou Fei—there are actually quite a few good-looking people at Falling Fortune Mountain.”

Xiaomi put her hand over her mouth and leaned close to Pei Qian’s ear, whispering, “The mountain sects can actually make money selling illusions, but it’s been said that the easiest money in the world is made from the immortal treasures.”

Pei Qian promptly grabbed Xiaomi’s ear, “What are you thinking? My master can’t make that kind of money!”

Xiaomi quickly corrected herself, “He can’t, absolutely can’t!”

Pei Qian released her and grinned, “But the big white goose, Wei Shanjun, and Zhou Fei could sell their good looks to make some money; who knows, they might actually bring in a fortune.”

Xiaomi hurriedly mimicked the motions of flipping through a book.

Pei Qian nodded, “Great! We can note that down in the accounts.”

Zhu Lian chuckled, “This is a good idea; next time when we discuss matters at the Ancestral Hall, we can bring it up.”

Pei Qian, focusing her voice, spoke to the old chef, “At the Great Sword Qi Great Wall, I saw a sword immortal named Mi Yu, who looked decent but was a bit foolish. When he gazed at the scenery, the mountains were filled with flowers, and he was so distracted he nearly got sliced by our Master and the big white goose when he provoked us. He could actually make up for his mistake by coming to Falling Fortune Mountain as the chief errand disciple, joining the big white goose and the others to help the mountain earn enough money to return home.”

Zhu Lian nodded, “Falling Fortune Mountain indeed needs a sword immortal to uphold its honor, even if it’s just for show.”

Then Zhu Lian suddenly burst out laughing, not explaining the reason to Pei Qian and Xiaomi.

Cui Dongshan had reached the fifth realm.

Wei Ban, the younger brother, was also at the fifth realm, and the lord of North Yu Mountain.

Reverend Zhou Fei, or Jiang Shangzhen, was even more of an immortal, now the sect master of the Jade Guizong.

If they added Mi Yu, the sword immortal of the Jade Purity realm...

These four were all individuals who wouldn’t mind getting their hands dirty, earning the kind of celestial riches that came from illusions.

Zhu Lian leaned back, glancing at the old spring festival couplets hanging in the main hall, weathered from wind and rain after a year of guarding the entrance. They were due for a change soon.

Zhu Lian explained, “The way we invite spring couplets in my hometown is a bit different. There’s a two-part invitation: one is during the Spring Festival when we put up the spring couplets, and the other is the day before the second of February, when we take them down. They then go for a walk in the incense burner, completing their purpose. According to old sayings, these spring couplets serve as offerings for the deities, and after that, we have to write and invite them again to protect the feng shui of every household. The character ‘Fu’ (福) should be pasted inside the house, not on the front door. It’s said that good fortune reaches the doorstep but doesn’t enter; some families, with their ancestors’ virtuous deeds and righteous family traditions, manage to keep it, while others simply can’t, so it’s best to paste it inside.”

Pei Qian rolled her eyes, “I’ve been wandering the martial world from a young age, making my home wherever I go, so what do I know about these rituals?”

At this point, Pei Qian whispered to Xiaomi, “It’s really just that we don’t even have a place to stay.”

Xiaomi nodded vigorously, “That’s how it is! Wandering! I like that word; it’s nice. I’m also a little wanderer who enjoys roaming around the Mute Lake.”

Xiaomi raised both hands, gesturing as if she were wandering around.

Pei Qian loved chatting with Xiaomi because she could talk about childhood stories without fear of embarrassment, as Xiaomi didn’t even recognize the difference between wealth and poverty.

Pei Qian pressed down on Xiaomi’s head, giving it a playful shake.

Zhu Lian remarked, “Strength doesn’t lie in weight.”

Pei Qian asked, “Is there a saying about that?”

Zhu Lian chuckled, “Do you think I was too rough with that Water Goddess of Yu Ye River?”

Pei Qian nodded, “It wasn’t exactly gentle.”

Zhu Lian then questioned, “Then what was the punch for?”

Pei Qian thought for a moment before replying, “To reason with her, earn money, and save her.”

Nobody understood Sister Xiu like Pei Qian did.

Zhu Lian further asked, “Where does the trouble lie?”

Pei Qian answered, “As a water deity, being in the martial realm, her conduct isn’t proper; she’s focused solely on making connections with heroes and immortals, neglecting the feng shui and the people in her territory.”

Zhu Lian nodded, “Very good. You could venture out into the martial world on your own now.”

Pei Qian rolled her eyes, “Without Master’s permission, I won’t leave the mountain!”

Xiaomi chimed in, “The outside martial world can be very dangerous!”

Soon after, they set the dishes on the table, not too lavish, but there was plenty of rice.

When Pei Qian was at the table, the main seat had to be left empty; during festivals, they even had to set up bowls and chopsticks there.

As the four were about to start eating, Ruan Xiu stepped from the front of the New Year’s shop into the backyard, standing at the threshold and saying, “Dinner is ready!”

Pei Qian stood up, exclaiming, “Haha, better late than never! Sister Xiu, come join us; I’ll share a stool with you!”

Ruan Xiu smiled, “Sure!”

Shi Rou quickly got up, grabbed some bowls and chopsticks, and sat with Xiaomi.

Xiaomi filled Ruan Xiu's bowl with a generous serving of rice, packing it tightly with the rice scoop, and brought it to the table.

Ruan Xiu patted the little girl’s head, sat down, picked up her chopsticks, and noticing everyone else had yet to start, smiled, “Let’s eat!”

Pei Qian hesitated, glancing toward the front of the New Year’s shop.

There stood the Water Goddess of Yu Ye River, who appeared anxious and unstable.

Regarding the apology, the Water Palace had provided one, but it wasn’t her personally visiting Falling Fortune Mountain; rather, it was the second-in-command from the Water Palace who came with a treasured artifact. She believed that was sufficient sincerity.

As for the old man who claimed to have a way to save her, she hadn’t taken it seriously at all.

Not only that, she had already written a secret missive intended for the Minister of Rites.

The Water Palace had a water monster from the Huangting Kingdom, which had brazenly summoned a Dragon King’s basket, attempting to suppress the shrine of the Water Goddess of Yu Ye River, intimidating the common folk, nearly causing a tragedy where the entire shrine’s populace would have perished.

Zhu Lian, managing Falling Fortune Mountain, had recklessly injured a local water deity who had contributed to the community.

Before sending that missive, she had advised her colleague from the Water God of the Danjiang River to bear the storm for a while; for their sake, it was best to maintain peace.

But how could she take it to heart? Besides, that colleague, a newly appointed deity with a godly status, had never earned her respect.

As for the convoluted backstory, she was an outsider to it all.

Ruan Xiu came from the Longquan Sword Sect, the famous daughter of Saint Ruan Qiong, but would she truly be willing to clash with the entire water laws of the Great Li for such matters?

Before the impending accident, everything had its reasoning.

Once she was detained in this little town at Qilong Alley, the Water Goddess of Yu Ye River felt like crying without tears.

That table of people felt like a harmonious family, eating their homemade meal.

The Water Goddess seemed to hold an empty bowl of cold rice, unable to even partake in the meal.

After finishing the meal, aside from Shi Rou cleaning the dishes, everyone else moved to the shop.

Ruan Xiu was choosing pastries.

Pei Qian stood behind the counter with Xiaomi, both standing on a little stool; otherwise, Xiaomi was too short to see anything.

Zhu Lian sat on a long bench, smiling as he spoke, “In street fights, a punch lands on whom, it hurts. In dueling with immortals, whoever takes a hit from a magical treasure—fundamentally, the principle is the same. If we really want to argue about it, there’s no distinction between right or wrong; wealth and status don’t matter. Do you understand, Lady Water Goddess?”

The Water Goddess nodded.

She didn’t truly understand, and even if she did, she wouldn’t accept it. However, given the circumstances, what other choice did she have?

If that Xiaomi wasn’t recognized as a disciple of Falling Fortune Mountain, if Falling Fortune Mountain hadn’t had ‘her’ step in to teach her a lesson, would things have come to this?

In the end, both sides were just travelers, exerting pressure on one another.

Ruan Xiu, with her back to everyone, frowned.

Zhu Lian smiled, “Pei Qian, take Xiaomi to the back.”

Pei Qian responded, “Oh!” and patted Xiaomi’s head.

Immediately, the Water Goddess knelt on the ground, facing the counter, saying, “I was wrong.”

Pei Qian scratched her head, exasperated, “Why does it have to be so complicated? It’s really just a matter of sincerely admitting a mistake! How is that so hard? How can you think that just because you’ve gone through the motions of courtesy, that everything is fine?”

Then Pei Qian lay her head down on the table, “I don’t like this. It’s all so simple—if that official from the Water Palace just apologized to Xiaomi and said sorry, wouldn’t that suffice? Yet the old woman and the official are calculating so many things—whether they admit their mistakes or not, each with their own malicious intentions, like a pile of black water weeds scaring people. What’s that all about?”

Zhu Lian chuckled, “You’re wrong; that’s truly the most challenging part for us. If others saw or heard this, they’d think we’re being unreasonable, making a big fuss over nothing, being aggressive. And what would make you angrier is that these outsiders’ empathy isn’t entirely a bad thing; on the contrary, it’s the baseline that keeps the world from becoming too terrible.”

Pei Qian felt a headache coming on, grumbling, “But we can’t just blow this out of proportion; if we killed a Water Goddess, how would outsiders view Falling Fortune Mountain? You’ve said it before; outsiders would side with Yu Ye River. Besides, I think even if this Water Goddess doesn’t admit her mistakes, it wouldn’t be necessary to kill her. If Master were here, how would he handle it?”

Zhu Lian thought for a moment and replied, “Perhaps the young master could sort out the entire Water Palace of Yu Ye River from top to bottom, inside and out. Right and wrong, it’s neither more nor less.”

However, there were some matters Zhu Lian chose not to share with Pei Qian, such as the connections entangled with the Qingfeng City Xu family, Zhengyang Mountain, and even further implications.

Dazed, Xiaomi had quietly bent her knees, hiding her head behind the counter.

“I know nothing; if I’m not in the shop, no one can see me…”

Zhu Lian wasn’t in a hurry.

All this could help Pei Qian cultivate her heart.

Otherwise, Zhu Lian would have already moved along with Miss Ruan’s actions.

Just like Pei Qian understood in her heart, the true nemesis of the Yu Ye River Water Palace was actually her sister Xiu.

It was possible she would either shatter the Water Goddess’s golden body or refine the entire Yu Ye River, leaving only the Water Goddess alive. If she thought that all matters, big or small, weren’t an issue, then she could use her logic to negotiate with the Great Li court.

Replacing her with a more responsible Water Deity would be quite simple for the current Great Li court.

As for some possibilities, ordinary people wouldn’t think of them, such as a little spirit being taken away, leading to the destruction of a mountain. As long as the incident hadn’t occurred, it wouldn’t be a consideration. Discussing hearts and matters has always been a difficult balance.

Pei Qian tentatively asked, “Old chef, how about we just let it go? I can’t figure it out, and I’ll ask Master when he returns.”

Zhu Lian smiled and nodded, looking at Ruan Xiu.

Ruan Xiu pinched a piece of peach blossom cake and popped it in her mouth, turning her head to mumble, “I’m easy-going.”

Ruan Xiu glanced at the kneeling Water Goddess, “Aren’t you leaving?”

The Water Goddess hurriedly fled.

She was furious at the Xu family of Qingfeng City, and even more so at the subordinate official who had provoked the trouble.

As for Falling Fortune Mountain, she didn’t dare harbor any resentment.

And towards that “Ruan Xiu,” she didn’t even dare to think.

Zhu Lian said to Pei Qian, “Cultivation isn’t about being unreasonable; it’s about better articulating reason. Within our capabilities, we should help the weak clarify their reasoning. There’s a world of difference between that and having a high realm of cultivation, where one’s fists become the reasoning.”

Then Zhu Lian added with a smile, “Just take your time; every act of kindness may vary in size, but kindness itself is kindness, without distinction.”

Ruan Xiu continued to select pastries, saying, “It’s really not that complicated.”

Pei Qian asked, “Sister Xiu, what do you mean?”

Ruan Xiu replied, “Just focus on your cultivation.”

Zhu Lian sighed in relief; he was genuinely afraid this young lady might say something shocking or unconventional.

Ruan Xiu picked up a piece of pastry, smiling, “Fresh pastries are indeed delicious.”

Pei Qian looked troubled, “I’m cultivating at a turtle’s pace.”

Xiaomi peeked out, saying, “Actually, turtles swim quickly in the water and can run on land; they’re quite fast! I’ve chased after them many times at Mute Lake!”

Pei Qian pressed her hand down on Xiaomi’s head, “What’s that about?”

Xiaomi shook her head and suddenly brought up a question she often thought about but forgot, “Why do some people like to bully others?”

Zhu Lian couldn’t help but chuckle. 

This question was indeed difficult to answer.

Ruan Xiu replied, “When people are hungry, they consume everything.”

Xiaomi laughed heartily, “Sister Xiu is great; you only like eating pastries!”

Zhu Lian remained silent.

Pei Qian blinked.

Ruan Xiu smiled. 

*(End of Chapter)*

 **Chapter 757: A Blank Sheet for Cui Dongshan (Part Two)**

A master and a maid, two riders journeyed south through the wind and snow.

Their destination was the southernmost point of the Treasure Bottle Continent, the Old Dragon City. However, their route was anything but straightforward; they detoured multiple times, visiting the Fox Kingdom of the Xu family in Clear Wind City, passing through the Stone Hair Kingdom, and stopping by the Book Slip Lake.

The young man sat atop his horse, dozing off. The maid, riding behind him, dared not ride alongside, keeping a respectful distance.

In Mud Bottle Alley, Song Jixin had a maid following him, and in Apricot Blossom Alley, this fellow, Ma Ku Xuan, also learned from him and took on a maid, naming her Shudian.

Behind them, Shudian likely couldn’t fathom the true reason she was still alive; it was simply because of this arrangement.

On their journey south, they encountered no more ambushes or assassinations, as those willing to protect her had all died.

The state of affairs on the Treasure Bottle Continent had gradually shifted from chaos to stability. However, because Ma Ku Xuan never took fairy boats and preferred to travel on horseback, he avoided the main roads, inevitably crossing paths with various beings—lost mountain dwellers, strange creatures, and spirits of the land who trembled at the thought of being marked as unclean. Many were exiled nobles, lamenting their lost kingdoms, while others, suddenly risen to power, arrogantly boasted about how great their Da Li was.

Ma Ku Xuan killed without hesitation, guided solely by his whims.

Those of higher realms whom he found displeasing would be slain; those of lower realms would meet the same fate. Even if one were not a cultivator, encountering Ma Ku Xuan would spell doom.

Yet Shudian still wondered why this heavily murderous prodigy could survive on the road, engaging in long conversations with woodcutters and farmers when he felt in good spirits.

Not long ago, in the Stone Hair Kingdom, Ma Ku Xuan had dispatched a group of elite young nobles who had come to admire the snow-capped mountains. They had seen the beautiful Shudian and mistakenly thought that Ma Ku Xuan and his maid, leading their horses, were nobility from their own Stone Hair Kingdom. All of them were born into the influential families of the capital, and with twisted thoughts, they approached her. The Stone Hair Kingdom had been ravaged by war, making it common for ordinary people to face unfortunate accidents when they traveled.

Ma Ku Xuan mounted his horse and presented Shudian with two choices: either strip naked and submit to their humiliation or demonstrate the demeanor of a fairy cultivator and slaughter the group of young lords.

Shudian’s face turned pale, even whiter than the snow.

Ma Ku Xuan, impatient, flicked his fingers, sending one of the young lords plummeting off a cliff. The sound of his scream was chilling, but the rest followed suit, all tumbling down, some even met their end crashing into the rocks. During this chaos, a local earth deity rushed out to plead for mercy for the noble youths, but he too was struck down by Ma Ku Xuan with a single slap. The balance of fate momentarily shifted towards Ma Ku Xuan, causing the deity to retreat.

In the end, Shudian was forced to suppress her cultivation level, bound by ropes, and dragged behind Ma Ku Xuan as they descended the mountain.

When they reached the foot of the mountain, Ma Ku Xuan finally released his magical restraint. Although Shudian was a cultivator and not seriously harmed, she was left in disarray, dazed and sitting in the snow.

It seemed Ma Ku Xuan had forgotten about the maid entirely, as he rode off alone.

After a long hesitation, Shudian, still battered by the wind and snow, mounted her horse and followed him.

At that moment, Ma Ku Xuan simply remarked with a laugh, “My killing spree is real, but to kill the innocent would be a misunderstanding.”

Shudian, emboldened by a sudden surge of courage, cried out, “You’ve killed so many! Many of them didn’t deserve death!”

Ma Ku Xuan chuckled, “The truly innocent who die aren’t as fortunate as you; they can’t even live to raise their voices.”

Finally, Ma Ku Xuan gazed at the sky and smiled, “In this manner of killing, heaven must thank me.”

Shudian sat slumped on her horse, utterly exhausted, mumbling, “You’re a madman, a madman.”

Ma Ku Xuan yawned and continued his leisurely ride.

Shudian silently told herself not to die, absolutely not to die. She had to see this madman; surely, someone who committed so many wrongs would face heavenly retribution!

Yet she soon noticed that this madman seemed to be in a good mood.

In fact, after passing Book Slip Lake, Ma Ku Xuan appeared even more cheerful.

In the southern mountains of Book Slip Lake, where various rogue cultivators gathered, Ma Ku Xuan had the leisure to visit a mountain peak as a guest. Sitting in the main seat, he asked a few questions and became even happier.

That guy from Mud Bottle Alley had been here for nearly three years, and apparently, things hadn’t been going well for him.

But Ma Ku Xuan was in high spirits.

He scooped up a snowball and turned to toss it at Shudian’s head. She didn’t dare dodge, and the snowball burst, scattering snowflakes and slightly obscuring her vision.

Stretching lazily, Ma Ku Xuan laughed, “Back in that little town, I’ve never played in a snowball fight. Well, I have, but I often got hit for no reason. Seeing them happy made me happy too.”

Thinking of that little town, that Pearl Cave, Shudian felt a chill run down her spine.

Everything today was a consequence of that journey.

Ma Ku Xuan waved, signaling her to follow.

He said, “During the opening of the Pearl Cave, you and your group are the last chosen. Don’t you have any thoughts about it?”

Ma Ku Xuan continued talking to himself, “You probably didn’t think about it; you just go with the flow, never considering the shore.”

Shudian replied, “I have thought about it.”

Ma Ku Xuan turned his head, grinning, “Oh? So you do have some brains?”

She said, “Since you hold such lofty ambitions and treat me so poorly, what’s the point?”

Ma Ku Xuan couldn’t be bothered to answer such questions. Instead, he asked, “Do you remember the ones who entered the Pearl Cave before you?”

Shudian fell silent.

Ma Ku Xuan extended his hands, preparing to form another snowball, and continued speaking, “The last time the Da Li court opened its doors to guests, the earliest group to reach the little town and enter the Pearl Cave to seek treasures—how simple could that be? You lot who arrived later are also the carefully selected ones by the former Empress Song of Da Li and the Xiu Hu. You’re not useless, of course, except for you.”

“Speaking of which, you are utterly useless, but the Iron Tide cavalry you’re connected to is somewhat useful to Da Li.”

Ma Ku Xuan shook his head, “Unfortunately, by a stroke of bad luck, they ran into me.”

Shudian cried out in despair, “You said one person does the work, one person bears the blame. You also made the first mistake by deliberately acting against me, ruining my cultivation. Even if I made a grave mistake afterward, why didn’t you just kill me? Why unleash such a massacre?”

Ma Ku Xuan had already turned his thoughts elsewhere. After a moment, he asked, “What did you say just now?”

Shudian fell silent again.

Ma Ku Xuan didn’t mind. If her heart was completely shattered, it wouldn’t be fun anymore.

Suddenly, he asked, “How about I take on a disciple who will definitely like you and let him help you take revenge?”

Shudian was taken aback.

Ma Ku Xuan seemed excited, “What do you think? I promise he won’t kill you before he comes for me, and afterward, he won’t kill you either. You just have to watch the show. I’ll only remind you of one thing: don’t let him get too close, and don’t pretend to fall in love with him. I don’t care about that—it’s just that he might get tired of you, turn the tables, and kill you to pledge his loyalty to me. Wouldn’t that be disgusting?”

Shudian stared at this madman.

Cultivators were supposed to be heartless and indifferent.

But how many could be as extreme as the man before her?

Ma Ku Xuan pouted, “Whenever you figure it out, just speak to me. I’ll surely grant your wish.”

He weighed the snowball in his hand, gazing into the distance where snowflakes danced, the path ahead obscured, and the world was bleak.

Ma Ku Xuan’s thoughts drifted far away.

Years ago, when he had departed for Da Sui, he had taken out three items: a bowl of water, a stone, and a twig.

He had half-jokingly told his teacher and the little Bottle that a mortal scholar needed to undergo countless transformations, silently transitioning through life and death many times.

The stone represented the human body, akin to a mountain, enduring the elements, bearing all things—it was a state of relative stillness and flow.

The water in the bowl symbolized the flow of thoughts. The twig was the fundamental thread, the rules governing the movement of the Great Way.

Over these years, Ma Ku Xuan had been contesting himself in these matters.

However, merely grappling with the general concepts of emotions and desires was far from sufficient.

The first porcelain figure he created, the boy Cui Ci, who was often seen with Li Xisheng, was quite adept at basic calculations. Yet when it came to “emotion,” it remained weak. In simple terms, the thread was too fragile, making it difficult for him to feel a sense of belonging. Additionally, confined by his simplistic physical and spiritual existence, the bottleneck of the Great Way was too significant; even forming a golden core was a luxury.

But this “little brother Gao” in front of him had more thoughts and a clearer and stronger thread, enabling him not only to play chess but also to cultivate to the bottleneck of the Nascent Soul realm. He would also be able to compose poetry and create everything related to emotions, genuinely believing himself to be a true “human.” There was no such thing as a purely “immovable silence” in the world; everything was pieced together from countless tiny entities, forming visible realities. Every minuscule event weaves into a dreamlike life. Books would yellow, mountains would rise and fall, plants would flourish or wither, and people would live, age, fall ill, and die.

Ma Ku Xuan lightly tapped the end of his brush against the empty sheet of paper before him, staring at it intently.

Years ago, during his travels in Da Sui, he had taken out those three items: a bowl of water, a stone, and a twig. 

Moreover, he had half-jokingly remarked to his teacher and the little Bottle about how many times a mundane scholar needed to be reborn, transitioning through life and death silently.

The stone represented the human body, akin to a mountain, weathering the storm and bearing all things. It was a state of relative stillness and flow.

The water in the bowl symbolized the flow of thought. The twig represented the fundamental thread, the rules governing the Great Way’s movement.

Over the years, Ma Ku Xuan had been grappling with these concepts within himself.

Yet merely grappling with the general ideas of emotions and desires was far from being enough.

The first porcelain figure he crafted, the boy Cui Ci, who had been accompanying Li Xisheng, was already adept at basic calculations. However, when it came to “emotion,” he remained quite thin. In simple terms, the thread was fundamentally too fragile, making it hard for him to have a sense of belonging, and limited by his simple body and soul, the bottleneck of the Great Way was too large; forming a golden core was a luxury.

But the “little brother Gao” before him had more thoughts; his threads were clearer and firmer. In the future, not only would he be able to play chess and cultivate up to the bottleneck of the Nascent Soul, but he would also be able to compose poetry and create everything related to emotions, genuinely believing he was a true “human.” 

In this world, there was no such thing as a purely “motionless calm.” Everything was pieced together, built from countless minuscule entities into visible realities. Every tiny occurrence formed a life that felt dreamlike. Books would yellow, mountains would rise and fall, plants would grow or wither, and people would live, age, fall ill, and die.

Ma Ku Xuan continued tapping the end of his brush against the blank sheet, lost in thought. 

After all, during his travels through Da Sui, he had once taken out three items: a bowl of water, a stone, and a twig.

He had half-jokingly mentioned to his teacher and the little Bottle how many rebirths a mundane scholar must undergo, the silent transitions through life and death countless times.

The stone represented the human body, akin to a mountain, enduring the elements and bearing all things. It was essentially a relative state of stillness and flow.

The water in the bowl symbolized the flow of thought. The twig represented the fundamental thread, the rules governing the operation of the Great Way.

Over the years, Ma Ku Xuan had been contesting with these concepts.

However, merely grappling with the general concepts of emotions and desires was far from sufficient.

The first porcelain figure he crafted, the boy Cui Ci, who was often seen with Li Xisheng, was already proficient in basic calculations. Yet, when it came to “emotion,” it remained quite thin. In simple terms, the thread was fundamentally too fragile, making it hard for him to feel a sense of belonging. Moreover, confined by his simple physical and spiritual existence, the bottleneck of the Great Way was too significant; even forming a golden core was a luxury.

But right now, this “little brother Gao” was full of thoughts, with threads that were clearer and stronger. In the future, not only would he be able to play chess, but he could cultivate to the Nascent Soul bottleneck. He would also be able to compose poetry and create everything related to emotions, genuinely believing himself to be a true “human.” 

In the world, there was no such thing as a purely “immovable silence”; everything was pieced together from countless tiny entities, forming visible realities. Tiny events wove into a dreamlike life. Books would yellow, mountains would rise and fall, plants would flourish or wither, and people would live, age, fall ill, and die.

Ma Ku Xuan quietly sighed, feeling troubled.

He beckoned to little brother Gao, encouraging the child to run around the room carrying things.

With a swift flail of his snow-white sleeves, he affectionately ruffled the child’s hair, mimicking the older sister, and cheerfully exclaimed, “Little brother, why are you so obedient?”

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 758: Waiting for Someone

In the southeastern region of Baoping Continent, a young man dressed in white paused in a deep mountain forest. Before him lay the dry riverbed of Yantai River, long abandoned and marked by clear signs of stone extraction from years past. It wasn’t a renowned quarry, but the creek was dry, and Cui Dongshan leaped into the riverbed, vigorously digging through stones and mud. Finally, he unearthed a slab of stone, just enough to make a passable inkstone. Tapping it lightly with his fingers and listening closely, he found the sound quality surprisingly good. He brushed off the dirt, growing more fond of it with each glance—such serendipitous finds were the most delightful, treasures that money could not buy. 

Cui Dongshan exhaled softly, smoothing out the stone's patterns and tiny crevices with his breath. After rubbing it against his cheek for a while, the stone's texture became even more exquisite in his hands. Meanwhile, a child squatted on the bank, his gaze blank, seemingly unable to comprehend what Cui Dongshan was doing. As Cui Dongshan climbed ashore, he accidentally dropped the inkstone, which landed squarely on the child’s head. Ultimately, Cui Dongshan emerged from the river, instructing the child to walk while balancing the stone on his head, forbidding him from using his hands for support.

Looking back at the riverbed, Cui Dongshan remarked, “Diving into the water and coming up on shore—truly a hero’s feat.”

He wandered aimlessly until nightfall, spending the night in a desolate graveyard. Lying on the ground, he used a thin blade of grass to carve an inscription onto the inkstone.

Then a young scholar appeared, squatting beside him with a smile. “I’ve seen you before; not bad, you’re quite the promising one. My senior brother might actually take a liking to you, willing to accept you as his disciple.”

Cui Dongshan, still holding the blade of grass, focused intently on the stone slab and asked, “You should thank me for helping you return to Baidi City. Aren’t you?”

The young scholar was none other than Liu Chicheng, who had previously visited Shujian Lake and Yunlou City.

Liu Chicheng chuckled, “I was supposed to stir up trouble in Baoping Continent, but now that I’m doing nothing, let’s call it even, shall we?”

Cui Dongshan scoffed, “You can forget that. You’ve been locked away for a thousand years; how do you expect to break out? You think I carefully selected you to help him escape by chance? Call it even? I might as well lock you back up and then we can talk about being even!”

Liu Chicheng plopped down, curious. “It’s been so long since I left Baidi City. How has your chess game been with my senior brother? Is his skill higher or lower than before?”

Cui Dongshan sat up, shook his sleeves, and wiped the inkstone with his arm. The inscription read: “Bathe in the sun and moon, both strong and spirited, defying the heavens.”
