Cui Dongshan asked, “Who was it that sent you to Baoping Continent for refuge back then?”

Liu Chicheng grinned, “That I cannot say. In this world, we must prioritize loyalty.”

Cui Dongshan nodded, tracing his fingers over the sixteen-character inscription, each stroke appearing like the riverbed itself, with golden streams flowing through it. “Impressive, truly impressive.”

Liu Chicheng immediately added, “A life-saving grace is a great righteousness. That name, I can share.”

On Baoping Continent, this young man was unmatched, and it had little to do with his realm.

It was all about intellect.

In the bamboo loft of Luopo Mountain.

After copying books today, Pei Qian went to the bottom of a small bamboo box at her feet, rummaging through a large stack of densely written volumes. She finally pulled out a blank book, shook it gently, and laid it on the table, preparing to keep accounts related to the Divine Mansion of Yuyue River. 

Zhou Milu dashed into the room, carrying a small golden yoke. Pei Qian quickly reached out to block her empty account book, frowning. “How reckless! This is a vital place in Luopo Mountain. You don’t even knock when you enter?”

Zhou Milu quickly turned and ran outside, knocking on the door. When Pei Qian called for her to come in, the girl hurriedly skipped over the threshold, facing her desk and whispering, “The old chef’s brother, Big Feng, went to Hongzhu Town and came back with a sack full of books. The expenses are quite hefty!”

Pei Qian nodded, “We’ll check the accounts soon. This is official business; if we hurt the old chef’s feelings, that won’t do.”

Zhou Milu tiptoed, stretching her neck to see what Pei Qian was doing. “What are you writing?”

Pei Qian waved her hand. “Stand at the door and guard. No one is allowed in except for Warm Tree.”

Zhou Milu responded with a “Oh,” but then suddenly leaned over the table, her slightly yellow brows knitted in thought, as if she wanted to say something.

Pei Qian asked, puzzled, “What’s wrong?”

Zhou Milu lowered her voice and said, “The little incense burner from the city god’s temple, we know him, right? He’s still a friend. He wants to take my previous position as the right guardian of Qilong Alley. What do you think?”

Pei Qian thought for a moment and shook her head. “Not a chance. Although I can decide the two guardian positions of Qilong Alley by myself, we can’t just agree because the little brat asked. Let’s put it on hold and see how he performs first.”

Zhou Milu sulked, having previously promised the other party.

Pei Qian sighed, “Alright, you can tell him I agree, but it’s a significant responsibility. He can’t neglect his duties and must report to me every month. As for any gifts, let’s skip that; he’s just a little pauper.”

Zhou Milu straightened up. “Understood!”

One rider left the capital of the Great Sui, heading south on a journey.

A young woman donned in red, with a narrow knife hanging at her waist and a silver sword-raising gourd.

She gazed up at the sea of clouds above.

In her childhood, a mere glance at the clouds would conjure thoughts that they were fairies dressed in beautiful garments, changing outfits like a parade.

Back then, it seemed every day brought a flurry of such whimsical ideas, akin to a rowdy bunch of mischievous little beings, too many to manage, too wild to contain.

Now, she took down the sword-raising gourd and took a sip.

Li Baoping felt a tinge of sadness.

“Little Master Uncle, after growing up, it seems I’ve lost those thoughts. They’ve all left without a word, never to return.”

After the dual sword cultivators exchanged insights, waves of demon forces began their northern migration to the battlefield.

This time, the commanding beasts of the army were the Lotus Blossom Master and the Golden Armored Deity.

This marked the first time two great demon kings had jointly presided over a military campaign on the battlefield.

The Lotus Blossom Master had refined half of a moon’s essence from the wild and chaotic realm. Previously, on the battlefield, he had a sparring match with Chen Chunan, the scholarly swordsman who journeyed along the Sword Qi Great Wall. No clear victor emerged, but it was evident that the Lotus Blossom Master suffered a slight disadvantage. This was due to the fact that neither side had exerted their full strength, or perhaps the battlefield’s complexity did not allow for such a display.

In the previous four battles, each had been solely managed by a single great demon: Bai Ying, the desiccated bone demon; Yang Zhi, the former master of the Fallen River; Huang Luan, who enjoyed refining structures to build celestial cities; and the bearded man responsible for the Sword Qi Great Wall, Liu Cha, who was both an enemy and ally of Ah Liang. Liu Cha, although less imposing than the others, observed the two sides’ formations from the rear, and after the battle concluded, selected a dozen young sword cultivators as his registered disciples.

Liu Cha’s first disciple, his only true successor, was the sword cultivator Zhu Qi.

These young sword cultivators, who seemed almost dreamlike, were still far from becoming Liu Cha’s direct disciples, facing two significant thresholds: first entering the sect, then entering the inner circle.

Once registered, if a disciple achieved success in their studies and passed the tests, they could be formally admitted. Only then could they enter the master’s inner circle, becoming a direct disciple and gaining access to their mentor’s teachings and lineage.

Even though the path ahead remained distant, the dozen or so of them were filled with excitement, forming a small hill of enthusiasm. 

After all, Liu Cha, the mountain-climbing swordsman, was the pinnacle of the sword path in the wild realm. To become his disciple, even if only temporarily registered, was a source of immense pride.

As for the closed-door disciples, their roles were just as significant as those of the first disciples. Often, the master entrusted them with their life’s work and knowledge, considering them worthy of rest once entrusted. The closed-door disciples were thus barred from outsiders, marking their importance.

Taking a master is akin to being reborn; selecting a disciple is akin to having a child, and for both parties, it is a momentous event.

Before the war broke out, Qi Shou had already entered the Nascent Soul realm, while Gao Ye Hou was on the verge of breaking through. Pang Yuanji, whose aptitude surpassed Gao Ye Hou and whose ultimate achievement was expected to surpass Qi Shou, found his sword heart muddied, his realm unstable—perhaps this is what is called the uncertainty of fate.

The grand battle was magnificent, with minor figures like Fan Dache advancing to the Golden Core stage—truly a small matter, merely a celebration shared among friends with a few drinks during the war’s intermissions.

The demon cultivators returned to the battlefield, continuing their clashes against the sword formations with a torrent of magical treasures.

Yet, the demon sword cultivators refrained from joining the fray, for they were far too precious and reluctant to expend themselves in a siege battle.

If the untransformed demons of the wild realm were akin to the most worthless copper coins, then the awakened and enlightened demon cultivators were like snowflake coins, and those who mastered their hearts could possess spirit artifacts and treasures—those demon sword cultivators were the most cherished and protected.

It was not that continuing to question the Sword Qi Great Wall was meaningless, but rather that with an unending supply of copper coins, similar achievements could be amassed without wasting the precious sword cultivators’ snowflake coins, which were hard to come by.

In the realm of Haoran, such sieges would lead to countless deaths, with the military camps daring to manipulate the lives of ants, sacrificing tens of thousands without a second thought. The resulting corpses would stain the battlefield for eternity. Yet in the wild realm, this was entirely acceptable.

For the first time in the wild realm, an ant swarm siege was observed.

Thereupon, the sound of horns echoed, resounding through the heavens, invigorating the military spirits in the wild realm.

The pure martial artists, the rugged fellows, had long awaited this moment, their fists brimming with intent, finally able to unleash their punches and slay demons.

The sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage continued their strategy of three-person rotations, taking turns to strike from the city walls.

The daily battle losses of both sides were meticulously recorded. Guo Zhujiu was responsible for compiling the records, and the atmosphere in the hall of the Summer Retreat Palace grew increasingly tense. Everyone was busily overwhelmed, and even Guo Zhujiu spent all day at his desk.

On the other side of the Upside-Down Mountain, nearly all the boatmasters engaged in trade had already visited Chunfan Studio at least once.

Yan Ming, Nalan Caihuan, and Mi Yu, along with Shao Yunyan and his direct disciple Wei Wenlong, were also busy.

While the battlefield was one of life and death, the battlefield also existed on the account books.

This was the Sword Qi Great Wall and the Eight Continent Trading Boats attempting to engage in trade through a new method, with numerous small frictions. Moreover, the collection of snowflake coins by the Aiai Continent Trading Boats was not progressing smoothly. The main issue was that the Liu family of the Aiai Continent had yet to express any stance, and since they controlled all the mines and profits related to snowflake coins, their silence and unwillingness to offer discounts hindered progress.

The few intercontinental boats were too hesitant to travel across the continents with snowflake coins; even a single ship’s worth would tempt Fifth Realm cultivators to act, rallying friends to ambush the boats, which could lead to disastrous consequences. Thus, the Aiai Continent Trading Boats dared not take such risks, and the Sword Qi Great Wall did not wish to see such outcomes either. Therefore, when the Aiai Trading Boats returned from their first trip to the Upside-Down Mountain, they didn’t bring any snowflake coins but instead requested various other supplies listed in the original Chunfan Studio account book.

The boatmasters from Aiai, including Jiang Gaotai, proposed that the Sword Qi Great Wall deploy sword immortals to escort the boats, ensuring that they had sword immortals stationed both ways.

Yan Ming and Nalan Caihuan felt this was impractical and suggested that the boats hire one or two Fifth Realm cultivators themselves. After all, this snowflake coin business, if successful, would earn the Aiai Trading Boats enough profit without relying on the Sword Qi Great Wall for protection. A round trip could often take six months or even a year, and they could hardly expect a sword immortal to be absent from the Sword Qi Great Wall for such long periods.

Shao Yunyan proposed a compromise: each trading boat didn’t need to stake their entire venture on snowflake coins. The Aiai Continent was rich in resources, with significant profits to be made.

These unexpected twists in such a big business required both sides to negotiate. If any single link went wrong, a transaction could be considered lost.

Chunfan Studio was already experiencing a sweltering summer, with the world’s furnace ablaze, while the Sword Qi Great Wall faced a snowless winter.

This left Guo Zhujiu feeling somewhat regretful. Initially, he had made an agreement with his master to build ten or more snowmen during the snow season, ensuring that all sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage would participate.

The sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage could at least find some comfort in the fact that the significant controversy surrounding the young hidden official’s use of the flying sword “Hidden Official” to send messages to the city walls had subsided. Or perhaps it still lingered, but no one had the time to voice their opinions anymore.

The war was brutal, with too many lives lost.

Even the swordsman Qiumiao, alongside Pang Yuanji and Lin Junbi, could only drag the true body of a soaring realm great demon, seizing a moment during the battle to stroll to the city walls and announce that the great demon was hiding in the Upside-Down Mountain, attempting to incite chaos. They tracked down its roots, decisively teaming up with several sword immortals, including Lu Zhi, to surround and slay it at sea.

Slaying a soaring realm great demon was no trivial matter, and the Sword Qi Great Wall was abuzz with excitement. Countless voices cheered in approval.

In the end, Lin Junbi couldn’t bear to sever its head, instead paying respects to the wild realm and stubbornly deciding to keep the entire true body of the soaring realm great demon, dragging it back to the Summer Retreat Palace.

Upon returning, the young hidden official saw the great demon’s head still attached and grinned from ear to ear, scolding Lin Junbi for being stingy, yet immediately storing the demon’s body in his spatial pouch, heartily patting Lin Junbi’s shoulder, laughing like a child who had just found a treasure.

Gu Yu and Wang Xinshui exchanged glances, knowing that Lin Junbi would surely receive credit from the Hidden Official.

That day, Chen Pingan left the hall of the Summer Retreat Palace for a walk, and Lin Junbi followed closely behind.

Chen Pingan smiled and asked, “Got something on your mind?”

Lin Junbi replied, “Regarding the Eight Continent Trading Boats, progress has been relatively smooth for now, but the largest issue lies not with the buyers and sellers, but with the views of the Haoran Academy.”

Chen Pingan raised an eyebrow, intrigued. “What do you mean?”

Lin Junbi expressed his concerns, “Previously, the Eight Continent Trading Boats operated haphazardly, and the Confucian Temple likely wouldn’t interfere too much. However, now that we’ve changed the situation, the Confucian Temple may have some backlash. To be honest, we have touched upon several fundamental interests of the Haoran realm. For every additional resource sent to the Upside-Down Mountain, Haoran loses that much.”

Chen Pingan nodded. “That’s true.”

Lin Junbi inquired, “If the Confucian Temple orders the Eight Continent Trading Boats to restrict their operations to the Haoran realm and not allow them to travel to the Upside-Down Mountain, what should we do?”

Although Lin Junbi was a sword cultivator, he was skilled in various techniques. He formed a hand sign with his fingers, using talismans and earth techniques to create a floating map of the realm, moving along with them. He pointed to the map, shaping water into new trade routes connecting the continents. “The resources from Central Divine Continent and Aiai Continent Trading Boats should only go to Nan Posa Continent, while Liuxia Continent and Golden Armored Continent support the southwestern Fuyun Continent. The Beiju Continent and Baoping Continent Trading Boats can only head southeast to Tongye Continent, building and fortifying the coastal defenses of these three continents. Even if the prices are lower than the Sword Qi Great Wall by ten to twenty percent, I believe the Eight Continent Trading Boats will comply out of necessity. As for the original trading boats from the three continents, including Posa, they will certainly not come to the Upside-Down Mountain.”

Chen Pingan strolled alongside Lin Junbi. “Regarding the Eight Continent Trading Boats, what you mentioned as the worst-case scenario, the swordsman Qiumiao warned me about this early on. However, there’s no way around it. We can’t let fear of this consequence prevent us from acting. We’ll take it step by step. Every time a trading boat docks at the Upside-Down Mountain, we’ll consider it as gaining more resources. We just hope the Confucian Temple doesn’t rush to a conclusion.”

Lin Junbi asked, “Mr. Confucian, can you really speak on such a significant matter at the Confucian Temple?”

Chen Pingan shook his head. “That’s quite difficult. The Confucians emphasize rank and propriety, stressing that one must have a valid reason for speaking.”

Lin Junbi pressed, “What if you include the scholarly Chen family? Is that not enough?”

Chen Pingan still shook his head. “Each side has its own difficulties.”

Lin Junbi bit his lip. “I’ll write a secret letter to my own master, asking him to say a few words for us?”

Chen Pingan stopped walking and said, “Remember, while you’re in the Sword Qi Great Wall, you’re just Lin Junbi, a sword cultivator. Don’t involve your own scholarly lineage, and definitely don’t drag the Shao Yuan Dynasty into this, because it will not only be of no use but could also backfire on you.”

Chen Pingan smiled. “I appreciate your goodwill.”

In truth, Chen Pingan could easily agree to Lin Junbi’s suggestion, regardless of whether Lin Junbi was acting impulsively or calculating. He could have Lin Junbi write the letter, sending it to the Shao Yuan Dynasty via a flying sword, and then have a sword immortal intercept it midway, allowing Chen Pingan to review the contents before deciding whether to keep the letter, archive it in the Summer Retreat Palace, or send it to the Central Divine Continent.

However, having spent enough time together, Chen Pingan understood Lin Junbi’s character well enough. For the sake of accomplishment, he would go to great lengths to achieve his goals, but Lin Junbi’s ambitions weren’t solely for personal gain; he also sought to stabilize the nation and the world.

With this thought in mind, Chen Pingan decided to be candid with Lin Junbi, suggesting he write the letter, going through the motions and ultimately archiving it in the Hidden Official lineage, hoping to find a chance to subtly inform the Haoran realm of this minor secret.

Perhaps one day in the future, it could serve to benefit Lin Junbi upon his return to the Haoran realm.

Lin Junbi was taken aback for a moment and sighed, “Is it really necessary to do so?”

Chen Pingan smiled. “Good deeds will be rewarded; what’s so strange about it? Ideally, altruism should leave no trace, but since the world is not yet so pure, we’ll settle for a lesser virtue. Isn’t it said that there’s such a thing as ‘lesser masterpieces beneath the true relics’ in literature and art? I think this will do just fine. Junbi, you don’t need to be so troubled about this matter; it’s not the only good deed in the world.”

Lin Junbi pondered for a moment, then nodded readily.

Chen Pingan said, “If the Confucian Temple truly acts this way, it’s not mere personal interest nor prejudice against the Sword Qi Great Wall.”

Chen Pingan sighed. “Opening the door to thieves is merely a means to close the door on dogs. To resolve the great hidden danger of the wild realm once and for all, the Confucian Temple has had such thoughts since ancient times. However, discussing this behind closed doors is one thing, but it cannot be spoken of outside; not a word can be leaked. The burden of benevolence is too heavy. The question of which lineage should bear the blame for this act of opening the door to thieves must be addressed. Someone must take the lead and advocate for this matter, right? The records on the Confucian Temple’s side will clearly document everything. Once the door opens, countless lives will suffer, and even if the final outcome is good, what then? How will the conscience of all Confucian disciples weigh against this? Will they not feel heartbroken, deeply disappointed in their lineage’s sages? As a moral sage who serves the Confucian Temple, how could one act with such disregard for lives, akin to a petty opportunist? Will the very lineage of literary tradition and道統 not collapse? When it comes to disputes among lineages, the sages can adhere to the principles of gentlemanly rivalry, but the countless Confucian students, many of whom are only half-hearted scholars, how could they all maintain such high moral standards?”

“Moreover, the bigger trouble lies within the lineage itself, where there are those who only care about their own lineage's honor and disgrace, regardless of right or wrong. In such cases, these individuals will certainly engage in the most vicious debates with outsiders, making matters worse and more wrong. How will the sages settle this? Will they prioritize dealing with external criticisms or suppress the rising discontent among their own disciples? Will they just say, ‘We admit our fault; you all should be quiet and stop criticizing’?”

“Ultimately, aren’t scholars and cultivators just individuals?”

As he spoke, Chen Pingan patted Lin Junbi on the shoulder. “Take your friend, that Mr. Xilu, for instance. Didn’t he gain notoriety for breaking statues and opportunistically seizing the moment? To say he has no knowledge or abilities is hard to believe, considering he could write the ‘Chess Manual of Kuai Zai Pavilion.’ To claim he hasn’t contributed to the literary tradition of the Shao Yuan Dynasty seems unlikely.”

The flattery of certain scholars could be as beautiful as a tapestry, yet they had long since rotted at the root. These individuals, once they set their minds to scheming, could easily ascend to high positions. It wouldn’t be accurate to say they hadn’t done anything; they simply enjoyed a comfortable life without contributing.

The complexity of the world lies in the fact that bad people can do good things, and good people can make mistakes. The merits and demerits of certain actions can vary based on context and individuals.

As the world becomes more aware of the news, able to connect facts into truths and accustomed to doing so, it should gradually improve.

Perhaps that’s what it means for the granaries to be full, leading to knowledge of rites.

Without knowledge, it’s hard not to feel disappointed. With more knowledge, even if disappointment lingers, there remains a glimmer of hope.

What’s truly frightening is when someone, in their despair, destroys the hopes of others.

Chen Pingan smiled and asked, “Lin Junbi, do you genuinely recognize this person?”

Lin Junbi, somewhat put off, fell silent.

Regarding the matter of breaking statues, Lin Junbi didn’t truly endorse it, but he wouldn’t stoop so low as to join the young hidden official in criticizing someone else. That would be beneath him.

Moreover, Lin Junbi found much to appreciate in that Mr. Xilu.

As autumn approached, the air was crisp, and countless bandits had been dealt with.

Today, Guo Zhujiu was flipping through the latest edition of the book, sweating slightly on her forehead.

Her master had once said that whenever the number of battle losses exceeded half among the sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage, they would convene to discuss matters.

On this day, someone visited the Summer Retreat Palace, abiding by the rules and waiting outside the door.

The swordsman Ku Xia would temporarily leave the Sword Qi Great Wall for a while, needing to escort Jin Zhenmeng, Yu Jianfu, and Zhu Mei to the Upside-Down Mountain, then send them to the territory of Nan Posa before returning.

Before leaving, Ku Xia brought the three to visit the Summer Retreat Palace, accompanied by three young children—two budding sword cultivators and a rare pure martial artist.

Lin Junbi received special permission from the Hidden Official to go out and see them off.

This showed that Lin Junbi held a somewhat special place in the Hidden Official’s heart.

As he approached the palace gate, Lin Junbi was filled with sentiment. Surely, that Mr. Cui hadn’t anticipated today’s events.

Was it not true that he had risked his life, tying his head to his waistband, just to barely reverse the game that Mr. Cui had left behind, relying on Mr. Cui’s moves to avoid further plays?

Upon reaching the door, Lin Junbi performed a bow, remaining silent, thus bidding them a quiet farewell.

For the first time, Yu Jianfu took the initiative to speak to Lin Junbi.

Yu Jianfu smiled and said, “Lin Junbi, just don’t die. When you return to the Central Divine Continent, you are welcome to visit the Yu family. We have peers of your age who have been skilled at chess since childhood.”

Lin Junbi chuckled, “I sincerely ask Miss Yu not to play matchmaker!”

Yu Jianfu beamed, “We’ll talk when we meet.”

Lin Junbi hesitated for a moment, then stepped back, bowing and apologizing. “I once had some unseemly calculations, and I apologize to Miss Yu here.”

Yu Jianfu laughed, “Your teacher has good taste, but it’s a pity that I’m not capable enough. Lin Junbi, since you’re so candid, then I’ll take the role of matchmaker.”

Indeed. Indeed!

Once again, Mr. Cui had hit the nail on the head.

What a close call.

Don’t be fooled by Yu Jianfu’s seemingly straightforward demeanor; she was actually the direct daughter of the Yu family, which was far from simple.

Yu Jianfu fell silent, rubbing the head of a small girl beside her, who would henceforth become her registered disciple, traveling together to explore the vast Haoran realm!

As for the other two young budding sword cultivators, their talent wasn’t particularly outstanding in the Sword Qi Great Wall but was still commendable within the Haoran realm. After all, which sect would reject sword cultivators? Moreover, to say they weren’t outstanding was only in comparison to prodigies like Qi Shou, Pang Yuanji, Situ Weiran, and Guo Zhujiu. In the Haoran realm, earth-level sword cultivators were still quite rare.

Jin Zhenmeng said, “Junbi, when we reach our hometown, if you don’t mind my abrupt retreat, you still consider me a friend, I’ll come find you for a drink!”

Lin Junbi nodded, “I do have some reservations, but if the wine is indeed good, I’ll hold my nose and drink it before cursing!”

The usually reserved Jin Zhenmeng couldn’t help but burst into laughter, stepping forward to pat Lin Junbi’s shoulder. “The young man before me is the Lin Junbi I hold in high regard! The finest talent of the Shao Yuan Dynasty.”

The swordsman Ku Xia felt quite satisfied.

Zhu Mei was also a bit cheerful, the atmosphere warm and pleasant—things had finally reached this point.

Zhu Mei’s words were succinct. “See you in our hometown, Lin Junbi.”

Lin Junbi smiled and nodded.

Upon entering, Chen Pingan leaned against the shadow wall, sipping wine from his sword-raising gourd, and softly said, “Junbi, if you leave the Sword Qi Great Wall now, you’ve already gained a lot. You haven’t really lost anything, and you could earn even more, but there’s a possibility of suffering many losses as well. Generally speaking, you can leave the gambling table now.”

This white-robed young man from the Central Divine Continent, a talented sword cultivator, had a spark in his eyes. “Bet big, win big!”

Lin Junbi laughed again. “Moreover, I’ve calculated that the Hidden Official won’t let me die at the Sword Qi Great Wall.”

Chen Pingan asked, “Outside, you’re still calculating human hearts, but do you find yourself happier when playing chess with others than before?”

Lin Junbi hummed in agreement.

Chen Pingan whispered, “Don’t lose the skills you had before; just get used to the ways of the outside world a bit. That will be just fine.”

Lin Junbi nodded.

Chen Pingan said, “When you see those with deeper hearts, remember that your own heart is already like a fish in the abyss, a dragon at the bottom of a well. There’s no need to fear this.”

Lin Junbi asked, “Why is that?”

Chen Pingan smiled. “The bright moon is reflected in the water. As long as you are willing to open your eyes to see, it will come into view, within reach.”

Lin Junbi hesitated for a moment but still chose to be honest. “Hidden Official, have you seen Yan Lyu and Jiang Guancheng? Do you find them irritating?”

Chen Pingan replied, “Aren’t they still with Yu Jianfu and Zhu Mei? Besides, the vast majority are those who are unwilling or unable to speak.”

Lin Junbi asked, “Hidden Official, when will you head to the battlefield?”

Chen Pingan smiled. “Even if I go, it can only be sneakily.”

Then Lin Junbi saw the young hidden official make a strange gesture, raising his hands to smooth his hair.

Lin Junbi didn’t dare to ask more, looking around, and saw no sign of that lady. Mi Yu and Gu Yu were the same; it was normal. However, seeing the young hidden official act like this was a bit odd.

Chen Pingan glanced at the sky and said, “I’m waiting for someone. He’s a swordsman.”

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 759: At the City Gates

On Luhua Island, the legendary Creation Cave, known for being a place where high-level cultivators practice their immortal techniques, witnessed a dramatic confrontation. A powerful demon, on the verge of ascension to the Immortal Realm, faced off against the swordsman known as Zuo You. After probing the enemy's strengths and weaknesses with a blade, Zuo You unleashed another strike, forcing the demon to retreat from Luhua Island. Ultimately, the demon met its demise at sea, cut down by Zuo You.

Upon landing, Zuo You and Wang Shizi of the Sword Sect sent two flying swords as messages to Chuanfan Hall in the Upside Down Mountain, detailing the encounter for the Jin Dan sword cultivators heading to Tongyezhou.

Wang Shizi, a Jin Dan sword cultivator, could only observe the battle from a distance. Though his cultivation was not high, he had seen many formidable demons in the Sword Qi Great Wall battles, allowing him to recognize that this demon from the Creation Cave was no ordinary adversary.

Even from nearly three hundred miles away, with the turbulent waves crashing like thunder below him, Wang Shizi could still clearly sense the ripples of sword intent emanating from Zuo You’s clash with the demon.

After sheathing his sword, Zuo You approached Wang Shizi, briefly relaying what had transpired before they continued their journey. Unable to contain his curiosity, Wang Shizi asked the silent sword immortal beside him, "Elder, do you think that demon has already ascended?"

Zuo You shook his head. "Not yet, but it is close. If we had arrived at Luhua Island any later, it would have been just a few years—at most ten—before that demon emerged as a true ascendant, and that would be troublesome."

Zuo You added, "But if we meet again in three to five years, and I am unscathed, it wouldn’t be too much of a problem."

Zuo You was not one for many words; when he spoke, he was direct and never exaggerated, nor did he need to feign humility. 

Regarding the message sent by the Sword Sect’s flying swords, it was simple: "On this trip to Tongyezhou, I encountered and eliminated a demon at the Immortal Realm, leaving no trace behind. The credit goes to my junior, Chen Ping’an."

If only Chuanfan Hall and the Sword Qi Great Wall received a message from Zuo You alone, they might have dismissed it as merely an encounter with an ordinary demon at the Immortal Realm.

At Chuanfan Hall, Yan Ming and Nalan Caihuan were initially shocked, before exchanging smiles. "As expected of Zuo You," they mused.

Wei Wenlong was left puzzled by the situation.

Mi Yu chuckled and said, "Wenlong, my friend."

Wei Wenlong felt a chill run down his spine and looked up, "What guidance do you have, Mi Sword Immortal?"

Mi Yu asked, "Do you know who Zuo You's junior brother is?"

Wei Wenlong guessed, "It must be the Hidden Official."

Though his cultivation was not high, he was clever enough.

Mi Yu looked at him with amusement.

Wei Wenlong quickly added, "Right?"

Mi Yu nodded with a smile. "Not bad—seems like you are indeed a talent favored by the Hidden Official. Wenlong, is there a girl you fancy but can’t have? Do you need me to share some tips? Don’t worry, it’s not anything unorthodox; I’m completely sincere."

Wei Wenlong hastily shook his head.

Even if there were such a girl, he would never dare let Mi Yu know.

With his fan in hand, Mi Yu asked, "If a girl who previously liked you suddenly turned her affections to me, would that still be someone worth pursuing?"

Wei Wenlong felt a bit distressed.

Nalan Caihuan, fed up with Mi Yu's antics, snapped, "What’s there to show off with such a repulsive facade?"

Mi Yu gracefully closed his fan. "Everyone has a love for beauty. If the women of the world meet Mi Yu and find me even slightly off-putting, that’s the only thing I can do."

Nalan Caihuan scoffed, "I find you extremely off-putting."

Mi Yu opened the fan again, hiding his face, "I’m willing to do more for Miss Nalan."

Wei Wenlong was taken aback by the exchange.

On Mount Chui Shang, the ancestral mountain of the Sword Sect, the sect leader Ji Hai had originally rejected Zhong Kui's proposal regarding a unique secret technique—it was Ji Hai's fundamental path, meant to be passed down exclusively to the successor of the sect leader. Moreover, Ji Hai had already set his sights on the next sect leader, a young man who had inadvertently exposed a hidden demon years ago. This boy had a special connection with the Sword Sect, as the ties of cultivation were paramount.

Ji Hai intended to formally accept this boy as his close disciple upon his return from studying at the Great Fulu Academy. The fact that he had not yet paid respects in the Ancestor Hall meant he wasn't Ji Hai's true close disciple yet.

Zhong Kui knew that relying solely on letters from the academy's teachers and the old heavenly lord of Taiping wouldn't convince Ji Hai to make an exception. It was also a matter of principle; he truly shouldn’t be so demanding. Only compelled by his master’s orders, Zhong Kui remained persistent, visiting Ji Hai for tea and conversation, to which Ji Hai eventually had to retreat behind closed doors. As a result, Zhong Kui set up a few tables outside the sacred cave of the Sword Sect, surrounded by books, claiming he was there to guard the place while reading daily.

Ji Hai ignored him.

Other matters could be discussed, but this issue was non-negotiable. Not even the old sect master of Yuguizong, Xun Yuan, or the new sect master, Jiang Shangzhen, could sway Ji Hai on this matter.

Huang Ting lacked Zhong Kui's audacity and left the mountain to travel.

For some unknown reason, the once-anxious master, Song Mao, and the old heavenly lord now encouraged her to take her time with breaking through her Nascent Soul bottleneck, emphasizing the importance of going with the flow. The old heavenly lord even gave a long lecture filled with absurd reasoning, ending with, "A woman of such high cultivation will find it hard to find a man."

While Zhong Kui was trying to outlast Ji Hai, Zuo You and Wang Shizi journeyed from the sea to the Sword Sect, prompting Ji Hai to finally exit his seclusion.

Upon hearing Wang Shizi's report about Zuo You slaying a major demon at the Immortal Realm and sending a message via flying sword to the Upside Down Mountain, Ji Hai, as a sect leader, had a greatly favorable impression of Zuo You, the one who had single-handedly weakened the Tongye Sect. In fact, Ji Hai viewed Zuo You as a benefactor.

Ji Hai, who harbored a deep hatred for demons due to the death of his partner at the hands of one, was particularly invested in this matter. Years ago, a demon had fled from him after he was severely injured, preventing him from pursuing it further. Three others, including the Taiping Mountain’s master, Song Mao, and the then-ancestor of the Tongye Sect, pursued the demon but ultimately failed. Coincidentally, that demon encountered Zuo You at sea, and according to Jiang Shangzhen, the demon inexplicably deemed Zuo You a nuisance and refused to avoid him, resulting in its untimely demise.

Now that Zuo You had landed with news of yet another demon's death, Ji Hai could not help but feel elated.

However, Zuo You remained indifferent to the overly enthusiastic sect leader. His impression of Tongyezhou was only mildly positive, primarily due to Taiping Mountain. 

Before descending the mountain, Zuo You casually remarked to Zhong Kui, "Are you planning to keep that little snow pick I lent you, hoping to get away with it?"

Zhong Kui nearly burst into tears on the spot. The matter of whether to return it was secondary; the key was that he had established a connection with this sword immortal—Zuo You was essentially his senior brother now. 

How could there be a more reasonable situation than this?

Feeling aggrieved, Zhong Kui began sharing his dismal experiences at the Sword Sect, detailing how he was looked down upon and often denied access...

Ji Hai’s face turned dark with anger; any guilt he felt was swiftly erased.

Zuo You pondered for a moment before telepathically inquiring about Zhong Kui and Ji Hai, ultimately suggesting, "Ji Hai, you could have Zhong Kui swear that this secret technique will not be passed to outsiders. Since he is no longer a Confucian disciple, he can serve as an honorary member of the Sword Sect. But I’m just an outsider, merely making a suggestion."

Ji Hai sighed and surprisingly nodded in agreement.

Zhong Kui had no objections either.

Ji Hai personally escorted Zuo You and Zhong Kui to the mountain gate. Zhong Kui couldn’t help but recall his previous ascent with Huang Ting—it was a stark contrast.

Zuo You happened to be heading to Taiping Mountain alongside Zhong Kui.

Curious, Zhong Kui asked, "Elder, how did you become Chen Ping’an's senior brother?"

Zuo You chuckled, "My master forced him upon me, so I begrudgingly accepted."

Zhong Kui was left speechless.

Even a kitchen knife, after chopping vegetables and meats for an extended period, would become dull over time. 

A dull knife needs sharpening.

But in the wild world, where battles come in relentless waves, the most vital aspect was to ensure that the sword immortals at the city gates had no chance to hone their skills. If they wanted to take a moment to rest and recover their swords, it would require the lives and flying swords of mid-tier Jin Dan cultivators in exchange.

In the past, siege battles in the wild were chaotic and sporadic, full of unforeseen events. The mobilization of troops on the battlefield, the arrival of reinforcements, and the individual assaults often broke the continuity, leading to prolonged lulls of months, or even half a year. When one side had their turn basking in the sun, the other would have their turn under the moonlight. During the outbreak of war, the battlefield would be exceptionally brutal, with blood and flesh flying, flying swords shattering—especially during the sudden clashes between large demons and sword immortals, which were astonishing yet could determine the fate of a battlefield or even the entire war.

Yet, there had never been a war so suffocating as the current one.

It felt as if no one could decisively determine the outcome. The demons showcased their various abilities, while the sword immortals struck fiercely, yet no one could seal the fate, and life and death became lost in the chaos of the battlefield.

The most intense battle, the most breathtaking slaughter, occurred when a major demon shifted the Five Mountains onto the battlefield. The demon lord took command, and the three sword immortals—Li Tui Mi, Chen Xi, and Zhong Kui—sacrificed themselves to break the deadlock. Zuo You later entered the fray, and amidst the concealed demons, the old sword immortal Dong San withdrew from the city gates to assist Zuo You, who ultimately fell into a trap laid by the Hidden Official Xiao Xian and was severely injured, marking the end of that encounter.

In the wild world, the sixty military tents continuously supplied reinforcements in phases, and the siege was executed seamlessly. The wild world clearly aimed to deny the Sword Qi Great Wall any chance to recover, especially to the upper-tier Jin Dan sword immortals. In this severe and pressurized situation, the initial constraints that made the sword immortals feel restricted in their strikes began to show their effects.

Previously, on the city gates, the overwhelming strength of individual sword immortals, their extraordinary prowess, had been diluted by the necessity of sacrifice, resulting in a greater collective strength for the sword formation.

Now, when a sword immortal would leave the battlefield to recuperate, the disadvantages would lessen.

The Hidden Official’s research into the sword formations had deepened. Not only were upper-tier Jin Dan sword immortals familiar with each other’s flying swords and divine abilities, but they also had become exceedingly well-acquainted with the flying swords of lower-tier cultivators.

Military strategies are fluid; soldiers have no fixed tactics. The sword cultivators on the city gates constantly adjusted their formations, changing defensive positions with many unfamiliar sword immortals they had never met before, collaborating in pairs with flying swords, even forming formations of dozens of flying swords, stacking their divine abilities. If they could endure the initial phase of adaptation, their power would dramatically increase.

Currently, there were as many as thirty-one sword formations in the Sword Qi Great Wall, crafted from the five elemental flying swords and divine abilities.

In the past, the Sword Qi Great Wall resembled a wealthy household, with its wealth of gold, silver, and fertile lands, likely unaware of its true fortune.

Now, the Sword Qi Great Wall was reduced to a single copper coin in the corner, to be picked up and noted down.

Thanks to this situation, every Hidden Official was an indispensable presence.

Among them, the contributions of the sword immortals—especially the deep understanding of flying swords and divine abilities by Chou Miao, the strategic vision of Lin Junbi, and Guo Zhujiu's flashes of inspiration—were the most significant.

However, during this time, there were still flaws and mistakes in the deployment of the Hidden Official’s forces, which required the sword cultivators on the battlefield to compensate with their lives and flying swords.

The sword immortals of the Hidden Official line also experienced significant arguments and grievances, as on a small battlefield, conflicting strategies often arose. Before the outcome was clear, no one could confidently declare which plan was superior. If the battlefield developed as expected, it would be manageable. But once problems arose, it would become troublesome—if one side was wrong, they would feel guilt, and if they were right, they would feel frustration.

The most heated argument occurred between Xu Ning and Cao Gun, where both nearly resorted to swordplay.

A proposal from the Summer Palace led to the death of two earth immortal sword cultivators from the Sword Qi Great Wall, along with thirty-one mid-tier Jin Dan cultivators, all perishing with their swords shattered.

Everyone felt heartbroken. Xuan Can, who was responsible for drafting the plan, was filled with regret. Although Xu Ning initially only expressed dissatisfaction, it only fueled the fire, and Xuan Can, feeling guilty, did not retort. Cao Gun, who had a good relationship with Xuan Can, couldn’t hold back and directly scolded Xu Ning, telling him to keep his mouth clean. 

Xu Ning replied by cursing Xuan Can’s ancestors.

Xuan Can was a skilled strategist in chess; otherwise, he wouldn’t often play against Lin Junbi and have moments of victory. His insults were sharp, leaving Xu Ning’s face pale and ready for a duel.

The atmosphere in the hall grew tense, and any duel would mean that for the Hidden Official line, there would be no true winner.

Luo Zhenyi remarked, "If Xu Ning’s proposal had been adopted initially, would we have suffered such heavy losses? If I remember correctly, it was rejected by you, so how is Xu Ning being the wise one after the fact?"

Chang Taiqing, a close friend of Xu Ning, weighed in with even harsher words, calling it foolish to not recognize one’s mistakes.

The foreign sword cultivator Song Gaoyuan, usually close to Luo Zhenyi, clearly sided with Cao Gun and Xuan Can, leading to an argument with Chang Taiqing.

Lin Junbi attempted to mediate but ended up displeasing both sides. He had to scold Xu Ning and Xuan Can, with the blame shifting to him.

Guo Zhujiu, unaccustomed to such a scene, found himself at a loss, as everything he said or did seemed wrong.

If not for Chen Ping’an and Chou Miao holding their ground, the local sword cultivators and foreign sword cultivators would have nearly torn apart their alliance.

After exchanging glances, Chou Miao, the sword immortal, urged Xu Ning to quiet down.

Then Chen Ping’an spoke, asking whether they wanted to reason or vent their emotions. If they wanted to reason, there was no need; the massive losses were the fault of the entire Hidden Official line, and everyone shared responsibility. He himself bore the greatest fault, as he set the rules, and every proposal was made accordingly. 

After the fact, holding someone accountable was acceptable, but it should not be aimed at any individual. The Hidden Official line was too small to handle that kind of blame game.

If anyone was simply angry and needed to vent through insults, that was fine too—a proper duel could resolve things. Three against three: Deng Liang against Luo Zhenyi, Cao Gun against Chang Taiqing, and Xuan Can against Xu Ning; it could be seen as a long-overdue trial. However, he'd have to note down the exploits of the sword immortals afterward.

The hall fell silent.

Only then did Chen Ping’an, alongside Chou Miao and Lin Junbi, begin to review and analyze the pros and cons of Cao Gun’s plan, not dismissing it outright due to the poor outcome.

At this juncture, most sword cultivators calmed down.

Chen Ping’an finally concluded, "Everyone here is extremely intelligent, and each has their own strengths."

"So those present must be more diligent in their work and principled in their conduct. I trust Xu Ning’s initial words were not malicious; I don’t even think it was inappropriate to say them. On the contrary, it must be made clear that Xuan Can should understand that making mistakes does not grant one immunity just because the intent was good."

"If it was wrong, it won’t change just because we are colleagues under the Hidden Official line. On the contrary, it’s precisely because we are friends that we can scold each other privately. We have been part of the Hidden Official line for over a year, and we know each other’s characters well. It’s easy to call out mistakes and insult each other, isn’t it? Don’t we all understand this?"

Chou Miao then stated, "What truly needs to be addressed isn’t Xu Ning and Xuan Can but rather Cao Gun and Luo Zhenyi’s respective defenses. Is it necessary to muddy the waters to appear loyal?"

Chen Ping’an chuckled, "If it weren’t for the sword goddess Chou Miao overseeing this, you all would have nearly beaten each other to death, wouldn’t you? I foresaw it; three of you went up the city to kill demons, separating you all. If not, by tomorrow, one of you would be missing, and in less than half a year, the Summer Palace would lose half its members. Each empty desk would require a single incense burner and three sticks of incense, and the costs would fall on whose shoulders? A fine Summer Palace would turn into a mourning hall. Should I scold you for being prodigal or miss your hard work and contributions?"

Here it comes, the Hidden Official’s signature sarcasm.

Chou Miao remarked, "Still, the Hidden Official is willing to take on the greatest blame."

Chen Ping’an turned to Gu Jianlong, but he didn’t receive the fair words he sought. Gu Jianlong silently turned to Wang Xinshui, who refused to take the burden and instead looked at Guo Zhujiu, who had her head buried in the records.

Chen Ping’an had no choice but to flip open a record book dedicated to documenting the merits and demerits of the Hidden Official line, preparing to write.

Moments later, Chou Miao asked, "Xu Ning and Luo Zhenyi have written their parts, Cao Gun and Xuan Can have too. Why don’t I see the words 'Hidden Official' or 'Chen Ping’an' anywhere?"

Chen Ping’an chuckled, "Chou Miao, shall we make a bet? Let’s wager whether I wrote down my own faults in this record."

Chou Miao nodded, "I’m in."

Chen Ping’an clapped his hands on the table, "Anyone can bet."

Except for Guo Zhujiu, everyone else followed Chou Miao in betting that the Hidden Official had not written anything down. Just a small wager with a few small coins.

In the end, Chen Ping’an flipped back a page and held up the book, smiling widely, "Everyone, open your eyes wide and see! Cash, cash!"

Guo Zhujiu leaped up, "Collecting money, collecting money!"

All the losers looked at Chou Miao.

Chou Miao looked resigned and turned to Chen Ping’an, smiling wryly, "I didn't expect to lose my reputation; then the split can't be four to six. It has to be fifty-fifty."

Chen Ping’an retorted, "Chou Miao, you’re not my accomplice!"

Gu Jianlong timidly added, "Hidden Official, allow me to speak fairly. The division of wealth is clear; this feels somewhat unfair."

Wang Xinshui nodded, "Your angry expression looks overly dramatic; it's gone too far."

Guo Zhujiu sighed.

Her master was indeed working hard to earn some private funds.

Chen Ping’an suddenly glanced at the scroll on the ground, speaking in a solemn tone, "We need to prepare for the sword immortals to leave the city gate and help separate the battlefield."

Chen Ping’an stood up, "In the previous few instances when I had the chance to head to the city gate, I gave those opportunities to you, considering the future. So now, I have about twenty days to leave the Summer Palace and venture out to kill demons. During this time, Chou Miao and Lin Junbi will oversee the situation. If something truly difficult arises, you can send a flying sword under the name of the 'Hidden Official' to the city gate’s sword immortal Wei Jin, and he will notify me to return here for discussions."

Luo Zhenyi hesitated for a moment, wanting to counsel this young Hidden Official against acting impulsively.

She had to admit that as the sword cultivators of the Hidden Official line grew more coordinated, Chen Ping’an's presence at the Summer Palace might not significantly alter the overall situation. But having him there would make a difference; at the very least, unnecessary arguments would decrease.

Unexpectedly, Chou Miao communicated with Luo Zhenyi through thought, "Let him go; the one who feels the most pent-up is not us. A person who has been emotionless for over a year is not easy."

Luo Zhenyi came to a realization; if not for Chou Miao’s reminder, she wouldn’t have considered this matter.

Chen Ping’an stood up and walked out of the hall. In the courtyard, he donned an old man's mask, strapped on a sword from the sword forge, and wore an extra robe from the clothing shop.

Gu Jianlong quietly reminded him, "Hidden Official, actually wearing the other mask would conceal you better."

Chen Ping’an turned with a smile, his posture slightly hunched, a natural aging quality. In a hoarse voice, he said, "You’re quite the smooth talker. When I return, we shall have a good chat."

Before Gu Jianlong could say anything further, Chen Ping’an's sword leaped from its sheath, and with a light leap, he stood atop the sword, soaring away.

Inside the hall, everyone exchanged glances.

He didn’t seem like a disguised sword cultivator at all.

In the Summer Palace, aside from the young Hidden Official, everyone was a sword cultivator, and they were all talented; they had enough insight to see through the disguise.

Chou Miao chuckled, "Come on, let’s bet whether the Hidden Official is truly a sword cultivator. This time, I’ll take the lead."

Then Chou Miao immediately added, "Guo Zhujiu, you’re not allowed to bet."

Otherwise, not only would there be no profit, but she would undoubtedly lose a fortune, possibly even to the point of financial ruin. This girl had quite the wealth, to say the least.

Just as Guo Zhujiu was about to stake all her possessions, she glared, "On what grounds?!"

As a result, not only Cao Gun’s group, but even Luo Zhenyi, Xu Ning, and Chang Taiqing also placed bets that Chen Ping’an was indeed a sword cultivator.

Chou Miao waved her hand, "What are you all betting for? You’re all young and your cultivations are poor, not focusing on your proper work. Hurry up and get to work! Guo Zhujiu, put everything back in the bamboo box!"

Guo Zhujiu rolled her eyes.

With no accomplices, how could she take the lead? Her master had once said that a gambling table should have ten people, including the dealer, at least eight should be accomplices to make it viable.

After Guo Zhujiu gathered her things, she looked around, ultimately unwillingly seeking out the highest-ranked, albeit somewhat dim-witted, sword immortal Chou Miao to ask, "Chou Miao, will my master be alright?"

Chou Miao smiled, "Don’t worry."

The other sword cultivators wore peculiar expressions.

Gu Jianlong remarked, "Whether the Hidden Official is fine or not, I only know that anyone targeted by your master is bound to face trouble." 

Wang Xinshui nodded, "What Gu said resonates with me."

Soon, the group fell silent.

A significant incident unfolded on the scroll.

On the battlefield, many demons would casually intervene while observing the fight.

This time, it was the demon Bai Ying, seated on the Throne of Bones, who unleashed a technique that was exceedingly brazen. In an instant, tens of thousands of skeleton puppets arose near the city wall, attempting to assist the army in their siege. Although these lifeless bones, lacking intelligence, were far weaker in this form than in life, the sudden surge of numbers on the frontline posed a challenge for the sword cultivators guarding the city.

Before these skeleton puppets could swarm the city wall, Wu Chengpei, a sword immortal at the Jade Purity Realm, summoned his divine flying sword, "Guanlin."

Upon manifesting, whenever blood soaked the earth, rainwater would rise from the ground, collecting towards the sky, creating a torrential downpour that seemed to invert heaven and earth, with only Wu Chengpei's sword intent rain descending normally.

After a deluge, the skeletal puppets and the nearby demon army were nearly annihilated.

Following this, Wu Chengpei repeatedly activated his divine sword, pushing out from the base of the wall. After five successive downpours, only a mere ten percent of those who survived were high-ranking demon cultivators or those with exceptionally tough natural bodies yet to take on human form. These beings then became targets for the sword cultivators atop the city.

Thus, the momentum of the wild world's siege began to wane.

Wu Chengpei then returned his sword, quietly shifting to another section of the wall to continue refining his sword.

It was hard to imagine that this was merely the action of a Jade Purity Realm sword immortal.

An older sword cultivator, stealthily climbing up the city gates, witnessed this scene up close.

Soon after, several sword immortals collectively entered the battlefield, stirring admiration.

Dong Sangeng, Chen Xi, and Qi Tingji, three old sword immortals inscribed on the city wall, also began to mobilize.

Alongside them were the likes of Lu Zhi, Nalan Shaowei, Yue Qing, Yao Lianyun, and Mi Hu, all of whom departed from the city gates.

Additionally, female sword immortals like Zhou Cheng, Yuan Qingshu, and Tao Wen followed suit without exception.

The three sages of Confucianism, Buddhism, and Daoism, stationed at the Sword Qi Great Wall, also began to employ their divine abilities to alter the battlefield.

Thus, the front lines where the sword immortals entrenched themselves became increasingly critical.

On the front line of the sword immortals, the ground swelled like a rolling river, created by the Daoist sage wielding a whisk, with golden characters forming two banks along the riverbanks. In the water floated golden lotuses.

The old sword cultivator followed the mid-tier Jin Dan sword cultivators, departing the city gates in a grand procession.

Once they landed, the old sword cultivator did not dare to charge to the frontlines. Though he held a sword in hand, he summoned a flying sword that circled around him. Seeing the surrounding sword immortals wielding their flying swords with boldness, he felt a twinge of guilt and guided his flying sword to stab a near-death demon, earning a glare from a nearby ocean-seeing sword cultivator, who cursed him, before he continued to stab at other half-dead demons. On the battlefield, it was only by defeating opponents that one could earn merits.

Although the demon army was numerous, the number of cultivators was relatively small, making it difficult to obtain any valuable achievements—losing out on some valuable merits, the old sword cultivator grumbled.

After a few exchanges, the old sword cultivator managed to claim several achievements from the weakened demons, laughing heartily. The nearby ocean-seeing sword cultivator scolded, "Get away from me!"

The old sword cultivator retorted, "I refuse!"

On the frontline, a demon with a Dragon Gate Realm cultivation had been intentionally revealing its true form, and as the ocean-seeing sword cultivator and the old sword cultivator quarreled, it suddenly charged forward, transforming into human form, aiming to crush the ocean-seeing sword cultivator's head with a palm.

However, the young ocean-seeing sword cultivator was no novice; he remained focused, quickly wielding his flying sword towards the demon’s forehead. The demon's rough skin and robust physique allowed it to grab the sword even as it pierced through, but it was determined to smash the sword cultivator's head with its palm.

The ocean-seeing sword cultivator also had a long sword, and as he waved it, he didn’t expect the incoming Dragon Gate Realm demon to suddenly sidestep and reach him at an even quicker pace, swinging its arm to decapitate him.

An old sword cultivator inexplicably appeared between the two, using two fingers to block the demon’s arm, after which the ocean-seeing sword cultivator pierced the demon's head with his flying sword.

The old sword cultivator immediately turned to curse, "You’re stealing my kill! This is a major demon…"

The sword cultivator who had been about to thank the old man stifled the words in his throat, cursing inwardly, "Demon, you bastard."

The old sword cultivator, however, was undeterred and followed him.

The two formed an unlikely partnership, fighting side by side through numerous dangers, yet each time emerging unscathed. When the ocean-seeing sword cultivator finally felt compelled to sincerely thank the old man, he found that the old sword cultivator had vanished.

He glanced back, noticing that the old sword cultivator had taken a brutal punch from a Jin Dan demon, sent flying and rolling in the dirt. Once he stood up, he saw the Jin Dan demon being overwhelmed by sword cultivators and staggeringly fled.

The ocean-seeing sword cultivator couldn’t help but feel puzzled; if this was truly an elder of the Nascent Soul or Jin Dan Realm, such shamelessness was somewhat typical in the Sword Qi Great Wall, yet among them, there were far fewer who were known, and one was more renowned than the next—like the one who would suddenly recite poetry after drinking from the bamboo sea cave’s wine, a notable figure among the elders. But this old man seemed unfamiliar.

The old sword cultivator wandered around, occasionally claiming small advantages. Eventually, he encountered a Jin Dan demon, who had been pursuing him for over a hundred yards. The old sword cultivator summoned another flying sword that bore a striking resemblance to his own, dodging the demon’s ferocious attacks while shouting, "You’d better not make me go all out! I have plenty of flying swords!"

The Jin Dan demon, enraged, seemed to attack recklessly, but was about to summon a powerful offensive treasure when it paused, taken aback by the old sword cultivator's words in the wild world’s grand language, "Quickly put away one of those flying swords and strive to survive to deliver the message."

The Jin Dan demon, though suspicious, decided to grab the old sword cultivator first. Just as it reached for the flying sword, it suddenly accelerated, piercing through the demon's head and destroying one of its eyes.

The Jin Dan demon screamed in agony, revealing its true form and attempting to summon its offensive treasure while shouting for its nearby demon forces to gather and surround the old sword cultivator.

However, the old sword cultivator had already vanished.

Once the demon revealed its true form and gathered around seventy to eighty demons, they found themselves targeted by several sword cultivators.

Far from this battlefield, a young sword cultivator was knocked aside, crashing into the ground, while a demon's treasure smashed into a large pit beside him. In the next moment, an old sword cultivator caught the young man, just as the surrounding demons began their encirclement.

With a sword on his back, the old sword cultivator neither drew his long sword nor summoned a flying sword. Instead, he merely pushed the young cultivator away, sending him far from the battlefield.

Then, the old sword cultivator casually assumed a boxing stance, scattering his intent, and the surroundings were reduced to powder.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 760: The Quest for the Golden Elixir

Upon witnessing this scene, the young sword cultivator was still in shock when the old sword cultivator had already withdrawn his fist stance, standing elegantly with one hand behind his back. He stroked his beard and chuckled, filled with self-satisfaction as he proclaimed, “Truly, my sword energy is invincible.”

The young sword cultivator remained dumbfounded for quite some time. The battlefield was now deserted; in the distance, some demon clansmen, sensing the imminent danger, despite their limited intelligence, understood the peril and quickly took a detour to flee to safer grounds.

The old sword cultivator surveyed the battlefield, noting that several low-ranked demon cultivators had been obliterated, their weapons and souls completely shattered without a trace—such a waste. He made a mental note to be more careful next time; even a mosquito's leg is still meat.

The young sword cultivator swooped down beside the old one, “Old senior?”

With a hoarse voice, the old sword cultivator smiled and replied, “Just call me Sword Immortal Senior. I’m not that old; I can’t bear the title ‘old’.”

The young sword cultivator was speechless, taken aback.

The old sword cultivator had already mounted his sword and soared away, his long sword gliding close to the ground as he swiftly navigated the battlefield like a fish swimming through water plants. He targeted the demon cultivators, killing when possible and wounding when not. His timing for each strike was impeccable, ensuring he wouldn’t interfere with the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

The young sword cultivator glanced at the figure of his “Sword Immortal Senior” and the way he wielded his sword, unable to discern the depth of his cultivation. Suppressing his curiosity, he gripped his sword and headed south toward the next battlefield.

In this sortie from the city, the Sword Qi Great Wall dispatched over six thousand mid-ranked sword cultivators. While that sounds like a significant number, in reality, it’s still a treacherous situation for everyone, given the vast expanse of the battlefield. Additionally, the numerous cave-dwelling and sea-watching sword cultivators were primarily there to hone their sword skills and familiarize themselves with the battlefield. They had to balance both killing demons and practicing their swordplay, necessitating the care of higher-ranked fellow sword cultivators. According to the rules of the Hidden Officials lineage, these cultivators sought to survive first, break through their realms second, and only then pursue killing demons. As for the highest-ranked Earth Immortal sword cultivators, their primary mission was to slay demons and secure the lives of the cave-dwelling and sea-watching cultivators as their secondary concern.

With sword cultivators stationed on the city walls, as long as the north-south front didn’t collapse too much, there was no need to worry about demons bypassing the sword cultivators to reach the city.

The sword cultivators of the Dragon Gate realm, positioned between the two extremes, were relatively straightforward, able to take on demons alone or team up with friends without much restriction.

During this time, many small groups of sword cultivators had formed, particularly unique ones where their flying swords’ innate abilities could synergize. As they ventured out to confront the enemy, they aimed to utilize their flying swords in a coordinated manner on the battlefield. For these sword cultivators protecting a certain Golden Elixir or Nascent Soul sword cultivator, their primary duty was to safeguard the former, while slaying demons was secondary. If the former's life path or flying sword were damaged, the Earth Immortal sword cultivators would incur severe penalties. Attempting to make up for it with military merits would be extremely unprofitable.

Once they left the city, the emergency regulations set by the Hidden Officials lineage were few, making each one particularly significant to the sword cultivators.

The old sword cultivator passed through a battlefield far from the city walls, where the fighting was especially brutal.

The fact that they had managed to eliminate all demons near the city walls and pushed southward for dozens of miles indicated that this group of sword cultivators possessed considerable killing power and an even greater thirst for battle.

However, the seven sword cultivators present were now trapped in a dire situation, surrounded by dozens of demon cultivators, with their forces numbering in the thousands, three of which were formidable Golden Elixir “great demons.”

The old sword cultivator recognized two familiar faces: Ren Yi, a Dragon Gate sword cultivator, and Pu Yu, a Golden Elixir sword cultivator. They were among those stationed at the three checkpoints on the main street. The old sword cultivator glanced at Pu Yu and sighed; this young man still had that eye-catching appearance that screamed ‘trouble.’

It was fortunate that this handsome young master wasn’t one of his own; otherwise, he would’ve berated him thoroughly. It was one thing to drink and spar with others in the city, but on the battlefield, to flaunt such an ethereal demeanor was inappropriate. That clothing from the tailor's didn’t cost him half a snowflake; why not drape on an extra piece? If not for the rule allowing each sword cultivator only one free garment, the old sword cultivator could have donned several and carried several more swords into battle.

This old sword cultivator, affectionately referred to as “Sword Immortal Senior,” was none other than the now infamous Hidden Official.

Following the titles of “Fair Merchant” and “One Punch to Defeat Chen Pingan,” he had now acquired another nickname, “The Hidden Official Who Looks Away from Death.”

On the city walls, after the earlier “betrayal” by the sword immortal Lian Ji, the Hidden Official’s lineage of sword cultivators had relocated to their domain. After a prolonged silence, the flying sword inscribed with the words “Hidden Official” transmitted a message to the city walls. Almost all sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall had already sensed what was happening. After all, during the demon clan's onslaught with a torrent of magical treasures and the two great battles against the sword cultivators of the savage world, the waterfall of sword energy on the city walls had undergone numerous formations, killing many Nascent Soul demon cultivators. After a series of these occurrences, the sword cultivators had pieced together the flavor of that wine shop.

Had it not been for the peak great demon’s ruthless slaughter of the sword immortal and the Hidden Official’s efforts to block the rescue, that young outsider, who had once been the second shopkeeper and then the Hidden Official, would have seen his reputation shift from extremely poor to extremely good within the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Chen Pingan wasn’t in a hurry to intervene; Pu Yu, as a Golden Elixir sword cultivator, was likely the protective sword master for this group of young sword cultivators. Ren Yi, being a Dragon Gate cultivator who could move freely on the battlefield, was probably aiming to join forces with Pu Yu to break the encirclement, providing mutual support while also killing more demons. Pu Yu’s innate flying sword, “Rain Mist,” was particularly good at creating illusions, easily misdirecting foes with its swift transformations and decent killing power.

Chen Pingan carefully observed the battlefield and felt no urgency; he assumed a posture of wanting to step in yet lacking the confidence to do so. He made several detours, cutting off some demons trying to bypass the entire battlefield and rush toward the city walls. After all, as long as the demon cultivators could reach the city walls, it would count as an accomplishment. If they could even ascend the walls, it would be a significant achievement, even if they ultimately died without any spoils. Both types of accomplishments would be recorded in the military accounts of the savage world and rewarded to their clans or direct descendants.

What Chen Pingan focused on was an inconspicuous demon cultivator. It wasn’t because the opponent leaked the aura of a great demon; instead, it was an instinctive feeling of “obstruction,” coupled with an unreasonable conviction of having the upper hand in this small battlefield, feeling invulnerable despite the impending danger. This demon cultivator, currently unaware of his own cultivation level, seemed to act recklessly, wielding a flashy attacking spirit artifact with great flair. However, encountering the “old sword cultivator,” it was truly unfortunate for him.

A Golden Elixir demon cultivator stationed at the battlefield also found the old sword cultivator, who was evasively circling around, quite bothersome. He sent three of his subordinates to probe the situation.

Chen Pingan wasn’t concerned about those three demon cultivators leaving the battlefield, nor was he focused on the commands of the Golden Elixir “great demon.” He remained fixated on that hidden demon cultivator, highly likely concealing his true cultivation level. The old sword cultivator further confirmed his suspicions, alerting the Golden Elixir demon cultivator to eliminate this unexpected element before it jeopardized their plans, such as ambushing Pu Yu and Ren Yi, the two young talents.

After all, both Pu Yu and Ren Yi weren’t low-ranked. They had fully participated in the previous two offensive and defensive battles. If they genuinely decided to disregard the lives of the other young sword cultivators, they had a great chance of retreating from the battlefield.

Pu Yu and Ren Yi were undoubtedly two of the Sword Qi Great Wall’s young prodigies. Just because they were on the same hill as the illustrious Qi Shou and Gao Ye Hou didn’t mean they were mere nobodies.

Even though Dong Heitan had privately commented on the two sword cultivators guarding the checkpoint, saying Ren Yi was younger among the Dragon Gate cultivators and had a quick flying sword, he had rated Pu Yu as the most ostentatious among Golden Elixir cultivators. This evaluation was accurate during actual combat and sword questioning, but it wasn’t comprehensive. The Hidden Official lineage held Pu Yu and his innate flying sword in high regard because his flying sword had exceptional effects on the battlefield, rated as tier C, second only to Qi Shou’s tier B flying sword, “Jumping Pearl.” As for tier A, that belonged to Wu Chengpei’s “Sweet Rain,” while tier B included Yue Qing’s “Hundred Zhang Spring,” “Lark in the Sky,” and the innate flying sword of the sword immortal Yuanqing Shu from the Posa Continent.

Many sword immortals’ innate flying swords were immensely powerful, yet they were rated low on the summer palace side.

Of course, this classification was a utilitarian assessment made by the Hidden Official lineage sword cultivators solely concerning the battlefield.

Now that he had identified the opponent’s true backhand, Chen Pingan no longer hesitated or meandered. He stepped onto the long sword from the sword shop, using the proper sword cultivator technique to charge toward the three probing demon cultivators. He glided close to the ground, tracing a large arc with his sword, just as he narrowly avoided an attack from an opponent’s spirit weapon. With a quick flick of his toe, his long sword surged toward one of the demon cultivators, moving as swiftly as a flying sword.

The old sword cultivator had already abandoned his long sword, unleashing his innate flying sword named “Account Book,” targeting another demon cultivator from the Sea-Watching realm. The flying sword pierced through the opponent’s head, and with a quick motion, he “held” the corpse to prevent it from exploding its innate orifice. He seamlessly snatched a copper bell from the demon’s waist and tucked it into his sleeve, then used the lifeless body as a projectile, hurling it toward a third demon cultivator amidst a dazzling magical attack.

The series of actions flowed smoothly, akin to the rhythm of flowing clouds.

With a grasp, he returned the long sword to his control, stepping onto it once more, ignoring the two low-ranked demon cultivators, and headed straight for the elusive great demon. With a flick of his toe, he dodged several magical attacks and strikes from spirit weapons, plunging the long sword into the ground. He leaped high into the air, fingers forming a seal, and his “Account Book” flying sword split into several copies, mirroring Pu Yu’s “Rain Mist.” However, the sword energy and intent of each flying sword varied in thickness, all aimed directly at the lurking dead warrior demon, vanishing in an instant.

Chen Pingan reminded Pu Yu and Ren Yi with his inner voice, his tone aged and hoarse, “Don’t be greedy for military merits; be wary of ambushes.”

The demon, seemingly a Sea-Watching realm cultivator after a prolonged battle, realized hiding was futile. He transformed, revealing himself as at least a Golden Elixir bottleneck cultivator.

A flash of sword light appeared between his brows, his innate flying sword—a mysterious power—sparkled with golden light, floating erratically around him, perfectly shielding his body. A series of crisp sounds rang out as he managed to repel the ten or so flying swords launched by the unknown old sword cultivator from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

This shifty dead warrior demon cultivator, possessing an innate flying sword radiating a hint of golden light, quickly gathered the light into a small particle, which grew increasingly brilliant as it shot straight toward the enemy’s head.

The old sword cultivator, sharp-eyed and having recognized the great demon’s identity, suddenly dove downward, agilely changing course to continue his advance.

The dead warrior demon casually grabbed a long sword left on the battlefield and slightly turned to the side, slashing at the old sword cultivator.

Bending his knees slightly, the old sword cultivator suddenly exerted force, kicking up dust as the ground trembled. His figure moved as quickly as a wisp of smoke, evading the flying sword and the long sword’s light, closing in.

The demon dead warrior cultivator felt reassured; his opponent had plenty of strange flying swords and wielded them skillfully. However, their killing power was average and not remarkable. Most of the flying swords likely concealed unknown innate abilities, which was the most troublesome aspect. Yet, seeing his enemy daring to engage in close combat, the demon cultivator felt emboldened; this old man didn’t know the meaning of danger and thought he could compete in physical resilience and strength!

In the blink of an eye, their flying swords clashed once more, summoning a flurry of golden sparks. Each side unleashed dozens of flying swords, and at a distance of less than five zhang, their innate flying swords once again collided. This time, sparks erupted as the sword energy rippled violently, causing a chaotic surge of spiritual energy. Many sparks touched the demon cultivators, inflicting excruciating pain, leaving behind gaping wounds that were bloodied and torn.

The demon sword cultivator grew even more confident; the two sides faced off, he still had some energy left, while his opponent appeared to be at their limit. The distance of five zhang allowed for clear visibility of both their expressions. As expected, the old sword cultivator’s innate flying swords, fast and numerous, were proving ineffective, causing him to feel a sense of retreat. A flicker of panic crossed his eyes as he slowed his next advance, feigning calm, then took a step back while pushing his flying swords to their limits, finally unleashing his innate ability—an interconnected sword formation that perfectly blocked the space between the two sword cultivators.

The demon cultivator had no more reservations. Although the old sword cultivator wasn’t a figure from the records, killing another Golden Elixir sword cultivator from the Sword Qi Great Wall would be an unexpected windfall—an accomplishment!

Using his innate flying sword to break through the opponent’s formation, the demon cultivator wouldn’t give the old sword cultivator a chance to retreat. He lunged forward, swinging his sword down upon the old cultivator’s head.

To dare to save someone, one must be prepared to pay with their life!

In his moment of panic, the old sword cultivator could only tilt his head, extending a hand to block the long sword; otherwise, he would inevitably be split in two.

Moments later.

The dead warrior demon cultivator appeared dazed as he looked down, his soul trembling, heart twisting in agony.

The old sword cultivator, mere inches away, still wore an expression of fear, yet his left hand firmly gripped the long sword. Not only that, but with his right hand, he had dug into the demon’s chest without breaking through the back, his fist clenched around an ethereal golden elixir. With a powerful surge of fist intent, he obliterated the nearby orifices, effectively sealing off the demon’s chance to detonate the golden elixir.

In his final moments, the dead warrior demon cultivator witnessed the old sword cultivator, seemingly engrossed in theatrics, wearing a sincere look of lingering fear. He then smiled and sheepishly admitted, “A small victory, a stroke of luck.”

The savage world’s siege army was split in two by a golden river forged by the combined might of the three teachings’ saints.

Sword immortals held their ground along the river, and the demon forces behind them could only fight desperately, isolated from any reinforcements, forced to engage with the mid-ranked sword cultivators leaving the city.

However, it wouldn’t be easy for the sword immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall to maintain their hold on the river and halt the advance of subsequent armies.

Every sword immortal needed to withstand the surging demon forces.

---

#### Outside the Battlefield

In the Jia Shen military tent.

Although the occupants were mostly young, this was the main tent among the sixty military tents, heavily guarded with numerous regulations. Visitors could only approach if they had pressing military matters. Even sword immortals or great demons would be executed on the spot if they dared to intrude.
