Today, two distinguished guests arrived at the Jia Shen tent.

One was a burly old man dressed in a bright red robe, his radiant attire shining like clouds, flickering with red light. This robe was of celestial quality, rumored to have originated from one of the entrances to the Great Abyss, a relic of immense power. The old man had a high status, comparable to the likes of Yang Zhi and Huang Luan, though their relationships were complex and fraught with enmity.

The old man was one of the candidates for the Throne of the Hall of Heroes in the savage world, possessing even greater combat strength than the great demon Chongguang. However, he had always worked alone, which is why his reputation didn’t match that of Chongguang. His last public appearance was when he had been rumored to have his lair partially destroyed by a hasty sword strike from a traveler named A Liang, which prompted him to team up with Chongguang in a furious pursuit of A Liang for tens of thousands of miles, ultimately stopping at the Sword Qi Great Wall, where he “incidentally” experienced Dong Sangeng’s sword when emerging from the city.

Beside the old man stood a young great demon, who carried five long swords on his back. Clad in a similarly famous green robe known as “Shu Jiao Lian,” he looked youthful and handsome. However, one of his eyes was devoid of life, a dull white. The young great sword immortal didn’t bother to conceal it, even neglecting to employ any illusions. If not for that eye's flaw, he could have easily matched the sword immortal Mi Yu of the Sword Qi Great Wall in appearance.

Yet, the one distinguishing factor from Mi Yu was that this sword immortal great demon was exceptionally skilled in swordsmanship and was the youngest among the upper five realms’ sword immortal demons. During the Thirteen Battles, he had bested the well-known great sword immortal Zhang Lu, leading to Zhang Lu’s disgrace, ultimately relegating him to guarding the gate of the Upside-Down Mountain, forced to spend his days with a young Daoist who enjoyed reading on a cushion. It was said that Zhang Lu had a close relationship with the sword immortal couple from Ning Mansion, though it seemed that the three friends all suffered unfortunate fates: two died in battle, and one was left as a laughingstock.

In the Jia Shen tent, the female sword cultivator Liu Bai accompanied the military tent leader, a young man in traditional wooden sandals, as they went out to greet their guests.

The young man respectfully said, “Greetings, Old Ancestor of Guanqu, Sword Immortal Shoucheng.”

Liu Bai spoke more casually, exuding familiarity as she smiled, “Good to see you, Old Ancestor of Guanqu, Senior Brother Shoucheng.”

The great demon Guanqu nodded with a smile, “Liu Bai is looking increasingly charming. When you arrive in the Haoran world, I’ll personally help you catch some gentlemen of the academy for you to choose from.”

This was the benefit of having a master.

Liu Bai’s mentor was the second-highest seat in the Throne of Hall of Heroes, known as the old bookworm Zhou Mi, praised as the “Ocean of Learning” in the savage world. Sword Immortal Shoucheng happened to be Liu Bai’s senior brother. Among Zhou Mi’s numerous disciples, all were sword cultivators: Shoucheng, Cai Ying, Tong Xuan, Tong Yin, Yu Zao, and Liu Bai, all regarded as the hundred seeds of sword immortals selected by the Moon-Viewing Mountain.

These hundred sword immortals were ranked not by the heights of their realms but by their potential. Liu Bai’s senior brother Shoucheng not only held a high current realm but was also highly ranked, right next to Liu Cha’s direct disciple Zhu Ke, and the Moon-Viewing Mountain’s closed-door disciple Li Zhen.

Liu Bai noticed something was off about Shoucheng and worryingly asked, “Senior Brother Shoucheng?”

Not understanding why, after just a few years apart, her senior brother had sustained such severe injuries. The last she heard, he was said to have left on a long journey under the command of his master.

Shoucheng pointed to the eye he had replaced behind him. Great demons had tough physiques, especially one at the upper five realms, but he hadn’t regenerated his eye nor refined the new one, seemingly allowing others to notice his blindness in one eye. He chuckled, “That old blind man took one of my eyes and fed it to his guard dog for a snack. It’s humiliating, but such is life. I can’t rest easy without avenging this grudge, but seeking revenge is no easy task. I can only show it to outsiders as a reminder, lest I forget over time.”

Wooden Sandal was utterly shocked.

Not to mention that old blind man who liked to command golden-armored puppets to move ten thousand mountains; that “guard dog” was said to be a great demon who had broken through the bottleneck to provoke trouble but ended up becoming a literal lapdog instead.

Years ago, when the great demon Guanqu had brought sword immortal Shoucheng to negotiate with that old blind man, they had hoped to enlist his help to slay their way into the Haoran world, but it had ended in discord.

Twelve against thirteen, with celestial beings opposing ascended demons; even if they couldn’t win, they at least had a chance to escape. But if the twelfth and thirteenth realms faced the next realm, there would be no room for negotiation. Of course, ascended celestial sword immortals still possessed fighting power, as long as their swords were fast enough to break through the manifestation of the Dao. The legendary fourteenth realm was not as simple as merely having a barrier-like small realm; it was said that wherever there was a person, there was the world, and the Dao pressed down everywhere, transcending the vastness of the ten thousand mountains. The ascended realm qi cultivators within would suffer the most. Hence, the celestial realm sword cultivator Shoucheng suffered greatly; it wasn’t that his sword path was lacking, but simply because that old blind man was too powerful—strong enough to be considered a deity in the savage world, akin to a “Second Elder.”

Unless the long-vanished “First Elder” was displeased and intervened personally, otherwise, all techniques and divine abilities were mere illusions, all ultimately ephemeral.

The great demon Guanqu smiled and said, “Let’s get down to business. The Jia Zi tent fears you children might feel stifled. According to military records, they’ve rejected the Jia Shen tent’s two major proposals. Hence, I was sent to discuss some insider information with you. Once we enter the Jia Shen tent, I’ll explain the situation, and you’ll know enough. But this information must not be leaked.”

Everyone in the Jia Shen tent stood up to respectfully welcome the two elders—one an ancient figure, a celestial being in their own right, with records of their name and exploits inscribed in many pages of the ancient text of the savage world; the other a young man, renowned for their military achievements, also a sword immortal.

The old man smiled and nodded, gesturing for everyone to sit, indicating they didn’t need to be overly polite.

Sword Immortal Shoucheng scanned the group. When his gaze landed on the young sword cultivators, he paused a little longer. Among them were Li Zhen, Zhu Ke, Yu Si, Tan, and his junior sister Liu Bai, making five budding sword immortals from the savage world present in the Jia Shen tent.

The great demon Guanqu stated, “Based on your plan, including me and Chongguang, how many sword immortal heads do you expect to obtain in one go?”

Wooden Sandal responded, “If we follow our strategy and only target the Sword Qi Great Wall’s Jade Purity realm sword immortals, specifically aiming to take down this group of outsiders, including Yuan Qing Shu and Pu He, if we kill two of them, the native sword immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall will surely not retreat, nor will they allow a chance to leave the battlefield. Thus, the best-case scenario is we can kill four or five Jade Purity realm sword immortals, plus two great sword immortals. In the worst case, we can still take down three Jade Purity realm sword immortals and one great sword immortal. After this, no matter what, the sword immortal guarding the river should withdraw.”

The great demon Guanqu nodded, “That’s an excellent outcome. The records from your tent were thoroughly reviewed by the Jia Zi tent, and your plan is meticulous. Even a one-for-one exchange with the Sword Qi Great Wall is entirely acceptable for us. This is also the reason why you’re so unwillingly invested, isn’t it?”

Wooden Sandal nodded, “Exactly. So many sword immortals have been forced to leave the city walls and engage in battle. Even if the three teachings’ saints designed a heavenly domain for them, granting some protection, it’s not unbreakable. As long as you all exert your full strength, if we collect fewer than four sword immortal heads, I, Wooden Sandal, would be willing to let Li Zhen behead me and present my head to the Jia Zi tent as an apology to you seniors.”

The elder chuckled, “The three teachings’ saints can create several rivers to help sever the battlefield and alleviate the pressure on the sword cultivators on the city walls. Have you deduced the outcome?”

Wooden Sandal shook his head, “We’ve made some guesses, but they were too esoteric, and we didn’t dare base our predictions of the battlefield’s progression on them.”

The elder replied, “This isn’t something to hold you accountable for. Such major matters can only be answered by the Jia Zi tent. You children could ponder for a hundred years and still be reliant on luck. The conclusion from the Jia Zi tent is three times. After that, the three teachings’ saints will harm the roots of the Dao.”

Wooden Sandal questioned, “The Jia Zi tent aims for the three teachings’ saints to perish here?”

The elder nodded, “After the Sword Qi Great Wall is breached, we can’t predict how the supporting saints stationed in the Haoran world will act, but the three teachings’ saints must die at the Sword Qi Great Wall. Therefore, the Jia Zi tent has reached a new decision. They won’t fully accept your plan, but they also won’t sit idly by and allow those sword immortals to flaunt their prowess. I, Chongguang, Shoucheng, and several others at adequate realms will all do our utmost to intervene. However, Shoucheng, Liu Bai’s master, and Zhu Ke’s master will not take action.”

The youth smiled brightly, saying, “The Jia Zi tent’s foresight is impressive. The younger generation of the Jia Shen tent deeply admires it.”

The elder lamented, “You are the future of our savage world; we are long past our prime.”

Then, the elder turned, smiling, “Of course, Shoucheng doesn’t count; he's still quite young.”

Wooden Sandal suddenly said, “Old Ancestor Guanqu, Sword Immortal Shoucheng, I have another request.”

The elder inquired, “What is it?”

Wooden Sandal detailed the previously agreed-upon encirclement scheme, hoping that when the time came for the sword immortals to guard the river, the five sword cultivators from the Jia Shen tent could join forces to ambush the new Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall, Chen Pingan. Thus, Wooden Sandal hoped that the Jia Zi tent would arrange for a senior to carve out a retreat route, ensuring that the Jia Shen tent would act judiciously, not rushing into action at the outset, which would put the senior in a perilous situation.

The elder stated, “This matter is significant. My nod of agreement won’t suffice; I need to discuss it with the Jia Zi tent. Wait for my news.”

The youth thanked him.

Liu Bai urged, “Senior Brother Shoucheng, be sure to get your master to agree.”

Shoucheng replied helplessly, “It depends on the effectiveness of your two plans. Otherwise, you know your master’s temperament too well.”

Aside from the major overall plan targeting the golden river, there was also a rising undercurrent of competition among the younger generation, ready to surge forth.

Leading from the Jia Shen tent, several military tents collaborated to carefully select a large group of demon dead warriors, mostly stagnant Golden Elixir or Nascent Soul bottleneck demons.

These formidable heroes, who had become sword cultivators yet remained as dead warriors, were given a booklet written by the Jia Shen tent before heading to the battlefield, detailing the information of fifty talented sword cultivators from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Ning Yao was featured on the front page.

Qi Shou, Gao Ye Hou, Pang Yuanji, Situ Weiran, Luo Zhenyi, Chen Sanqiu, Dong Huafu, Diezhang, Yan Zhuo, Xu Ning, Chang Taiqing, Gu Jianlong, Guo Zhujiu, Gao Youqing...

A long list of names, realms, flying swords, innate abilities, temperaments, and styles of combat, practically exhaustive in recording familiar friends likely to appear on the same battlefield, almost as detailed as the files kept by the Hidden Official lineage.

It was noted that Pang Yuanji’s name was recorded but then crossed out, with “Not to be Killed” scrawled in red ink.

During this period, a bold old Golden Elixir demon cultivator who had volunteered to serve as a dead warrior was suddenly found by the military tent cultivators and executed on the spot.

Nearby, other demon cultivators were astonished but didn’t think much of it. Those who were dead had simply died earlier, while those still alive had no need for mockery; they were just delayed in dying.

It was likely a traitor attempting to inform the Sword Qi Great Wall.

This small story about the demons and humans, sword cultivators and the cycle of life and death, the savage world and the Sword Qi Great Wall, thus vanished forever in the river of time, like a drifting leaf, floating for a long while before spinning away, leaving no trace behind.

This generation of the Sword Qi Great Wall has produced numerous talents, heralded as the second great year for sword immortals in ten thousand years. What the savage world must do next is to use the lives of their Earth Immortal sword cultivators to grind down this rival’s great year into a small year.

Though it may seem accomplished, it’s not truly a profit.

In reality, it has been proven that the pure sword intent left behind by the Sword Qi Great Wall, the older it is, the less it rejects the sword cultivators from the savage world. As long as the latter possess a pure and clear sword heart, they can also gain the favor of those ancient sword intents and seize opportunities for the Dao.

Across the realms, when it comes to sword paths and fortunes, the Sword Qi Great Wall is undoubtedly the most grand and prosperous.

Once the Sword Qi Great Wall is breached, sword immortals perish, and the younger prodigies left alive dwindle, the savage world will seize even more, allowing the seeds of a hundred sword immortals to flourish rapidly as if receiving sweet rain.

On the battlefield, Pu Yu was not idle, fully unleashing his innate flying sword “Rain Mist.” Even if he couldn’t contribute greatly, he aimed to ensure that the old sword cultivator, who seemed precarious, wouldn’t fall into a dire situation while trying to save them. After all, for sword cultivators, nurturing their flying swords not only tempered their sword intents but also refined their physiques. Given the demons' natural toughness, if they managed to become sword cultivators, their physical resilience would reach an exaggerated level.

Ren Yi worked alongside Pu Yu’s flying sword techniques, swiftly piercing through demon cultivators. However, the presence of the Golden Elixir demons meant that they deliberately abandoned Pu Yu and Ren Yi. Unless their flying swords got close enough, they specifically targeted the younger sword cultivators of lower ranks, making it challenging for the two young prodigies to unleash their swords freely.

The other young sword cultivators had received Pu Yu and Ren Yi’s warnings and focused on mutual support, controlling their flying swords to protect themselves.

That old sword cultivator who had stealthily secured a Golden Elixir into his sleeve seemed to have sustained a severe injury. He was blown away, rolling to his feet, “coughing blood” into his palm, before summoning his flying sword to poke at the already lifeless body of the dead warrior demon. Then he darted sideways, sliding several zhang across the ground, unsteadily rising and wiping blood from his face.

The old sword cultivator reached down and grabbed the long sword from the ground.

Another fierce streak of sword light shot toward him.

Another Golden Elixir demon cultivator!

The old sword cultivator held his long sword and blocked the incoming sword light, sending him skidding backward, carving a deep trench in the ground.

Ultimately, the long sword from the sword shop was broken by the sword light. The old sword cultivator pinched his fingers and commanded the broken sword back to his sheath, facing off against the isolated Golden Elixir dead warrior cultivator from a distance.

Not only were the young sword cultivators from the Sword Qi Great Wall, like Pu Yu, utterly stunned, but even the Golden Elixir demons and their subordinates were also perplexed. When did their side suddenly gain two of the most valuable sword cultivators from the savage world?

Chen Pingan had a rough idea.

The savage world had long arranged a backhand for this battle. For instance, Pu Yu and Ren Yi had each summoned a Golden Elixir sword cultivator as dead warriors.

They were older and likely those who had stagnated for years at their bottlenecks with no hope of breaking through, making them perfect candidates for dead warrior assassins.

If such situations proliferated across the battlefield, it was a meticulous scheme premeditated by the savage world, posing significant trouble for the young prodigy sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Thus, Chen Pingan no longer intended to linger long. After surveying this battlefield, he would first send a message to Wei Jin at the city walls, relaying the information to the Summer Palace before hurrying to the next battlefield.

After all, he was still Fan Dache’s protective sword master, and he needed to fulfill his promise.

Chen Pingan rolled up his sleeves, planted a foot on the ground, and instantly vanished from sight.

The Golden Elixir demon cultivator clearly felt disoriented. With his flying sword already drawn, he couldn’t find his opponent and was at a loss for what to do. 

In an instant, this weary-looking Golden Elixir cultivator was sent flying backward, his resilient body crashing through the encirclement, and the demons he struck burst apart, dying on the spot.

The old sword cultivator, dressed in the sword shop’s garments and the tailor’s robe, followed closely behind, and without waiting for the Golden Elixir cultivator’s body to hit the ground, he delivered a second punch, shattering the body along with its Golden Elixir.

The next moment, the old sword cultivator landed gracefully, quietly sending a message to the city walls. The Earth Immortal sword cultivators stationed there needed to mobilize some of their ranks to leave the city. Afterward, they should conceal their auras, aiming to ambush the opposing dead warrior cultivators.

The demon army on this battlefield scattered like birds and beasts, fleeing in a panic. Several Golden Elixir demon cultivators hastily summoned their defenses, aiming to retreat toward the south without straying too far. Transitioning to another battlefield to continue fighting wouldn’t be a mistake; besides, the battlefield was now severed, and the supervising officers from the savage world could hardly manage issues of cowardice at this point. The demons in the fray, while all desperately striving for military merits, ultimately didn’t seek death; even touching the city walls was beneficial, as it would still count as an accomplishment.

Among the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall, only Pu Yu pursued the fleeing demons.

Ren Yi cast a glance at the old sword cultivator retreating on his sword, his expression complicated.

Pu Yu said helplessly, “No need to guess; it’s that damned second shopkeeper.”

But neither of them quite understood how, in just a year apart, he’d transformed into the new Hidden Official, seeming like an entirely different person. 

Especially the weight of his final punch felt unsettling to these young sword cultivators, almost suffocating.

What would it feel like to face him on the battlefield?

The two battle-hardened prodigy sword cultivators simultaneously cleared their minds, achieving a state of clarity, their sword hearts pure and serene, striving to draw their swords faster.

As for whether that young Hidden Official had truly cultivated or was merely donning a new guise, neither cared to speculate; whatever the truth was, only heaven knew.

Regardless, they recognized that this was, in essence, someone of their generation.

Now, slaying Golden Elixirs felt as easy as picking up weeds.

Beneath both fists and swords, they felt like mere ants.

*(This chapter ends here.)*

 ### Chapter 761: Opening the Formation

Above the vast sea of clouds in the Sword Qi Great Wall, an esteemed Daoist sage stood to greet the visitor with utmost respect, bowing deeply before smiling and saying, “It’s a rare honor, truly a rare honor.”

Chen Qingdu chuckled, “To stand tall and see far is certainly better than the view from my humble little straw hut.”

Once the pleasantries were exchanged, there was little left to discuss. The venerable sword immortal merely gazed towards the bustling battlefield in the south.

Suddenly, the Daoist sage asked, “Why does that young Hidden Official seem to harbor some bias against me?”

Chen Qingdu replied, “He has grievances with the Daoist sect as a whole, not just against you personally. In fact, he is aware that such feelings are unreasonable, but it’s difficult to change one’s mindset instantly.”

There are always peculiar individuals who can easily let go of grievances aimed at themselves, yet hold onto grudges against others’ words and actions, finding it hard to forgive. The old sword immortal had encountered many such people. Without delving into distant memories, even those around him, including Pang Yuanji, fit this description.

The sage raised his sleeve and began to calculate with his fingers. Although he preferred not to engage in such practices privately, with the old sword immortal appearing, he felt no restraint. After a moment of calculation, he remarked, “I never imagined there would be such a significant grudge entangled here. No wonder, no wonder.”

This Daoist sage was the most detached person from the mundane world within the entire Sword Qi Great Wall. He had truly achieved a state of purity in his cultivation. Not only did he ignore the affairs of the Great Wall, but he also paid little attention to the rise and fall of his own sect.

No one sought him out, and he did not seek anyone in return.

The sage, responsible for safeguarding the Sword Qi Great Wall, was the most accomplished disciple of the Dao Ancestor. If he were to return to the White Jade Capital of the Celestial Realm, in the five cities and twelve towers, one of the towers—extremely high—would be his immortal abode, his place of cultivation.

Chen Qingdu said, “All these years, it’s been a waste of your time, making it difficult to progress further. You’ve worked hard.”

The Daoist quickly bowed again. “I’m honored, truly honored.”

Chen Qingdu sighed, “If that young man were to meet you in person, I suspect you two would indeed have a lot to discuss.”

The Daoist shook his head after calculating again. “Not necessarily, not necessarily.”

Chen Qingdu was not inclined to say more. It was not ideal to come and leave without saying anything, so he stood still, overlooking the southern battlefield.

The Daoist suddenly exclaimed, “Our young Hidden Official actually has some connection with that Daoist Sun from the Xuandu Temple?”

The head of the Xuandu Temple, Sun Huaizhong, was already well-versed in swordsmanship. He was also praised as the fifth person in the Celestial Realm who was unshakeable, even when struck by lightning.

The Daoist sighed, “I never expected this Sun Daoist to leave his own realm to venture into the Vast World.”

Counting was one thing, but calculating for a long time was another, almost akin to divine prophecy.

Chen Qingdu chuckled, “The lineage of the Daoist sword immortals still has some merit. That Sun Daoist is, indeed, quite interesting.”

For the old sword immortal to say that someone had “some merit” regarding swordsmanship was no small compliment. Otherwise, why would Chen Qingdu, with nothing better to do, frequently find someone to say that their swordsmanship wasn’t high enough? It was well-known that he was already the unrivaled first person in the Vast World.

The four immortal swords represented the four major schools of swordsmanship in the world.

One was from the Celestial Master’s estate in Longhu Mountain, another from the most accomplished scholar in the Central Continent, one belonged to Daoist Lao Er, and the last was claimed by the Sword Suppression Tower, one of the nine grand towers in the Vast World.

In fact, the sword possessed by the scholar of the Central Continent should rightfully belong to the Daoist sword immortal lineage. In both sentiment and reason, it should be enshrined in the ancestral hall of Xuandu Temple. However, this involved an extremely complex web of origins, and since Sun Huaizhong was more of a chivalrous man than a Daoist, he had always been unwilling to retrieve it forcefully for the Xuandu Temple.

Thus, the scholar later achieved the feat of breaking the Yellow River cave with a single strike, giving rise to the phrase that spread throughout the world: “Bai Ye’s poetry is unmatched, the most accomplished in the mortal realm.”

The Daoist reminisced, “I suddenly recall that at Xuandu Temple, when the peach blossoms bloom, if there are yellow orioles among the flowers, it is especially enchanting; the eyes dare not move, the heart and soul stirred.”

Chen Qingdu laughed, “Isn’t it ‘extremely beautiful, extremely beautiful’?”

The Daoist shook his head, “That is too mundane.”

————

At the wine shop with three storefronts, business was rather slow. It wasn’t just this shop; all the taverns and inns in the city were similarly quiet.

The elderly, young, women, and children—only those whose life-force swords had been broken or those unworthy of being called sword cultivators remained in the city; especially with the fierce battle raging over the city wall, few would spend money on drinks at such a time.

The two young attendants in the shop, the boy Qiulong and the girl Liu E, were puzzled because the youngest colleague in the shop, the child Taoban, had previously rushed over to Feng Kangle and whispered something, then ran off together. When they returned, the two children were already bruised and dusty. After taking their seats, Feng Kangle had his father prepare two big bowls of plain noodles, and the two, being too small, had to lean over the table to eat, their feet dangling off the ground. There were no condiments because Taoban said that without buying drinks, they couldn’t have any, as it was the shop’s rule.

Liu E sat down beside them and asked with a smile, “What happened?”

Feng Kangle was sullen, burying his head in the noodles.

Taoban huffed, “A bunch of little bastards said our second shopkeeper is heartless, not a good person, and said a lot of nasty things. Aren’t they asking for a beating? So, Kangle and I gave them a good thrashing.”

The girl teased, “So who beat up whom?”

Feng Kangle scoffed, “They had more people, okay? How could the two of us fight? A good man travels the rivers and lakes, but two fists can’t take on four hands; it’s written in books, don’t you know that?”

Taoban was getting angrier, “What’s most infuriating is those who just watched from the sidelines. They heard our second shopkeeper’s untold stories and didn’t even help us. These guys are even more heartless.”

Liu E bit back her laughter, “I’ll get those two eggs for you; you can use them for your bruises.”

Taoban nodded, “Kangle, let your dad make us two bowls of plain noodles; we’ll each have a bowl with a fried egg. That’ll be delicious.”

Feng Kangle leaned over, whispering, “No, no, no, we’re injured—better wait a bit, it’s best if the second shopkeeper doesn’t see us.”

Taoban asked, “Why? The second shopkeeper is so stingy; he won’t give you any money.”

Feng Kangle chuckled, “I want to hear more stories.”

Taoban rolled his eyes, “And then tell that little girl? You’re too young; you don’t realize that these pretty girls are clever. Whether they have money at home is what truly matters.”

Feng Kangle laughed, “My family is rich now.”

Taoban quietly ate his plain noodles.

Feng Kangle scratched his head and softly said, “Taoban, if you ever run out of money, remember to borrow from me first. I have a pot full of copper coins; it’s so heavy now I can barely lift it! But that’s all my wife’s money. When you get a wife, remember to pay me back.”

Feng Kangle and Taoban talked about everything. Once, he recounted his grievances about getting up in the middle of the night to relieve himself, only to fall asleep next to the broom at the door. His parents searched for him all night, eventually finding him, leading to a beating that made him cry out loud. Upon hearing this, Taoban lowered his head and began to cry. Later, Feng Kangle learned that Taoban’s ancestors had all worked in a clothing workshop, and he hardly ever saw his parents.

Taoban suddenly smiled, “Actually, I quite like that little girl.”

Feng Kangle was stunned.

Taoban burst into laughter, “Just kidding! What’s so good about a girl?”

Feng Kangle laughed along.

The young boy Qiulong brought over two eggs and said, “Put it on my tab.”

Taoban imitated the second shopkeeper, giving a thumbs up. “Generous!”

Feng Kangle nodded, “I’m good friends with the second shopkeeper; our relationship is strong. I’ll have him act as a matchmaker and set you up with Liu E.”

The boy was left speechless.

The girl’s face turned beet red, her face resembling a blossoming peach flower.

———

The Hidden Official’s cold-weather palace was usually empty, but today it was filled with over ten people.

Apart from an elderly woman with white hair, all were children, the youngest being four or five years old, the oldest no more than seven or eight, with both boys and girls among them. They came from very different backgrounds, some being wealthy children from Tai Xiang Street and Jade Ruler Street, while others were street urchins who had to fight and scrape to survive.

The old woman said, “You are all budding warriors. In the past, we had martial arts masters in the Sword Qi Great Wall, but most didn’t live long. It’s challenging to survive past a hundred years. The path of martial arts relies on talent, but even more on diligent practice. Thus, if one lives a shorter life, their realm is naturally limited. I count as one of the fortunate ones. Do you know who I am?”

A bold child from Tai Xiang Street, despite being young, replied confidently, “You’re Granny Bai from the Ning House, a tough old lady.”

“Correct, I am Bai Lianshuang, from the Ning House, a female warrior with decent boxing skills.” The old woman smiled and nodded, then kicked the child in the abdomen, sending him flying and rolling on the ground, curled up in pain with tears and snot streaming down his face.

The old woman asked, “Do you know why I’ve gathered you here?”

A pale-faced girl from Jade Ruler Street trembled and said, “Granny Bai, I want to become a sword cultivator. I don’t want to learn martial arts; martial arts lead to no future.”

The old woman rubbed the girl’s head and pressed down gently, causing her to sit on the ground. She glanced at the more delicate child on the floor, gauging carefully; she could only say that his bone structure was acceptable. With a smile, she said, “Whether you want to become a sword cultivator or not is a different matter from whether you can become one. In my early years, I had similar thoughts as you, but not being able to become a sword cultivator is simply unavoidable. One cannot force it.”

Just as the girl was about to speak, the old woman smiled and continued, “Don’t rush. A month from now, those who want to learn martial arts may not necessarily stay, while those who don’t want to may end up staying.”

The old woman turned her gaze to the group of children who were cautious but had fiery eyes. “The aptitude for martial arts is not as crucial as learning swordsmanship, at least not in relative terms. However, to succeed, you must endure significant hardships. Would you agree?”

The children nodded in unison.

The old woman said, “First, I’ll teach you a couple of basic stances. Without stances, there can be no martial arts. I’ll teach you a standing and walking stance. It’s simple to start, but mastering it is not easy. Practicing martial arts, you must first achieve proficiency.”

After teaching the eight children the standing and walking stances, she walked slowly, observing the children awkwardly trying to hold their stances, and said, “To punch a thousand times leads to natural movement. Whether you believe this statement or not, understand the principle behind it: you must practice your punches more. What you shouldn’t doubt is that just because you’ve punched a thousand times, it doesn’t mean you will naturally master it. Even if you are a martial arts genius with excellent bone structure, talent, and temperament, merely punching a thousand times is still insufficient to grasp the essence of the punches.”

The child who had just rolled on the ground sat up and grit his teeth, saying, “What about that genius martial artist from the Central Continent, Cao Ci? Doesn’t he need to practice a thousand punches for the same technique? Certainly not!”

The old woman was not angry; she looked at the child and smiled, “In the Vast World, martial arts are grand, and pure martial artists can punch without reason, yet they also pay attention to learning etiquette before mastering the techniques and virtue before practicing martial arts.”

The child crossed his arms, sneering, “I’m talking about martial arts, and you’re lecturing me on principles? Granny Bai, I doubt your martial arts skills are that impressive.”

The old woman’s expression softened further, as she walked around the eight children who were beginning to sway in their stances. “A righteous heart leads to righteous punches, while a wicked heart leads to wicked punches. Thus, teaching punches is teaching people.”

The child observed the increasingly smiling old woman and sensed something was amiss, so he loudly declared, “You’re just an old lady! Learning punches from you is worse than learning from the second shopkeeper; he’s a real expert! I’ve seen him strike firsthand! Sure, he lost to Cao Ci three times earlier, but didn’t he win against Yu Jianfu three times afterward?”

The old woman laughed heartily, “You little brat are quite clever! Alright, enough! Stand up and join the others in their stances. If you stand well, you’ll take fewer hits. The six-step walking stance I taught you just now is from Mr. Chen.”

The child stood up, rubbing his belly, and grinned through gritted teeth; it genuinely hurt.

The old woman smiled; the child’s pain was real, merely flesh wounds, and he would soon endure it.

The child muttered, “A family with a handful of grain won’t eat this way.”

The old woman shot him a glance.

The child immediately howled, “I’ll learn! I’ll learn, alright?”

The old woman felt somewhat helpless. Dealing with children was indeed more suited for her son-in-law.

In truth, even teaching punches was not her forte.

Even if Bai Lianshuang had once been the only tenth-tier martial artist of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Even if she had fed punches to her son-in-law in the Ning House, the old woman herself felt guilty and truly couldn’t bring herself to be harsh or deliver heavy strikes.

However, her son-in-law had said that the seeds of martial artists in the Sword Qi Great Wall were inconspicuous, but how they would fare in the future was uncertain. Even if one had a skill, it was ultimately a good thing.

————

Chen Pingan found a secluded area and swiftly changed his appearance to that of a youthful figure.

Secretly taking out a borrowed long sword from a sword workshop, he stowed the broken sword behind him into his spatial item, intending to return it to Pang Yuanji later.

Once he resumed sword riding, his aura instantly transformed from that of a worn-out elder into that of a vibrant young man, with bright eyes and an energetic demeanor.

The great refining swords were to be drawn only during crucial times; unless in emergencies, one must not unsheathe a sword. 

All of his celestial-grade swords, the “Sword Immortal” and his golden robes, had been handed over to Ning Yao.

Thus, Chen Pingan’s sword riding journey, coupled with the summoning of one or two of his “ledger” swords, served as the best disguise for him to enter the battlefield as a genuine sword cultivator.

As for the face masks made by Zhu Lian, those were secondary.

After all, having more skills than necessary was always beneficial.

Chen Pingan’s heart stirred as he soared quickly to a higher vantage point, surveying the battlefield’s situation before descending back down closer to the ground.

On the battlefield, thousands of sword cultivators were steadily advancing southward, continuously compressing the demon army.

The fiercest fighting was along the golden river, where the demon army surged and crashed against the sword immortals defending the river. Often, after a sword immortal struck, the gaps left behind allowed the demon army to quickly form a sloped hill, pressing against the invisible barrier of this small world, causing the golden river’s waves to splash blood everywhere. Each retreat of the waves left behind countless bones, which were subsequently covered by the demon horde, layer upon layer, constantly eroding the words inscribed along the banks of the golden river.

The sword immortals could only slightly retract their swords, sweeping their blades across the immediate battlefield to prevent too many bones and flesh from accumulating in place, which would wear down the golden river.

Each character inscribed in gold, akin to tiny flying insects, and each golden lotus swaying in the river, were constantly disappearing. It was only because the three great sages were continuously bestowing their powers from afar that this small world did not dissipate too quickly.

On that battlefield, several mighty demons had already appeared, many of whom wielded innate supernatural abilities, such as moving mountains and diverting rivers, continuously hurling mountains at the golden river and the heads of the sword immortals, or unleashing torrents of heavy, foul rain.

Some of the larger demons directly employed spells to tear the earth apart, boring into the ground, and with a thunderous roar, they would rip through the surface, braving a sword immortal’s strike to attempt to turn the unyielding golden river into a suspended one, thus swiftly linking the demon armies from the southern battlefield to those in the north.

Sitting at both ends of the city wall, two sages simultaneously unleashed their great abilities, causing the waters of the entire river to surge violently as if cascading down in waterfalls. At the same time, the roots of each golden lotus plunged deep into the earth along with the flowing river, where lines of delicate golden characters wound around them, the content consisting of famous poems praising the lotus by literary masters and poets of the world.

Among the golden river beneath a female sword immortal, a particularly large and beautiful lotus bloomed, towering over a hundred feet high, its fragrance wafting far and wide, condensing strands of golden spiritual energy that eventually coalesced into beads of water, cascading down onto the lotus leaves, creating a tinkling sound.

Lines of golden characters danced like birds and swayed like trees, charmingly graceful.

“Flowers of water, land, and plants; how many are truly lovely?” 

“Not vine-like nor brambly, standing tall and pure. Emerging from the muddy waters, yet not stained.”

The female sword immortal, Zhou Cheng, landed gracefully on the ever-expanding lotus leaf, standing amidst the golden lotus, the heavens and earth appearing a bit clearer, and spiritual energy abundant.

With each strike she made, her movements became increasingly fluid and expressive.

At that moment, the already stunning female sword immortal became even more breathtaking.

Alongside her, a male sword immortal, Mi Hu, fought fiercely, his strikes flowing seamlessly, and at the same time, he communicated with her through thought, “You really don’t want to be my sister-in-law?”

Zhou Cheng replied nonchalantly, “Mi Yu is nothing but a decorative pillow, and he likes to say things that I don’t understand—extremely annoying.”

Mi Hu fell silent for a moment before asking, “Then what about me?”

Zhou Cheng also paused for a moment before responding, “Too ugly.”

Recently becoming a great sword immortal, Mi Hu was not angered; instead, he burst into hearty laughter, launching another strike, showcasing his extraordinary style.

In the face of life and death, one could see the great charm of sword immortals.

Chen Pingan rode his sword swiftly, heading towards a certain part of the southern battlefield, searching for those sword cultivators who were advancing southward the quickest.

With Diezhang and Dong Heitan leading the way, it was difficult to slow down.

The demon army also abandoned the thought of charging headlong, as if they could successfully slay those sword cultivators emerging from the city, their contributions would be far greater than merely attempting to scale the city walls. Moreover, once they approached the city wall, the sword immortals stationed there would only become fiercer, leading to swift deaths. Surrounding and hunting those sword cultivators on the battlefield would at least grant them a few more moments of life.

Thus, south of the Sword Qi Great Wall and north of the golden river, a series of encirclements of varying sizes inadvertently formed on the vast battlefield.

Whether near or far, many familiar faces were visible.

The sword immortal Tao Wen stood at the front lines of the most distant battlefield, steadfastly guarding that golden river alongside other sword immortals.

Closer to the action, besides the previously encountered Pu Yu and Ren Yi, there was also the Yuan Ying sword cultivator Ye Zhenchun, who had taken on the role of a protective formation sword master, as well as frequent patrons of the wine shop who had consumed many bowls of plain noodles and many drinks, alongside various gamblers and scoundrels.

While searching for Ning Yao and the others, Chen Pingan could only do what he could to save a few sword cultivators in dire situations, allowing them to temporarily escape the encirclement.

According to the regulations established by the Hidden Official’s lineage, in the southward advance to carve formations and eliminate the demon army, sword cultivators of different realms would have different distances to progress. Once they reached that distance or eliminated the corresponding number of demons, they could retreat back to the base of the Sword Qi Great Wall for rest; if they had the strength, they could continue southward, but if they suffered severe losses, they would have to ascend the city wall, swapping out for a fresh batch of sword cultivators to replace them in the battlefield. It was absolutely forbidden to be greedy for merit or to think of exchanging lives with the demons.

The sword cultivators on the city wall above and below the same battle line were to retreat and advance, the former needing to be decisive; otherwise, once the descending sword cultivators became overly attached to battle and refused to retreat, suffering heavy casualties, the latter would have to exit the city early to fill the gaps. Over time, the entire north-south battle line would become utterly rotten, turning into a mess requiring additional sword cultivators to clean up.

In the end, the Hidden Official’s lineage still hoped that the sword cultivators could survive and continue to strike, thus allowing them to save more lives.

However, a war inevitably meant that people would continue to die, and die again.

Life and death, on the battlefield, were like neighbors facing each other through a door.

The demon army, blocked from retreat, had to be annihilated, and the middle-tier sword cultivators beneath the Sword Qi Great Wall needed to minimize their battle losses.

The migratory troops from the Savage World heading towards the northern battlefield continued to arrive, but every time a sword cultivator from the Sword Qi Great Wall fell, it meant a loss of strength for the Great Wall. These were merely cold calculations on paper; what about the calculations of the human heart?

On the battlefield where both sides were slaughtering each other, the group of sword cultivators closest to the golden river, who had emerged from the city, suddenly halted their advance in unison.

Even the fierce Diezhang sheathed her sword, choosing to retreat a few dozen feet, holding her great sword firmly while bending slightly, the tip of her sword resting against the ground, standing shoulder to shoulder with Dong Huafu.

Their innate flying swords continued to strike down enemies without pause.

The reason was simple; they had broken the formation too quickly, and demons surrounded them on both sides.

In the further back of the battlefield stood Ning Yao, wearing golden robes and carrying a sword box containing the Sword Immortal, holding only one sword in her hand.

Twenty feet to Ning Yao’s left and right stood Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo.

Fan Dache stood even further back.

This group of sword cultivators should have advanced over a hundred and fifty miles before beginning to retreat and cut down the numerous stragglers behind them.

However, just a moment ago, Ning Yao had said something felt off.

The situation that could make Ning Yao feel uneasy was something Diezhang and Dong Heitan had to treat with utmost caution.

Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo liked to wield their respective swords, “Scripture” and “Purple Lightning,” as flying swords.

Apart from their innate flying swords, the trajectories of their two extra swords were extremely orderly. Chen Sanqiu’s long sword “Scripture” flew in a large circle around him, while Yan Zhuo’s “Purple Lightning” traced a somewhat higher circle, both swords not conflicting. If any demons were to rely on luck or brute force to sneak into their encirclement, they wouldn’t need to interfere, leaving it all to Ning Yao and Fan Dache to clean up—simple and direct.

As for the careless Diezhang and the clumsy Dong Heitan, Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo didn’t bother with them.

After all, if there was truly an unexpected situation, the one in charge, Ning Yao, would take action to resolve it.

Chen Sanqiu originally had another cloud-patterned sword, which he had lent to Fan Dache.

These highly ranked swords were all borrowed from the imitation White Jade Capital of the Great Li Dynasty by A Liang.

Only the “Vast Energy” sword that Diezhang favored had been taken to the Vast World by a certain Confucian gentleman.

Ning Yao then said, “There must be an ambush. I’ll hold off the highest realm opponents for a moment; you all just focus on retreating.”

Her tone was similar to her usual light-hearted manner, but only Diezhang, another woman, could detect the subtle undertones.

Ning Yao held a slight grudge.

Diezhang felt helpless as well; ever since all the sword cultivators of the Hidden Official’s lineage moved to the cold-weather palace, the young Hidden Official had not shown up on the city wall for too long.

Even Fan Dache, who had finally reached the Yuan Dan realm, had not come to celebrate, and he was the first to want to share the good news—not his friend Chen Sanqiu.

Ning Yao glanced around; the battlefield situation was, in fact, not unusual; after all, the area was swarming with demon forces from every direction.

Ning Yao frowned. She was about to remind Fan Dache to retreat first, and let Diezhang and Dong Huafu guard him from behind to prevent him from being surrounded by the demon horde. As for herself, she could afford to return to the north a bit slower alongside Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo. Both of her friends had protective charms and life-saving talismans, and Yan Zhuo was particularly adept at self-preservation. Their killing speed might not match Diezhang and Dong Heitan, but they maintained a good balance between killing and self-defense.

However, before Ning Yao could convey her thoughts, she was surprised to see Fan Dache already soaring into the air on his sword, decisively withdrawing to the north without a word.

Ning Yao was puzzled; when did Fan Dache become so perceptive?

Not only that, but he was also being guided by a boy who appeared to be “swaying” as he rode his sword, narrowly dodging the demon army’s magical artifacts. Eventually, the boy firmly grabbed Fan Dache’s shoulder, cheerfully calling out, “Let’s go!” as he swung his arm, delivering a solid kick to the hilt of Fan Dache’s cloud-patterned sword, propelling him and his sword away swiftly.

The somewhat awkward exit of the golden dan sword cultivator Fan Dache became a quick retreat; he wasted no time, focusing solely on fleeing.

The reasons were twofold: the long-awaited call of “Dache!” and the newcomer’s succinct words, “Aren’t you going to run? Do you want to give away your life?”

Simultaneously, every sword cultivator’s heart resonated with an all-too-familiar voice, quick and decisive, “Retreat in order; I will be the rear guard with Ning Yao. Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo will provide support in the center. Diezhang and Dong Heitan will clear the way behind Fan Dache. We must maintain a distance of over a hundred feet between us—not too far, not too short. There are many hidden ambushes; I’ve presently identified two locations: one northeast of Diezhang, about thirty feet away, and one southwest of Fan Dache, roughly a hundred and twenty feet away. Be cautious; the opponents are likely sword cultivators starting at the Yuan Dan realm, with the highest likelihood of some Yuan Ying-level cultivators, possibly even Jade Skin sword immortals. Stay alert.”

“Especially be cautious of opponents targeting Dache first; they may attempt to encircle him. Dache, please be more subtle with your sword’s trajectory; do you plan to crash right into their flying swords?”

“Sanqiu, Fat Yan, be prepared to use your most trusted protective artifacts at any moment. The enemies in this ambush are determined to achieve their goal. The death warriors are all demon sword cultivators, and they will not let us retreat easily. Remember to protect Fan Dache at all times.”

The usual nagging, chattering voice.

Chen Pingan could only arrange the formations at the fastest possible pace; there was no need for further speculation.

There were bound to be two or three Yuan Ying-level death warriors hiding well, waiting for the right moment to strike. Perhaps there might even be an even deeper-hidden Jade Skin sword immortal among the demons, ready to disregard their life to issue a strike.

The reasoning was simple: apart from the newly promoted Yuan Dan Fan Dache, everyone else among the sword cultivators was on the Savage World’s death list.

Ning Yao, Chen Sanqiu, Dong Huafu, Diezhang, and Yan Zhuo—all were among the elite of the Sword Qi Great Wall in recent years.

Ning Yao raised an eyebrow, appearing somewhat annoyed by the person’s incessant chatter, but in her eyes, which were the most beautiful in the world, there was a subtle ripple of happiness, joy, and pride.

Like ripples in a lake stirred by a gentle spring breeze.

A tall boy hovered on his sword beside her.

They were no longer merely Ning Yao of the Sword Qi Great Wall and Chen Pingan of the Vast World.

They were sword cultivators appearing together on the battlefield.

Every beginning is difficult, and this guy next to her tended to overthink, making things even harder than the initial challenge. 

But once he got started, she didn’t have to worry about him anymore.

For instance, when he liked her.

Or when he practiced fists.

Or when he aimed to become a sword cultivator and eventually a great sword immortal.

Ning Yao asked telepathically, “Innate flying swords?”

Chen Pingan smiled and replied, “Two.”

Ning Yao fell silent again.

See? 

Chen Pingan had no idea what Ning Yao was pondering and couldn’t afford to guess her thoughts.

What worried him the most was that the enemy’s death warriors had chosen to remain silent, continuing to conceal their tracks.

The battle line that Ning Yao and the others were responsible for, on the city wall side, had neither subsequent sword cultivators to replace those descending from the city nor did they need to kill more enemies; they had to carve formations as swiftly as possible, penetrating deep into the enemy lines to approach the golden river for their mission to be accomplished.

Once both sides reached a stalemate, the newly minted Yuan Dan Fan Dache would become the best breakthrough point.

It would not make sense to require Fan Dache to directly leave the battlefield and watch from the sidelines, both sentimentally and reasonably.

No matter what, Chen Pingan could only confirm that his arrival might have killed one unexpected outcome but could also bring forth an even larger unforeseen event.

This was akin to the two plans proposed by Xuan Can and Xu Ning—before the results were revealed, no one knew which choice was better.

The most helpless part was that Xu Ning’s plan, once implemented by the Hidden Official’s lineage, might not necessarily yield a better result than Xuan Can’s, but at that moment, Chen Pingan was unwilling to voice such heavy words, nor could Miao Shi say it, and Lin Junbi was too afraid to say so.

Calculating human affairs compared to the calculations of heaven gave a sense of insignificance and helplessness, no matter how hard one tried to plan.

This was Chen Pingan’s most profound realization after becoming the Hidden Official.

The group continued to fight while retreating.

Diezhang and Dong Heitan did their best to protect Fan Dache as they withdrew from the battlefield, with Ning Yao and Chen Pingan stationed behind them. Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo were free from concerns, focusing on slaying demons.

Ning Yao did not summon her flying sword; she simply wielded her sword, still giving the impression that the essence of swordsmanship in the world boiled down to the notion of straightforwardness.

With one strike after another, Ning Yao’s demeanor shifted from calm to swift, her sword energy cutting through and dismembering a large expanse of foes.

As a result, Chen Pingan, riding his sword close to Ning Yao, found himself momentarily idle, attentively observing the intricate details of the battlefield.

Adding to this, the two death sword cultivators who had previously exposed themselves were discovered by Chen Pingan, along with a demon sword cultivator emanating Yuan Dan energy, who had unwittingly been swept by Ning Yao’s sword energy, narrowly dodging it. To conceal his identity, he intentionally suffered some injuries, allowing his shoulder to be sliced by the sword energy, leaving a large gash.

Ning Yao’s strikes aimed for speed, sometimes appearing somewhat aimless, clearly intentional, allowing Chen Pingan to observe more subtle details.

When Ning Yao’s group of sword cultivators, who had been the most rapid in breaking formations and closest to the golden river, unexpectedly became the sword cultivators closest to the city wall instead.

Chen Sanqiu and the others didn’t mind this at all.

After all, the demon army along this line wouldn’t contest their advance.

Furthermore, no one felt they would penetrate the formation any slower than the sword cultivators in other lines.

Because with Ning Yao, and now Chen Pingan, everyone felt this was the most reasonable outcome.

Having temporarily distanced themselves from the precarious situation, Fan Dache hesitated to speak.

Chen Sanqiu whispered, “It’s alright; don’t feel embarrassed.”

Diezhang and the others similarly thought that Fan Dache was planning to return to the city first.

However, Fan Dache said, “Since I have the lowest realm and the least skill, let me be the bait. I’m not afraid of thieves; I’m afraid they’re covetous. Instead of everyone being distracted, it’s better to take the initiative.”

Chen Pingan was somewhat surprised.

Fan Dache looked towards Chen Pingan, “Protective formation sword master, what do you say?”

Chen Pingan thought for a moment and nodded with a smile, “Alright.”

He glanced towards the battlefield ahead, where an immensely peculiar scene unfolded: the demon army clustered in a line just one hundred feet away from this group of young sword cultivators from the Sword Qi Great Wall, and they surprisingly showed no inclination to advance.

Chen Pingan said, “I’ll guard the rear. You all just focus on your strikes.”

Then he looked at Ning Yao, who nodded, “Alright.”

Ning Yao returned her long sword to its sheath behind her, but the Sword Immortal was still in hand, “I’ll open the formation.”

Diezhang and Dong Heitan exchanged glances, laughing, “Alright.”

Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo were filled with anticipation.

The reasoning was simple: what would it feel like to fight alongside Fan Dache?

Then for Chen Sanqiu and the others, who had fought alongside Ning Yao over the years, it was even more profound.

Because Ning Yao had always accommodated and cared for these “geniuses”; she had been constrained for too long in her strikes.

Finally, Ning Yao added, “Opening the formation will be quick; don’t fall behind.”

(End of this chapter)

 ### Chapter 762: No Sword to Draw

In the realm of martial arts, Cao Ci was to fists what Ning Yao was to swords. It was as if they were born with an innate connection to the grand cosmic forces of heaven and earth. This was a stark contrast to Chen Ping'an's first life sword, "Caged Sparrow," and Qi Jinglong's self-proclaimed sword, "Regulation," both of which represented their own unique mastery of flying swords and could create a small realm of their own. The former two, however, were on an entirely different level.

Thus, when Ning Yao stepped out of the formation, holding her sword poised to break through the enemy lines, the originally stalled demonic army inexplicably began to retreat. This caused the front lines of the army to become more densely packed, almost comically cumbersome.

Perhaps this was the instinctive response of all living things to the changing tides of nature, just as humans can sense the seasons shift between warmth and cold. 

Chen Ping'an was genuinely looking forward to witnessing Ning Yao unleash her sword without reservation. He had never seen the true Ning Yao on the battlefield before. As for the sword spirit that had taken him countless hardships to tame, which had a temperament as prickly as a nobleman, it now behaved like a sweet young girl in Ning Yao's hands, and he didn't mind one bit.

Ning Yao walked calmly forward, not in haste to strike the first blow. The sword in her hand shimmered with golden light, and her striking golden battle robe made her appear like a divine being walking among mortals on the battlefield.

Seizing the opportunity, Chen Ping'an communicated with Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo through his thoughts, inquiring about the battlefield details from their previous assaults. He asked for information on the high-ranking, uninjured demon cultivators at the Dragon Gate and Golden Core levels—their approximate numbers, appearances, and magical abilities. During their earlier retreat, Chen Ping'an had focused more on searching for the hidden sword cultivator death warriors, inevitably missing a substantial number of details.

Asking about Diezhang or Dong Huafu would have been fruitless; after all, they had been too busy fighting and dodging flying swords to keep track of their contributions.

Chen Ping'an quickly reminded everyone through his thoughts, "As we break through the enemy lines next, don't overly concern yourselves with killing enemies on the spot. I and Fan Dache will cover a few strikes; aside from Ning Yao breaking the formation, just focus on that. Sanqiu, for you four, the most important thing is to rely on large-scale 'friendly fire' to force the death warriors to reveal themselves. I'll clarify their identities and positions one by one. If the timing is right, feel free to act on your own. Fan Dache and I will adapt and follow up. If things get out of hand, listen for my reminders and adjust accordingly to aim for a joint kill."

Fan Dache was feeling somewhat anxious; after all, he worried about becoming a burden to his friends. However, after hearing Chen Ping'an's detailed battle arrangements, he felt a little more at ease.

"Dache," Chen Ping'an said to him, "how can the heroism that comes from a moment of heated impulse not be heroism?"

Fan Dache took a deep breath and replied with a smile, "That's true."

Now, Dong Huafu’s appearance was caught between that of a youth and a young man; he only had the wrong name given by his parents and none of the nicknames from his wandering friends. Dong Heitan (Dong Black Charcoal) was indeed a bit dark and would likely never shake off that nickname. He was known for his lavish spending and never borrowing anything.

He chose the sword named "Rouge," delicate in style and whimsical in design, with a blade as slender as a willow branch.

Diezhang held the "Zhenyu" sword, a one-armed shopkeeper whose graceful figure made her look like a strikingly beautiful woman, wielding a broad sword.

With the bloodlustiest Dong Huafu and Diezhang following closely behind Ning Yao, they aimed to assist her in tearing a larger hole in the demonic army.

If Ning Yao's sword strike determined the speed at which their group of sword cultivators could break the formation, then Diezhang and Dong Huafu had no small responsibility. If the overall killing power of their seven-person sword formation wasn’t overwhelming enough, even if they successfully penetrated the enemy's lines at top speed, their advancement toward the golden river where the sword spirit was stationed would ultimately hold minimal significance for the entire battlefield.

Positioned behind Diezhang and Dong Huafu were Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo, tasked with helping the former two secure the front line and eliminate more demons across the battlefield.

As the formation was about to open, Chen Ping'an gathered himself, his mind immersed. He kept his sword hovering just a few feet above the ground. While he might not be able to conceal his identity from certain death warrior sword cultivators, he had a hidden purpose. If those sword cultivators, seeking stability, alerted certain important demon cultivators outside the death warriors via their thoughts, then with just one or two careless glances toward the "young sword cultivator," Chen Ping'an would have the opportunity to identify one or two critical enemies.

To do great deeds, one must be meticulous.

As the six sword cultivators advanced, Chen Ping'an found himself unknowingly positioned at the very back of the battlefield and suddenly chuckled. Indeed, Ning Yao looked best in that golden robe.

As for the earlier disdain he had for the young master Pu Yu’s snow-white robe, that thought had completely slipped his mind.

Of course, Ning Yao, being on the battlefield, was not subject to any illusions; her sword friends were all younger geniuses from the same generation, and more importantly, Ning Yao’s swordplay was far too conspicuous.

After all, someone like Chen Ping'an, who advocated that skills should never weigh one down, would find it unnecessary to exert twice the effort to defeat an enemy when half would suffice. When he was ruthless, he was even willing to cover for a woman, pretending to be a demon's inside man, a rare sight indeed.

In the blink of an eye, Ning Yao flashed forward, covering dozens of yards in an instant, and swept her sword horizontally.

The front lines of the demonic army, spanning over a hundred yards, were severed in half by the golden sword light.

A Yuan Ying demon cultivator overseeing the battlefield issued commands from the rear and, using a spell, obliterated dozens of retreating demons who were already hesitant on the battlefield.

Ning Yao glided forward in a straight line, after delivering one strike, she was too disdainful to strike again. Instead, she relied on her overwhelming sword aura to forge a path, which, in its essence, resembled the highest sword arts. The sheer abundance of sword energy and overwhelming momentum created an indestructible mini realm of sword formations, making it so that whether she targeted an enemy depended on whether they were worthy of her attention.

The demon cultivators, reluctant and fearful, unleashed numerous spiritual artifacts and a few life treasures, wildly hurling them at her sword aura. Their concern for collateral damage among their own forces had long since vanished. They only hoped to wear down that unmatched sword aura, or else if they allowed Ning Yao to break through, their losses would be catastrophic, and their forces would dwindle rapidly. A grand war, sweeping and tumultuous, could yield results through sheer numbers, but in certain specific battlefields, that was not always the case.

Facing Ning Yao, there was no hope for such a consideration.

In any case, all they needed to do was regard Ning Yao as a sword immortal, regardless of her cultivation level.

Whether she was a Golden Core or a Yuan Ying sword cultivator was irrelevant.

This was a universally acknowledged truth between the Sword Qi Great Wall and the savage wilderness.

In an instant, Ning Yao traversed the battlefield littered with corpses. Wherever her sword aura touched, demons were pulverized, their souls shattered alongside them. Earlier life treasures and spiritual artifacts lay broken or fragmented, unable to impede her advance. With her single sword, she swiftly made her way into the heart of the demonic army. With one hand, she applied a gentle force to the sword spirit wrapped in golden light, and with her other hand, her fingers converging, she casually executed a sword art. The golden rays on the sword spirit exploded outward, and in a radius of several miles on the battlefield, except for the Golden Core cultivators who managed to escape in time, and those who fought with life treasures as shields, everyone else perished.

From a distance, Chen Ping'an observed this scene, as if a golden lotus had bloomed in his heart.

In another instant, Ning Yao shot several hundred yards away, targeting a Golden Core demon. With one sword strike down, she looked up and softly called, “Come here.”

The Golden Core demon, panicking as it commanded its troops, never expected such "good fortune" to face a sword strike alone. It immediately summoned a life treasure, an ancient weapon resembling a spear, inscribed with golden symbols. Gripping the weapon with both hands, the Golden Core demon spun it around, creating a faint golden circle of protective symbols, similar to a defensive array. Furthermore, a string of pale golden cloud-like glyphs wrapped around its body, providing an effect akin to a protective armor.

With the symbol array firmly guarding its front and an armor-like shield draped over it, the demon’s physique was already quite resilient. 

That treasure, both offensive and defensive, was undoubtedly a remarkable celestial artifact. In the heart of the righteous world, even a Yuan Ying cultivator would feel envy upon seeing it.

Sadly, as the golden line fell from above, the symbol array, the golden armor, and the Golden Core demon cultivator were all cleaved in two.

The ground was carved by that astonishing golden line, creating a long ravine.

The breaking of the symbol array, the golden armor, and the demon’s body—all were mere consequences of Ning Yao's casual sword strike.

When Ning Yao paused slightly, revealing herself on the battlefield, the surrounding demonic army had already begun to retreat frantically. However, when she casually uttered the words "come here," an extraordinary phenomenon unfolded.

Around Ning Yao, four strands of ancient pure sword intent roamed the heavens and the earth, as if summoned by her command, they all descended straight to the ground. The originally fleeting sword intent suddenly gained life and spirit, not only summoned forth for the first time by a junior sword cultivator from the Sword Qi Great Wall, but also able to absorb the abundant sword energy from the world. The four strands of exquisite sword intent reached high into the clouds and deep into the earth, continuously expanding like grand columns of a great hall.

In the end, four mighty pillars of sword intent connected the heavens and the earth.

Instantly, countless thin strands of sword intent branched out, weaving through the entire realm.

This time, not a single person remained alive on the battlefield around Ning Yao, and all the demonic army was reduced to a pulp, their bodies and souls, along with the cultivators' life treasures and weapons, utterly obliterated.

Ning Yao once again surged forward, creating a significant distance between her and the sword cultivators behind her. 

The four strands of sword intent converged once more into a singular line, shadowing Ning Yao's movements.

Thus, Ning Yao, outside the grand sword formation, was also surrounded by sword intent. 

The gold sword in her hand had few places to wield its power.

Even Fan Dache, witnessing this scene from afar, felt a chill run down his spine. 

If Lin Junbi had the chance to see this, he would likely congratulate himself for having lost honorably, feeling nothing but joy instead of sadness.

In the path of swords, losing to Ning Yao held no shame whatsoever.

If one didn't believe it, they could ask Pang Yuanji, Qi Shou, and Gao Yehou if they had the capability to summon Ning Yao to personally strike.

Looking back, before Ning Yao became a Golden Core sword cultivator, she had likely been on the battlefield primarily for her own training and to slay enemies, while trying to ensure her friends' safety as best she could. 

However, after returning from the righteous world and three battles later, it seemed like she was only helping Diezhang and Chen Sanqiu practice their swordplay.

She appeared to have no sword left to practice.

Far behind Ning Yao, the battlefield was desolate; some smaller demon cultivators and those still vestigial in intelligence were easily dispatched by Diezhang and Dong Huafu, who were trying their best to keep up with Ning Yao.

Dong Huafu even had the leisure to scratch his head, muttering softly, “Sister Ning, at least leave some for us, would you?”

Diezhang executed a swift turn and hurled her weapon, the Zhenyu, directly killing a demon cultivator at the Sea-View stage. With a wave of her hand, she left her sword unfurled, her toes lightly touching the ground as she flew toward Ning Yao, closer to the southern sword intent. She and Dong Huafu were still over a hundred yards away.

Turning her head in complaint, she said, “What are you grumbling about? Keep up! Otherwise, we won’t even see Ning Yao’s back soon.”

Diezhang certainly did not complain about Ning Yao; she was just venting at Dong Huafu, which was no problem at all.

Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo had even less to do than Diezhang and Dong Huafu.

Chen Sanqiu, being naturally laid-back, didn’t mind being in this awkward position where there were no enemies to slay. Yan Zhuo, however, was a bit concerned but felt helpless.

Fan Dache simply focused on propelling his sword forward.

At the very back, Chen Ping'an merely took a slightly longer route with his sword, wandering around, making minimal gains.

In fact, Chen Ping'an was the most helpless. It seemed that watching the battlefield made no difference; whether he looked or not, the results were the same. The few clues he had painstakingly uncovered either fled in panic or were too slow and ended up dead before he could even speak. However, it wasn't entirely meaningless, as he was too far from Ning Yao, so he planned to use his thoughts to communicate with Chen Sanqiu, hoping to relay a warning to Dong Huafu that a demon cultivator with at least Golden Core or even Yuan Ying cultivation was hiding and about to attack.

Just as Chen Ping'an was about to speak, 

Ning Yao, continuously breaking through the enemy lines, finally paused again on the distant battlefield. Leaning on her sword spirit, she pressed the sword's hilt lightly, and the golden long sword instantly sank into the earth, disappearing from sight.

Clearly, she had sensed the sneaky movements of that Yuan Ying demon.

The ground beneath her feet cracked, and her golden long sword was the first to greet the enemy. Nearby sword energy poured down like torrential rain, rapidly infiltrating the earth. She couldn’t be bothered to spend time precisely locating the hiding demon cultivator.

She cast a glance at a few relatively high-ranking demon cultivators on the edge of the "sword array" and said indifferently, “Come again.”

Again, four strands of ancient sword intent, which countless sword cultivators had brushed past over the millennia, manifested in response to the two words spoken by this young woman.

In addition to the previous four strands, a total of eight strands of ancient sword energy enveloped Ning Yao, forming a more substantial sword formation.

Inside this formation, casualties were innumerable.

Even so, Ning Yao still felt it wasn’t enough.

With her fingers forming an ancient sword art, her thoughts stirred, and the eight strands of sword intent seemed to coalesce into flesh and blood, with sword intent as their framework, magically conjuring up eight pale-robed sword spirits. These eight sword spirits, each with a cold demeanor, wearing flowing white robes and towering several meters high, extended their hands, each gripping a long sword formed from the surrounding sword energy, and simultaneously turned to scatter in all directions to kill.

These ancient "sword spirits," devoid of intelligence, could not return to peak condition, but their combat power was equivalent to Golden Core sword cultivators. They also lacked life swords and magical abilities. 

However, the power of eight Golden Core sword cultivators, even if destroyed by the savage world’s demon army, was merely a matter of reconsolidating the battlefield’s sword energy. They would persist, tireless and unyielding, with no need to worry about spiritual energy accumulation, making it easy to wreak havoc on the battlefield. As long as Ning Yao's mental energy didn’t deplete excessively, combined with the eight pure sword intents as the "fundamentals of the Dao," and without being forcibly interrupted by enemy Yuan Ying sword cultivators or upper-level sword immortals, these eight ancient sword spirits could persist on the battlefield indefinitely.

“Ning Yao’s swordsmanship, sword intent, and sword Dao, as long as she is given time—and it doesn’t even need to be long—all three can reach great heights.” 

This was what the senior sword immortal Chen Qingdu himself had said.

Why was it that no one in the Sword Qi Great Wall, which boasted a plethora of sword cultivator geniuses, ever called her a genius? Because if she were to be labeled a genius, then Qi Shou, Pang Yuanji, and the rest of that young sword cultivator group would all have to downgrade their status, not even qualifying as geniuses.

Ning Yao.

Always one of a kind.

From the day Ning Yao first picked up a sword in her youth, there had been no peers, even those a generation above her, willing to spar with her, let alone exchange sword arts.

There was simply no need.

The ground where Ning Yao previously stood had already crumbled and collapsed.

Ning Yao hung suspended in mid-air, turning to glance back, likely checking if Diezhang and Dong Huafu were following.

In just a few blinks, when the Yuan Ying cultivator was located by the golden long sword, Ning Yao plummeted rapidly, disappearing from view.

By the time Diezhang and Dong Huafu reached the edge of the large pit, Ning Yao had already revealed herself at the southernmost part of the pit and continued southward to open up the formation.

She had already located a Jade Purity realm death warrior.

However, the opponent surprisingly chose to retreat without a fight.

Facing south, Ning Yao raised her hand to wipe away a faint scar on her face from a blade, merely a scratch.

Diezhang glanced into the depths of the pit, where a Yuan Ying demon had revealed its true form—a colossal monkey, seemingly a remnant of ancient mountain-moving creatures. Its demise could likely be described as being torn apart, with remnants of golden sword energy still lingering in the gaps of its corpse.

It was evident that it had been slain by the sword spirit in Ning Yao's hands, without even having the chance to self-destruct.

At the bottom of the pit, beside the corpse, there hovered a narrow white knife, which appeared like a delicate needle compared to the massive body. Its blade shimmered erratically, quite eye-catching.

Dong Huafu was about to descend to retrieve the treasure.

However, Diezhang shot him an incredulous glare. “Are you stupid?”

Dong Huafu exclaimed, “Oh!” and quickly followed Diezhang southward.

Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo followed the edge of the pit, moving southward as well. Their life swords and companion swords were primarily used to collect a few battle merits from the side battlefield, making the most of the situation so as not to appear utterly useless. They were like farmers gathering scattered grains, yet even now, their bowl still had not filled.

Fan Dache felt a bit lost.

Wasn’t the plan for me to be the bait?

Arriving at the southern end of the pit, Fan Dache looked back to see the second shopkeeper squatting there picking up scraps, her movements surprisingly graceful.

Since Fan Dache was closest to Chen Ping'an, he realized that even though he was the bait, being slightly distracted wouldn’t hurt. He knew that the second shopkeeper, as she moved southward, was accumulating small gains. She hadn’t missed a single piece of broken spiritual artifact or life treasure fragment, which still made for a considerable quantity. By the time she finished scouring the pit, she likely would have secured some quality treasures.

Chen Ping'an left the pit, feeling complicated emotions. It didn’t seem right to be scavenging like this.

It appeared that the demon sword cultivator death warriors had lost the courage to strike.

Chen Ping'an could only remind Chen Sanqiu and Yan Zhuo through thoughts, “We probably can’t keep up. Let’s find an opportunity to eliminate the already identifiable Golden Core demons. If there are Yuan Ying ones, we’ll work together to intercept them and prevent them from slipping to other battlefields.”
