Unexpectedly, Ning Yao to the far south, one step ahead, had stopped the ancient sword spirit from slaughtering the demons on the north-south battlefield, instead beginning to hunt for those attempting to escape to the sides. Once she discovered them, she would slow her pace southward, wielding the sword spirit, and pursue them.

The Jade Purity realm sword cultivator death warrior seemed exceptionally adept at hiding, much like Lord Nalan. Ning Yao didn’t ponder much and simply avoided it.

In this way, Diezhang and Dong Huafu finally caught up with Ning Yao.

Chen Ping'an scratched his head.

Then, this group of sword cultivators proceeded southward.

It seemed the demon death warriors had initially hoped that Ning Yao would eventually show signs of mental exhaustion, but they could never have predicted that she would maintain her forward momentum, breaking through the lines without any signs of fatigue or depletion of spiritual energy.

Also, the two Golden Core death warriors and a Yuan Ying demon cultivator were subsequently slain, with Ning Yao personally dealing with the Yuan Ying, while the two injured Golden Cores were left to Diezhang and the others to handle.

Ning Yao couldn’t even be bothered to pretend, disdainful of luring her enemies into action.

I can find you.

And then, you can die.

This was the essence of Ning Yao’s sword strikes.

In stark contrast to that infamous second shopkeeper, the two were completely different styles on the battlefield.

And just like that, they continued southward.

As they neared the golden river, a sword immortal greeted Ning Yao with a smile.

Ning Yao nodded in acknowledgment to the senior sword immortal.

Finally, Ning Yao came to a halt, and for the first time, the seven sword cultivators gathered together.

Ning Yao looked toward Chen Ping'an and asked, “Shall we head back? Diezhang and the four of you can switch to another battlefield, while the three of us—me, you, and Fan Dache—will take a different route. Does that sound good?”

Chen Ping'an smiled, “What’s there to disagree with?”

Diezhang and Chen Sanqiu’s group headed toward another battlefield, turning north back to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

On this journey, aside from some minor skirmishes, it seemed like no one had to draw their swords; having no swords to draw was also awkward.

Ning Yao accompanied Chen Ping'an and Fan Dache, the three of them returning north to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Fan Dache felt increasingly redundant.

Chen Ping'an ceased to wield his sword, stowing his sword from the forge on his back and shaking his sleeves.

Fan Dache was the first to soar northward, yet he dared not create too much distance between himself and the two behind him.

Chen Ping'an even omitted the words “Dache,” realizing that after more than a year apart, Fan Dache had matured quite a bit. It was no wonder he had reached the Golden Core stage; he must have drunk his fill at the Bamboo Sea cave.

After Fan Dache had taken his leave, Ning Yao suddenly asked, “Is being an Hidden Official tiring?”

Chen Ping'an chuckled, “Not so much right now.”

Ning Yao hesitated for a moment, feeling somewhat awkward, but still softly voiced her feelings: “When you’re with me, you can think less.”

Then Ning Yao raised an eyebrow.

This was the truth. 

What was there to be embarrassed about?

Chen Ping'an turned, raised his hand, and gently brushed the scar on her face with his thumb, then pinched her cheek, smiling softly, “Who says otherwise?” 

**(End of Chapter)**

 ### Chapter 763: Breaking Through Casually

Previously, when Ning Yao set out alone intending to breach the formation first, the frontline of the demon army was stalled. By the time she cut through their ranks and led six sword cultivators to the vicinity of the Golden River, the demon forces on both sides of the battlefield hastily advanced, trying to stay as far away as possible from this woman, the "Sword Immortal," whose strikes were too fierce.

In that moment, Ning Yao resembled a commanding officer, urging the demon army to fight desperately onward.

Thus, Fan Dache, having left the two of them first, found himself inexplicably transformed into a Golden Core sword cultivator, chasing after the vast demon army all alone. 

Fan Dache thought that given this situation, he should treat himself to the finest wine from Qing Shen Mountain when it was all over. His achievements in battle were enough for him to finally stop borrowing money from Chen Sanqiu to buy alcohol.

Chen Ping'an glanced at the battlefield ahead. The formation of the demon army was growing denser and more compact, advancing rapidly. The higher-ranked demon cultivators were increasingly distancing themselves from the three of them, primarily to avoid Ning Yao alone, with both he and Fan Dache in tow.

He said, “The pressure on the sword cultivators on both sides will increase significantly because of us.”

Ning Yao replied, “Then let’s strive to meet the sword cultivators at the front as soon as possible. Specifically, how shall we proceed?”

Standing atop the sword from the Sword Workshop, Chen Ping'an was becoming more accustomed to flying close to the ground. He quickly rolled up his sleeves and said, “This time, I’ll lead the formation, and you’ll cover me from the back. If any Golden Core or Nascent Soul demons appear, it will be your responsibility to handle them.”

Ning Yao asked, “Aren’t you planning to summon your flying sword?”

“I’ll rely solely on my fists. It’s just right for polishing my martial arts bottleneck,” Chen Ping'an said. “Don’t worry, my speed in breaking through the formation won’t compare to yours, but compared to other battlefields, it won’t be slow.”

Ning Yao nodded, “Then just focus on throwing punches.”

Taking a deep breath, Chen Ping'an maneuvered the sword like a bolt of lightning, following Fan Dache closely, speaking to him via thought, “Dache, you attack from the center while I lead the formation. During this time, regardless of what happens, just focus on advancing with your sword. I might not be able to take care of you too much, but with Ning Yao covering us, it shouldn’t be a problem.”

Fan Dache replied solemnly, “Understood!”

In truth, the moment the second shopkeeper didn’t utter his usual “Dache” was when Fan Dache realized he needed to be extra cautious.

In an instant, Chen Ping'an, dressed in two layers of official robes, accelerated on his sword, cutting through the air in a straight line.

As he flew, when still over a hundred feet away from the demon army, Chen Ping'an had already adjusted his stance, one foot firmly planted. The sword beneath him tilted downward, unable to bear the weight, and transformed into a true ground-skimming flight. To Fan Dache’s astonishment, Chen Ping'an's figure vanished in an instant; he hadn’t even used the Earth-Shrinking Talisman but had achieved its effect. Could it be that after just over a year of reaching the Golden Body realm, he had broken through again, becoming a Master of the Wandering Realm?

Ning Yao chose to fly on her sword and explained to Fan Dache, “He’s still only at the Golden Body realm and hasn’t reached the Wandering Realm. Wearing three layers of robes isn’t merely for protection; it’s to suppress his fist intent. Coupled with a certain degree of sword qi pressure, the three elements reinforce each other, serving as a form of training. It’s similar to how those martial artists in the Jianghu bind sandbags to their feet.”

Ning Yao was willing to elaborate on this, of course, because it was related to Chen Ping'an. Furthermore, Fan Dache was a mutual friend of hers and Chen Ping'an, and Chen Ping'an had taken care of Fan Dache the most. It wasn’t solely because of Fan Dache’s insufficient cultivation level; it was as if in Fan Dache, Chen Ping'an could see many fragments of his own past years. Piecing them together naturally made him feel particularly close to him.

However, the specific reasons behind this were beyond Ning Yao’s comprehension. She believed that when Chen Ping'an had the time, or when the Hidden Official finally found a moment of respite amidst his busy schedule, he would surely share them with her.

Ning Yao continued, “When he first started learning martial arts back in his hometown, he tied bags filled with gravel to his legs. During his first journey, he used half a jiao talisman and an eight-ounce talisman. He has long been accustomed to this, and he himself doesn’t know how heavy or fast his punches are. Since he doesn’t know how hard he can hit, then neither will his opponents.”

As she spoke, Ning Yao swung her sword, and a Golden Core demon cultivator from another battlefield glanced her way. Sensing her presence, she unleashed her sword qi. After just one strike, she cut through the demon cultivator’s body cleanly, splitting him in half. A Golden Core exploded, causing collateral damage to countless others.

Ning Yao recalled a small incident from the past. She remembered when a young Chen Ping'an came to the Sword Qi Great Wall for the first time, carrying a Huai wood sword box with two swords inside. During their moments alone, he enjoyed making small talk, sharing many tales from the countryside, such as how an artisan would pluck ink lines with great precision.

Ning Yao stole a glance at the battlefield after her strike; it resembled that memory.

Fan Dache had no idea how to strike up a conversation. Standing beside Ning Yao, he felt an immense pressure—something unimaginable. His good friend, Chen Sanqiu, had privately told him that when he and his friends like Diezhang were at a lower realm than Ning Yao, he felt fine. But once they were at the same realm, he genuinely questioned his existence. Am I really a sword cultivator? Is my cultivation level even real?

Yet, Fan Dache had watched Chen Sanqiu leisurely sipping wine and complaining, all the while sporting a smile.

The second shopkeeper had once said that wine was the best fishing rod in the world, able to reel in the heartfelt confessions of drunkards, especially the Bamboo Sea Cave wine from his establishment, which was even more extraordinary.

Being able to befriend Ning Yao, even someone as gifted as Chen Sanqiu would feel pressure but still find joy in drinking.

Fan Dache remained vigilant, watching the surroundings of the battlefield, which seemed empty and devoid of immediate danger. Still, he worried that some sneaky demon cultivator might stab him from underground or drop a magical artifact on him.

Such occurrences were numerous on the battlefield.

Fan Dache had once witnessed a fellow sword cultivator of exceptional talent being caught off guard by a Mountain-moving demon cultivator, who had calculated the trajectory of his sword and burst forth from the ground, seizing the sword cultivator’s ankles and tearing him apart.

On the battlefield, the most terrifying enemies were often not the powerful demons who were at a bottleneck, crushing a particular battlefield with their might. Unless it was a life-or-death situation, one could easily avoid their sharpness. What was even more daunting were the demon cultivators who initially sought not for accomplishments but for refining their skills. They acted insidiously, adept at disguise, always aiming for a lethal strike, killing invisibly. If they missed, they would promptly retreat. Such demon cultivators thrived on the battlefield, living longer and stealthily drifting through various battlefields, accumulating impressive war achievements.

It was said that the youngest Sword Immortal of the Upper Five Realms in the Wildlands, a demon named Shou Chen, had risen step by step using such underhanded tactics.

What was even more terrifying was that even after becoming a Sword Immortal of the Upper Five Realms, Shou Chen still preferred to act stealthily, concealing his demonic aura and intentionally suppressing his Sword Immortal demeanor, pretending to be a Golden Core demon cultivator to remain on the battlefield, waiting for the right moment to strike.

Because of this, Ah Liang had once personally sought Shou Chen’s whereabouts during a battle and ultimately found him, managing to send a sword from a distance. However, Shou Chen was a Sword Immortal, and at that time, he had used a protective talisman from his mentor, allowing him to escape the battlefield.

Fan Dache suddenly froze.

Wasn’t his second shopkeeper just like this? He could even be considered a master of this craft?

What a pity he became the Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Otherwise, even if the second shopkeeper didn’t act as Fan Dache’s guardian sword master, letting Chen Ping'an roam freely across battlefields, he would still be a pure martial artist. Coupled with Chen Ping'an’s keen understanding of the battlefield and precise calculations regarding the strengths of enemies and allies, he believed that whether in accumulating war achievements or growth speed, he wouldn’t be any inferior to that Shou Chen demon.

Ning Yao’s Sword Immortal demeanor was certainly breathtaking and captivating.

However, no matter how much one revered or admired her, Ning Yao was simply Ning Yao. No one among her peers at the Sword Qi Great Wall could replicate her.

Yet, the second shopkeeper’s style of combat was something even Fan Dache could learn. As long as one was willing, witnessing it firsthand, listening more, observing more, and remembering, one could incorporate it into their own practice. Even a slight increase in odds on the battlefield could often help a sword cultivator eliminate unforeseen threats.

Ahead on the battlefield, Chen Ping'an had ceased using his sword and actively plunged into the thick encirclement of demons.

With his fists wide open, an overwhelming intent surged forth like a river, reminiscent of the small realm that Ning Yao had previously established with her sword qi.

Anyone who accidentally or daringly approached would find themselves facing his fist intent.

A large demon, naturally robust as a gazebo, had become a cultivator and possessed two personal artifacts specifically for enhancing defensive magical techniques. Relying on its innate strength, it rampaged across the battlefield.

Yet, it was directly cut in half by Chen Ping'an as he forged a path with his punch, a torrent of blood being scattered outward.

Striking a thousand times may not be as effective as one decisive blow.

Chen Ping'an engaged in combat with just a single punch.

Trapped in the enemy’s encirclement, surrounded on all sides by foes.

He still aimed for a single punch to kill, to injure their foundation, shatter their souls.

Each punch seemed to save energy, yet every strike was immensely powerful, pushing forward without hesitation. His pure fist intent subtly caused the surrounding sword qi to avoid him.

A demon cultivator unable to evade—a towering figure, two zhang tall—swung a massive hammer down at him.

Facing the legendary Ning Yao may have meant certain death, but against this “young man” who had no flying sword and relied solely on his exceptional fist techniques, he at least possessed the heart to fight.

Chen Ping'an extended his hand to block the incoming hammer, his entire form enveloped in shadow. He shifted his ankle slightly, redirecting the immense force into the ground. Even so, the impact caused his knees to sink into the earth.

He could have evaded but chose not to, deliberately withstanding the heavy blow, all to entice the hidden demon cultivators around him into believing they had an opportunity.

A demon cultivator clad in fine iron armor approached Chen Ping'an with a blade, exuding might as he swung down.

Additionally, a Golden Core cultivator emerged from his sleeve, tossing out two golden talismans adorned with images of the Five Peaks and winding rivers, then raised a hand, lifting them high.

The ground beneath Chen Ping'an’s feet was first encased in ice by the Golden Core cultivator’s technique, sealing off a radius of several dozen zhang.

The golden mountain talismans materialized into five vividly colored mountains, each the size of a fist. Four of them hovered beside the young martial artist, while only one of the talismans targeted his head.

With one hand anchored against the hammer, Chen Ping'an raised his left hand, seizing the thick black blade, its filth as dense as ink. The pure fist intent in his palm clashed with the black blade’s brilliance, sparks flying.

With a twist of his wrist, he yanked the unwilling cultivator forward, colliding him with the miniature mountain created by the talisman.

The hammer-wielding demon, having already completed his role as bait, found himself unable to strike down with his weapon any further. He momentarily withdrew, raising his arm high for another attempt.

The martial artist demon, sensing the ill fate, sought escape, unwilling to be struck by the oncoming mountain or suffer injury from the hammer, decisively kicked Chen Ping'an in the chest to gain distance.

In the next moment, Chen Ping'an, who had been employing the Zhu Lian-style monkey fist stance, suddenly transformed into the peak stance of Zong Qiu, his previously relaxed shoulders and hunched back straightening to normal as he regained his composure. With his fist intent thickening, he shattered the surrounding spell seals with a single punch, smashing the miniature mountain to radiant golden splinters.

Still holding onto the blade near its tip, Chen Ping'an slipped back, evading the second heavy hammer strike from the hulking demon.

With his left hand retracting the blade slightly, his right fist opened to form a palm knife, slashing down to forcefully sever the black blade in two. This caused the demon cultivator, who had aimed to destroy his own offensive artifact, to instead injure himself, spitting out a mouthful of blood. He cast a glance at the young man still surrounded by the four mountains created by the talismans, and the martial artist cultivator fled, riding the wind away from the battlefield.

The four golden mountain talismans, though small, retained an impressive aura as they hovered in the air, forming a powerful formation that encircled Chen Ping'an and the hammer-wielding demon, though lacking a central mountain, creating a slight deficiency.

Fortunately, another golden talisman had transformed into a water serpent several zhang long, ultimately establishing the layout of mountains and flowing waters.

The hulking demon, now forced to fight for his life against the young man, lost all fear of death on the battlefield, ready to trade blows if necessary.

With the massive hammer in hand, the fierce demon charged at the young man with unreasonable strength, fully intending to exchange his life for the young man's.

In the end, the young man’s punch shattered the demon's chest cavity. Prior to that, the talisman serpent had already battered the hulking demon to the point of being unrecognizable. This outcome likely caught even the Golden Core demon cultivator off guard, culminating in a mutual downfall, for after Chen Ping'an struck the demon down, he leapt high, pressing the hulking demon’s head against the serpent, choosing to obliterate the Golden Core demon along with the serpent, reducing them to ashes.

The Golden Core cultivator observed as the young man tore off his tattered robe, revealing yet another robe beneath it. 

His face, too, was battered beyond recognition, and the young man casually gathered it into his sleeve, even making the large hammer vanish, storing it within his pocket dimension.

The Golden Core cultivator wasted no time, disregarding the four mountain talismans entirely as he executed a unique technique, transforming into several wisps of green smoke that darted underground, fleeing in all directions.

Chen Ping'an did not intentionally pursue the Golden Core cultivator. The loss of one robe only invigorated his fist intent further, and he pushed the teetering four miniature mountains away, charging forward as he sent out four punches, unleashing four bursts of golden light, resulting in nearly a hundred demon casualties on the battlefield. 

Without faces to conceal their identities, the demon army was the first to cry out “Hidden Official,” and the forces, which had been trying to regroup under the previous supervision, scattered in disarray.

As Chen Ping'an continued breaking through, his path was no longer a straight line but rather a large circle on the battlefield, slightly off-centered as he advanced. The faster they fled, the more punches he unleashed.

With the pure energy of a martial artist flowing through him, he continued to punch until exhaustion nearly overtook him, looking for a moment to catch his breath; if the situation grew dire, he would fight through it.

On the battlefield, as he faced ten realms of martial artists, could anyone match the weight of his fists? Dealing with the latter was truly a matter of life and death; the so-called resilience of the body was like paper against the fists of a peak ninth realm martial artist.

He could only rely on intuition, instinct, and the bond with his fellow martial artists as he fought.

For Chen Ping'an, as long as there weren’t any hidden Nascent Soul sword cultivators lurking nearby, the so-called one-man encirclement wasn’t a battlefield at all; it had always been a matter of matching opponents.

Li Er once said that during a duel where he almost accidentally killed Song Changjing, that prince of the Great Li had talent, of course, but his punches were still too light at that time. The reason Song Changjing managed to endure for so long was because he wasn’t merely a martial artist; he was a warrior forged in the fires of battle. Having honed his fist techniques on the battlefield for so long, he naturally exuded an aura of “one man against a thousand.”

Now, Chen Ping'an found himself in battle, seeking the first layer of that aura. With mountains and rivers before him, how many could truly match him?

As long as his punches were heavy enough, his movements swift enough, and his eyes keen enough, he would merely tread through the water and over the mountains, slowly progressing through each encounter.

After that, driven by a surge of excitement, Chen Ping'an became increasingly pure in his movements, whether walking or flying. He continuously adopted the six-step stance, his punches embodying the essence of the Iron Cavalry Charge, Divine Beating of Drums, and Cloud-Forming Great Marsh.

Though Li Er was a tenth realm martial artist, he had said little about fist theory during their time training at the ruins of the Lion Peak. When he occasionally spoke, he was straightforward, attributing his understanding to the frequent musings of Zheng Dafeng. He told Chen Ping'an that these words might be useful for him, but such discussions of fist theory lacked weight and couldn’t suppress anyone.

Among those words was the idea that one must have an enemy in sight to strike, while an absence of enemies in mind led to a transcendent state. The ultimate fist technique is omnipresent, seamlessly integrated with the laws of martial arts, and free from obstruction.

This time, as Chen Ping'an led the formation, he wouldn’t mercilessly slaughter the roaring, fierce demons, nor would he show restraint against the young demon cultivators filled with fear and pleading eyes.

A pure martial artist simply throws punches.

Those of higher technique live; those with lighter punches die.

On the battlefield, Chen Ping'an’s expression was solemn, his gaze indifferent.

Ning Yao merely reminded Fan Dache with one sentence, “Stay away from him.”

Chen Ping'an’s thoughts grew fewer, as all prior considerations faded away, drawing ever closer to the state of “forgetting oneself” that Li Er described.

He didn’t use the Earth-Shrinking Talisman, nor did he employ the Initial and Full Moons techniques. He didn’t even summon his Pine Needle or Thunder, which could anchor his form.

As for his two main flying swords, Cage Bird and Well Bottom Moon, they were of great use, and he would never reveal them prematurely.

At that moment, Chen Ping'an had completely forgotten that he was a sword cultivator, possessing four flying swords, and even two main flying swords.

At the thickest point of the demon army’s formation, his presence had not yet arrived, but his fist intent was already there.

Ning Yao continued searching for those high-level Golden Core and Nascent Soul demons.

Fan Dache still found himself with little to do. Fortunately, compared to when Ning Yao had led the formation, everyone simply followed her on their swords. This time, as Chen Ping'an led with his fists, Fan Dache found more opportunities to strike.

Earlier, with Ning Yao wielding her sword, the formation had been too swift.

The sword cultivators on the north and south battle lines were still far from the Golden River, not even halfway through their assault. As they progressed, the speed of breaking formations and killing enemies would only slow down further, and it was highly likely that they would need to retreat before reaching halfway, returning to the Sword Qi Great Wall to regroup with the second wave of sword cultivators, who rested atop the walls, ready to take turns in this grueling war of attrition.

In the vast battlefield between the Golden River and the city walls, the fastest group of sword cultivators advancing southward had barely reached the halfway mark, thanks to the assistance of the Nascent Soul sword cultivator Qi Shou.

Diezhang and his three companions were heading back north, engaging in a gruesome battle with the demon army alongside a dozen sword cultivators from the southern line.

The four young genius sword cultivators stood in a row, keeping a distance of seventy to eighty zhang apart. They no longer pursued speed or depth in breaching the formation but began to inflict as much damage as possible on the demon army. Thus, each sword cultivator began to step onto their swords: Zhen Yue, Hong Zhuang, Jing Shu, and Zi Dian, summoning their respective main flying swords, making their way back to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Chen Sanqiu’s main flying sword was named “White Deer.” One of its innate abilities was the appearance of a great white deer, as large as a house, carrying spirit mushrooms in its mouth. On the battlefield, a white deer shimmering like snow would appear, gathering spirit energy, showcasing remarkable powers.

On the battlefield, that massive, snow-white deer wreaked havoc, its killing power immense.

It was said that before Chen Sanqiu had forged his main flying sword, he had a dream one afternoon in which a doe knelt before him in submission, willingly recognizing him as its master.

Thus, Chen Sanqiu was renowned among the younger generation of the Sword Qi Great Wall, and it was no surprise.

With a good family background, a pleasant demeanor, good looks, great interpersonal relationships, and excellent potential, the only drawback was that Chen Sanqiu’s drinking habits were somewhat poor; otherwise, one could hardly find fault with him.

Moreover, the White Deer, an extraordinary creature, was often linked to ethereal literary fortunes. Therefore, the ancient sword “Jing Shu,” which Chen Sanqiu possessed, complemented him well. Because his main flying sword was one of the rare few possessing dual innate abilities, besides summoning the white deer, it could also invisibly enhance Chen Sanqiu’s literary fortune. Thus, Chen Sanqiu was not only a natural sword talent but also inherently a scholar.

It’s worth noting that in the Haoran world, there were only two Confucian saints with Sword Immortal status among the three major academies and seventy-two schools.

Unfortunately, Chen Sanqiu was born in the Sword Qi Great Wall, where scholars were few and far between. The most critical factor was that Chen Sanqiu’s surname was Chen, preventing him from going to that foreign land filled with schools and the sound of books.

Every sword cultivator who could earn the title of genius at the Sword Qi Great Wall had their story.

As long as they were sword cultivators who enjoyed drinking, anyone could get drunk, even to the point of dying, and have their reasons.

Ning Yao kept a distance, neither too far nor too close, following Chen Ping'an, who was solely focused on throwing punches.

Ning Yao vaguely sensed a thought from Chen Ping'an, perhaps something he himself was oblivious to at that moment.

If my fists soar high into the heavens, anyone who stands against me, Chen Ping'an, on the battlefield south of the Sword Qi Great Wall won’t need to draw their swords; they will all perish.

Ning Yao didn’t think this was a bad thing, but she also felt it might not be the best. The reason was simple: he was Chen Ping'an.

So Ning Yao called out, “Chen Ping'an.”

On the battlefield, Chen Ping'an immediately ceased his punches and paused, turning his head in confusion.

Fan Dache felt a momentary destabilization in his sword heart, a strange sensation that flitted away.

Ning Yao said, “Keep throwing punches; I’ll be right behind you.”

Chen Ping'an hesitated, unsure why Ning Yao would say that, but he nodded with a smile.

The robe he had borrowed from Pang Yuanji had already been shredded and put away, and this one had been damaged to the point of being unnecessary to fold away. He simply dispersed it with his fist intent, watching it scatter like dandelion fluff.

Not only that, but he also stored away the green shirt robe from the Ning family, leaving him now clad in merely the most ordinary long robe.

Chen Ping'an took a deep breath, expelling a mouthful of congealed blood. Unbeknownst to him, within a radius of several dozen zhang around him, there were no living demons left on the battlefield.

He shook his wrist and lightly clenched and relaxed his fists. His hands, now bare of skin, felt entirely normal. The pain was natural, but this familiar sensation brought him a sense of reassurance.

What’s the point of practicing martial arts or honing skills without feeling a bit of pain?

Chen Ping'an gazed into the distance, lifting his eyes, only to discover the large character carved on the city wall—familiar beyond recognition.

**Fierce.**

The character was poorly written.

Instinctively, Chen Ping'an looked up at the sky.

It can arrive late, but just don’t fail to arrive.

Even if it’s just to return to the Sword Qi Great Wall, half of my hometown, and take a look, as for whether to draw swords, we can decide after they come.

Chen Ping'an reached out to grab but remembered that the sword from the Sword Workshop had already shattered.

So he took out the法刀 of the Mountain-moving demon from the pocket dimension, slim and sharp, with a bright and pure treasure light.

Gripping this unclaimed法刀, a top-tier treasure, he weighed it lightly. If it was heavy enough, then he would continue leading the formation.

A moment later, Fan Dache couldn’t help but turn to look behind him.

Ning Yao was rubbing her temples.

In front of the two, Chen Ping'an was wielding his blade in a frenzy.

Fan Dache thought this must be akin to robbing a thief.

In an instant, Ning Yao shot out a sword.

It wasn’t to rescue Chen Ping'an; even if the attacker was a hidden Nascent Soul sword cultivator.

And the one coordinating the assassination against Ning Yao was precisely that earlier mysterious Jade Purity Realm Sword Immortal.

In the case of ordinary mountain deity companions, if a higher realm cultivator were to choose, even if they wouldn’t save a lower realm one, there would inevitably be some hesitation.

Yet Ning Yao had no such thoughts; her sword heart grew ever clearer and brighter.

She could kill her enemies, but she could also stay alive.

Ning Yao believed in herself, and she believed in Chen Ping'an.

Having intentionally suppressed her breakthrough at the Golden Core bottleneck for many years, Ning Yao now casually crossed into the Nascent Soul bottleneck.

After Ning Yao struck, she could still spare a glance at the city wall.

Chen Qingdu stood atop the wall, hands clasped behind him, a smile on his face.

Beside him, Wei Jin chuckled bitterly, “Why does the elder Sword Immortal intentionally suppress Ning Yao’s breakthrough?”

Chen Qingdu laughed, “There’s no rush. No need to compete for those superficial titles. Does it matter to become the first Sword Immortal under thirty in history?”

Wei Jin, who became a Sword Immortal at forty, still couldn’t comprehend, “Ning Yao isn’t forcing her growth; she is naturally progressing. Elder Sword Immortal, why would you use the entire Sword Qi Great Wall’s sword path to suppress her at the Nascent Soul bottleneck?”

Chen Qingdu replied with a grin, “Am I Wei Jin?”

Wei Jin was left speechless.

He started to reminisce about the times spent with his predecessors on the wall.

The implication in the elder Sword Immortal’s words was that you are the real Chen Qingdu?

Chen Qingdu continued, “Suppressing the sword path? You underestimate Ning Yao too much.”

The gray-clad elder from the Wildlands, regardless of how fierce the battle was, remained indifferent, meditating within the military tent.

At this moment, the elder opened his eyes, directly engaging Chen Qingdu with a smile, “Now, that’s breaking the rules.”

Chen Qingdu responded, “Not satisfied? Come up to the wall and have a go?”

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 764: Kindred Spirits

On the other end of the Gengzi ledger, there was no response. Chen Qingdu's expression turned somewhat regretful. After all, the entire wilderness world was under the influence of that old fellow, and here he was, merely occupying a Sword Qi Great Wall. Was he really too afraid to ascend the wall for a battle?

It seemed that if a man wasn't a sword cultivator, he was simply not up to par.

After a moment of silence, Chen Qingdu suddenly asked, “Is it really that difficult to break through the bottleneck of the Jade Purity Realm?”

Wei Jin replied candidly, “For me, it is indeed very difficult. Back then, when I fortuitously encountered Senior Ah Liang, breaking through to the Nascent Soul bottleneck was already a stroke of luck. I felt guilty for taking credit for a feat that was not entirely mine.”

He had expected the Sword Immortal would mock him a bit, but to his surprise, Chen Qingdu nodded. “Reaching the Immortal realm is no easy feat. In fact, for sword cultivators, every realm has its challenges.”

Wei Jin inquired, “Senior Sword Immortal, could you offer me some guidance?”

Chen Qingdu turned to this renowned sword master of Baoping Continent and acknowledged him as a young man troubled by his emotions. As for Wei Jin, being able to ascend to the upper five realms of sword immortals by the age of forty in a world where sword luck was relatively sparse, was an impressive achievement, especially within the Sword Qi Great Wall.

How did Wei Jin manage that? Apart from his innate talent, it was largely thanks to that rascal Ah Liang, who imparted clever strategies to him. The ancient records of the Sword Qi Great Wall were like gold standards for sword cultivators in the wilderness world, but only if one could actually turn the pages. Ah Liang had no trouble with that; he had almost finished reading them all, charmingly calling it the scholar's way of stealing knowledge, which could also be seen as a form of cultured thievery.

Ah Liang assisted Wei Jin in taking risks and breaking through prematurely, allowing him to become a prominent figure in Baoping Continent's sword cultivation. Strictly speaking, his methods weren't particularly noble and didn't showcase exceptional skill. Having lived for ten thousand years, Chen Qingdu could naturally see through Wei Jin's cultivation foundation. The notion that strong practitioners relied on strong luck held some truth; as long as Wei Jin reached the upper five realms and remained on Baoping Continent, he could easily dominate the continent, sitting atop the mountains, with winds and storms at his command. He could freely seize the sword luck of Baoping Continent. With his innate talent, he could take his time over the next hundred years to steadily advance; unless something unexpected occurred, attaining the Immortal realm was inevitable.

What was remarkable about Wei Jin was his ability to know when to retreat. After a brief encounter with the Northern Julu Continent's Celestial Xie Shi, which solidified his Jade Purity cultivation, he immediately abandoned the easily obtainable path to the Dao and instead came to the Sword Qi Great Wall. If not for the sudden emergence of the new Hidden Official, Wei Jin might have perished in this foreign land, leaving Baoping Continent with nothing more than a distant, vague legend of a sword immortal.

Chen Qingdu had always appreciated such a young man.

He dared to fight for great fortunes and was willing to risk death!

In contrast, there was another little rascal who was quite reluctant to die. However, preferring to live a miserable life rather than face death was acceptable in Chen Qingdu's eyes—it was something he could relate to.

After hearing Wei Jin's earnest plea, Chen Qingdu did not rush to give an answer. He smiled and said, “Why did you only ask this today? You, Wei Jin, are quite clever; living in that little hut behind me, you should understand that this is my tacit approval. First, there was Cao Ci, then Chen Ping'an, and now you—it's not everyone who can be neighbors with Chen Qingdu.”

Wei Jin gazed towards the battlefield in the south and softly said, “As the only sword immortal from Baoping Continent, I hope to come to the Sword Qi Great Wall with a heart free of selfish desires, and ultimately leave with dignity. This is one reason. Moreover, I wish to trade my swordsmanship for insights from the Senior Sword Immortal. When Senior Ah Liang guided me, I don’t want our next reunion to leave him thinking he once aided a useless person who failed to achieve anything significant, becoming just another sword immortal who idly waits on the realm ledger, living off his past.”

There were some things Wei Jin left unspoken.

Once, when he drank with Senior Ah Liang, he had teased him, saying that those who were infatuated in this world often find it hard to be with their lovers, especially given that the threads of fate were so chaotically intertwined nowadays. One couldn't just force a girl into a wedding carriage. So, one should take a step back and strive to improve oneself. Let the girl he missed harbor a subtle regret; perhaps in the future, when she argued with her husband, she might reminisce and say, “That so-and-so was once my admirer.”

Chen Qingdu liked Wei Jin's straightforwardness and chuckled, “From now on, every now and then, when you accumulate a bit of merit in battle, I will teach you a sword technique of considerable rank, one that is foundational to the Dao of an old friend from my youth.”

Wei Jin clasped his fists in gratitude but said nothing.

To him, the heart of a sword cultivator lay in the act of drawing the sword.

Chen Qingdu shook his head. “Not very wise.”

The old man rubbed his chin, clicking his tongue. “Thanks to Senior Ah Liang, he spent a hundred years sharpening his ears. Now that he’s gone, there's another manager taking charge. It seems the transition from extravagance to frugality is truly difficult.”

Wei Jin sighed, “I can’t learn that.”

The old man laughed, “No need to learn; besides, you wouldn’t be able to.”

Wei Jin asked, “Will Senior Ah Liang return to the Sword Qi Great Wall?”

Chen Qingdu countered, “Have you ever thought about why Ah Liang taught you the methods for closing off and breaking through?”

Wei Jin replied, “I have pondered it, but I couldn’t quite grasp it.”

“Ah Liang didn’t just happen upon you; he sought you out on purpose and then taught you swordsmanship. He wasn't calculating that you would certainly come to the Sword Qi Great Wall, nor did he think you were lacking and merely gave you a handout so that you, the future master of sword luck on the continent, would feel grateful. Rather, he genuinely hopes that you, Wei Jin, can stand side by side with him in the future. This applies to you, and to all the kindred spirits who walk behind you—Ah Liang treats them the same.”

Chen Qingdu continued, “This answer encapsulates the essence of the sword technique I will teach you. Sword cultivators need to associate with the weak and seek guidance from the strong. Those who regard others as mere ants are themselves ants. Remember, back in the day, who wasn't an ant beneath their feet?”

Wei Jin seemed to grasp something.

The old man clasped his hands behind his back, glanced at the sky, then turned his gaze back to the southern land.

Sword cultivators are sword cultivators, soaring in the heavens while walking the earth.

When a sword cultivator, clearly an immortal, chooses to humbly identify as a mere sword practitioner, it carries a special meaning.

In Chen Qingdu’s view, Wei Jin was just a step short of that understanding. Although this young sword immortal had always been in the martial world, he never truly felt like he belonged; he saw himself as a transient in the mortal realm, ultimately destined to ascend the mountains as a celestial being, taking his sword along while striving to sever ties with all worldly affairs, fearing entanglements of fate.

Yet.

As Chen Qingdu gazed into the distance, he recalled a picture from his youth.

Sword cultivators ascend heights and seek guidance from the heavens; the highest among them become increasingly intertwined with the world. Gradually, step by step, they tug the entire realm upward, as if dragging the world along with them.

This was the essence of the early sword cultivators—this was true purity of sword heart.

With immense will and great aspirations, they shouldered heavy burdens and endured severe trials, determined to elevate all of humanity to greater heights.

Today’s sword cultivators and other practitioners of Qi all wish to cultivate a heart free of desires, severing ties with the mundane, hoping to become untainted celestial beings on the mountains. 

Even if the vast majority of cultivators think this way, it is still acceptable; however, if everyone were to adopt this mindset, that would be a significant problem.

Chen Qingdu clasped his hands behind his back and lightly tapped his palm, muttering to himself, “We need more of the former and fewer of the latter; both types must exist, and neither can be absent.”

---

On the southern battlefield.

That Jade Purity Realm sword immortal, a death warrior, exchanged a strike with Ning Yao, sustaining a minor injury. Yet, he showed no inclination to continue fighting, immediately employing a strange secret technique to escape. Where blood flowed on the battlefield, intricate ripples emerged, clearly the remnants of the demonic sword immortal's soul. His escape route was not a straight line; it seemed he had used some formation.

Ning Yao's second strike missed entirely. Moreover, a place sixty zhang behind her where blood had pooled began to ripple. For a sword cultivator, that distance was almost negligible, yet the sword immortal death warrior seemed intent on a desperate blow. Ning Yao, more ruthless, resolved to exchange injury for death. Even though she could have avoided it, she deliberately paused, giving the demonic sword immortal a chance.

However, the death warrior ultimately abandoned the opportunity, completely discarding any intent to assassinate and chose to retreat from the battlefield.

The golden robe Ning Yao wore was, according to the records in the Gengzi ledger, undoubtedly of immortal-grade quality, which was extremely restraining for a top-tier assassin like her who aimed for a successful strike.

Unable to locate her opponent, Ning Yao surveyed her surroundings. Noticing no sign of him on the nearby battlefield, she decided to cease her pursuit.

However, she had memorized the death warrior's escape route and silently deduced it in her heart. If she had another chance to confront him, her strikes would be more precise.

What truly vexed Ning Yao was that the Nascent Soul sword cultivator who had targeted Chen Ping'an also retreated decisively after a failed attack. The demon army acted as a natural barrier. When Ning Yao initiated her third strike, that Nascent Soul sword cultivator barely dodged it. With a hand gesture, the sword cultivator transformed into hundreds of sword lights that scattered rapidly. As Ning Yao raised her hand, the many discarded and broken weapons on the ground surged forth like flying swords, all in pursuit of the escaping sword lights.

The sky above the battlefield resembled a torrential downpour of fragmented flying swords.

Meanwhile, Ning Yao darted ten zhang away, avoiding the distant Chen Ping'an, and slashed forward.

However, the flying sword from the earlier attack on Chen Ping'an had missed. The so-called failure merely meant the sword had not killed him. Chen Ping'an was trapped in a great formation, and a sudden strike from a Nascent Soul sword cultivator left him with nowhere to hide. All he could do was avoid fatal blows; thus, the sword pierced through his shoulder, leaving a gaping wound. The sword cultivator's flying sword was not only sharp; it was the residual sword energy that posed the real threat, creating a subtle and intricate battlefield within the injured person's microcosm—a myriad of sword intents, like countless dragons crossing a river, with the sword energy flooding through his acupoints.

Injuries caused by a sword cultivator’s flying sword were notoriously difficult to heal, a universally accepted fact, and sword cultivators had earned their place as the most troublesome foes on the mountains.

On the battlefield, Fan Dache could no longer see Chen Ping'an.

The vast demon army surged from all directions, overwhelming the area, clearly intent on surrounding and killing the young man.

The first to recognize the young Hidden Official's face was a demon cultivator, who revealed his identity. Immediately, the army began to scatter, driven by a primal instinct for survival.

This was not only because the young Hidden Official had recently triumphed over Li Zhen, a disciple of the Tuo Yue Mountain, but he had also frightened Li Zhen, a top genius of the wilderness world, nearly to the point of losing his soul. This incident had already spread throughout the demon army, and the news was destined to spread slowly southward, becoming a hot topic across the vast wilderness, in towns and streets, year after year, like the grass on the plain, thriving and wilting in cycles. Even a hundred years from now, those who witnessed the events might recount the story over meals.

Moreover, the Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall had become synonymous with the girl named Xiao Xian, who had braids like a sheep's horn.

Once the demon army remembered that this Hidden Official was not the same as the previous one, coupled with the fact that Chen Ping'an was alone, too deeply infiltrated into enemy lines, and Ning Yao appeared to have no intention of providing support, many demon cultivators who had lost close friends at the hands of that young warrior were resolute in their desire for revenge. They were willing to sacrifice their lives to injure the young man. Meanwhile, others, feeling that he was just one person and their army was strong, secretly unleashed spells or launched their life-bound items, confident of their success. There were also cunning Gold Core demons and sword cultivator death warriors, striking precisely and viciously, not hoping for a lethal blow but merely seeking to inflict pain.

On the battlefield, the chaos was infectious; individuals often followed the tide, whether to flee, transform, bravely fight to the death, or generously face death.

And then, with the injury inflicted by that Nascent Soul sword cultivator onto the young Hidden Official, the atmosphere was thick with murderous intent, overwhelming all around.

In the distance, Fan Dache murmured, “This formation shouldn’t have been opened so widely; it’s too perilous. In such a battlefield, isn’t danger everywhere? This is no mere contest of strength.”

If not for Ning Yao holding the line, the second manager’s reckless strike would have surely led to death.

Ning Yao said, “It’s precisely because I’m here that he would dare to strike like this. That’s the order of things; it must be understood this way.”

Ning Yao also knew why Fan Dache was so anxious—ultimately, he was worried about Chen Ping'an’s safety.

Ning Yao didn’t elaborate; after all, Fan Dache was not a pure warrior. The path of sword cultivation and the gradual ascension of pure warriors, while they may seem to converge, were fundamentally different.

This was true martial combat—fighting with strength and courage—merely a small path of martial arts. To contend against heaven and earth with one's own power and fists, that was the true grandeur of the Dao.

In the distance, the center of the encirclement had almost transformed into a slowly moving hill.

As Fan Dache was sheathing his sword, he couldn't help but ask, “Is everything really okay like this?”

“Something is wrong on their end,” Ning Yao replied.

Fan Dache fell silent.

He could only continue striking from the edge of the battlefield, doing his best to relieve some of Chen Ping'an's pressure.

In truth, it didn’t hold much significance, but one had to do something.

In dealing with others, when one lacks the ability, seeking peace of mind is a good habit to cultivate.

Ning Yao wielded her sword, weaving through the battlefield. A golden line wove through the demon army, its brilliance lingering. There were both straight paths and crooked golden trails, extending thousands of zhang. Wherever she passed, remnants of limbs and corpses were severed by the golden long sword, which itself formed a natural array, laden with potent sword intent. The surrounding sword energy overflowed, causing the demon army great distress; many five-realm cultivators simply lay down to avoid the increasingly dense golden lines.

Many Dragon Gate and Gold Core demon cultivators quickly fled from the suspended golden sword formation.

Once Ning Yao gathered enough sword energy, she pinched a technique with her fingers and lightly swiped downward.

It was as if a storm had paused in mid-air, like an enormous pond just above the ground, before abruptly crashing to the earth.

On Chen Ping'an's battlefield, the ground shook, and the force of his punch roared like thunder.

Nearby demons splattered away as the small hill formed by the demon army seemed to shatter from within.

Fan Dache let out a sigh of relief, finally catching a glimpse of Chen Ping'an, who appeared somewhat disheveled, his clothes torn and bloodied, yet his overwhelming fist intent was almost visible, enveloping him as if protected by a divine presence.

Perhaps this was the most genuine embodiment of a martial artist's golden body.

Although Fan Dache was a sword cultivator who dreamed of becoming a sword immortal, witnessing this scene forced him to acknowledge the sheer ferocity of a martial artist entrenched in battle, unyielding even in the face of death.

After being struck by a brilliant spell on his back, Chen Ping'an staggered only a step before propelling himself forward, charging ten zhang ahead to clear a path with his fists.

He was struck midsection by a powerful demon cultivator with a heavy weapon, sending Chen Ping'an flying dozens of zhang, along with a barrage of spells and numerous life-bound weapons attacking him from all directions.

In the blink of an eye, as soon as Chen Ping'an landed, a small hill formed again on the battlefield, and he vanished from sight.

Fan Dache felt increasingly alarmed. Were the demon cultivators going mad? Were they truly so willing to risk their lives?!

Ning Yao continued to leave the frontline to the injured Chen Ping'an. At most, she would help with a few strikes, thinning out the demon army's ranks on either side with the sword immortal, cutting down some of their lateral strength.

As a piece of immortal-grade equipment, the sword immortal had developed a certain connection with Chen Ping'an, akin to a child beginning to speak. It was evident that it was now quite exhilarated. 

In the past, under Chen Ping'an's command, it had indeed felt stifled, being called upon at will by a master who wasn't even a true sword cultivator. What was crucial was that in every fierce battle, the sword immortal had never felt fully satisfied.

Ning Yao remained calm and composed, her sword heart steady, executing her strikes with precision; yet, that didn’t mean she felt no concern for Chen Ping'an’s predicament.

In the battlefield, what merit would there be for the Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall if he were to perish?

Among the sixty military tents of the wilderness world, there was considerable debate over this matter, with opinions roughly divided into three camps.

One faction, led by the Gengyin tent, believed that killing the Hidden Official Chen Ping'an should be regarded as equivalent to slaying a Jade Purity Realm sword immortal. Their reasoning was that, although Chen Ping'an held a high position and great power as the new Hidden Official at the Sword Qi Great Wall, commanding troops and strategies that inflicted great losses on the wilderness world, he was not a sword cultivator and, in terms of realm, was not particularly high. Although he had managed to defeat Li Zhen in a direct confrontation, he did not necessarily possess the combat power of a peak Nascent Soul sword cultivator. Therefore, adding the title of Hidden Official and considering him as a Jade Purity Realm sword immortal was quite reasonable.

Another major faction, led by the Dingmao tent, supported by the endorsements of two prominent demon lords, Yang Zhi and Huang Luan, contended that this young Hidden Official posed a significant threat, both in terms of real power and the symbolic significance to the Sword Qi Great Wall. Thus, killing Chen Ping'an should be considered equivalent to defeating an immortal realm sword cultivator, worthy of being regarded as a great sword immortal.

Beyond this, there was a solitary Jia Shen tent that proposed an even more shocking view: as long as one could kill Chen Ping'an, the merit should at least be regarded as between that of killing Dong Sangeng, Chen Xi, Qi Tingji, and Lu Zhi, or Lao Long'er and Nalan Shaowei. Even if the merit were to be equivalent to that of a sword cultivator from the Ascension realm, it would not be unreasonable!

The debate raged on. The Gengzi tent compiled opinions and ultimately decided that the merit for killing Chen Ping'an would be assessed as that of slaying a great sword immortal, but it should rank between Nalan Shaowei and Yue Qing, not to be simply seen as an ordinary great sword immortal.

Fan Dache's heart trembled.

On the distant battlefield, the first time Chen Ping'an was struck by a demon cultivator, he was sent crashing towards Fan Dache's direction with a double-fisted blow.

In mid-air, Chen Ping'an twisted his body, evading several crucial spells and magical artifacts. He braved the remaining attacks and landed gracefully, sliding back five or six steps. With a heavy stomp, he regained his balance, returning to the battlefield at an even faster pace, directly confronting a demon cultivator who was also a pure martial artist. This opponent was not only the leader of a demon army but also a cultivator, and after transforming into human form, he was tall and robust, armed with no weapons.

On the line, the two pure martial artists clashed head-on, their fists colliding, sending shockwaves that pushed back the surrounding demon army.

The distant traveling demon cultivator and Chen Ping'an each took a punch without retreating, instead exchanging blows anew. The impact resounded like muffled drums on the battlefield.

The traveling demon cultivator roared, signaling the nearby Gold Core and Dragon Gate cultivators to disregard their own lives and unleash all their magical artifacts and spells.

In the blink of an eye, Chen Ping'an switched his stance, delivering sixteen consecutive punches.

Since the opponent dared to stand still, he would not take a step back either. Regardless of their identities or factions, in martial combat, nothing was more exhilarating than trading blows without moving.

Direct and straightforward, as long as the martial art was superior and the punches heavy enough, the opponent would fall obediently, like acknowledging the superiority of one’s power in the art of fists!

---

Among the sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage, Deng Liang was the most stable in temperament. Originally a wild cultivator who had later been accepted into the sect as a record-keeper and immortal teacher, he understood the taste of the muddy world and had been influenced by the ethereal aura of the mountain's cave abodes. Thus, he was naturally not prone to impatience.

Almost everyone’s calmness is honed gradually.

However, today, for some reason, Deng Liang suddenly overturned the writing desk.

Instantly, he became quiet, muttering an apology, and after a moment of sitting in a daze, he got up to tidy his desk.

Sword Immortal Chou Miao gently shook his head, signaling everyone not to speak.

With Chou Miao's stance, the other sword cultivators could only follow suit and ignore him. Even those like Xuan Can and Cao Gun, who were also outsiders like Deng Liang, remained silent.

Dong Budu shot a glare at Guo Zhujiu, who was making exaggerated gestures towards him.

What did it matter? Just because Deng Liang liked her didn't mean she should feel the same.

Deng Liang's expression was gloomy as he took out a wine jug and drank silently.

During the earlier process of seeking sword guidance at the Sword Qi Great Wall from the wilderness world, three young geniuses had discarded their life-bound flying swords.

Among the three sword cultivators considered outstanding even within the Sword Qi Great Wall, their paths were cut off without any doubt, and there were no further chances.

Subsequently, during this chaotic battle, four had been ambushed and killed by the sword immortal death warriors. As for the young sword cultivators not recorded in the ledger, there were even more.

This was still in the context of the Sword Qi Great Wall having two stationed sword immortals and over forty earth immortals temporarily descending from the city to support and lay ambush.

The spiritual energy of the Sword Qi Great Wall was rapidly dwindling.

The daily consumption of resources was an astronomical sum that no sect in the wilderness world could fathom. Once calculated into immortal money, even the cultivators responsible for managing finances would feel their hearts waver upon merely glancing at the figures in the ledger.

As the world shifted, it was being subtly accelerated by the wilderness world.

According to the hidden secrets revealed by that Hidden Official, every previous strike by the three sect saints had not been easy. After jointly crafting that golden river that cleaved the battlefield, it was more like a resolute choice, one with no turning back. Or perhaps they had originally had a path but chose not to take it.

The situation loomed like a tide; regardless of how hard the Hidden Official lineage struggled or how the sword cultivators on the city wall forgot about life and death, exerting their utmost to slay enemies, it seemed that delaying the momentum for even a moment would ultimately be futile.

Deng Liang, a wild cultivator, could accept failure, but he had never felt so stifled, humiliated, and indignant, eventually succumbing to a sense of despair, relying on wine to drown his sorrows.

The more he remained in the summer palace and accessed firsthand information, observing the overall situation, the clearer he saw the ebb and flow of the battles and the losses on both sides. The more profound his comprehension of the war’s trajectory became, the more helpless he felt.

Lin Junbi was busy with her tasks.

Chou Miao glanced at Lin Junbi, and the young sword immortal subtly nodded. Lin Junbi, a prodigy from the Central Land, had lofty aspirations.

Lin Junbi was unaware of how highly she was regarded in Chou Miao’s eyes.

After arriving at the Sword Qi Great Wall, the first lesson Lin Junbi learned was to lower her stance as much as possible.

In fact, while she radiated intelligence, wit, and spirit, making her exceptionally outstanding, she still didn’t seem as trustworthy as Chou Miao, who was more grounded and reserved.

The young sword immortal, laden with a plethora of legendary tales, had become a sword cultivator of the Hidden Official lineage, yet she was not the new Hidden Official herself. She was slightly lesser in stature, having never uttered any words that would cause people to gasp in awe or committed any acts that would leave others astonished.

Yet, she was able to command respect and inspire trust.

Everyone in the Hidden Official lineage likely contemplated who would become the next Hidden Official if anything were to happen to the young one. It would surely be Chou Miao, not Lin Junbi.

Lin Junbi bore no resentment over this. Recognizing her own inadequacies, she accepted it. She was never afraid to deal with masters; she learned quickly, and as long as it wasn’t a life-and-death situation, any sparring would only enrich her own skills.

Lin Junbi knew very well that Chou Miao’s ability to gain the crowd’s favor was not solely due to her high cultivation realm.

There were many aspects of Chou Miao worth emulating and learning from.

For instance, no one would think of Chou Miao as the kind of extraordinary and cunningly intelligent person.

Everyone’s first impression would certainly not be that way.

If Chou Miao is skilled in swordsmanship but gentle in temperament, without sharp edges, then the impression left by the young Hidden Official was that she was not particularly high in realm but could fight well. She had deep internal schemes yet was genuinely kind-hearted.

Moreover, with the diverse strengths of the sword cultivators in the Hidden Official lineage, Lin Junbi benefited greatly from her experiences there. So why would she leave?

Even if Chen Ping'an urged her to go, Lin Junbi might not choose to leave.

Lin Junbi glanced at the temporarily unoccupied main seat and gently shook her head. She would not leave, but she absolutely would not take on the role of the Hidden Official.

---

Chen Sanqiu observed the situation near the battlefield, took a moment to consider, then called for Dong Hua Fu to join him as they flew closer to Chen Ping'an. He also instructed Dong Pangzi and Diezhong to muster some strength; once they caught their breath, they would immediately return to support.

The two changed battlefields, forming a triangular formation with Chen Ping'an and Ning Yao.

Dong Hua Fu squatted atop the long sword and began to draw conclusions. “Compared to Sister Ning's opening formations, this is a bit slower.”

Dong Hua Fu thought for a moment and recalled the second manager's life-bound divine ability, which was accounting, and added, “But Ah Liang once said, men shouldn’t be too quick.”

Chen Sanqiu burst into laughter.

Unexpectedly, just then, the second manager was struck by a demon cultivator clad in golden crow armor, a punch that seemed to break through the formation, piercing through the army's arrangement that Chen Sanqiu had just thinned out. The demon cultivator fell not far from Chen Sanqiu, and after rolling over, stood up, shattering a life-bound artifact that clung to him like a parasite. With a sudden intake of pure qi, he stabilized his stance, but the wounds on his body burst open, blood flowing.

The clothing borrowed from the sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage had nearly all been expended. He wore the last remaining one, which was already in tatters, leaving his upper body almost exposed, with injuries revealing white bones. Chen Ping'an donned the last piece of the Ning family's green shirt robe and turned to look at Dong Heitan.

Chen Ping'an smiled.

Ning Yao smiled from a distance too.

Dong Hua Fu responded with a silly grin.

Chen Ping'an leaned back, narrowly dodging a severe sword light that attacked from behind. Before falling to the ground, he slapped the earth, flipped his body, took a step forward, and finally used the shrinking ground talisman for the first time, reaching the side of a sneaky demon sword cultivator who had attacked multiple times. With a sweeping arm, he severed the demon's head, then bent down to use the lifeless body as a shield, crashing sideways.

A demon cultivator with a dull expression, resembling a middle-aged man, picked up a broken sword from the ground—its quality was poor, barely resembling a sword at all. He stepped forward and struck down, lacking brilliant sword light or sharp intent, yet silent like the sword holder himself. Chen Ping'an did not even have time to activate the square inch talisman; his fist intent reached its peak, and he struggled to grasp the sword's edge, but still, he was struck down into the ground.

The man did not intend to use brute force to sever both of Chen Ping'an's hands and shoulders. Instead, he casually drew out the ordinary long sword and slashed towards Chen Ping'an's neck.

Chen Ping'an directly raised his left hand to block his heart, and the man was clearly slightly surprised. His sword would indeed change trajectory midway, shattering Chen Ping'an's heart. At the critical moment of changing his sword, the man took a step forward, his form becoming ethereal like a flying sword, appearing directly behind Chen Ping'an. The sword tip twisted casually, stabbing back, hitting Chen Ping'an's spine. Almost simultaneously, Chen Ping'an gathered his fists into a dragon form, the sword tip momentarily stalling before propelling him forward faster. Sure enough, the “second” sword-wielding man appeared right in front of Chen Ping'an, bringing down his sword straight down.

The man smiled slightly, increased his strength, and gripped the long sword tightly.

On the battlefield, nearly a hundred sword cultivators quickly surrounded Chen Ping'an in a circle, all holding swords, none wielding life-bound flying swords, with various stances aimed directly at Chen Ping'an.

Moreover, in six other locations outside the circular sword formation, there were men holding swords, seemingly waiting for Chen Ping'an to use the square inch talisman.

In addition, in front of Ning Yao, Fan Dache, Chen Sanqiu, and Dong Hua Fu, another vast circular sword formation, filled with sword-wielding individuals, emerged.

One person pointed his sword at Chen Ping'an, Ning Yao, Chen Sanqiu, and Dong Hua Fu, two young geniuses noted in the Gengzi ledger, plus another Gold Core sword cultivator not listed.

This man was truly targeting both Chen Ping'an and Fan Dache.

As for the outcome, he had already handed the choice to all the sword cultivators of the same age in the Sword Qi Great Wall; he didn’t care much for the result.

When a sword cultivator draws their sword, it is most important that they are true to themselves. The merits of the battle are secondary.

Each sword-wielding individual was real or fake, sharing the burden of combat power, requiring precise calculations.

The sword-wielding man seemed somewhat helpless, and his already elusive form burst apart.

The remaining sword-wielding individuals were targeted by at least two to three, up to five or six flying swords.

And that young Hidden Official remained immobile.

At the same time, the man who concealed his face and aura, who had vanished and reappeared, glanced at Chen Ping'an, sharing a knowing smile, and in the elegant language of the righteous realm, uttered, “Kindred spirits.”

This strange sword cultivator, who had appeared mysteriously and vanished like a ghost, was no longer around.

Chen Ping'an sheathed all his flying swords, returning to a single “Moon at the Bottom of the Well.” The essence of this flying sword's life-bound divine ability was the moon reflecting in a deep well; as long as ripples stirred in the heart lake, every draw and sheath of the sword would represent a cycle of the moon, shattering and then reforming, all depending on the thoughts of the sword cultivator.

Finally managing to nurture two life-bound flying swords, he found himself having to reveal the Moon at the Bottom of the Well ahead of time.

Chen Ping'an inwardly cursed the damned kindred spirits.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 765: Where is the Hometown of Sword Cultivators?

Ning Yao allowed Chen Ping'an to return to the city first, reminding him to be careful on the way back.

Dong Hua Fu felt that this statement was a bit unnecessary.

Speaking plainly had always been Dong Hua Fu's style.

Chen Sanqiu chuckled, "Between men and women, if there aren't a few unnecessary words, it would be troublesome."

Dong Hua Fu nodded in agreement and then asked, "Do you have any chance to say those unnecessary words?"

Chen Sanqiu responded with a smile reminiscent of the shopkeeper's.

Dong Hua Fu, fearing that the shopkeeper might hold a grudge, wasn't particularly worried about Chen Sanqiu—who dreamed of becoming her brother-in-law—so she added some fuel to the fire with her words. "The reason my sister became a sword cultivator under the Hidden Official lineage isn’t because she’s deliberately avoiding you, right? If that's the case, then fine, I'll help you out later. This is the least I can do for a friend."

Chen Sanqiu shook his head. "That's not the case. Your sister is straightforward; she likes what she likes and doesn't like what she doesn't. She wouldn't be so deliberate about it."

When you like someone, everything about them seems wonderful.

Moreover, from the time Chen Sanqiu was a child, wearing short pants, he felt that the neighbor's older sister, Dong Bu De, was genuinely good, not just because she caught his eye.

It was like when he first saw the words "childhood sweethearts" in a book; he thought that was the most touching term in the world, far surpassing any tranquil lakes or fiery autumn mountains.

If one were to say Dong Bu De was extraordinarily beautiful, that wouldn't quite be the case.

It was just that over the years, the more Chen Sanqiu drank, the fonder he became of her.

Before Chen Ping'an arrived at the Sword Qi Great Wall, during the previous skirmishes, as long as Chen Sanqiu finished his sword practice early, he would go watch Dong Bu De from afar. Once, during a particularly tense situation, he lent her a hand. Afterward, Dong Bu De thanked him and followed up with a blunt remark that pierced his heart. It was the second time she had made it clear that they were both sword cultivators and acquaintances. While it was fine to help each other on the battlefield, she advised him not to entertain any thoughts of becoming that mountain companion of hers; just thinking about it made her skin crawl. After that encounter, Chen Sanqiu returned to the city and, having drunk some wine, found himself pushing against walls and crashing into trees again.

Chen Ping'an was injured quite severely; it wasn't just superficial wounds but also serious internal injuries left by the flying swords of other cultivators and the attacks from various demonic practitioners on his life source. Despite this, his spirit seemed to be rising rather than diminishing. Ning Yao hadn't seen such a bright-eyed Chen Ping'an in a long time.

At that moment, his entire being was a chaotic mess of energy, which wasn't entirely a bad thing. As Li Er had once said, his junior brother Zheng Dafeng had some insights after visiting that Crab Workshop sign, and upon returning, he mentioned that a person's body was like an ancient battlefield site, so there was no need to seek outside for help—this wasn't just empty talk about cultivating the mind.

So right now, Chen Ping'an was essentially a martial training ground himself. He excelled at unraveling the threads of his own condition and using pure true energy to overpower the spiritual energy of other cultivators.

He picked up a damaged long sword of unknown origin. The sword itself wasn't particularly mystical; it was just extremely heavy, indicating the forging material must be of decent quality—worth a considerable amount of celestial currency. 

In the martial world of the minor states on Treasure Bottle Continent, this would be a genuine divine weapon, one that even the local water gods might fear.

Chen Ping'an took the lead, riding his sword northward, selecting a weaker point in the demonic army’s formation and occasionally throwing a punch along the way.

Instead of heading directly to the city wall, he flew upwards to the highest "horizontal bar" of the wall, sitting cross-legged. He took out his sword nurturing gourd and drank a few mouthfuls of osmanthus wine, watching the battlefield unfold closely. As he calmed his breath, he skillfully bandaged his wounds.

Every large character carved into the wall, especially the horizontal strokes, was an excellent place for cultivation.

However, when it came to the stage of the ant-like siege warfare, these natural sword cultivation grounds often turned into places of certain death.

Thus, those old sword cultivators who could practice here for hundreds of years must possess tremendous killing power and exceptional survival skills.

Not far from Chen Ping'an sat an elderly sword cultivator with his eyes closed, nurturing his spirit. The old man did not rise to greet him, so Chen Ping'an remained silent, not wanting to disturb the elder’s quiet meditation.

The elder appeared to be Yin Chen, a sixth-page infant sword cultivator from the third volume. Though he was advanced in years, he had been stuck at the infant realm, unable to break through. His temper was fierce, and he was a solitary figure, without close friends. Most sword cultivators at the Sword Qi Great Wall had close friendships, whether living or dead, but Yin Chen had none. Whenever he entered battle, he was full of killing intent, and once he drew his sword, he would not distinguish between friend and foe, resulting in a large number of kills among both demons and fellow sword cultivators alike. His accumulated military achievements were minimal, even less than many younger golden core sword cultivators, as much of his merit was erased. Consequently, Yin Chen's reputation was poor; few were willing to approach a monster who might even kill his own kind.

Each native sword cultivator noted in the first and third volumes had different annotations from the Hidden Official lineage. If the interpretations from the Summer Palace sword cultivators were too numerous, they would be mixed with a few extra sheets.

Regarding the highly ranked Yin Chen, there were surprisingly few insights recorded, with only a few notes from Chou Miao and Lin Junbi, which were entirely different from the general views of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

If battlefield friendly fire was common, almost every sword immortal would have experienced it. However, it could hardly be said that they bore the blame. Yin Chen was different; many times, the old man's sharp sword strikes were calculated to guarantee the deaths of a few sword cultivators.

According to the responsibilities of the Hidden Official lineage, the elder sword cultivator Yin Chen should merely guard his position and not engage in battle.

After bandaging his various wounds, Chen Ping'an summoned a purification talisman, swiftly erasing the bloodstains. After all, he was a guest; even if the host wasn't particularly welcoming, there was no reason for a guest not to show basic courtesy.

The elder opened his eyes, his voice hoarse as he spoke, "You're quite the amusing lad. I've seen a few pure martial artists at the Sword Qi Great Wall. Others throw punches, constrained by flying swords and magical treasures, but here you are, holding yourself back."

Chen Ping'an turned his head and smiled, "Elder Yin, you have a keen eye."

The elder asked, "You didn't feel any discomfort for not calling me 'Lord Hidden Official'?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "Not at all."

Yin Chen gazed toward the battlefield front. To the north of the golden river was Ning Yao lending assistance, while southward were the sword cultivators tasked with forming the array. Yin Chen sneered, "Every time I see these so-called young talents, I can't help but feel a bit disheartened. It's impossible to compare."

Chen Ping'an chuckled, "More sword cultivators will feel the same way when they see you, Elder Yin."

In fact, Yin Chen had once been one of those young talents, and he was exceptionally outstanding. Back in the day, his glory at the Sword Qi Great Wall was roughly equivalent to the current Gao Ye Hou and Situ Weiran.

The practice of swordsmanship had gone smoothly for him, breaking through realms like cutting through bamboo, until he reached the infant realm, where he unexpectedly stagnated, wasting hundreds of years.

Yin Chen coldly laughed, "What can a useless person do besides looking up at others and drooling? For example, me—sitting here all year round, I've gone from a young useless one to an old useless one."

One who can be harsh even on themselves is practically unbeatable when it comes to arguing.

Chen Ping'an asked, "Did you see the sword-wielding man earlier, Elder Yin? Did you discern his roots?"

Yin Chen scoffed, "The Hidden Official lineage gets weaker with each generation. You, an outsider, have already reached a decent realm, yet relying on some superficial connections, you managed to claim Elder Xiao Xun's summer palace, overflowing with records and secrets, yet you don't even know this bit of information? Can't you at least make an educated guess?"

Chen Ping'an didn't mind the elder's harsh words. You can scold all you want, I'll just keep probing. He continued, "Is he the proud son of the Hundred Swords of Tuo Yue Mountain? Ranked about the same as Zhuo Qiao and Li Zhen?"

Yin Chen retorted, "I reckon the whole Sword Qi Great Wall has heard all sorts of nasty things about Elder Xiao Xun, right? Just a bunch of brats without fathers to teach them. If I were Elder Xiao Xun and I broke through the Sword Qi Great Wall, I'd hunt down every sword cultivator who insulted me—those who dared to curse me to my face would live, and those who didn't would die. That's how it should be. By the way, earlier, when the great demon Yang Zhi was slaughtering that southern traveling sword cultivator, you, for the sake of the greater good, must have taken quite a bit of flak, huh? How was that experience? If it happened again, would you allow those reckless sword cultivators to die?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "Ah Liang once told me, if a person can avoid death, they should do so at all costs. If taking a few insults can save many lives, is there a more worthwhile deal than that? I think very few."

Yin Chen immediately fell silent.

It wasn't that the young man's logic was particularly sound; that wasn't the issue at all.

This young Hidden Official was a disciple of the scholarly lineage known for its seclusion, a junior brother of sorts, even having a good relationship with the elder sword immortal. However, the moment he got involved with that Ah Liang, Yin Chen felt a headache coming on.

For over a century, Yin Chen had been thoroughly exploited by that despicable fellow. It was like catching a fat sheep and mercilessly plucking its wool.
