Once the wool was gone, the sheep had grown thin, but now that the fat sheep was recovering its vigor, it was time to pluck it again. If Ah Liang only had those methods, Yin Chen could ignore him. However, that fellow could genuinely sit beside him, chattering away for hours just to say, "As long as I can have a word with Elder Yin, this trip to the Sword Qi Great Wall will be worth it." At that time, Yin Chen couldn't help but curse him to get lost, only for the other party to retaliate and pin him down for a good beating.

When Ah Liang left, he was in high spirits, striking a signature pose, running his hands through his hair, and leaving behind the words, "What a thrill! I’ve had over eight hundred battles, and still undefeated!"

Yin Chen had laid on the ground for half a day, bewildered.

After that, Ah Liang often came to find the old sword immortal, claiming to chat and bond, while sneakily boosting his win count.

Recall that Ah Liang, Yin Chen wasn't entirely resentful; after all, neither of them had ever really practiced swordsmanship together. Most of their interactions revolved around Ah Liang boasting about how popular he was with good girls in the world of Haoran. Yet, throughout it all, he never managed to mention a single girl’s name. However, the occasional serious words from Ah Liang often targeted Yin Chen’s bottleneck in the infant realm.

Regardless of how bad his temper was, Yin Chen still felt he had to acknowledge that kindness.

He might not be good at socializing, but he could still tell the difference between good and bad people.

Sometimes, perhaps because he was too discerning, he simply felt too lazy to socialize.

They didn’t know each other well, and with their vastly different personalities, there wasn’t much to discuss. Besides, Yin Chen didn't like drinking; otherwise, Chen Ping'an would have offered him a jar of bamboo sea cave wine.

Suddenly, Yin Chen said, "Is this how pure martial artists of the Haoran world practice their punches?"

Chen Ping'an shook his head, "The routes to practicing punches are actually quite similar; it all starts with getting hit first—just the intensity varies."

Yin Chen asked again, "In front of Ning Yao, you picked up so much trash, and you still have the audacity?"

Now that was a topic worth discussing.

Chen Ping'an smiled, "I have a habit of being a bit careless, but fortunately, Ning Yao doesn't mind."

Yin Chen queried, "You don't look particularly impressive; how did you win her over? I only heard that Ning Yao traveled through the Haoran world and didn't expect her to fall victim here. If I’m being honest, you’re nowhere near Cao Ci; I specifically went to peek at him on the city wall. His looks and punches are both noteworthy; you simply can't compare."

Now this was getting interesting; the old senior was complimenting someone.

Chen Ping'an promptly got closer to the elder, took a sip of wine, and chuckled, "While I admit my punches can't compare, I think our looks aren't too far apart."

To his surprise, Yin Chen suddenly turned hostile, "I’m nurturing my sword now; could you please step aside, Hidden Official? You're quite bothersome here."

Chen Ping'an, feeling somewhat dejected, rose and flew away on his sword.

Yin Chen rested his fists on his knees, chuckling. The scholars of the Haoran world were all infuriatingly arrogant.

Chen Ping'an made his way to the straw hut on the city wall, first greeting Wei Dajian, who supported half of the tavern's business, with a smile.

Wei Jin smiled, "What a splendid punch! It certainly looks impressive! You have the style of an invincible god of punches, but it was a bit slow on the attack."

He had literally pummeled a far-traveling martial artist from the Wild World to death with his bare hands. This achievement, compared to a sword immortal’s strike, was naturally minor, but it was still rare.

It would make for a delectable accompaniment to wine.

Chen Ping'an chuckled, "Next time I visit the tavern, I’ll treat you to a bowl of plain noodles to sober you up so you won’t talk nonsense."

Wei Jin pointed back at the hut, "The elder sword immortal isn't in a good mood. If you know how to speak, then be a bit more talkative."

After parting ways with Wei Jin, as soon as Chen Ping'an landed on the city wall, the elder sword immortal stepped out of the hut, hands clasped behind him. "Oh, the Divine Warrior Chen has arrived—my humble abode is now graced."

Chen Ping'an found it strange; the elder sword immortal hadn’t been this “polite” before. His impression of the elder was that he was dignified and sparing with words.

Chen Qingdu glanced at Chen Ping'an, noting he was injured but had reaped significant gains. He communicated through thought, "I owe you two secrets. I can tell you now."

Chen Ping'an composed himself.

What followed were two so-called secrets, each more astonishing than the last.

One was about the hometown of all the imprisoned sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

The earliest batch of ancient prisoners had origins split evenly between the Wild World and the now-established Fifth Realm.

Chen Ping'an was taken aback.

This meant that half of the prisoners and their descendants had, from the very beginning, been in their hometown.

Thus, having been born and dying at the Sword Qi Great Wall, it was all in their hometown?

As for the remaining half of the prisoners’ descendants, if they wished to return home, it would be related to the Fifth Realm. As long as they could survive, there was at least a chance to return home?

The second secret was even greater.

The elder sword immortal's explanation was shocking: the path to becoming a pure martial artist was actually a path to becoming a deity, which would also involve military cultivators.

Though Chen Ping'an had speculated on this before, hearing it from the elder sword immortal clarified many connections. For instance, he was no longer puzzled as to why there was a Golden Body realm in martial arts. In the world, all mountain and water gods sought to manifest a Golden Body as the foundation of the Dao. 

Not to mention those ghostly spirits achieving divinity, just the experience of living humans becoming deities, similar to the experience of Yang Hua, the water god of Iron Symbol River, "the form dissolves but the bones remain," was a necessary path. This was actually quite similar to martial artists refining their bodies and honing their bones.

Chen Qingdu didn’t lay everything out, knowing that this young man liked to think. There would be plenty of time to ponder over the earlier pages of this old history.

As they walked slowly, since they had already started strolling, they couldn’t turn back too soon. The elder spoke a bit more, "Since ancient times, there has been a distinction between gods and immortals. Why the order of gods before immortals? According to current definitions, if a person's soul does not dissipate after death, they are considered a god. Enjoying the incense and sacrifices of the human realm, they need no cultivation to stabilize their Golden Body."

"To not die as an immortal is akin to those cultivators who lie on the mountains now. Historians always trim and cut their histories, and over time, the truth becomes more and more distant. If you ever get the chance, you might want to visit the three great academies. Being that old scholar’s closed-door disciple means you’ll only be flipping through a few worthless old books, but it should still hold some weight."

Chen Ping'an merely listened and remembered, finding little immediate significance in these words. If he were to be more practical, they might even seem meaningless.

However, what came next was something that made Chen Ping'an perk up, fearful of missing a single word.

"First travel far and then reach the mountain peak, followed by the tenth realm of martial arts, which is further divided into three layers: Qi Flourishing, Returning to Truth, and Reaching the Divine. What does 'Reaching the Divine' mean? I remember there's a saying in your hometown, what was it?"

"Reaching the Door!" 

Chen Ping'an blurted out, "If a person’s skill is good enough, whether they're a farmer or a porcelain maker, they are often praised as having 'reached the door.'"

Chen Qingdu nodded, "Reaching the door—what door is that? How does one walk that path? Who will guard the door? The answers are all in your hometown… what was it again?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "Yuzhe."

Chen Qingdu smiled and nodded, elaborating further on the three layers of the tenth realm.

Yet the elder's expression occasionally showed a hint of nostalgia.

In the Treasure Bottle Continent, there was an old friend who had been trapped in that "Ten Thousand Year Light Yin" for a long time.

Thus, Chen Qingdu remarked, "Cui Zhan from Xiuhuo is indeed formidable."

Chen Ping'an responded, "During the first Heart-Questioning Match, we passed through safely because Mr. Qi was present. When he wasn't there for the second match, I couldn’t hold out no matter what. That was still because Cui Zhan didn’t exert full effort."

Chen Qingdu said, "All the hardships that are hard to endure and yet survived are like a pit dug in one’s heart. The larger the pit, the more it can bear in the future."

Chen Ping'an nodded.

But it was also possible to spend a lifetime filling that pit. For instance, the more the world owes someone in their childhood, the more that person will strive to make up for it as they grow older.

Leaving the city wall, Chen Ping'an flew his sword towards the private residence of the summer palace, beginning to rest and heal.

Just two days later, Chen Ping'an made a trip to the summer palace, coming and going freely, holding a jade token without needing to consume a single Spatial Shrink Talisman.

He chose a secluded spot to observe Bai Mama teaching the children how to punch, explaining what it means for "the whole body to be a punch," what the intention is, how to learn, and how to practice.

Among the children was one he recognized—a little girl named Yuan Zao Hua, to whom he had given two folding fans. She was the only child capable of genuinely tricking the shopkeeper’s celestial money with her skills.

The other children were not strangers to Chen Ping'an either, as they had all been carefully selected as martial seeds by him and the Hidden Official lineage. One of the children had already been taken to the Central Divine Continent by Yu Jianfu, while the others who were still learning punches were all here.

There were many sword cultivators at the Sword Qi Great Wall, but pure martial artists were few and far between.

If the Sword Qi Great Wall were to fall, becoming part of the Wild World, would all those martial fates be left for the Wild World?

Of course not.

Yet, Chen Ping'an understood that temporarily clinging to hope, pushing these children to compete for the title of "strongest" was a slim chance. Moreover, the Sword Qi Great Wall inherently had a significant advantage; the Dao clashed fiercely, which he hadn't understood before but began to after being pointed out by the elder sword immortal on the city wall. The female martial god Pei Bei from the Central Divine Continent was likely well-prepared, while Cao Ci, training purely, had never sought the martial fate. In this regard, Chen Ping'an felt he couldn't compare to Cao Ci at all. Now, as long as the martial fate was willing to come, he wished he could welcome it all at once, calling it "relatives" and "family," welcoming them with open arms.

However, even if these children rushed to practice punches without earning martial fate, it wouldn’t matter much. As long as they had a skill, laid a solid foundation, they would have greater chances of survival no matter where they ended up. In a chaotic world, wanting to secure a foothold often had little to do with status.

At the training ground, Bai Mama threw a punch. The distance was short, just half an arm's length, but the intention behind the punch was heavy and natural.

At the level of a seventh realm martial artist, the so-called moves had already become a competition of the depth of punch intent, akin to a manifestation of a simple Dao.

With no warning, Bai Mama struck toward a stout boy standing nearby, who remained motionless, wearing an expression that seemed to say, "Go ahead, if you can."

This was Jiang Yun, hailing from a well-off family, distinguished by his exceptional aptitude.

After Bai Mama withdrew her punch, the boy, oblivious, was already drenched in sweat.

This was a rare potential talent.

Bai Mama threw another punch, almost touching the forehead of a girl from Yu Hu Street. Although she was slightly less capable than Jiang Yun, she didn’t move, but her figure swayed slightly.

Ten or so children stood in a line, and Bai Mama walked past each one. Some kids stepped back; others gritted their teeth and stood firm.

Yet Bai Mama hadn’t thrown a single punch.

But Chen Ping'an could tell that when Bai Mama approached several children, the intent of her punch had already reached them. Unfortunately, only one child named Xu Gong from Mu Meng Alley had the right instinct. As Bai Mama’s intent stirred, he had already stepped back early, distinctly opposite Jiang Yun, but both had the potential to develop their punch intent sooner.

Looking at Yuan Zao Hua, she appeared tense, but still didn’t notice Bai Mama’s quietly radiating punch intent.

Chen Ping'an felt that none of this was particularly concerning. The path of martial arts did emphasize aptitude and foundations, but it wasn’t as harsh as that of Qi practitioners, nor was it as reliant on luck as sword cultivators. You couldn't become a sword cultivator by just enduring hardship, but practicing punches, with a certain level of talent, could allow one to progress steadily, slowly seeing results. Of course, the third realm would be a significant threshold, but these children would definitely surpass the third realm eventually, just a matter of time and effort.

Leaning against the corridor pillar, Chen Ping'an watched the children, noticing that those who were eager to learn often came from impoverished backgrounds like Yan Qi Alley and Mu Meng Alley, while those who were less interested were usually from affluent families like Jiang Yun’s.

The children began practicing standing stances. Bai Mama occasionally helped them with their postures, and then one child would end up rolling on the ground, crying out in pain.

Watching this, Chen Ping'an, who had initially been calm, couldn't help but feel a sense of schadenfreude and chuckled.

However, seeing Yuan Zao Hua and a child from a poor alley fall to the ground in pain made him feel a twinge of sadness.

Bai Mama glanced over at her son-in-law's direction, her expression kind. The old woman’s gaze held a hint of inquiry.

Chen Ping'an quickly waved his hand, signaling that he was merely here to observe.

To his surprise, Bai Mama smiled and said, "Lord Hidden Official, someone here said they want to learn punches from you, complaining that my punching style is too delicate. Why don’t you teach them?"

Just as Chen Ping'an was about to decline, Jiang Yun raised his arms across his chest, shouting, "Where is the Hidden Official?!"

Damn it, who is the Hidden Official here?

Chen Ping'an glanced at the little boy who had sat up, silently raising a hand, his arm shaking as he wiped the dust and sweat from his face.

Bai Mama wore a smile.

Reluctantly, Chen Ping'an walked to the training ground.

He didn't do much, just briefly shared some insights on the six-step stance, keeping it concise. 

Jiang Yun thought he was just getting started, only for the young Hidden Official to fall silent. The child couldn't help but ask, "Is that it?"

Chen Ping'an nodded, "Punch theory is never too complex; it’s like how thinner books often contain greater knowledge."

He spoke only halfway.

In the philosophies of the Three Teachings and the Hundred Schools, the more fundamental the tenets, the more elaborate the annotations became over generations, eventually flourishing and becoming all-encompassing.

However, when dealing with children, the more intricate the explanation, the more bewildered they would become.

Bai Mama laughed, "Lord Hidden Official, if you’re not in a hurry to return to the summer palace, it's just about time for the standing practice to finish up. You could teach them the Shaking Mountain Punch stance."

With outsiders present, she naturally couldn’t call him son-in-law.

Chen Ping'an thought for a moment; staying here for half an hour would be fine, so he nodded in agreement. "This stance originates from the Shaking Mountain Punch."

Jiang Yun interjected, "Wait, that name isn’t impressive enough; Shaking Mountain? Aren’t all the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall capable of leveling mountains with a single strike?"

Chen Ping'an smiled, "Then why don’t you teach me your punching technique?"

Jiang Yun frowned, "Speak properly and make some sense!"

Chen Ping'an chuckled knowingly and continued, "The name of the punch might not sound great, but let me elaborate a bit."

He broadly discussed the plight of martial artists in the Haoran world, stating that those not from prestigious backgrounds were often mixed in their techniques. As long as they could crack bricks and shatter stones with their punches, they were already doing quite well, so the term "Shaking Mountain" actually carried significant weight. His words mingled with his own observations, capturing the children’s attention. After all, it was a rare opportunity to slack off, avoiding the punishment of standing while dodging hits; who wouldn’t prefer that?

After finishing, Chen Ping'an demonstrated the stance a few times, helping the children correct their postures. After a stick of incense had burned, during the break, he first discussed the martial struggles in the city, then shared tales of the grandeur of martial artists at the peak of the ninth and tenth realms. The children loved hearing this, as the summer palace was essentially a cage; they couldn’t escape anyway. Jiang Yun once urged the little girl from Yu Hu Street to run away together. Just as they climbed the wall in the dead of night, they were dragged back by the ferocious wife of the innkeeper, punished to stand, causing the young girl to faint and Jiang Yun to fall asleep standing.

While Jiang Yun and the girl were being punished not far away, there were two children who proactively stood in stances, only to be quickly sent back by Bai Mama.

Training in martial arts should never be done to the point of exhaustion.

Whether one is poor in academics or rich in martial arts, training requires a good teacher to guide the way. Strengthening one’s body is also costly; otherwise, it’s easy to go astray, and practicing punches without proper guidance can lead to injuries and deplete one's vitality. Before the punch intent manifests, it feels like one is possessed by a ghost, which is the greatest suffering for many martial artists without a master to guide them.

Chen Ping'an gauged the time and took his leave.

Bai Mama continued to teach the children.

Jiang Yun muttered under his breath, "What a letdown when you meet them in person."

Bai Mama smiled, "When the day comes that you believe you’re worthy to ask the Hidden Official about punches, you’ll understand what despair truly means."

Jiang Yun shook his head, "Never mind. That shopkeeper is too clever. Once I reach a higher realm, if I catch up to him, I’ll definitely test the waters first. As long as he agrees to my request to spar, I won’t fight back."

Bai Mama shook her head. The Jiang family was rather straightforward; how did they raise such a foul-mouthed brat?

Jiang Yun glanced at the old woman, wondering what on earth his grandfather had seen in such a woman.

Chen Ping'an returned to the summer palace and then called upon Chou Miao, heading to the Spring Banner Hall of the Upside-Down Mountain, making a stop at the Plum Blossom Garden. The account book that the rosy-cheeked lady sent to the summer palace was quite substantial, so Chen Ping'an brought along two additional items from his trip to Upside-Down Mountain, borrowed from Yan Ming and Nalan Caihuan. In the empty Plum Blossom Garden, Chou Miao watched the eager Hidden Official moving things and couldn't help but ask, "Is this how you act in the Ning residence's treasury as well?"

Chen Ping'an couldn't be bothered to argue.

How could that be the same?

Upon reaching the Spring Banner Hall, he carefully reviewed the account books while Wei Wenlong quietly explained some of the nuances. Chen Ping'an noticed that Mi Yu the sword immortal seemed somewhat drowsy.

The outcome that Chou Miao and Lin Junbi had feared most had yet to materialize.

The ferryboats across the Eight Continents remained uninterrupted, enabling them to smoothly reach Upside-Down Mountain.

On their way, Chou Miao suggested they could raise their bids appropriately, and Chen Ping'an agreed, discussing the details with Yan Ming, Nalan Caihuan, and Shao Yunyan. Some key resource prices remained unchanged, or else the financial flow of the Sword Qi Great Wall would be under too much pressure. Even with the substantial assets of the Spring Banner Hall and Plum Blossom Garden added in, it still fell short. However, for some of the second-rate "extra" supplies from each ferryboat, they could afford to provide more concessions, taking it step by step.

Upon returning to the Sword Qi Great Wall, this was Chen Ping'an's first close encounter with the mirage to the north of the city. He didn't step inside but merely observed from afar.

Chou Miao looked up at the sky and conveyed through thought, "Setting aside the strength of your strikes, can you achieve the level of the elder sword immortal?"

Chen Ping'an shook his head, "It’s difficult to achieve."

Over at the Sword Qi Great Wall, Ning Yao's group of sword cultivators led the way back to the city.

Everyone was injured, with Die Zhang suffering the most.

Chen Qingdu stepped out of the straw hut.

Chen Sanqiu called out to his ancestor, and Chen Qingdu responded with an "Mm."

That was all.

If an outsider were to encounter the Chen Sanqiu during a drinking session, it would be hard to imagine that this charming young drunkard was actually the descendant of Chen Qingdu.

The elder sword immortal Chen Xi had once privately inquired of the ancestor Chen Qingdu whether he could allow Chen Sanqiu to leave and follow some Confucian sage to study in the Haoran world.

Chen Qingdu only asked one question.

Would Chen Sanqiu still carry the Chen surname afterward?

Ultimately, Chen Xi left the city wall in disappointment.

Chen Sanqiu respectfully took his leave and was the first to mount his sword and depart.

The Chen clan's descendants had always been like this.

Having an ancestor proficient in swordsmanship was tantamount to not having one, or even worse.

Dong Hua Fu, Yan Zhuo, and the others also took their leave, planning to return to the city for a few days of recuperation, while Die Zhang needed a longer time to recover.

Only Ning Yao remained.

Chen Ping'an flew his sword to the city wall.

Sitting beside Ning Yao on the city wall, Chen Ping'an gently swung his legs.

Ning Yao asked, "For the past year or so, you've been staying in the summer palace, hiding your thoughts and avoiding me?"

Chen Ping'an hesitated.

Ning Yao said, "Unless you’ve developed feelings for someone else, there's nothing you can't say."

Chen Ping'an chuckled wryly, remaining silent for a moment before saying, "I hadn’t planned to talk about it, but I suddenly realized that what I thought was best might just turn out to be the worst. After all, when two people like each other, it’s really not just one person’s matter. So I thought I should discuss it with you. After you hear it, you can hit me, but don’t get angry."

After hearing this, Ning Yao nodded.

Chen Ping'an shared what he had discussed with the elder sword immortal regarding a certain promise.

Ning Yao didn’t respond.

Chen Ping'an softly asked, "Not angry?"

Ning Yao countered, "What’s the use of being angry?"

Chen Ping'an thought for a moment and realized it seemed to be of no use.

He just didn’t dare to say that.

Ning Yao raised an eyebrow.

That was that.

She didn’t have to say it explicitly.

Chen Ping'an gently tapped his heels against the wall.

Being with Ning Yao, as well as everything that had happened before—from meeting her to liking her, then walking to her side, traversing mountains and rivers, and traveling far—could be tiring, but it would never be exhausting to his heart.

Ning Yao asked, "If you have such heavy matters in the future, just say it directly. Even if I get angry, I will let you know."

Chen Ping'an gently held her hand, and the two of them quietly gazed into the distance.

Chen Qingdu took a stroll, never going too far, walking slowly and then returning along the same path.

He glanced at the silhouettes of the young couple in the distance.

Chen Qingdu smiled, recalling a very interesting little incident.

The reason he had a good impression of Chen Ping'an when they first met years ago had nothing to do with anything.

It had nothing to do with Chen Ping'an daring to ask Cao Ci three rounds of punches—he could throw punches and could admit defeat; it didn't matter. 

It had nothing to do with the young man traveling alone to the Sword Qi Great Wall to deliver a sword to the girl he loved, either.

Even the connection between Chen Ping'an and that senior had nothing to do with it.

Chen Qingdu had seen that originally gifted young man, whose potential had been broken at the Bridge of Eternal Life, particularly when he looked into the boy’s eyes, full of vitality, which made Chen Qingdu feel... both amused and exasperated.

Unlike many old martial artists and senior figures who viewed Chen Ping'an with disappointment, Chen Qingdu might be the only one who saw Chen Ping'an as lively and full of vigor.

Years ago, when he was still a teenager, Chen Ping'an seemed to be silently asking the universe with an exuberant spirit.

Am I truly capable of becoming a great sword immortal? Can I make the girl I like love me and continue to love me? Can I protect the girl I like? Will I definitely not disappoint certain people? I can surely achieve all this, right?!

Chen Qingdu thought that was quite wonderful.

No wonder that old scholar had relentlessly pursued him before leaving, asking again and again, "Is my closed-door disciple good? Are you envious? I’m genuinely envious, aren’t I? Alas, it’s a pity I can’t be envious! If I were your brother Chen, I’d have given you a punch right away, otherwise, how could I quell my resentment?!"

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 766: Unknowingly Fifteen Years

At the Bull Horn Mountain Ferry, it was no longer just the military ferries of the Great Li transporting troops back and forth; more and more merchant vessels were coming and going. 

Pei Qian’s eyes sparkled, imagining all the heavenly coins rolling into Master’s pocket. 

On this trip "far from home," since they were on familiar territory, the girl in black beside Pei Qian, shouldering a small burden and holding a hiking staff, felt she couldn't possibly look more impressive. 

Zhou Mili felt a twinge of regret that she couldn’t stick two pieces of paper to her forehead—one labeled "Right Guardian of the Fallen Mountain" and the other "Mysterious Lake Monster." 

Not far away, Chen Nuanshu was chatting about trivial matters with Chen Lingjun, who was about to set off for North Julu Continent, and she noticed that Chen Lingjun kept yawning. 

Pei Qian crossed her arms, glancing around at her master's beautiful landscape, nodding in satisfaction. 

Zhou Mili quietly asked, “Chen Lingjun is leaving soon, shouldn’t we say a few words? Maybe shed a few tears to show our sincerity?” 

Pei Qian rolled her eyes. “Did you eat the Fallen Mountain’s rules for breakfast or something?” 

Pei Qian freed a hand to pat the little winter melon’s head and said earnestly, “My master once said, ‘Reason is like a big white bowl; everything else is just food to fill it. As long as the bowl doesn’t get lost, we can always find something to eat.’ But what exactly is ‘reason’? I can’t figure it out, and you, with your muddled brain, definitely can’t either. So we just need to remember the rules of Fallen Mountain, and we won’t go wrong.” 

Zhou Mili furrowed her brow but soon relaxed, understanding. She whispered, “Once we talk to Chen Lingjun, we’ll need to give him a parting gift, right? But we’re already so close, so let’s skip the pretentious stuff!” 

Pei Qian playfully tugged Zhou Mili’s cheek and laughed heartily, “What are you talking about?” 

Zhou Mili giggled along with her. 

Pei Qian stood still, taking a deep breath, then began to throw punches slowly, muttering to herself, “A single finger pokes a needle, a punch sweeps a wide area; throwing punches is like shooting arrows, retracting punches is like flying swords…” 

Zhou Mili asked, “What are you doing?” 

Pei Qian continued her slow punches, solemnly declaring, “After the Mad Sword Technique, I’ve created my own exceptional boxing style, and the mantra is all of my own making. It’s incredibly powerful.” 

Then Pei Qian started rambling, “In the world of boxing, aside from my master’s techniques being the strongest, there are two others that are quite formidable: one is the self-taught ‘Turtle Boxing,’ and the other is learned from the Bridge Sect.” 

Zhou Mili felt she wasn’t foolish; she just had her doubts, “So what makes your boxing so special? If you practice it, can you fly?” 

Pei Qian replied irritably, “That’s something only a martial artist at the Realm of Wandering can achieve. I’m still far from that; it’ll take years of hard work.” 

Zhou Mili stomped her foot, frustrated. “So long! How many sunflower seeds will I have to eat to get there?” 

Pei Qian sighed helplessly, “You think becoming an Eighth Realm martial artist is easy?” 

Zhou Mili looked momentarily stunned, holding her hiking staff and scratching her cheek, “But you’re Pei Qian!” 

Pei Qian beamed, withdrawing her fists and ruffling little Mili’s hair, “You little airhead, you may look small, but you’re quite sharp!” 

Zhou Mili swayed her head back and forth for a while before suddenly sighing, “Why hasn’t the Mountain Lord returned home yet?” 

Pei Qian smiled, “Didn’t I tell you? Over at the Sword Qi Great Wall, thanks to Master promoting you, there are now countless stories about the Mysterious Lake Monster circulating. That’s a whole other world! You should just enjoy it.” 

Zhou Mili began scratching her cheek again, “But I’d rather he not tell stories and come back sooner.” 

Pei Qian made a face, “When Master comes home, will you treat him to some pickled fish?” 

Zhou Mili frowned, timidly saying, “Just a small bowl, not a big one?” 

Pei Qian laughed but felt a tinge of melancholy. 

As they grew up, it became increasingly difficult to experience life as they once did. All the little worries felt like guests knocking on the door to one’s heart—they came quickly, but left just as fast. 

Pei Qian used to struggle to understand why Master didn’t want her and Sister Baoping to grow up too fast. 

Now, watching little Mili, Pei Qian finally understood. 

As Chen Lingjun prepared to board the intercontinental ferry, Pei Qian patted Zhou Mili’s head, “Come on, let’s say goodbye. Remember, Master said that if a friend is taking the fairy ferry on a long journey, we can’t wish them a smooth sailing.” 

Zhou Mili nodded vigorously, “Got it, got it!” 

A silly Chen Nuanshu, along with Pei Qian and little Mili, bid him farewell. 

Chen Lingjun felt a bit awkward but was also somewhat pleased, though he didn’t want to show it on his face. 

After Chen Lingjun left, the three of them waited until the ferry disappeared into the sea of clouds before returning to Fallen Mountain. 

Chen Nuanshu turned back to take a glance at the sea of clouds. 

Pei Qian softly said, “Don’t worry, everything will be fine. Chen Lingjun may seem careless, but he’s actually quite clever.” 

Chen Nuanshu smiled. Pei Qian took one girl by each hand. 

Now Pei Qian had outgrown both of them significantly. 

Finally, she was starting to look like a young woman. 

Inside the ferry, Chen Lingjun had nothing to do and was simply resting his head on the table in a daze. 

In fact, the moment Chen Lingjun stepped onto the intercontinental ferry bound for the Bridge Sect, he regretted it. He wanted nothing more than to jump off the ferry and sneak back. After all, with Fallen Mountain's vast territory, he could easily find a place to hide. It was likely that Wei Ban would find him annoying and wouldn’t want to bother with the old cook or Pei Qian. After a few days, he could just show up at Fallen Mountain with some excuse, casually pick a lucky day on the calendar, and forget about the Mysterious Lake, not even saying goodbye to his friends in Jianghu. Staying home and diligently practicing his cultivation didn’t seem so bad… 

On the table rested a large bamboo box, which was a rare display of generosity from Wei Daxian, who had even lent him a small item. 

Inside the box were many maps of North Julu Continent, some drawn by celestial beings on the mountain and some secret documents from various government offices, alongside a jumble of local records, as well as a few booklets personally penned by Chen Ping’an containing numerous important notes. As the old cook would say, it was as if he had written down every little detail, even where to relieve oneself. If he couldn’t successfully traverse Jianghu with all this, he might as well drown. 

Chen Lingjun was actually still scared. 

Previously, when he was at the Yujiang area of Huangting Kingdom, he didn’t like moving around. He had recognized the Yujiang Water God as a brother and enjoyed his share of power alongside him. Upon arriving at Fallen Mountain, he didn’t move either. Pei Qian and Zhou Mili would occasionally visit Hongzhu Town, but Chen Lingjun stuck around the surrounding hills of Fallen Mountain, wandering about, chatting aimlessly with the old celestial neighbors, and patrolling with that black snake, living a carefree life. 

Ever since that blind old man named Jia Cheng moved from Qilong Alley to Huang Lake Mountain to cultivate, Chen Lingjun often visited him. They got along well, and if bragging really had an effect, the entire Haoran world would be their private garden. 

However, Chen Lingjun was now clear that the other party treated him well primarily because of Chen Ping’an’s influence. 

Chen Lingjun didn’t dislike this arrangement; in fact, he enjoyed it. 

Even with the good atmosphere at Fallen Mountain, there were still distinctions between those who were close and those who were distant. 

He and Nuanshu, that little silly girl, were among the earliest “elders” of Fallen Mountain. 

Later came the old cook, Pei Qian, Shi Rou, and others, including that silly Ceng Yuanji, the naive girl Yuanbao, and the dimwit Yuanlai. Afterward, Chen Ping’an even brought back little Mili from North Julu Continent. 

Sometimes Chen Lingjun felt that these guys, like Wei Ban, looked down on him. It was no wonder they had such lofty aspirations; he could only blame himself for being complacent, enjoying a life of leisure, and boasting. 

There were many people and the atmosphere was lively—what a good thing. 

Being all alone and running all the way to North Julu Continent to cultivate? 

What a waste of time—Pale Bone Marsh, the Bridge Sect, the Mural City, Master Zhu Quan, and those two named offerings from Fallen Mountain—what a mess! The Mysterious Lake, Liu Zhiqing, Spring Dew Garden, Cloud City, the river spirit, Central Dragon Palace, and the farthest mountain… not to mention Lion Peak, the couple Li Er, Li Huai’s sister Li Liu, little Baoping’s brother Li Xisheng, and the Fire God Temple where his friend Liu Jinglong from Taihui Sword Sect was… 

Was he really heading towards a bright future by cultivating? Or was he going door to door, making visits and delivering gifts? 

He had to jump on a ferry! 

Chen Lingjun gathered his belongings and slipped down to the ferry's lower deck. Just then, Wei Ban appeared out of thin air near the ferry’s railing. 

Chen Lingjun laughed heartily, “Wei Daxian, why so polite? No need to send me off!” 

Wei Ban smiled, “The entire North Yue territory is under my jurisdiction; have you forgotten?” 

Chen Lingjun scampered over to rub Wei Ban’s arm eagerly, “How could I forget? Even if I had to pee, I’d hold it in, afraid of sullying the beauty of North Yue!” 

Wei Ban said, “The Mountain of the Crown Prince of North Yue is located at the northernmost tip of Baoping Continent. I’ll have a word with that mountain god and see you off as the ferry sets sail. After that, you’re free to jump whenever you like. You can take your time returning, and whether you land on Eastern Yue’s territory or Gan Prefecture Mountain depends on your mood.” 

Chen Lingjun was dumbfounded. 

In the bustling Qinfeng City, year after year, the celebrations continued unabated. Dynasties rose and fell, landscapes changed, but this city built at the foot of the mountain remained steadfast. One emperor after another showed great respect towards the Xu family. 

The Xu family had established a grand connection through their ancestor, allowing them to possess a fox kingdom worth half a blessed land. 

It was said that the fox fairy encountered by the Xu family’s ancestor back then already had seven tails—whether that number had increased since was unknown. 

The beautiful fox-fur beauties produced by the Xu family in Qinfeng City were priced exorbitantly, prized for their rarity and in high demand. 

They were a unique treasure of Baoping Continent, and as the intercontinental ferries between North Julu and Qinfeng City became more frequent, the Xu family’s wealth grew immensely. Especially in recent years, the head of the Xu family changed ancestral practices, allowing the fox kingdom to open the Mirror Flower Water Moon. One fox-fur talisman now commanded a price double that of before. 

The Xu family invited renowned artists to create the Four Beauties and Eighteen Maidens series, either through meticulous engravings or careful copies, along with a smattering of scholarly items like folding fans, which once released, sold out immediately. 

Some celestial beings on the mountain who weren’t fond of Qinfeng City expressed envy, claiming that Xu Hun was on the verge of selling spring palace paintings. If Xu Hun dared to sell those, then he would truly be a hero. 

They deliberately belittled Xu Hun, calling him a man who rolls in the realm of cosmetics. 

However, this man was, in reality, a formidable Yuanying realm warrior, and after acquiring that peculiar pockmarked armor, he became even more powerful, uniquely capable of outstanding feats among those below the Fifth Realm on Baoping Continent. 

In a private room of a tavern in the bustling city center, a young man continued to dine while a scholarly figure in a blue gown had already put down his chopsticks, standing by the window and watching the bustling street outside, filled with beautiful women. 

Liu Chicheng waved a folding fan, smiling, “This couple from Qinfeng City, one focuses on cultivation while the other manages finances, truly a perfect match.” 

The young man simply buried his head in his food. Liu Chicheng rarely touched his own chopsticks but ordered an entire table of dishes, leaving plenty left over. 

Liu Chicheng turned to the young man and asked with a smile, “Gu Can, you’ve never said why you wanted to come here and deliberately avoid Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi. Can you tell me now?” 

Gu Can paused his eating, swallowed, and looked up to say, “I have a friend who was almost killed by a man named Lu Zhengchun. That Lu Zhengchun is from the Lu family on Fortune Street, and it seems he’s been doing well in Qinfeng City with the Xu family.” 

In Li Zhu Cave, the major clans among the top ten surnames—Song, Li, Zhao, and Lu—were all great families. 

However, the small-town Lu family had too many ties to the fallen dynasty, suffering the most severe consequences. After Li Zhu Cave fell to the earth, the little town Lu family was left with nothing to show for it. 

Only Lu Zhengchun had followed a woman from the Xu family in Qinfeng City when he left the town in his youth. The Xu family treated him well, providing ample cultivation resources and even granting him a direct lineage identity as a protective talisman; they gave him face. 

Liu Chicheng had no interest in Lu Zhengchun, but he curiously asked, “Someone like you actually has friends?” 

Gu Can nodded, “I do have one.” 

Liu Chicheng chuckled, “It’s only Chen Ping’an, isn’t it?” 

Gu Can shook his head, “He has never regarded me as a friend; the age difference is too great. To me, he feels more like a half-relative. As for Liu Xianyang, he only became closer to me because of Chen Ping’an. Otherwise, we’ve never been on the same path, not in the past, and won’t be in the future. So he’s barely a friend.” 

When Liu Xianyang returns from Nanshuo Continent, he should become the direct disciple of the Dragon Spring Sword Sect’s Ruan Qiong. Liu Xianyang was brought away from home because his ancestors were the Chen family’s tomb keepers. 

What Gu Can admired most about Liu Xianyang was his innate ability to adapt to his surroundings, never suffering from any discomfort. 

As for himself, once he arrived at the Book and Letter Lake, he had lost his greatest asset—patience—completely. 

Looking back at that seemingly glorious time on Qingxia Island, Gu Can realized he had been walking step by step towards a dead end. 

Being young was no excuse. 

Gu Can looked at the dishes on the table and resumed eating. 

Suddenly, Liu Chicheng said, “Once you reach Baidi City, it’s best to sever these ties.” 

Gu Can remained calm, eating without saying a word. 

Liu Chicheng didn’t believe he could change Gu Can’s character; it would probably depend on his older brother’s teaching methods. He changed the subject, “Earlier, when you said ‘doing well,’ how well is that? Since he’s around your age, is he a Jindan Sword Cultivator? Or a Yuanying Qi Practitioner?” 

Gu Can replied, “Currently, he’s a Fourth Realm Qi Practitioner. Within ten years, he hopes to reach the Cave Dwelling realm. He helps the Xu family manage a small part of the trade from the fox kingdom. His cultivation isn’t fast, but he can pile it up with heavenly coins.” 

Liu Chicheng closed his folding fan and tapped his own head, laughing, “Future little brother, are you kidding me or telling a joke?” 

Gu Can’s expression was calm; he didn’t drink, ate slowly, and savored each bite. “If killing someone means I have to run away, will I ever have a stable place to settle down in this life?” 

Liu Chicheng was dumbfounded, laughing and shaking his head. “A waste of space like you, and you think you’re worth killing? I’m easy to talk to; just nod, and I’ll deal with it for you. It’s just one Xu Hun; not even at Fifth Realm, it’s a trivial matter.” 

Gu Can retorted, “What if? Why take the risk?” 

Liu Chicheng fell silent. 

Gu Can put down his chopsticks and smiled, “But if I really have to deal with an enemy, I’ll make sure there’s no one left to collect the body.” 

Furthermore, he had to ensure that no one could find fault. 

As for others, there were only two types—Chen Ping’an and everyone else. If he had to choose, he wouldn’t care about the latter. 

In any case, Chen Ping’an would never be able to completely sever ties with him in this lifetime. 

Liu Chicheng grinned brightly. 

This kid was growing more and more likable. 

Being a protector was just like a maiden stepping into the bridal sedan for the first time; it was only a matter of willingness, and he found it quite comfortable. 

This made Liu Chicheng ponder about taking a disciple. 

Gu Can asked, “If I really become your little brother, can I learn the most outstanding techniques and divine abilities?” 

Liu Chicheng chuckled, “Baidi City has a rich collection, so if you become my little brother, you can certainly learn; you can pick whatever you want. Whether you can master it is another matter.” 

Gu Can said, “I want to learn it all.” 

Liu Chicheng pointed his folding fan at Gu Can and laughed, “You’re young and ignorant, dreaming foolish dreams.” 

It wasn’t that he didn’t know Gu Can had excellent cultivation aptitude; otherwise, he wouldn’t have thought of taking him to Central Divine Continent as a stepping stone for reentering Baidi City. However, his older brother’s Baidi City was no ordinary dojo. 

Liu Chicheng had deep grievances against his older brother, but he didn’t bring up those old grudges. His brother was indeed the person Liu Chicheng most respected in his life. 

After that came Grand Master of Longhu Mountain, and then there was Cui Chen, with whom he had played the game of colorful clouds. 

Just these three. 

Liu Chicheng couldn’t help but remind him, “My older brother is unpredictable; you might just reach the pinnacle of success or fall into the mundane world, or worse, lose several lifetimes. Don’t think it will come easy. My older brother once spent six hundred years polishing a potential closed-door disciple. For that poor soul, it was eight lifetimes spent making garments for the last lifetime’s Baidi City disciple. In the end, when that person reached their ninth lifetime, for some reason, they were still abandoned by my older brother. He is best at multitasking—cultivating, playing chess, managing Baidi City, refining tools, and taking on disciples... He excels at everything and remains composed in every aspect.” 

Gu Can nodded, “Then I’ve found a good master.” 

Liu Chicheng laughed heartily. 

Gu Can stood up to settle the bill. 

Suddenly, Liu Chicheng exclaimed, “What a stunning girl!” 

Gu Can didn’t pay attention. 

Liu Chicheng exclaimed in surprise, “Not often seen, not often seen. That silver-white gourd, if I’m not mistaken, is one of the highest-ranked seven sword-nurturing gourds.” 

Gu Can frowned, quickly walking to the window to look at the young woman leisurely walking by with a red dress, hanging a wine gourd at her waist and wielding a narrow blade. 

It was Li Baoping. 

Why was she in Qinfeng City? 

Gu Can said, “We’re in no rush to leave; let’s wait until she leaves Qinfeng City before we go. Regardless of any disturbances during this time, I owe you a favor.” 

Liu Chicheng asked in confusion, “Do you know this girl?” 

Gu Can remained silent. 

Liu Chicheng calculated and suddenly cursed, quickly covering his nose, which was still bleeding. 

His expression turned serious, and he rarely showed such seriousness, “Don’t get involved! Consider this a suggestion from your future little brother!” 

Gu Can gazed at the red-dressed woman’s retreating figure, replying, “I must get involved. If something happens, you save her, and I’ll take care of myself.” 

Liu Chicheng glared, “What are you thinking?!” 

Gu Can closed his eyes, beginning to calculate everything about the intelligence in Qinfeng City. 

Liu Chicheng sighed, leaning against the window, self-deprecating, “This busy life of mine…” 

Before Zheng Dafu went to the Yang family shop, he visited a tavern, where the liquor vendor was an old friend. They were still a bit short of being lovers. 

The woman was bold, and the townsfolk called her Huang Erniang; her real name had long been forgotten. 

Years ago, when a drunken man knocked on the widow’s door at night, she opened the door and swung a kitchen knife, nearly chopping him to death. Afterward, she paid a hefty sum, but after that incident, men who used to hang around her, even daring to peek over the wall, all disappeared. For the sake of the second son, risking the life of the eldest didn’t seem worth it. 

Moreover, in the tavern, Huang Erniang didn’t mind any crude banter; it was all back and forth, mostly men begging for mercy. When serving food and drink, she would let drunkards touch her hand, but they’d only receive a kick in return and a few playful curses. This business was profitable; if a handsome young man came in to drink, the treatment would be different. The bolder ones wouldn’t even receive a glance. Ultimately, who was taking advantage of whom was open to interpretation. 

The tavern thrived, bustling with patrons. Years ago, Master Ruan, who had transformed from a blacksmith to a celestial being, often came here to buy liquor. Over time, Huang Erniang’s drinks became a golden signboard for the little town, drawing many outsiders hoping to bask in the divine aura of the Great Li’s foremost offering, Ruan Shengren. The business was flourishing, much like the cakes from the auspicious shop in Qilong Alley, which were also thriving. 

Zheng Dafu stood outside the shop, feeling a bit troubled. With so many scruffy men staring, he guessed Huang Erniang would definitely feel too embarrassed to tease him. Moreover, now that the shop had expanded, hiring two workers, Zheng Dafu felt that drinking wasn’t as enjoyable as before. 

It was not like when the shop was quiet, and he was its biggest patron. When Huang Erniang saw him, it was as if she had seen her own man return home. She would always sway her hips, round the counter, and greet him with “Dafu Brother.” Sometimes she’d pinch his arm and whisper a few words of playful scolding, making him feel like a piece of peach blossom cake. 

She insisted on wrapping her arm around his as they entered the shop. How could such a heavy weapon exist in the world? It was quite painful; Zheng Dafu was afraid he’d hurt his arm. Every time he sat down, he had to rub it for a long time before he could lift the wine bowl. 

With seven or eight tables filled with people, Zheng Dafu planned to return when it was less crowded. Unexpectedly, at one table, all local men were present, and one of them waved, “Yo yo yo, isn’t this Dafu Brother? Come sit with us, but let’s be clear, you’re treating today. How many drinks have you mooched from us at every wedding? Now that you’re helping the celestial beings on the mountain, what a big shot! Truly, when a man has money, he stands tall.” 

Zheng Dafu, whose stature was hunched, hurried over to sit on the long bench next to them, laughing, “What do I treat? I’m saving up for a wife, not like you, Liu Dazhong, who sold two ancestral houses and bought two big houses and several shops in the state capital all at once!” 

“Dazhong” was a local term meaning someone who is clueless. 

The Liu man wasn’t angry; he was used to bantering with Zheng Dafu, and their back-and-forth was just a lighthearted exchange—whoever got angry lost the match. 

The man hadn’t visited the town in years; he had sold both large ancestral houses long ago and didn’t dwell on the past. When visiting the graves, he used to pass by but later became too lazy to even visit the grave mound. The road was too far; during the Qingming Festival, he just burned more yellow paper outside the big house in the state capital, thinking he had fulfilled his filial duty. 

The man lowered his voice, “Did you know that widow in Mud Bottle Alley is doing quite well now? She’s genuinely rich and noble.” 

He raised his thumb, “In terms of family background, that charming widow can be compared to none.” 

He immediately regretted it, “If I had known back then, I would have tried harder. Now, in the state capital, I could have had not just a few houses and shops but entire streets under my name!” 

Zheng Dafu poured himself a bowl of wine, which wasn’t as good as the liquor personally served by Huang Erniang. The taste was lacking. Zheng Dafu raised his wine bowl, toasting the whole table, downing it in one gulp. The few present were about the same age as Liu Dazhong, former neighbors who had all built their own businesses in the state capital and were enjoying lives they hadn’t even dared to dream about before. The old-faced women who entered first and the younger, alluring concubines made for a lively household, with the occasional witty maid adding to the noise—every day was busier than the previous New Year’s celebration. 

Zheng Dafu raised his wine glass, and aside from one relatively honest acquaintance who returned the toast, the others ignored him, pretending not to see. 

Zheng Dafu didn’t care; he was just there to drink for free—what did he have to lose? 

He quickly poured another bowl of wine, wiping his mouth and smiling, “Not too clear. I wasn’t very familiar with the Gu family’s lady back then, as you know.” 

Liu Dazhong teased, “I find it strange. They’re both charming widows, but the Gu lady in Mud Bottle Alley is soft-natured. Why didn’t you try to court her? Why only Huang Erniang?” 

Zheng Dafu chuckled. 

Another man on the long bench, known for being shrewd and miserly, casually asked, “Dafu, I heard you’ve been hanging around with that kid from Mud Bottle Alley? Your prospects look dimmer now, huh? Once a door guard, you’re now just helping a younger generation. Aren’t you ashamed? Besides, with your current situation, it doesn’t look like you’re doing well. Why don’t I lend you a hand? We’ve been good brothers for years, and you still have that little shack on the east side of town, right? I can help you find a wealthy buyer in the state capital.” 

Zheng Dafu just started to mix the ingredients and didn’t refuse; he dragged it along, knowing he could still drink for free next time they met. 

In the end, the entire table lost patience with Zheng Dafu, and when they left, they didn’t settle the bill. 

Zheng Dafu called over a familiar face, who then called over his own acquaintances to drink, and Zheng Dafu thought it was time to slip away. 

He didn’t expect the woman to be sharp-eyed, smiling, “Dafu Brother, are you short on cash or just lacking something else? If it’s cash and you can’t pay the bill, we’re good friends, so just forget about it. But if you’re lacking something else, I can’t help you.” 

Zheng Dafu kept walking, pretending not to hear. 

Huang Erniang slammed her hand on the table, “Zheng Dafu! Get back here! You think you can eat my tofu and not pay? You think the King of Heaven lent you the guts to do that?” 

Zheng Dafu turned around, sauntering over to the counter, and said softly, “Short on cash, short on cash. When am I not short on cash? As for the other stuff, Huang Erniang, you should know me well enough. I’m the courageous and robust Zheng Dafu, not just a name.” 

Huang Erniang leaned against the counter, munching on melon seeds, “Why aren’t you gambling anymore? Did you fall into the pigsty?” 

Zheng Dafu laughed, “I gamble just for fun, never to make money. Have you ever seen me win at gambling?” 

Then Zheng Dafu added earnestly, “Money earned at the gambling table is just a piece of farmland by the river. Life and death money, after turning for sixty years. A skillful trade, money from craftsmanship, three generations of inheritance. A small piece of land, farming money, lasting for thousands of years.” 

Huang Erniang rolled her eyes, “You just love pretending to be a scholar.” 

Zheng Dafu glanced at the woman’s attire and reached out, “Miss, what fabric is this? So sturdy, let me have a look.” 

The woman just continued eating her melon seeds, not dodging or avoiding him. She truly didn’t believe this guy would dare to touch the fabric on her chest. 

As expected, Zheng Dafu withdrew his hand, feigning innocence. He wiped the table and complained, “Miss, it’s not that I’m scolding you, but you really should find someone more diligent to help out. Look at this table, it’s greasy; even a fly would struggle to take off. If you’re not careful, you could end up crushed by two mountains.” 

The woman merely scoffed, “You have the nerve to call me ‘Miss’? Count how long it’s been since you took care of this shop!” 

Zheng Dafu leaned on the counter, turning to look at the noisy tables, laughing, “What’s the point of taking care of it now? It’s not like I need those few bowls of wine.” 

As he spoke, the woman, seizing the opportunity while the hunched man was looking elsewhere, had her eyes turn red for a moment, but she quickly concealed it. 

In the blink of an eye, many years had passed. 

When she first opened this shop, she was still a young girl, even prettier than she was now, without those crow's feet at the corners of her eyes, and her hands were still tender. She recalled the days she bravely served drinks to guests, with nearly all the drunkards’ eyes fixed on her chest, except for one young man, who not only looked at her chest but also admired her delicate hands, saying many charming words that sounded like they came from a book—words she couldn’t quite comprehend, but they brought joy to her heart. 

The shop managed to survive the early years of hardship, and that young man helped a lot, not just by drinking. 

However, when she was at her most beautiful, she was too busy being flattered by those words. Now, as she aged, she understood more about human affairs, and she wasn’t as beautiful anymore. 

She only felt that Zheng Dafu was different from other men. 

Both his eyes and mouth were indeed not honest, but his hands were honest. 

The woman only learned much later that he was the true honest man. 

Zheng Dafu turned around, “Old habit, put it on the tab, and by the way, give me another bowl.” 

The woman slammed the bowl on the table, personally scooping wine into it. Facing the wine jar, as she turned and bent over, she knew that man was definitely watching her. 

Huang Erniang poured the wine and leaned back against the counter, looking at the man taking small sips, softly saying, “That Liu Dazhong and his group are eyeing your house; be careful. It might be that they came back to the town specifically for you this time.” 

Zheng Dafu nodded, “You’re still caring.” 

“Don’t take it lightly,” she urged, her tone slightly more serious as she frowned, “I’ve heard that these people have money now, and they’re not so respectable in the state capital. Money in good people’s hands is heroic, but in the hands of these scoundrels, it becomes a tool for harm. Your little house may be small, but the location is good. Just east of the town is the Immortal Tomb, which has now turned into a Martial Temple. Over the years, how many high-ranking officials have gone to burn incense and worship? How impressive? Don’t you know? But I also want to advise you, if you find a suitable buyer, just sell it; don’t hold on too tightly. Be careful if the authorities come to buy; when that happens, the price will drop. If it falls too low, will you sell or not? If you don’t sell, will your life be peaceful?” 

Zheng Dafu grunted in acknowledgment. 

If we’re talking about dirty secrets and annoying matters, there are plenty in the marketplace, and every household has its share of filth. But if we talk about those who are clever and kind-hearted, there’s a whole lot of them. Every household has a few bowls of clean rice, right? 

Suddenly, the woman felt a wave of sadness. “We’re getting old.” 

Zheng Dafu laughed, “That’s true; your son is now a scholar, right? I heard he’s even earned the nickname ‘Little Scholar’? How about it, Dafu Brother never lies; that kid looks like a good material, a proper seed of knowledge. The Spring Festival couplets at the tavern were written by him, right? Quite impressive; you should just look forward to enjoying the blessings. The family treasure lies not in wealth but in the good deeds one accumulates.” 

Huang Erniang glanced at him. 

Zheng Dafu pretended to be shy, blocking his face with the wine bowl, “Miss, your gaze isn’t very proper; Dafu Brother feels like he’s walking out without clothes on.” 

Huang Erniang had no choice but to roll her eyes. 

She truly had to thank him for teaching her about raising children. In those early days when the young widow was carrying a little burden, she truly felt like she would rather cut off her flesh than let the child eat well and dress warmly. As the child grew older, she couldn’t bear to scold him at all, and he became wild, daring to skip school. She felt it wasn’t right but didn’t know how to teach him; she urged him, but he didn’t listen. Every time he promised to do better, he still often went to the river to catch fish or climbed mountains to catch snakes. 

Then one time Zheng Dafu was drinking and joking around, he concealed a saying: “To earn money, one must be precise; be generous to others, but be strict with one’s descendants.” 

Huang Erniang took that to heart. After a thorough beating, the child became obedient. 

Suddenly, Huang Erniang said, “Half-heartedness leads to indecisiveness; there are all sorts of chaos. What a coward.” 

This had once been Zheng Dafu’s way of cursing at the tavern. 

In reality, it didn’t have much force; it was overly sour and didn’t hurt or itch. 

However, Huang Erniang found it amusing and remembered it. Unlike the women who would scold first and scratch later, and those rural men, their insults seemed to come from a different place. 

Zheng Dafu pretended he didn’t understand and began to lament, “A single man’s woes, cold and lonely. How poor am I? Even a starving mouse has to move away. Mosquitoes and lice can barely sip on a little wine. After saving enough for a wife, which girl would be willing to come knocking?” 

Huang Erniang laughed, asking, “What age girl are you looking for?” 

Zheng Dafu glanced at the woman, grinning, “Age doesn’t matter; as long as they’re old enough, it’s fine.” 

Huang Erniang threw a handful of melon seeds at him. 

Zheng Dafu dodged, and there was a time to finish the wine bowl. Putting it down, he patted his face, “What a saying: ‘Drinking like a long whale sucking streams; drunkenness like a jade mountain about to collapse.’ Miss, you’re fortunate.” 

Huang Erniang scoffed, “You’re just a simpleton. If you get drunk and fall into a latrine, drown, or eat to the point of bursting, it’s all on you.” 

Zheng Dafu replied, “I’m leaving now; I’ll definitely settle the debt later.” 

Huang Erniang suddenly asked, “Are you going far?” 

Zheng Dafu replied, “Not too far.” 

That lotus root blessed land wasn’t far, just near Fallen Mountain. 

Huang Erniang lowered her voice, “Haven’t you suffered enough? What’s so good out there?” 

Zheng Dafu turned his head and smiled, “I once saw a saying in a book: ‘Huang Si Niang’s flowers bloom along the path; they can’t compare to Huang Erniang.’” 

Huang Erniang asked, “Can’t you just stay? The wine bill is still outstanding.” 

Zheng Dafu shook his head and left. 

The woman watched as the man, who had his arm around another, gradually walked away, until he became increasingly indistinct. 

Zheng Dafu arrived at the Yang family shop to lend a hand. His sharp-witted junior sister Su Dian and the clueless junior brother Shi Ling Shan had both gone out to gain experience. 

Currently, only a Yang family descendant was watching over the shop. Zheng Dafu had thickened his skin over the years; although he still received no warm treatment from his master, it was fine as long as he stayed in the front shop, avoiding the back courtyard where the old man was. 

Approaching the shop, Zheng Dafu discreetly dispersed the smell of alcohol from his body. As he entered, the young assistant was dozing off. Hearing Zheng Dafu move a small stool, he woke up only to fall back asleep. The Yang family had been annoyed with Zheng Dafu for years, not wanting to get involved with him, a door guard who returned after nearly losing half his life on a distant trip, only to continue guarding the door. How much potential could he have? If not for the old Yang family’s few words, even a slovenly man like Zheng Dafu wouldn’t have been allowed to help at the shop. 

The Yang family hadn’t been doing well these years, and even the Yang family’s several branches were struggling. Among the four surnames and ten clans, aside from a few that moved to the Great Li capital, those remaining behind were all thriving in the state capital, leading to jealousy and ambition among the younger generations. The old Yang family’s grandfather was growing cold-hearted, unwilling to intervene, letting these unworthy descendants fend for themselves. 

The only thing the old man relied on was that medicinal recipe in the back courtyard. 

However, only three people in the family could handle this business, three generations just right, and there were no worries about a lack of successors. 

The more descendants there were, the more the head of the family would favor those who truly had potential, while the less fortunate would be supported but not overly so. Those who could make money would only grow wealthier. 

Zheng Dafu dragged a stool to sit at the shop’s entrance, enjoying the sun without cost. Whether basking in the sun or mingling below the mountain, both were good. 

Zheng Dafu looked up at the sun, wondering if all matters could be seen clearly? 

He gazed for a long time; it had been like this since childhood. After looking long enough, it didn’t hurt the eyes anymore; it felt nothing. Later, when Zheng Dafu practiced boxing and martial arts, he stopped giving it much thought. 

Zheng Dafu withdrew his gaze, patting his knees, “Last year I hoped this year would be good; this year is still a torn cotton jacket. This year I wish for next year to be good, and next year…” 

The young man behind the counter grumbled, “You’re so annoying.” 

Zheng Dafu turned his head, laughing, “Am I dead?” 

The young man glared, “How can you talk like that?!” 

Zheng Dafu looked confused, “Do I not use my mouth? Am I supposed to use my butt?” 

The young man slammed the table, “Zheng Dafu, keep your mouth clean!” 

Zheng Dafu chuckled, raising a hand and lightly patting the table a few times, patiently saying, “Keep it down; our common folks’ tables are either for placing rice bowls or incense burners. Nothing else matters. For example, that abacus, it’s nothing serious. So don’t slam the table; it’s disrespectful to the heavens and spirits; that’s unacceptable.” 

The young man mocked, “Don’t talk nonsense here; you’re a good-for-nothing who’s spent his life guarding doors.” 

The sharpness of words could hurt more than knives. 

However, Zheng Dafu’s most frequent sparring partner was not with his master Li Er’s martial arts but rather this verbal sparring. 

There weren’t many townsfolk, but the best tongue-fighters were plentiful. 

Mud Bottle Alley, Apricot Blossom Alley, these places were rich in talent, with many outstanding figures. 

Just like that quiet Chen Ping’an during his youth, he never really made a move; in fact, this skill was being accumulated day by day. 

Zheng Dafu immediately became amused; Su Dian was too stubborn, Shi Ling Shan was too naive, but finally, a conversationalist had arrived. Feeling pleased, Zheng Dafu moved his stool closer to the threshold, smiling and saying, “Yang Shu, I heard you love going to the Iron Symbol River Water God Temple to burn incense? Do you know the real rules for burning incense? Speaking of which, this matter should be done according to the old traditions, right? Do you know why you should hold the incense in your left hand? And do you know that you’re left-handed? That’s not ideal.” 

The young man named Yang Shu felt a bit shaken, but his expression remained dismissive, too lazy to respond. 

Zheng Dafu cheerfully continued, “Fifteen loves the neighbor’s wife. At thirty, he favors someone else’s son. At fifty or sixty, he cherishes his daughter-in-law. The Yang family’s third branch has a great family tradition.” 

Yang Shu’s face flushed red, and he grabbed the abacus, smashing it towards that bastard. 

The Yang family’s third branch had indeed been poorly reputed in Fortune Street and Peach Leaf Alley; they were the type of wealthy people who “never tied their belt.” 

Zheng Dafu caught the abacus, “This is your Yang family’s money-making tool; don’t break it. If it’s damaged, who will pay for it? I’m a barefoot man; you have a little wealth. Even if you splash dirt on me, what use is that? Who do you think will end up paying? You’re about to wade into muddy waters in the state capital to earn some dirty money; I’d say it’s better not to go. The family’s prosperity relies on etiquette and righteousness, not on wealth or poverty. Study a bit, if you can’t, then have a few sons; at least there’s hope for your descendants to bring glory.” 

Yang Shu’s face turned pale with rage, trembling all over. 

Zheng Dafu shook his head, raising a hand, “Don’t get into a fight with me; I don’t hold back. One punch from me, and you’ll be practicing drunken boxing, self-taught.” 

Yang Shu turned to walk past the counter, not wanting to fight but to head home. 

Just then, the curtain lifted, and the old man said, “Yang Shu, are you really going to argue with a gatekeeper? You don’t mind losing your dignity?” 

Yang Shu snorted, but with that, he had a way out, still leaving the Yang family shop. However, he slowed his pace, walking more steadily. 

As Yang Shu brushed past the doorframe, finally walking away, the old Yang man emerged at the entrance, saying, “Is it fun to argue with a waste of space? Do you think he can understand human language?” 

Zheng Dafu had already stood up, trying to straighten his back as much as possible. 

The old man who took on disciples held respect for teachers and valued incense; this was paramount. 

Zheng Dafu followed the old man to the back courtyard. The old man lifted the curtain. Once past the threshold, he casually let it drop. Zheng Dafu gently supported him, and once he passed through, he continued to hold it, lowering it gently. 

The old Yang man sat on the steps in the main house, tapping his smoking pipe, reaching for his waist pouch. 

Soon, he began to exhale smoke. 

The fine bamboo pipe was a gift from someone, and the tobacco leaves were given by the little brat Li Huai. Over the years, the once vibrant green pipe had been rubbed and smoked into a light bamboo yellow. 

The old Yang man said, “What significance does a small lotus root blessed land hold?” 

Zheng Dafu replied, “At least it’s in the Haoran world.” 

The old Yang man glanced sideways at his disciple. 

Being too clever was never a good thing. 

Zheng Dafu helplessly said, “I’m listening to my master.” 

Well, it seemed he was truly going far now. 

The old Yang man said, “Once you get there, start anew. The road will be harder, but as long as the road isn’t difficult, there will be many people. The reason why Fan Junmao became the Lord of South Yue and not you is not without reason.” 

Zheng Dafu listened to the teachings. 

The old Yang man asked, “Why do you think it is that the Confucians opened a fifth realm at this very moment? That realm had been discovered long ago.” 

Zheng Dafu answered, “To prevent the impending war, all the schools of thought won’t help but instead pull each other down. Now that a new realm has appeared out of nowhere, those with the ability should compete for it.” 

The old Yang man further asked, “Do you know why only the Haoran world can accommodate both Daoism and Buddhism? Do you think the Qingming world and Confucian academies have a standing?” 

Zheng Dafu’s expression turned grave; he knew that this question couldn’t be answered solely through his own thoughts. 

The old man waved his hand, dispersing the smoke, asking, “Have I ever cursed the three sages as pixiu?” 

Zheng Dafu nodded. 

The old man laughed, “I just don’t know which one will slap me first.” 

Now, his master didn’t mind saying more to him. 

Yet, Zheng Dafu missed the early days when “the master spoke little, just ten characters” were such bleak times. 

Zheng Dafu suddenly froze. 

The old Yang man sneered, “Have you finally remembered? You think you’re not as smart as Li Er but still refuse to accept it.” 

Li Er had once reminded Zheng Dafu to think carefully about why his master always spoke less than ten words to him. 

Back then, Zheng Dafu could only guess that it was because his master found him bothersome and didn’t want to say more. 

Ten. 

The martial artist’s ten realms. 

Once, at the pinnacle of the Wandering Realm, he had traveled south to the old dragon city, guarding that dusty shop. Later, he met Chen Ping’an, then broke through, almost—just almost—breaking through two bottlenecks, directly reaching the Tenth Realm! 

The old Yang man coldly laughed, “If you had the ability to make me say one more word back then, you would have already reached the Tenth Realm. How could there be so many complications now? You wander east and west, asking Qi Jingchun and idly chatting with that old Yao, and what good does it do? Are you at the Tenth Realm now or still at the Eleventh Realm? Hmm, multiplied by two, and it’s almost enough.” 

Zheng Dafu was more accustomed to this kind of master. 

However, Zheng Dafu found it rare to retort, “Both Mr. Qi and Old Yao have great knowledge. My own understanding is lacking, and I can’t grasp the subtleties.” 

“Did I say you understood well?” 

The old Yang man pinched some tobacco leaves, his face full of disdain, “The most damaging thing to a house is what? Broken window paper? A rotten door? These are not big issues. Even the impoverished households of Mud Bottle Alley and Apricot Blossom Alley can afford to fix this. Just look at Chen Ping’an’s old home; the little brat can take a machete and go up and down the mountain, replacing the old with new in one trip. No matter how well you learn others’ principles, if you think you understand them thoroughly, it’s just a matter of sticking up door gods and hanging spring couplets, which will fade after a year of wind and rain.” 

Zheng Dafu said, “It’s about replacing beams and pillars, making major renovations.” 

The old Yang man nodded, “Do you think others' principles are that easy to learn? To replace the original beams and pillars means a complete renovation of the heart, which is the true meaning of self-cultivation, competing with oneself; that requires endurance.” 

The old Yang man sighed, “Let’s not even talk about the distant past. Take Qi Jingchun, who spent a century in Li Zhu Cave pondering his heart and never managed to think of a ‘reasonable’ path. Now look at Chen Ping’an; how many principles does he think he knows? Not many—just a few. How to be a person, how to understand this world through learning, how to cultivate and survive in this world, and how to get along with the world and live better. Just these three matters, just a few principles. Is it so difficult to be a good person? Simple as can be, but is it easy to put into practice? It’s hard.” 

The old Yang man could roughly guess the academic trajectory of Qi Jingchun back then. 

The Dao Ancestor once said, “Lose the Dao and then gain virtue; lose virtue and then gain benevolence; lose benevolence and then gain righteousness.” 

Qi Jingchun was probably contemplating how to solve this matter, possibly attempting to reverse it, not in order, but still in order. 

Even what Qi Jingchun was thinking could be much greater. 

Unfortunately, everything had become just a fleeting memory. 

Zheng Dafu asked, “What about the disciples?” 

The old Yang man retorted, “The master leads the disciple in, but cultivation relies on the individual. Do I need to teach disciples how to eat and relieve themselves?” 

Zheng Dafu said, “Once I reach that world, I’ll think it through properly.” 

The old Yang man raised his hand, shaking his sleeve, and a pocket-sized temple that had been refined and hidden was tossed out. The old man waved his hand, and the golden light sparkled, vanishing into Zheng Dafu’s brow. 

Zheng Dafu remained motionless. 

The old Yang man said, “Return things to their rightful owner; it's not a bother to me, as I wouldn’t even glance at it, just a headache.” 

Those golden lights were Zheng Dafu’s soul. 

Zheng Dafu stood up, cupping his fists in gratitude, “Thank you, Master, for imparting the teachings and guarding the path.” 

The old Yang man continued exhaling smoke. 

Zheng Dafu immediately sat down. 

Standing there felt disrespectful. 

Zheng Dafu turned his head, and not long after, a spirited young man in a Confucian robe entered, carrying a bamboo box and a hiking staff. 

Zheng Dafu stiffened his face. 

The dust-covered young man hurried to the old Yang man’s side, squatting down and kneading his shoulders, clicking his tongue, “Rest assured, rest assured, these muscles and bones are still strong, just like a young man. It wouldn’t be too much to marry a wife. Dafu, you’re really something; as a disciple, you don’t even consider picking out a wife for your master? Is it that hard to find a wife, or is it equally hard to find a master’s wife?” 

The old Yang man didn’t mind. 

Zheng Dafu was used to it. 

The biggest bravery in this world is probably only Li Huai daring to treat the old man this way. 

The old Yang man asked, “Are you going to the Piyun Mountain Forest to study at the Deer Academy again?” 

Li Huai straightforwardly sat down on the ground, “That’s secondary; I want to duel with Pei Qian, but it’ll be a battle of wits. After a few years, we’ve both accumulated a lot, and now we’ve scheduled a showdown at the plaza outside the Master’s Hall on Zise Peak, a grand event of top experts clashing in the martial world. She went to the Sword Qi Great Wall, and we met at the academy; she said she was going to prepare her treasures for a rematch.” 

Li Huai lamented, “It’s a pity that Li Baoping has gone off on her own adventures; if I lose to Pei Qian, that’s fine. But if I accidentally win, without Li Baoping to back me up, I fear I won’t be able to leave Fallen Mountain.” 

Zheng Dafu laughed, “You still have people you’re afraid of?” 

Li Huai nodded, “Of course, I’m afraid of Qi Jingchun, afraid of Baoping, afraid of Pei Qian; there are so many teachers at the academy that I’m afraid of.” 

Zheng Dafu jested, “What about Chen Ping’an, is he someone you fear?” 

Li Huai thought seriously, “If he’s around, I’m not afraid.” 

On Fortune Street, there were scholars like Li Xisheng, who was traveling to Daisui Mountain, and Li Baoping, who was studying at the Great Sui Cliff Academy, along with Zhao Yao, who went to Central Divine Continent. 

In Peach Leaf Alley, there was Xie Ling, the direct disciple of Dragon Spring Sword Sect, and Wei’s servant girl Tao Ya, who was headed to the Great Li capital, as well as Lin Shouyi, who was focused on both cultivation and studies. 

In Mud Bottle Alley, there was Chen Ping’an, who went to the Sword Qi Great Wall, and Gu Can, who had stirred up waves at Book and Letter Lake, now began to hibernate again. 

There was Song Jixin, who became a prince of the Great Li, and the maid Zhi Gui. 

In Apricot Blossom Alley, there was a young genius leader of the continent, Ma Kuxuan. 

The siblings Li Liu and Li Huai. 

The businessman Dong Shuijing. 

At the Yang family shop, there were also Su Dian and Shi Ling Shan. 

The town’s luckiest often had heavy roots, like Li Huai and Gu Can. Back in the day, the old locust tree had the most leaves, actually belonging to Gu Can, who had secretly stuffed a large pocket. When he returned to Mud Bottle Alley, Chen Ping’an reminded him, and only then did he realize how many locust leaves he had. 

The strongest fate probably still belonged to Chen Ping’an.
