But all of this, the children and youths of Li Zhu Cave’s streets and alleys, had unknowingly passed nearly fifteen years. 

Everyone had their own circumstances, opportunities, and achievements, not all of which were smooth sailing. 

Unknowingly, fifteen years had passed, and many children in the town had already reached the age of adulthood, while the group of young men from back then were now nearing thirty and standing firm. 

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 767: Standing Beneath the Bright Moon

A tall young man and a strikingly beautiful woman entered the Dragon Prefecture of the Great Li Dynasty, a land that had become a feng shui treasure after the destruction of the Li Pearl Cave and its subsequent roots in the earth. 

This place was filled with numerous mountains and rivers, brimming with stories, and it was one of the finest cultivation grounds in the Baoping Continent. Yet, everything about the mountains and rivers felt shrouded in a mist that made it hard to see clearly.

As the two made their way along the Iron Talismans River towards Huaihuang County, they passed a bustling temple dedicated to the Water Goddess. Due to their identities and cultivation backgrounds, neither dared to enter and burn incense. When they finally caught sight of the eastern city gate, the young man sighed in relief and remarked, “We’ve finally arrived. Miss Ma, should we visit Mr. Chen at the mountain first, or should we pay a visit to Gu Can’s home in the state city? It might be harder to find Luopo Mountain, while the state city is relatively easier to navigate.”

This pair had not had an easy journey northward through Longzhou. The main reason was that Gu Can had suddenly instructed them to go north alone, while he and the peculiar scholar named Liu Chicheng were headed to Qingfeng City to visit the Xu family. This left the timid Zeng Ye feeling quite anxious. Years ago, he had been pulled from the fiery pit of Maoyue Island by the steward Zhang Ye and brought to the small hut at the mountain gate, where he met that accountant. His life had since undergone a tremendous transformation. Afterward, he met Gu Can, transitioning from fear to familiarity, and now to dependence—all in the span of just a few years. For someone who preferred quiet meditation, it felt like a mere moment.

At some point, Zeng Ye, who used to have nightmares just from a casual glance from Gu Can, now found himself feeling uneasy without Gu Can by his side, as if he were walking on unstable ground while exploring mountains and rivers. 

In fact, Zeng Ye, who was naturally suited for ghostly path cultivation, had made rapid progress over the years. He could even be considered exceptionally quick, though he had remained inconspicuous due to Gu Can’s presence. 

Zeng Ye was now a legitimate Qi Condensation cultivator, someone who could be regarded as a “mid-tier immortal lord” in the martial world of ordinary vassal states. 

Because he practiced esoteric techniques that leaned heavily towards the yin, Zeng Ye was able to approach various mountain temples and immortal peaks while Gu Can was with him. However, once they parted ways, he lacked the confidence to do so, especially with Ma Duyi by his side, who exuded an ethereal presence. She relied on a talisman made from fox fur to walk among mortals, and to those profound cultivators on the mountains, both Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi could easily be seen as unclean and heretical beings.

Ma Duyi had a jade token hanging at her waist, a peace talisman left for them by Gu Can. After some thought, she smiled and said, “Let’s head to Luopo Mountain first. We’re quite familiar with Mr. Chen, so we shouldn’t be turned away. Even if Mr. Chen isn’t there, it shouldn’t be too hard to find someone to share a cup of tea with, right?”

Zeng Ye grinned and replied, “Sure, I was thinking the same.” 

There are always some people whose thoughts bring a sense of reassurance.

After passing through Huaihuang County and asking locals for directions, they faced a language barrier and struggled to communicate. After much effort, they finally found a shopkeeper who spoke the Great Li dialect, but even he couldn’t provide a clear address for Luopo Mountain. He only offered vague directions, saying to head past the small town until they reached the Pearl Mountain, a small hill, and then look for an opportunity to ask the mountain’s immortals for guidance.

Once they entered the spirit-filled continuous mountains, it took them quite some time to find the grayish mountain that was part of Luopo Mountain’s domain. After heading south, they arrived at the foot of the sheer cliffs on the southern side of Luopo Mountain, not far from the main gate to the south. However, Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi were met with an unfathomable scene. 

First, they saw a little girl dressed in black, facing away from them, gazing up at the clouds hanging like a white belt high on the cliffs. The girl carried a golden small yoke on one shoulder and a green bamboo walking stick on the other, shouting loudly, “Pei Qian, Pei Qian, don’t jump wrong this time! It’s such a hassle to fill the pit!”

Zeng Ye glanced around the little girl, noticing the ground was pockmarked with pits. 

That green bamboo walking stick looked very familiar!

Suddenly, the black-clad girl turned around, her eyes locking onto the two outsiders, and she dashed away in an instant.

Zeng Ye quickly looked up.

A dark spot broke through the clouds, accompanied by a whistling sound as it plummeted down. In an instant, a slender figure landed heavily on the ground, causing a massive thud that shook the earth and sent dust flying.

Zeng Ye focused, staring into the distance.

In the huge pit, a slightly dark-skinned, slender girl crouched down slightly, slowly rising to her feet. She turned to the little girl, who was huddled at the edge of the pit, and reproached, “Little Rice Grain, what’s going on? If it weren’t for my keen eyes, you would have fallen into the pit if you had taken a different route. What would happen if you got hurt? Didn’t I tell you to stay put…”

As she spoke, the astonishingly agile girl casually took a few steps and positioned herself between the little girl and the two outsiders.

Ma Duyi noticed that the girl was wearing a pair of crudely woven straw sandals, with blood trickling from her feet.

Unable to help herself, Ma Duyi glanced at the cliff before looking back at the girl.

Was she attempting to commit suicide by jumping off the cliff, or was this just a game?

Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi were not purely martial artists, so they didn’t understand the intricacies of that girl’s cliff-jumping “ground slam.”

She was using her body to test the ground.

She had to condense all the divine intent of protection into pure physicality, utilizing the momentum from her fall, as if delivering the heaviest punch from the heavens to the earth.

In the girl’s words, it was about delivering a heavy blow to the ground!

This method of training was something the girl came up with herself. Warm Tree, of course, disagreed, thinking it was too dangerous. Pei Qian was still at the fifth realm bottleneck, and her body wasn’t resilient enough. Little Rice Grain believed it was feasible, and since it was two against one, they could try. Warm Tree wanted to consult the old chef, but by the time Pei Qian stepped onto the six stone slabs laid out on the bamboo building, she leaped and disappeared from sight.

Zhou Mili was crouched at the edge of the cliff, and Warm Tree was getting anxious. The old chef had already appeared at the cliff’s edge, glancing at the ground, tsk-tsking.

Warm Tree breathed a sigh of relief, seeing it wasn’t a big deal.

Soon after, Pei Qian climbed up the cliff, limping a bit but with her eyes sparkling as she laughed, “That felt great!”

Zhu Lian said nothing and turned to leave.

And so, more pits appeared on the ground.

Zhou Mili made a playful gesture at Pei Qian, scolding her for making Warm Tree angry.

This was the scene that Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi witnessed today.

If this was how Luopo Mountain entertained guests, it was certainly a unique approach.

Pei Qian glanced at the two unfamiliar visitors and asked, “Was the sound of the abacus on the left or the right?”

Zeng Ye was baffled.

Ma Duyi replied, “Facing the mountain gate, it’s the left side’s accountant.”

Only then did Pei Qian smile and clasp her fists, saying, “I am Pei Qian, the first disciple of Luopo Mountain, pleased to meet you, Daoist Zeng and Sister Ma!”

Ma Duyi was somewhat astonished—what a clever girl! Her insight was exceptional! It was known that Gu Can had privately stated that Liu Chicheng had cast an illusion to help conceal their yin presence, but Gu Can had also said that this matter should not be revealed to Zeng Ye. While traveling, Zeng Ye should be careful where he stepped. Ma Duyi had laughed and scolded in jest, “Are you worried I might accidentally stir up trouble?” Gu Can had only smiled and remained silent, handing her the invaluable peace talisman.

Only then did Ma Duyi refrain from confronting Gu Can. Ultimately, it was Gu Can who was more cautious and worldly. Sometimes, when she and Zeng Ye interacted without Gu Can nearby, she couldn’t help but feel that Gu Can learned too quickly, regardless of what it was. In matters of cultivation, there was no need to elaborate; with various local dialects and the heroes of the martial world they encountered, as well as the officials and common folk they mingled with, Gu Can always seemed to fit in perfectly, creating a significant distance between Ma Duyi and Zeng Ye.

At this point, Zhou Mili stood next to Pei Qian, tilting her head and frowning, then pretending to understand everything, nodding lightly as if she were well-versed in the ways of the martial world.

Since they were guests, it was inappropriate to return home via the cliff path. Pei Qian led the two visitors around to the mountain gate.

Of course, she didn’t forget to introduce the right protector of Luopo Mountain, Little Rice Grain.

Zhou Mili quietly reminded, “She is the right protector of Luopo Mountain, formerly the right protector of Qilong Alley, but now given to Xian…”

Pei Qian coughed lightly.

Zhou Mili immediately shut her mouth, standing on her toes with her palm covering her mouth, “Let’s not keep track of anything; I haven’t let anything slip yet.”

Pei Qian rubbed her little head, saying nothing. What was there to keep track of? Little Rice Grain and Warm Tree only had a record of their contributions; there wasn’t any small ledger at all. However, such matters couldn’t be spoken of; otherwise, Little Rice Grain would easily become proud.

Ma Duyi’s expression remained unchanged, though she was stunned for a moment. Zeng Ye, on the other hand, was relatively calm, as Mr. Chen had always approached worldly affairs with a tranquil heart, as long as there was no conflict with the principles.

Upon reaching the mountain gate, Zheng Dafeng was already absent.

Now, the young Yuan Lai was temporarily stationed there, responsible for guarding the gate.

Cen Yuanji happened to be practicing her fists, coming down from the mountain peak. She was now a fourth realm martial artist, though she had struggled a bit to break through the third realm bottleneck. The old chef said she was doing quite well, but Cen Yuanji was not entirely satisfied. Despite having a good relationship with her peer Yuan Bao, both of them were pure martial artists, and there would inevitably be competition.

Women often behaved like this; even in the best of relationships, there would be small competitions hidden within their charming gazes and smiles. Such emotions were merely human nature—more subtle and captivating than the blatant struggles of men.

Moreover, Yuan Bao’s teacher was Lu Baixiang, while Cen Yuanji had always regarded Old Master Zhu as her mentor. Since Old Master Zhu and Lu Baixiang had similar standings at Luopo Mountain, neither of them competed openly. However, as their disciples, she and Yuan Bao would still engage in a bit of rivalry.

The young man in the green shirt, Yuan Lai, was sitting under the wall, reading, taking advantage of his sister's absence. When Cen Yuanji arrived at the foot of the mountain after her six-step training, she lost interest in her book and turned her attention to the young lady.

Uncle Zheng had left many books for Yuan Lai in the study before his long journey and had told him earnestly that when he grew older, he could visit the old chef’s private library, where the knowledge would be vast. The young man was somewhat fascinated.

Seeing Pei Qian and the others, the boy had no choice but to pull his attention away from Cen Yuanji’s beautiful eyes and quickly walked toward the mountain gate. After hearing Pei Qian’s introduction, he bowed to the two visitors who were old friends of the young mountain lord. He suddenly realized that this was a scholar’s etiquette, and if his sister found out, he would be scolded, so Yuan Lai hastily cupped his fists and smiled.

After Cen Yuanji greeted them, she continued to practice her fists up the mountain.

Old Master Zhu had previously advised that as long as the path beneath one’s feet was correct, diligence would compensate for shortcomings. Practicing martial arts shouldn’t become a rigid endeavor; if one wishes to embody the intent of their techniques, they must find a source of vitality within their martial arts. This was the so-called martial artist’s practice of climbing high while establishing a purpose in their heart first. In the end, Old Master Zhu encouraged Cen Yuanji to contemplate what she truly sought from her martial arts practice; once she understood, training would no longer be a burden.

Upon reaching the mountain, Pei Qian discovered that the old chef was not at home.

Fortunately, with Chen Nuanshu around, there was no worry about neglecting the two guests.

As long as one was a guest of Luopo Mountain, there was no distinction between high and low status.

Zhu Lian had gone to the Sword Offering Platform.

Sword cultivators Cui Wei and the young Zhang Jiazhen were currently residing there.

Wei Ban stood at the foot of the mountain, slowly ascending with Zhu Lian, whom he called over.

Wei Ban laughed, “Fortunately, the current manager of the Longquan Sword Sect isn’t Master Ruan, but Miss Xiu Xiu. Otherwise, even I might not be able to cover everything.”

Zhu Lian’s expression was not relaxed, “Is that woman’s identity confirmed?”

Wei Ban nodded, “She is indeed the ferrywoman we were instructed to look for by Chen Ping’an, the ferrywoman of the Jiao Mountain ferry, Chunshui.”

Years ago, after the ferry across the continent sank in the territory of the Zhu Ying Dynasty, she miraculously survived and took on the alias Shi Qiao. On a small mountain peak of the immortals, she revealed the collusion between the Heavenly Monarch Xie Shi and the Song family of the Great Li Dynasty, framing the Zhu Ying Dynasty.

Regarding this matter, the Great Li Emperor’s imperial study had discussed it carefully. If it weren’t for the national teacher Cui Shao’s belief that the leak of such information would lead to a so-called exposure, or if Cui Shao was hoping to lure a big fish to bite the bait, otherwise, even if that ferry maid were secretly taken away, with the current intelligence network of the Great Li, a fifth realm female cultivator would find it hard to escape death even with a powerful rescue.

Zhu Lian said, “This situation is quite troublesome.”

Wei Ban laughed, “Of course, if it weren’t troublesome, would I have called you over? Such matters, seemingly big or small, ultimately tread on forbidden ground.”

Zhu Lian said, “It’s not too troublesome; I need to confirm one thing.”

Wei Ban nodded, “As long as you have a clear mind, that’s enough. I, on the other hand, have a notorious reputation, so I’m not worried about this matter.”

Zhu Lian shook his head, “It’s not that simple. Alright, I know the way; I’ll go myself. You return to Piyun Mountain and act as if you know nothing.”

Wei Ban frowned.

Zhu Lian said, “If you want to maintain good relationships, then don’t ruin them. Brother Wei, friends are friends, but matters are matters. Since we’re friends, some things shouldn’t involve you.”

Wei Ban laughed, “Then I’ll keep an eye on the Sword Offering Platform and, if anything stirs up, we can discuss a plan then.”

Zhu Lian nodded.

Being kind to friends should be met with kindness in return.

This is the code of the martial world.

Earlier, it was Wei Ban who had “detained” that group of people from the edge of the North Mountain Territory to the Sword Offering Platform, and he dissipated into thin air.

Zhu Lian soon saw a weary group arriving.

The Golden Pill bottleneck sword cultivator Cui Wei was confused, merely watching the inexplicably appearing people on the mountain.

A young man with the surname Dugu, a maid named Meng Long, and a woman named Shi Qiao.

After Zhu Lian arrived, he nodded to Cui Wei, who then took off on his sword.

Zhu Lian turned toward the woman with the real name Chunshui, asking, “Miss Chunshui, I have two questions that I’d like you to answer honestly.”

Meng Long, the maid, looked somewhat displeased.

The pale-skinned young man, however, remained composed.

Chunshui nodded.

Zhu Lian’s expression softened as he smiled, “First, did you come to find my young master on your own accord? Second, when did you have this thought? Was it after the ferry sank that you sought to find the only person you could trust in a foreign land, or was it that you were left with no other choice now?”

Chunshui’s eyes were clear as she replied, “I never thought about finding Chen Ping’an before. The reason I changed my mind now is that I don’t want to put Young Master Dugu in danger. I only hope that Young Master Dugu can survive, and I can be handed over to the Great Li Dynasty.”

Chunshui paused slightly and added with sincerity, “It may seem childish, but it’s the truth.”

Zhu Lian nodded, smiling, “I trust Miss Chunshui.”

Then, the stooped old man turned and smiled, “The exiled nobles of the Zhu Ying Dynasty, am I right?”

Young Master Dugu nodded, “Indeed. I wouldn’t dare deceive you, senior. My real name is Dugu Duanshun, but now I go by Shao Po Xian. As a person of a fallen nation, I truly don’t wish to die just yet; that’s why I resorted to this.”

Zhu Lian asked, “Do you believe that by coming to this unknown Luopo Mountain, you can survive, or is it a desperate gamble?”

Young Master Dugu replied, “The latter.”

The three of them had faced two ambushes during their flight; one was an unexpected encounter, while the other was a well-prepared attack from the Great Li’s accompanying cultivators.

Zhu Lian laughed, “What kindness do you owe to Miss Chunshui? Tell me, I’m just an errand boy here at Luopo Mountain, not very learned. I truly want to inquire from you, Young Master Dugu.”

Dugu Duanshun was momentarily speechless.

His reasons for saving “Shi Qiao” were certainly not noble; they were far from any chivalrous act.

Meng Long’s expression was pained.

How did her master end up in such dire straits?

After a moment of silence, Zhu Lian asked, “Where did the last ambush occur?”

Dugu Duanshun replied, “Around Nanjian Country, far from the Great Li’s Dragon Prefecture. The reason for the ambush was that among the Great Li’s accompanying cultivators, someone possessed the Zhu Ying Dynasty’s imperial jade seal, allowing them to trace me. After the ambush, I pretended to head south, and midway, I broke the dragon vein in my personal small world before quietly heading north. I believe I wasn’t being monitored by the Great Li.”

The young man’s words were succinct.

As for the dangers and costs involved, those were not for outsiders to know.

Zhu Lian asked, “Shao Po Xian, do you wish to linger in a small area or to generously risk your life for your country?”

Dugu Duanshun chuckled, “That question is unnecessary, old senior.”

Zhu Lian nodded, looking at the downcast young woman, he smiled and said, “Miss Chunshui, do you know that what you’re doing will bring major problems to my young master?”

Chunshui was about to speak when Zhu Lian interrupted, laughing, “What do you think? I have a good memory; once I hear something, I remember it, so I’m merely stating a fact now.”

Chunshui nodded, biting her lip until it bled.

She hid one hand in her sleeve, tightly clutching something, her arm trembling slightly.

Aside from repaying the life-saving grace to Young Master Dugu, she had her own selfish motives.

She hoped to deliver something to Luopo Mountain. After that, even if Luopo Mountain used her to negotiate with the Great Li’s Song family, she wouldn’t mind.

Zhu Lian chuckled, looking around.

The Sword Offering Platform was filled with wild persimmon trees. In winter, the bright red persimmons hung from the high branches, delightful to behold.

In her hometown in the Lotus Flower Blessed Land, persimmons had a nickname, quite elegant—the Frost-Resisting Marquis.

Finally, Zhu Lian said to the dazed young woman, “If my young master were here, he would be very pleased to reunite with Miss Chunshui after a long separation.”

After saying this, Zhu Lian left the Sword Offering Platform.

Meng Long quietly asked, “Young Master, what does this mean?”

Dugu Duanshun laughed heartily, “To live under someone’s roof and have a meal is not a bad thing.”

After Zhu Lian stepped down from the Sword Offering Platform, Wei Ban appeared.

Zhu Lian said, exasperated, “Are you a mountain lord who courts trouble?”

Wei Ban laughed, “I’m just bored.”

Zhu Lian, with his hands behind his back, slowly said, “That ‘Shi Qiao’ girl is definitely someone we need to save. As for the other two, we merely need to clarify one thing.”

Wei Ban asked, “That is, who told him that coming to this unremarkable Luopo Mountain would guarantee survival?”

Zhu Lian exclaimed in shock, “Brother Wei, you have a keen insight!”

Wei Ban responded with a polite smile.

Zhu Lian scratched his head, chuckling, “Well, I can find something serious to do. I can’t just be the cook who’s always blamed for the saltiness or blandness of the dishes. It’s about time for us at Luopo Mountain to actively resolve some troubles. Otherwise, unnecessary troubles will only grow.”

Zhu Lian scoffed, “Picking soft persimmons to squeeze?”

Wei Ban chuckled knowingly.

It seemed that the matter regarding the Water Goddess of the Yuyue River had not yet settled.

Wei Ban gazed toward Luopo Mountain and said, “Coincidentally, another guest has arrived.”

The two vanished into thin air, appearing atop Luopo Mountain.

Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi then saw the handsome immortal figure.

As for the kind-looking old gentleman beside him, he was indeed overshadowed by the strikingly handsome young man with golden earrings.

Chen Nuanshu quickly got up to introduce Zhu Lian and Wei Ban, the head steward of Luopo Mountain and the North Mountain Lord of the Great Li, respectively.

Zeng Ye and Ma Duyi were nearly scared out of their wits.

Currently, among the Five Great Mountain Lords of a continent, Wei Ban ranked the highest in cultivation and also had the greatest reputation!

Pei Qian reminded, “Old chef, it’s almost mealtime; make sure to showcase your best skills.”

Little Rice Grain wiped her mouth, “Can we not?”

Zhu Lian gently called out, “Alright then,” and immediately went off to the kitchen in the back courtyard.

It seemed that the small kitchen was Zhu Lian’s little world.

Wei Ban felt helpless inside.

More reliant on his looks than Jiang Shangzhen, yet he insisted on being a cook.

At the Qilong Alley’s New Year’s shop, old friends were also reuniting.

Dong Shuijing, Lin Shouyi.

And there was that girl who had once worried about the nickname “Little Stone” spreading, who had moved to the Great Li capital with her family and had now married.

Shi Jia Chun.

Li Baoping’s closest friend once upon a time.

The New Year’s shop and the neighboring Grass Head shop had once been the family business of Shi Jia Chun.

Also, Shi Jia Chun and Shi Ling Shan from Taoye Alley were somewhat related, though Shi Jia Chun was of a higher generation. If they were to meet, she would have to call her aunt.

Life is unpredictable; the former classmates and friends had scattered after parting ways in the small town over a decade ago, and now they were all in radically different situations.

Shi Jia Chun was now happily raising her family. Her husband was from a prominent family, named Bian Wenmao, whose family had been settled in the Great Li capital for hundreds of years. Their ancestors were from the Lu Dynasty’s aristocracy, and perhaps due to their long lineage, combined with the saying that “trees move and people thrive,” the family in the Great Li had a respectable status. While their family’s officials were not particularly renowned, most of them held honorable positions, being well-known scholars from the early days of the Great Li’s literary scene.

Moreover, the family of the mountain deity, who was nominally worshiped, was not shabby either. One was an elder of the Changchun Palace’s ancestral hall, while the other had an unfortunate fate. Years ago, with a few long-residing friends in the mountains, he had a conflict with the sage Ruan Qiong while passing through the jurisdiction of the Li Pearl Cave. The outcome wasn’t good, but at least he survived, which was fortunate compared to another friend who died and vanished entirely.

This reunion was initiated when Dong Shuijing went to the Great Li capital for business and sought out Shi Jia Chun. She wanted to set a time for their old classmates to gather back in their hometown of Huaihuang Town.

But since Li Baoping happened to be traveling south, she missed it.

So Shi Jia Chun was now complaining about Baoping.

The group sat in the back courtyard of the shop reminiscing, while the shopkeeper, Shi Rou, brought over tea and snacks and then left quickly.

Listening to Shi Jia Chun’s chatter, Dong Shuijing laughed, “Baoping really doesn’t value your face at all; it’s quite unreasonable.”

Lin Shouyi nodded, “I’ll have Li Huai mention it to her later.”

Shi Jia Chun rolled her eyes, “Li Huai? Forget it, he has the audacity to speak grandly in front of Baoping!”

Suddenly realizing that her husband was sitting next to her, Shi Jia Chun quickly straightened her posture and composed her expression.

Bian Wenmao was a charming seed of a scholar with a well-chosen name, and now he was working in the Hanlin Academy, editing history books. Among the local officials of the Great Li, he was considered a refreshing figure. He wasn’t particularly outstanding, but at a young age, he had firmly established himself in the literary scene of the Great Li capital, working in the Hanlin Academy, which was often regarded as the “land of future ministers.” Once he gets promoted, his official rank wouldn’t be small.

In other places, Bian Wenmao would have been a top guest in any government office, but in Huaihuang County, where the two prominent families, the Cao and Yuan, had disputes, he found himself in a bit of a dilemma. 

Bian Wenmao’s impression of these two young men was one was very ordinary, while the other was somewhat decent.

The ordinary one was Dong Shuijing, who came from a merchant background.

The somewhat decent one was Lin Shouyi, who had studied at the Cliff Academy in Great Sui.

As for their family backgrounds, Shi Jia Chun had mentioned them in passing; they were just casual words. Dong Shuijing's family wasn’t very wealthy, but he had established himself early on. As for settling down, there were some uncertainties.

Lin Shouyi’s father had served under three different supervisors of the Dragon Kiln, and it was said he was also working in the Great Li capital now, but he had no connections with the Shi family, and Bian Wenmao didn’t feel it was worth pursuing a relationship with Lin Shouyi, who was an outsider. However, Lin Shouyi being able to study at the Cliff Academy and eventually entering the Great Li officialdom should mean he wouldn’t fare too poorly.

Li Huai rushed into the back courtyard, “Hey, it’s been so many years since we’ve seen each other, and you’re already talking bad about me?”

Shi Jia Chun turned her head, stunned for a moment. The once small and round Li Huai had suddenly grown into a tall young man.

Lin Shouyi and Dong Shuijing hadn’t changed much; they were still the same as before. But Li Huai? He was completely different from the impression he left in their childhood.

For instance, when he threw his shorts up a tree, Li Huai would roll on the ground crying just to call for Mr. Qi.

Shi Jia Chun stood up and teased, “Li Huai? Have you been eating well these years?”

Bian Wenmao slowly stood up, smiling but saying nothing.

Li Huai was a classmate with whom Shi Jia Chun had shared many stories, thus he was someone Bian Wenmao found least interesting. He could tell that this person was a dullard who hadn’t opened his mind in school; he had only gotten into the Cliff Academy due to his ancestors' merit. People like him would inevitably fall back to the ground sooner or later. Dong Shuijing, on the other hand, had some skills and was rumored to have connected with both Cao and Yuan.

Li Huai greeted Bian Wenmao and could see that he was not particularly fond of him. The atmosphere was polite yet distant. He couldn’t let his good friend Shi Jia Chun down, so he forced a smile.

Then he plopped down in front of Shi Jia Chun, grabbing a piece of pastry, mumbling, “Before Baoping leaves, she said she would stop by the capital to see you.”

Shi Jia Chun laughed, “At least she has some conscience.”

Lin Shouyi and Dong Shuijing sat across from each other. They had always had a good relationship but were somewhat at odds, which made Shi Jia Chun find it amusing. The reasoning was simple: they both liked Li Huai’s sister.

Shi Jia Chun didn’t believe that Lin Shouyi’s better background would guarantee that Li Liu would like him.

Shi Jia Chun had always felt that Li Liu, who often went to the school to pick up her brother, was a bit odd, though she couldn’t pinpoint why. Logically, Li Liu was older and had already been a young lady, appearing gentle and delicate, unlike the more spirited Zhi Gui from Ni Ping Alley. Both were beauties, but Shi Jia Chun felt that if they were to get along, the unsmiling maid Zhi Gui might be easier to approach than Li Liu.

Bian Wenmao had another social engagement in the state city, but as his wife rarely returned to the capital, he remained patient, not revealing any emotion.

After spending about half an hour at the New Year’s shop, Shi Jia Chun stood up to leave, heading to the state city where a carriage from her husband’s friend awaited.

Li Huai and the others followed her to the shop’s entrance just as Yu Lu and Xie Xie were coming down from the Lin Deer Academy, planning to go to Luopo Mountain together.

Earlier, Li Huai had gone once, returning to Piyun Mountain Academy, repeatedly lamenting his loss.

Bian Wenmao didn’t mind too much, politely bidding farewell to everyone as he helped his wife into the carriage, bowing one last time.

After watching the carriage depart, everyone returned to the back courtyard to continue their chat. Li Huai crossed his arms behind his head, “That Bian Wenmao thinks too highly of himself.”

Lin Shouyi calmly replied, “Shi Jia Chun is looking for a husband. As long as Bian Wenmao truly likes her, that’s enough. Shi Jia Chun isn’t looking for a friend for us.”

Dong Shuijing nodded.

Li Huai pouted, “I just think Shi Jia Chun could find someone better.”

Lin Shouyi shook his head, “There’s no reason to argue.”

Suddenly, Li Huai became anxious, “Is Baoping really safe traveling the martial world alone? She’s not a cultivator!”

Lin Shouyi thought for a moment but refrained from revealing the truth.

Yu Lu and Xie Xie shared the same sentiment.

The only one who was oblivious to the situation was Li Huai, who believed that his luck depended on whether he stepped on a dog’s poop.

Before heading to Luopo Mountain, Lin Shouyi asked Li Huai and the others to wait a moment. He went to the ancestral home, cleaning the courtyard and the ancestral hall. The young scholar recited the family teachings in silence.

Finally, he lit three incense sticks, mumbling, “Thank you, ancestors.”

Li Huai was impatient, saying he would head to Pearl Mountain to wait.

Not far from his ancestral home, Pei Qian and Zhou Mili were already waiting there.

Pei Qian remarked, “A general who has lost his army!”

Li Huai quickly retorted, “Even in defeat, there is honor; I dare not speak of bravery!”

Pei Qian nodded and led the way.

Pei Qian asked, “What about our two subordinates from the branch?”

Li Huai felt guilty, “Those two wrote the wrong articles and got scolded by the teacher, so they’re currently gnawing on their pens.”

Pei Qian shook her head, then pointed at Little Rice Grain beside her, “Zhou Mili will be the deputy leader of our branch from now on.”

Zhou Mili was stunned on the spot, her joy overwhelming! She now had a proper title!

Li Huai was thrilled.

Originally, the branch only had three people, and now it finally seemed a bit more substantial.

Afterwards, the group made their way to Luopo Mountain.

Upon reaching the mountain, Yu Lu stopped at the gate, saying he would ascend later to chat with the boy Yuan Lai, who was flipping through books.

Xie Xie also wandered off, meeting Cen Yuanji, who was practicing her punches on the mountain top, along with the standing Yuan Bao.

Xie Xie appeared somewhat dazed.

It was as if she saw her carefree self from years ago, practicing cultivation on the mountain.

After that, Pei Qian, after exchanging nods with the old chef and Wei Ban, took Little Rice Grain to the Lotus Flower Blessed Land, following the paths they had previously walked, hiking through mountains and rivers, reaching the capital of the Nanyuan Kingdom.

Passing through the Scholar’s Lane, they went to a temple to burn incense, and then sat in the corridor in a daze.

Zhou Mili merely accompanied Pei Qian; when Pei Qian was happy, she would say more, and when Pei Qian was not happy, she would stay silent.

Finally, Pei Qian chose a private residence, one she had secretly purchased with her own money, which the old chef also knew about but chose to turn a blind eye to.

It was the tranquil dwelling where the great demon Ding Ying had once stayed with Ya Er and the flower boy from Chunqiao Palace, Zhou Shi.

Pei Qian sat cross-legged there, mimicking her master’s actions, rolling up her sleeves, and began to meditate, nurturing her martial intent.

The reason she came here was to break through the martial path’s barriers.

Pei Qian intended to seize back whatever martial fortune belonged to her from the Lotus Flower Blessed Land through her own efforts.

Moreover, when the time comes, Wei Ban would open the gates of the blessed land, and Pei Qian would scatter all the martial fortune she had won from the Haoran World, just as her master had done, feeding it back to the Lotus Flower Blessed Land.

Old Master Cui may be gone, but there was no way to return home.

So she would take back the martial fortune that Old Master Cui had left behind here to Luopo Mountain.

In the central region of the Baoping Continent, a great ancient river leading to the sea was under construction, involving dozens of rivers and numerous mountains with mountain god temples and earth deity shrines.

Such an ambitious project, even the exiled elders couldn’t help but sigh. The Great Li rabble truly dared to envision what others wouldn’t dare to, and do what others couldn’t.

The Great Li court was exhausting the people and wasting resources, while the young emperor was so eager for achievements and grandiosity. Didn’t he fear that he might rise high today and fall into oblivion tomorrow? In the end, wouldn’t it be the common people who would suffer?

However, it was said that the Guanhul Academy’s highly reputed new Zhongyue and the historic Jiang Clan of Yunlin were both participating in the project, which only stirred more emotions.

Was it possible that the entire Baoping Continent would truly fall under the Song clan’s rule, becoming a land governed by a single family?

The Great Li court dispatched three officials from localities to oversee the construction of the great river: Guan Yiran, the direct descendant of the Guan family, Liu Xunmei from the capital’s Chi’er Street, and the civil servant Liu Qingfeng from the Qingsuan Kingdom.

Aside from the last one, who was unfamiliar, the Great Li capital’s officials were not strangers to Guan Yiran and Liu Xunmei. Both hailed from noble families and were young talents among their peers. Especially Guan Yiran, who had early on immersed himself in the borderlands, growing up among the dead as a military cultivator. Liu Xunmei was not bad either, having fought his way south.

Guan’s family had long held the position of a stable and esteemed minister in the Great Li’s Ministry of Personnel. The flowing positions of deputy ministers and officials were often just jokes, as it was said that once there were two governors from the Ministry of Personnel who met by chance, both were former deputy ministers from the Ministry.

As for Liu Qingfeng, he was largely unknown in the Great Li court. In fact, even the highly regarded old master of the Guan family in the Ministry of Personnel had little familiarity with Liu Qingfeng, having to sift through records. 

The evaluation of the Qingsuan Kingdom’s reopening of shipping routes was average; they only managed to achieve a fair rating. Merely having some minor contributions, he had been appointed as a local governor and unexpectedly needed to travel north, engaging with numerous mountain deities and immortal beings. His rank jumped from fourth to third, as the Great Li court appointed him as a temporary river supervisor.

Guan Yiran and Liu Xunmei’s ranks remained unchanged, making it seem as if they had become subordinates of a vassal state’s official.

However, Liu Qingfeng was not the first to be suddenly promoted from a vassal official to a prominent figure in the Great Li court. The former vassal Huang Tingguo had a county magistrate named Wei Li, who was also promoted several ranks to become the current governor of Longzhou. Among the mountain spirits, some land deity from the Red Candle Town territory became a city deity.

The Grand General of the Qingsuan Kingdom, Wei Liang, was rumored to have signs of a promotion as well, with whispers from the Great Li’s Ministry of Personnel.

The southeastern Qingsuan Kingdom of the Baoping Continent had inexplicably transformed from an isolated area into a favorable location for officials.

Officials were clearly divided into pure and corrupt streams. The most significant distinction among the people of the Baoping Continent now was whether they originated from the Great Li itself.

However, compared to Wei Ban’s swift rise to the position of mountain god of Piyun Mountain, and then to the North Mountain Lord of an entire continent, these changes in the officialdom were not particularly surprising.

The Great Li cavalry had been waging war to the south for many years, with many young faces rising among the military generals, including those from humble origins.

Yet, the rapid loss and promotion of the Great Li border troops had become commonplace, and the people had long grown accustomed to it. The civil officials and the mountain spirit’s genealogical system operated with strict discipline, which made sudden appearances of new figures quite eye-catching.

Today marked the first gathering of the three main officials overseeing the river construction. There were no welcome banquets; they simply convened by a large river.

Liu Qingfeng was accompanied by Wang Yifu.

Guan Yiran was perplexed, as the descendant of the upper minister, according to his great-grandfather, he was supposed to be responsible for a north-south ferry route, even arranging friends to accompany him. Yet, he found himself here, naturally receiving a scolding.

Liu Xunmei, flanked by two guards, Cao Jun and Wei Xian.

Wei Xian had followed the sword genius Cao Jun from the Ni Ping Alley, and alongside Liu Xunmei, who seemed nothing like a noble scion, he was doing well for himself.

Wei Xian, with the identity of a military cultivator, had gained a martial honor through genuine achievements and now held real power, being Liu Xunmei’s right-hand man.

Rumors had it that Wei Xian was well-known among the second patrol officer, Cao Ping.

As for Cao Jun, he was already quite famous in the Great Li military.

The three introduced themselves.

Guan Yiran and Liu Xunmei were close friends.

Thus, the only one who needed to be acquainted was the suddenly emerging Liu Qingfeng.

Not far away, a young man in white approached, riding on a child’s back, holding a branch, and shouting, “Giddy up!”

As he got closer, the young man laughed heartily, “I have a little donkey, who never complains of hunger!”

In Qingfeng City, a young woman in red led her horse out of the city, walking into the hills thirty miles outside the city under the night sky.

In the depths of winter, peach blossoms were blooming all along the way.

Li Baoping walked slowly while leading her horse, surveying her surroundings, enjoying the pleasant scenery.

Surrounded by green mountains, white clouds rose continuously from within the mountains.

A bit farther ahead lay her destination for this trip to Qingfeng City, a thatched cottage embraced by green water and wood.

Li Baoping glanced at the sky, where the large round moon hung high—was that not the biggest mooncake?

Thinking of this, Li Baoping suddenly smiled.

It felt as if she had transformed back into that little girl who once walked through green mountains and water with her little master uncle, her mind filled with such thoughts.

But back then, she had also carried a small bamboo box on her back, wearing little straw sandals.

The little girl in her red cotton jacket loved to revolve around her little master uncle, and no matter how far the mountains and roads were, she was never afraid.

Li Baoping’s gaze fell on the snow-white dagger at her waist and the sword-feeding gourd.

Li Baoping stood still.

The face amidst the peach blossoms stood beneath the bright moon.

(End of Chapter)

 **Chapter 768: Who Can Spare the World First?**

Li Baoping led her horse as she searched for someone—a fellow townsman and an elder, a friend of her grandfather's. One claimed to be unbeatable in the chess circles of Fortune and Prosperity Street, while the other touted himself as the top player of Peach Leaf Alley. The two would engage in their matches with utmost seriousness, as if the reputation of their respective neighborhoods was at stake. However, Li Baoping herself had little interest in chess. As for the prowess of her elders in the game, it was hard to say; what was more apparent were their ever-changing excuses for resigning, which were far less amusing than those of Mr. Qi.

Back in the day, the elder's ancestral home was at the very end of Peach Leaf Alley, not far from Fortune and Prosperity Street. Of course, for a little girl in a red cotton jacket, the small town felt like a vast playground with no distant corners. She would go to the Fairy Tomb to catch crickets, visit the Weaver Mother, scour Old Porcelain Mountain for fragments, fish for shrimp and crabs in Dragon Tail Creek, and gaze at the high-hanging mirrors of various households. She would leap down the steps in Dragon Riding Alley, and even from afar, she could smell the sweet aroma of peach blossom cakes and hear the chattering of swallows from a nearby nest.

Every tomorrow of Li Baoping's childhood seemed filled with endless fun and excitement, with each day packed to the brim. This compelled her to run swiftly, her feet moving like the wheels of a cart—never stopping. It felt as if running too fast would leave her childhood behind; as one grew up, childhood remained stationary, and every glance back revealed an ever-increasing distance, becoming more and more blurred.

Suddenly, an elderly man dressed in a high crown and flowing robes emerged from a thatched cottage. With a hearty laugh, he called out, “Baoping!” and hurried to open the gate, his face brimming with delight.

In what felt like just a few blinks, young Baoping had grown so much! Truly, a girl transforms greatly at eighteen, and she had become much more serene than before. 

Was she still that lively little girl who enjoyed climbing walls, twisting her ankles, unsure whether she had caught crabs to take home or if the crabs had simply decided to move in with her? 

Even so, the elder still genuinely cherished this junior. Some children always had a particularly good rapport with their elders. Here, Baoping from Fortune and Prosperity Street and Zhao Yao, who once served as Mr. Qi's attendant, were both among such children.

Li Baoping quickly approached the door, bowing respectfully. Straightening up with a smile, she greeted, “Grandpa Wei.”

The elder, surnamed Wei, named Benyuan, was once the head of the Wei clan, one of the four clans of the town's ten surnames. Before the Ruins of Lijuzhou collapsed, there had been correspondence with the outside world, and the messenger was a clear-eyed young lad in straw sandals. Although Wei Benyuan had only met him once, the memory lingered vividly. Sure enough, that boy from the alley had grown up; it hadn’t been twenty years yet, and he had already built a large enterprise and become Baoping's little master uncle. Such fateful connections were truly remarkable.

Wei Benyuan smiled upon seeing Li Baoping, “No need to tie up the horse; just let it roam free.”

Li Baoping released the reins and gently patted the horse's back, watching as the magnificent steed trotted off towards the creek for a drink.

“Where’s Sister Taoya?” Li Baoping asked.

Wei Benyuan replied, “Unfortunately, she went to the Fox Kingdom some years ago for training. She encountered a stroke of fortune and needs to hone her Dao heart. Once she becomes a Qi practitioner at the Ocean Observation level, I’ll have her accompany you on your travels.”

Li Baoping refrained from expressing any polite refusals; she wasn’t particularly keen on wandering the rivers and lakes with Sister Taoya. Being close to her was enough; she didn’t need constant companionship.

Being a good person didn’t mean being a pushover, nodding in agreement at every turn and never refusing anything. It was challenging to balance caring for oneself while also being considerate of others.

Moreover, Li Baoping had never liked being constrained. Otherwise, she wouldn’t have been the last to arrive at school and the first to leave all those years ago.

Yet this didn’t hinder her respect for Mr. Qi.

The two walked into the courtyard, where stone tables and benches stood resilient against rain and sun—naturally made from celestial materials. The elder opened a small container and began to brew tea. The teaware was mostly porcelain, gleaming brightly; even those unfamiliar with fine craftsmanship would find joy in their beauty. These were some “second-rate” pieces acquired through connections at the kiln supervision office during Wei’s heyday in the town.

Just like Li Baoping's grandfather, who was a rare practitioner of the Dao in their small town, Wei Benyuan was also an early cultivator. However, Li Baoping’s grandfather focused on talismans and had exceptionally high attainments. It was unknown why he had declined the invitation from the Song clan's late emperor and had not become a court worshipper of the Great Li dynasty. In contrast, Wei Benyuan excelled at alchemy and had left his hometown early. The Wei clan's ancestral home remained unoccupied in the town, while the younger generation of Wei had spread out across different places, flourishing in their pursuits. The Wei family was lucky in terms of both fortune and the character and talents of their descendants, producing both scholars and cultivators.

Wei Benyuan had chosen this auspicious location on the outskirts of Clear Wind City, where peach orchards and streams harmonized splendidly, ideal for crafting alchemical furnaces. He hoped to break through the bottleneck of the Golden Core stage. This secluded paradise was a trade with the Xu clan of Clear Wind City; the former emperor had treated the local gentry well, allowing them to purchase the western celestial mountains at a very low price. However, Wei Benyuan found the noise and chaos of that location too bothersome and instead exchanged it for this long-cherished plot of ancestral land. Still, he had refused to become a vassal of the Xu clan, despite the repeated pleas of Xu Hu, the clan leader, and several attempts from the clan's matriarch.

Wei Benyuan felt a sense of concern. Li Baoping’s horse and the white scabbard of the dagger at her waist were both too conspicuous.

Unable to hold back, the elder asked, “Have you encountered any accidents on this trip?”

Before Baoping could respond, he continued in irritation, “That old Li really dares to be so careless! His poor chess skills and half-baked knowledge are bad enough, but now his mind is getting muddled too?”

Li Baoping laughed, “Grandpa Wei, I’m not a child anymore.”

Wei Benyuan replied, “I don't care how old Li is. If anyone bullies you, just tell Grandpa Wei. Although my realm isn’t high, I have enough connections to deal with such matters. Many are what I’ve left behind for my descendants, and I can’t take them to the grave…”

Li Baoping shook her head, “Really, Grandpa Wei, there’s no need for that. I haven’t made any enemies on this journey.”

Wei Benyuan joked, “Have all the suitors gone blind? Can’t they see how beautiful our Baoping has grown?”

Li Baoping sighed, “Grandpa Wei, please show a bit of elderliness.”

Wei Benyuan laughed, “Does my grandson really not see her worth?”

Li Baoping shook her head.

Suddenly, Wei Benyuan burst into laughter, “It would be strange if my Baoping liked that boy!”

Although the elder was never one to wear a stern face, he usually didn’t laugh so heartily with his own descendants.

He paused, having sensed Li Baoping's thoughts. He nodded, responding silently to indicate that there was no need to worry; there were no spies from the Xu clan in this area. The peach orchard itself was protected by a great formation, which even ordinary Golden Core practitioners would find hard to approach without making noise. Even though Xu Hu wasn’t a typical Golden Core practitioner, he possessed considerable strength and was well-versed in offensive techniques, known for his prowess throughout the continent. Thus, there was no need for concern about anyone using great powers to spy on the mountains and rivers.

Only then did Li Baoping take out two blue talismans and hand them to the elder, explaining, “These were sent by my brother from Northern Julu Prefecture. The letter didn’t say much; it only mentioned the names of the two talismans—one is a Golden Core talisman, and the other is a Mud Pill talisman. Originally, Grandpa should have delivered them in person, but since I was heading out, he let me take them along.”

Wei Benyuan accepted the talismans and, upon hearing their names, placed them on the table, shaking his head. “Baoping, although you are also a practitioner, you might not understand just how invaluable these two talismans are. I cannot accept them; doing so would mean I can never repay this favor in my lifetime. In cultivation, having a high realm is a great benefit, but it would make it awkward for me. If I must choose, I’d rather keep my heart than gain a higher realm.”

Wei Benyuan smiled, “It’s my own stubbornness. I appreciate your brother’s good intentions. He is indeed worthy of being the one I taught chess to since childhood; he truly doesn’t mean to be polite. You know what kind of person Grandpa Wei is, don’t you?”

The two blue talismans on the table, the Golden Core talisman, shimmered like a small door to a blessed land with golden light radiating from it, filling the room with a celestial glow.

The Mud Pill talisman featured a lotus symbol, resembling a high altar in a Daoist temple, surrounded by swirling purple qi, exuding an immense aura.

Li Baoping seemed to have anticipated this outcome, smiling, “My brother said that if you don’t accept the two talismans, I shouldn’t come to visit you again. I listen to my brother.”

Wei Benyuan waved his hand.

“Cultivation is serious business, especially regarding fundamentals; it’s not a child’s game, not something to be taken lightly.”

Li Baoping insisted, “I really do listen to my brother.”

Wei Benyuan frowned and asked, “Your brother is out there wandering in another land, and it’s certainly not easy for him. Why would he give away such good fortune?”

Wei Benyuan found it hard to criticize Li Xisheng, who was far away in Northern Julu, and Li Baoping, who was right before him; they were both excellent juniors, and he couldn’t bear to say anything harsh. So he began to scold the old Li again, “Old fool! Truly an old fool! Head filled with glue; no wonder his chess skills are so terrible, and his character is even worse!”

Li Baoping said, “Grandpa Wei, my brother is measured in his actions.”

Wei Benyuan thought for a moment, “I’ll accept them for now. Unless your brother makes it clear to me later, I’ll consider it as Grandpa Wei temporarily holding onto them for him.”

Li Baoping smiled, “That’s not my concern.”

Wei Benyuan reminded her, “Clear Wind City is a place where all sorts of people gather; if you plan to travel to the Fox Kingdom next, I’m truly worried. Smart people can be quite deceptive, so one must be cautious. Yet those who are both foolish and bad are the real troublemakers—they forget loyalty for profit, are swayed by appearances, and rely solely on gambling for success. It’s a chaotic world.”

Li Baoping nodded, “Alright, then let Grandpa Wei accompany me for a while. Otherwise, I fear that going to find Sister Taoya in the Fox Kingdom might bring me trouble.”

Wei Benyuan chuckled wryly, “With you putting it that way, it seems like Grandpa Wei is plotting something.”

Though Taoya was a servant of the Wei clan, Wei Benyuan had always treated her as his own junior. As for Li Baoping, she was even more like a granddaughter than a granddaughter.

Li Baoping laughed but said nothing.

Her grandfather once mentioned that Wei Benyuan’s inability to break through the Golden Core bottleneck was not due to a lack of talent but rather because he was too soft-hearted and kind. For a practitioner, being overly ambitious and seeking the Dao aggressively might not be wise, but being entirely without ambition was even worse.

Wei Benyuan asked, “Care to play a game of chess with me?”

Chess, fishing, and enjoying the reflections of flowers in water were regarded as the three great pleasures of the mountain dwellers, perfect for passing the time in leisure.

Li Baoping politely declined, “Grandpa Wei, you know I’ve never liked playing chess. Just watching you all play back then was already the limit of my patience.”

Wei Benyuan frowned and stood up, looking towards the summit of the green mountains, coldly laughing, “What’s this sneaking around? Can’t you show your face?!”

Had Li Baoping not come, Wei Benyuan might have had a pleasant exchange with the unexpected guest.

At the summit, a figure obscured by swirling clouds and mist looked down at the cottage nestled in the valley, smiling as he said, “The alchemical furnace is just starting up, and the celestial peaches are falling into bloom. Your alchemical skills may not be high, but you certainly know how to pick a place. The Xu clan treats you well, but it’s a pity you’ve chosen to court death, unwilling to even be a nominal worshipper. Ah, humans…”

After intentionally revealing himself to Wei Benyuan, this practitioner appeared nonchalant, exuding confidence, not in the least bit anxious.

His confidence did not stem from simply relying on his cultivation level; he had also meticulously laid down a formation surrounding the entire valley.

Breaking through Wei Benyuan’s mountain and water formation would require unraveling it thread by thread to find the flaw, and then striking with brute force. Once the formation was broken, there would be no more hiding.

Wei Benyuan gestured with his hand, trying to gather the mountain winds and water mists to obscure the stranger’s vision.

Unexpectedly, the practitioner, who spoke in the elegant language of Baoping Prefecture, seemed to possess profound techniques. The clouds that connected with the valley formation dissipated on their own.

Wei Benyuan looked around, realizing the other had some exquisite methods. The water in the creek began to shimmer with a ghostly green light, indicating the presence of hidden treasures.

That shimmering light quickly spread ashore, like a swarm of ants scattering.

Alchemy relies heavily on the balance of water and fire; the reason Wei Benyuan chose this place to forge his alchemical furnace was because of the vital water flow from the innate stream. Without hesitation, he silently recited an incantation, intending to use the technique of flipping the turtle’s back to shatter the water flow at the mountain's base, risking failure in alchemy to disrupt the opponent’s encroachment on the mountain and water formation.

The stranger didn’t care for Wei Benyuan’s clumsy tricks; his own treasured artifacts and unique secret techniques were not something a mere Golden Core practitioner could unravel.

After a moment’s thought, the practitioner worried that Wei Benyuan was trying to stir up some commotion to seek help from Clear Wind City, so he silently recited an incantation. The ghostly light that had come ashore immediately burrowed underground. Wei Benyuan’s “Mountain Flipping” technique couldn’t even stir the creek’s water.

The practitioner laughed, “Your techniques are quite good, but it’s a pity you’ve used them poorly. Once I capture you, I’ll imprison your soul and ask a few questions. What a delightful surprise! Fortune truly has come knocking, and it can’t be stopped.”

As his gaze shifted, he looked at Li Baoping and said, “The little girl’s family background is truly frighteningly rich; I didn’t even dare to act hastily before. I’ve followed you all this way and even helped you deal with two groups of minor cultivators. How do you plan to repay my life-saving grace? If you’re willing to pledge yourself to me as my personal maid, I wouldn’t mind. I’ll take a sword gourd, that auspicious blade, and those two unexpected talismans, and I’ll spare your life.”

Li Baoping patted the small wine gourd at her waist, “Come and take it if you dare. Enough with the nonsense.”

The stranger sneered, “A measly Golden Core who knows nothing of attack, who only knows how to brew some elixirs and make connections. At this critical moment, you can’t protect this little girl.”

Wei Benyuan’s heart sank in shock.

Firstly, he believed that the narrow blade Baoping carried was a treasure of the mountains, unaware of the true nature of the silver gourd. On the contrary, the man at the mountain peak seemed to know exactly what he was dealing with. He even called the narrow blade by its name, having followed Baoping for a while, clearly confident of his footing. This man’s cultivation level was at least at the bottleneck of the Golden Core stage, and if he were a venerable Nascent Soul who had been dormant for countless years, he would be even more formidable.

Wei Benyuan felt a deep regret; if he had agreed to become a vassal of the Xu clan, he would have had the means to signal for help, and perhaps the opponent wouldn’t have dared to be so bold. Yet now, the mountain and water formation that isolated him from the outside world had become a prison.

Taking a deep breath, Wei Benyuan steadied his Dao heart and spoke silently to Li Baoping, “Don’t be afraid, Baoping. Grandpa Wei will definitely protect you as you leave. If I destroy the alchemical furnace, it will create a great commotion, and they’ll surely notice in Clear Wind City. After you leave the Peach Orchard, don’t look back; just head to Clear Wind City. I may not be strong in combat, but with the right timing and location, I can definitely keep you safe.”

The stranger shook his head, “I find that hard to believe. If breaking through the Golden Core bottleneck is this difficult, what’s the point of living?”

Wei Benyuan felt as if he had fallen into an ice cave, knowing that this was definitely a deep-rooted Nascent Soul.

The Great Li cavalry had shattered the mountains and rivers of a continent, leaving many hidden cultivators from the mountains to come out and take advantage of the chaos.

Li Baoping said, “If I had known this would happen, I would have sent the talismans to you earlier.”

Wei Benyuan laughed in anger, “What nonsense are you talking about!”

Li Baoping didn’t explain further, her heart rippling, listening intently; some matters were perhaps best left unspoken.

The practitioner’s attention was still largely fixed on Li Baoping’s narrow blade.

In terms of earthly beauty, it seemed insignificant compared to the pursuit of eternal life. 

That narrow blade, named Auspicious Sign, was a divine artifact from the ancient Shu Kingdom, a national treasure capable of suppressing and gathering martial fortunes. Such a treasure could be classified among the “treasures of mountains and rivers.” Although it had the classification of a magical artifact, it was essentially a semi-divine weapon.

The sword gourd appeared to be of extremely high quality, but its exact nature was hard to determine for now.

In any case, after obtaining the goods, it would be wise to travel to another continent, as the current Baoping Prefecture was no longer a suitable place for wild cultivators to thrive.

Li Baoping whispered, “Grandpa Wei, if a fight breaks out, I can’t afford to lose this place of cultivation. It’s alright; I’ll have my brother compensate you later.”

Wei Benyuan couldn’t help but smile bitterly. Was this really the time for such discussions?

The practitioner had already found the way to break the formation and was cautiously weighing his options, feeling that all unexpected events had been accounted for.

When practitioners from the “Celestial Scribe” sect descended for training, they often liked to pay their respects to the mountain. Since this little girl’s backing was someone like Wei Benyuan, who didn’t even have the qualifications to become a guest in Clear Wind City’s Xu Hu’s court, it was very safe.

It was impossible for a formidable Nascent Soul practitioner not to be cautious.

No matter how high the realm of a wilderness cultivator was, they only had one life.

Those who rested in the halls of their ancestors, enjoying the fruits of their labor, even if their realms were low, had two lives!

Thus, it was a decisive moment to act.

In an instant, the practitioner’s figure shimmered uncertainly, growing as large as a mountain, taking on the form of an ancient mountain spirit. Not only that, but the golden body of the law avatar had green dragon-like arms wrapped around it, wielding a great halberd. The spiritual energy of the surrounding mountains and waters was in complete chaos, and this massive “deity,” embodying the essence of mountains and waters, descended from the peak towards the creek-side cottage, carrying the pressure of a mountain.

In mid-air, the golden body laughed heartily, “You little girl, what a big mouth! Your brother? If you’re trying to scare me with your ancestor, I might believe you a little! What, is your brother a true martial artist from Zhenwu Mountain, or the great swordsman of the Yellow River from Thunderstorm Garden?”

As Wei Benyuan was about to summon a precious Golden Core to fight with the Nascent Soul rogue, Li Baoping took a step forward, her thumb nudging the narrow blade out of its sheath by an inch. In her other sleeve, a different object quietly appeared. This object, once revealed, emitted no trace of aura, making it far less noticeable than the narrow blade.

But at that moment, the golden body of the law avatar inexplicably hovered mid-air, neither ascending nor descending.

It wasn’t as if the little girl had stumbled while jumping from a wall; she hadn’t even landed yet!

Li Baoping turned her head to look elsewhere.

Atop another green mountain peak stood a young man wearing a pink Daoist robe, floating gently in the air, extending two fingers and spinning them lightly.

With each step he took, a white cloud would drift in from the distance, forming steps that landed perfectly beneath the young man's feet.

The enormous law avatar, seemingly immobilized, began to flip, becoming a puppet in someone else’s hands.

Wei Benyuan felt shaken.

What a powerful figure at the mountain peak!

Was there such a person in Baoping Prefecture who possessed such a bearing?

A Taoist High Master? Or was it the Heavenly Sovereign of the Divine Script Sect, Qi Zhen? It was impossible; that lineage of Daoists had strict rules; their hats and robes could not have a single flaw.

Moreover, how could the esteemed Qi lord come to Clear Wind City for a stroll?

The young man’s brightly colored robe billowed as if made of clouds.

Finally, the young “Daoist” lightly leaped, sitting cross-legged upon the head of the golden body law avatar. His fingers curled, giving a soft tap, much like an elder admonishing a mischievous younger relative, “You like to act all high and mighty, huh? Your ancestor is right here, what a laugh.”

Wei Benyuan felt no sense of relief; instead, he grew increasingly anxious, fearing this was a conflict between tigers and wolves. If the latter harbored ill intentions, he wouldn’t be able to protect Baoping.

Wei Benyuan murmured, “Just casually severing the connection between heaven and earth, how am I going to deal with this? What should I do?”

The Nascent Soul rogue, rendered mute by the sudden turn of events, lamented internally. It wasn't that he didn’t want to escape, but he truly couldn’t move. The other party had casually created a barrier isolating the golden body law avatar, making it impossible to use either his Golden Core or Nascent Soul techniques to escape. How would he find a way out of this deadlock? Unless he was a sword cultivator of the Nascent Soul stage, but if he were such a sword immortal, would he need to hide and seek for hundreds of years?

The young Daoist casually sat atop the towering law avatar, smiling at Wei Benyuan, “Wei Benyuan, I owe your Wei family a favor from a long time ago. I won’t go into details; old stories are just dust, no need to dwell on them.”

Of course, Liu Chicheng was fabricating a story.

He had no choice; Gu Can didn’t want to reveal his identity, so Liu Chicheng had to come up with a flimsy excuse. However, mountain practitioners were generally gullible, and it was very believable.

For example, Wei Benyuan believed him to some extent.

Li Baoping, however, did not buy it at all.

Liu Chicheng tilted his head, continuing to restrain the golden body law avatar. A mere junior Nascent Soul practitioner could easily break free from this gentle restraint; he just didn’t dare to act impulsively.

This was correct.

After traveling with Gu Can, he had grown tired of the dullness. 

Thus, Liu Chicheng felt he lacked a companion to alleviate his boredom, and having a junior Nascent Soul practitioner from the mountains accompany him was a meager consolation.

If Liu Chicheng’s most despised “Celestial Scribe” practitioner were here, he would already be dead.

Attacking the young would lead to confronting the old? How old? Should he wrestle with someone from Baidi City? No matter how formidable a cultivator was, Liu Chicheng would stand still; his opponent wouldn’t dare to act.

In any case, he would be heading to the Central Divine Continent soon, and he didn’t want to leave behind any mess. Liu Chicheng was concerned that Gu Can wouldn’t focus on his cultivation.

Gu Can was a promising seedling; only by facing life-and-death situations repeatedly could he grow quickly.

He was not afraid of “pulling seedlings to encourage growth.”

This was exactly what Liu Chicheng’s brother most favored—promising talents.

Suddenly, Liu Chicheng squinted.

It seemed that his brother had a penchant for trouble?

And this little girl?

Moreover, his brother’s chess skills appeared to have hit a bottleneck, nearing a breakthrough. Just as he was preparing to return to Baidi City, he happened to encounter her. Wasn’t that fortuitous?

Liu Chicheng laughed heartily, turning his gaze towards a certain direction, speaking silently, “It’s not up to you anymore. Perfect, the three of us will head back together.”

Gu Can ceased hiding his figure, replying silently, “Liu Chicheng, I advise you not to do this; otherwise, once I succeed in my studies in Baidi City, you’ll be the first I kill.”

There was no impatience in Gu Can’s tone; his response was measured, just as he was in character.

Liu Chicheng smiled, “Am I afraid of you? I might fear you in the future, but that’s a matter for later.”

Li Baoping, sensing the tension, loosened the scabbard and tightened her grip on the peach talisman.

This was given to her by her brother, saying that in times of trouble, with a thought, the talisman would resonate. Even if a nefarious person had some skills, she wouldn’t need to worry if her heart remained calm.

Li Baoping shook the peach talisman vigorously.

Was her brother lying?

No response.

Li Baoping exhaled and rubbed her palm, yet still, no reaction.

Never mind.

Li Baoping planned to pull out a few sheets of paper from her sleeve, all copied from various texts, ones that resonated with her.

She didn’t blame her brother, Li Xisheng, but she felt a bit miffed that her little master uncle wasn’t around.

Li Baoping subtly wrinkled her nose.

Forget it, what else could she do? Tomorrow, she would no longer hold such feelings for her little master uncle.

Gu Can made no movement.

It wasn’t that he didn’t want to intervene; it was simply meaningless.

The disparity in their realms was too great.

Gu Can felt a surge of anger within.

This unpredictable Liu Chicheng must die at his hands in the future.

So, Gu Can immediately communicated with Li Baoping, “Li Baoping, I am Gu Can from Mud Bottle Alley. Don’t act impulsively; just stay alive.”

Li Baoping shook her head, “I don’t want to die, but I will not live in disgrace.”

Then she smiled, “Isn’t it allowed for others to err in good intentions? Besides, it’s not a major issue. Gu Can, I must thank you. Stay safe, and remember to tell my little master uncle that I miss him dearly.”

Liu Chicheng glanced at the paper in her hand, noticing the characters flowing on it!

His brows furrowed, and his expression grew serious.

If it was related to the Academic Scribe, it could be troublesome.

After all, the entire Haoran world was a realm of scholars.

On the other side of the peach orchard, a scholar in a Confucian robe had initially chuckled at Li Baoping shaking the peach talisman. 

It was rare to see the little girl looking so innocent and adorable.

At this moment, he took a deep breath, stepping forward to Li Baoping's side, looking up at the golden body law avatar and the pink-robed Daoist.

Li Baoping exclaimed, “Brother?!”

Li Xisheng nodded, turning to smile, “Your brother is angry and doesn’t want to talk much.”

Li Baoping laughed, “My brother can get angry too?”

Li Xisheng smiled and nodded.

Liu Chicheng had an immediate sense of foreboding.

Yet, this young scholar didn’t appear to have a high realm. He didn’t seem to be using any tricks, so he definitely wasn’t a celestial being, nor was he at the Ascension stage… Liu Chicheng wasn't delusional.

Since leaving Baidi City, he had faced two significant setbacks in a thousand years; one was being personally suppressed by the Grand Celestial Master, and he didn’t even need that figure to summon any seals or draw swords—just pure technique would suffice. 

The reason the Grand Celestial Master acted personally was to signal to Baidi City and prevent Liu Chicheng’s brother from intervening.

The second time was in a small decrepit temple, where he inexplicably received a strike from a sword, a simple wooden sword that effortlessly broke through Liu Chicheng’s protective formation.

In an instant.

Liu Chicheng’s instincts were solidified.

Time stood still.

Outside his little world, a larger realm appeared.

Li Baoping, Wei Benyuan, the golden body law avatar, and Gu Can on the mountain peak—all thoughts ceased to move.

Except for Liu Chicheng, who had been intentionally left unrestrained.

In this tranquil moment, with the heavens high and the earth broad, millions of miles spread out.

Liu Chicheng felt helpless.

It seemed there was no way to fight back.

Clearly, he was up against an unreasonable opponent.

“Cultivators should always respect the heavens and maintain a sense of conscience,” Li Xisheng said slowly as he approached, “That’s enough; this is the view of a scholar.”

Liu Chicheng laughed, “Alright, alright, let’s discuss reason. I’m someone who listens well to scholars’ reasoning.”

Li Xisheng continued, “Now, I will speak to you from the perspective of Baoping’s older brother.”

Liu Chicheng was about to distance himself from the scene, using his little world to collide with the larger one to escape.

As for the matter of realms and the dignity of a Nascent Soul cultivator, he tossed it aside; it didn’t matter whether he picked it up or left it.

Suddenly, a middle-aged Daoist’s law avatar appeared between heaven and earth.

Liu Chicheng’s legs softened, and just as he was about to rise, he sat back down.

He struggled to suppress the almost shattered Dao heart, swaying unsteadily as he stood, bowing in silence.

Li Xisheng asked, “What good is an apology if you disregard the principles of the Dao?”

The towering middle-aged Daoist raised an arm and brought it down.

With one slap, he sent both Liu Chicheng and the Nascent Soul rogue’s law avatar crashing into the earth.

No technique, no divine artifact; the law avatar descended with just a single slap.

Liu Chicheng lay in the pit, his mind racing with a single thought: could the scholars of Baoping Prefecture please stop this?

As Li Xisheng withdrew his law avatar and approached the pit, looking down at the nearly lifeless pink-robed Daoist, he calculated with his fingers, sneering, “When you return to Baidi City, tell your brother I’ll come to play chess with him.”

Liu Chicheng felt despondent.

His brother had once jokingly mentioned that the art of chess was enough to prevent Baidi City from ever raising the banner declaring “First in the World to Spare” again. 

While Cui Zhan had a chance, it was slim, for that person wasn’t in the Haoran world but in the Azure Sky’s Baiyu Capital.

That was the second disciple of the Dao Ancestor, Lu Chen, the eldest disciple of the Master.

What kind of Daoist would he be, one could only imagine.

Liu Chicheng struggled to rise again, remaining silent. He was sincerely respectful, bowing properly in a traditional Daoist fashion.

Once Li Baoping “came back to her senses,” her brother Li Xisheng still stood beside her, and the pink-robed Daoist remained perched atop the golden body law avatar.

Everything was as it had been.

Liu Chicheng appeared to smile, yet he was drenched in cold sweat.

Time flowed backward!

Crucially, Wei Benyuan remained frozen at a certain point in the river of time, still motionless.

“Earlier, I spoke with that esteemed figure; everything is fine now,” Li Xisheng said softly, smiling. “This time I came, let’s not mention it to Grandpa Wei, or he’ll insist I play chess. Back in our hometown, there were only a few chess manuals, and Grandpa Wei’s constant ramblings about chess theory can be quite annoying.”

Li Baoping nodded earnestly.

Li Xisheng’s figure dissipated, returning to the remote vassal state in Northern Julu Prefecture.

Such intercontinental travel, given his current realm, was not easy.

Thus, swift come and go was necessary.

Li Xisheng suddenly smiled, “You’ve grown up without saying hello to your older brother.”

Li Baoping grinned widely.

Li Xisheng shook his head with a smile and vanished.

Wei Benyuan returned to his usual state.

Then Liu Chicheng immediately stood up, preparing to take his leave, claiming he was merely joking with the little girl.

As for the Nascent Soul practitioner beneath him, he had already retracted his law avatar, leaving alongside Liu Chicheng, who communicated silently with Gu Can, “I’ll be waiting for you in Clear Wind City. No rush; you go ahead and catch up.”

Gu Can stifled his doubts, riding the wind towards the thatched cottage, directly addressing Li Baoping, “Li Baoping, I’m sorry for today’s events. In terms of heart and matter, I bear half the blame.”

Li Baoping was taken aback.

This side of Gu Can made it hard to understand why her little master uncle had been so heartbroken back then.

Had Gu Can changed so much in just a few short years?

Li Baoping thought for a moment and told Wei Benyuan she would take a walk by the creek with this fellow townsman.

Wei Benyuan, still in the dark, nodded, “Be careful.”

Li Baoping walked alongside Gu Can by the creek.

The two had only crossed paths in their childhood but had never spoken.

One was lively, the other quiet. They barely acknowledged each other when they met in their hometown, merely passing by.

At most, the red cotton jacket girl would vaguely remember the small boy with a runny nose.

The small-nosed child thought the little girl in red seemed nothing like a wealthy child, as she didn't appear to enjoy the comforts of life.

These two were arguably the naughtiest children in the town, differing only by their backgrounds—one was born on Fortune and Prosperity Street, while the other in Mud Bottle Alley.

The girl in the red jacket dashed through streets and alleys, leaving even the geese in her wake.

The small-nosed boy, however, preferred to stay put under the sun, fishing for eels by the old locust tree, or sitting beneath it, shooting at yellow sparrows with a slingshot.

Gu Can’s family owned a few tea fields, and as a small child, he carried a bamboo basket that fit him well. He would pick tea leaves faster than those helping out, but he didn’t enjoy such work, flattening the tea leaves in his basket and then sneaking off to a shaded spot to rest.

After all, Liu Xianyang was his only friend; how could he not want to enjoy himself?

Yet it was still only the small-nosed boy from Mud Bottle Alley who was his only true kin in this world.

The creek was shallow, crystal clear.

The two remained silent for a long time.

Li Baoping finally spoke, “You should think more about the hardships of my little master uncle.”

Gu Can responded, “I’ve thought about it.”

Li Baoping smiled, “Don’t misunderstand; regarding you and the matters of the Book Simplifying Lake, my little master uncle hasn’t said much. He usually doesn’t like to speak ill of others behind their backs.”

Gu Can chuckled.

Of course, he wouldn’t misinterpret it.

Moreover, what good would it do to discuss it? Gu Can had never liked suffering, yet he was quite adept at enduring scoldings and beatings.

Deep down, Gu Can didn’t care at all about others' opinions.
