Even Chen Ping’an didn’t know that Gu Can had visited Fortune and Prosperity Street and Peach Leaf Alley before him. He had heard Liu Xianyang mention that there were many wealthy people there, and that their pockets were often so full that they dropped coins on the ground. Gu Can had gone to pick up coins, but after failing to find any, he had lost patience, feeling quite angry when he caused a ruckus in Peach Leaf Alley, not letting a single peach tree escape his grasp. Whenever he encountered passersby, he would pretend to squat under the tree to watch ants.

Now reflecting on it, Gu Can thought those fallen peach blossoms, leaves, and branches should have been gathered and hidden away.

Li Baoping continued, “But since my little master uncle is so familiar with you, if you ever achieve even the slightest success, he wouldn’t hesitate to praise you a few times. The first time my little master uncle traveled far, almost all his discussions about our hometown revolved around you and Liu Xianyang. However, after returning from Book Simplifying Lake, he seldom mentioned you again.”

Li Baoping raised her hand, pointing to her eyes, “Here is where one speaks the most truth. My little master uncle didn’t say anything, yet he said everything.”

Gu Can responded with a quiet “Mm.”

Li Baoping said, “That’s it for our conversation.”

Gu Can didn’t linger, preparing to take his leave. He suddenly stopped, smiling, “Li Baoping, thank you.”

Li Baoping laughed and asked, “Now you remember to be polite?”

Gu Can’s eyes sparkled as he shook his head, “Not politeness; it’s because you were the first to accompany him out of his hometown. Without you by his side back then, he perhaps wouldn’t have reached Gu Can’s side later.”

Li Baoping laughed.

Gu Can laughed too.

Recalling the past, in that little temple filled with names on the walls, Liu Xianyang stood on a ladder while Chen Ping’an held it steady. Gu Can had tossed bits of charcoal to Liu Xianyang, writing their three names.

The positioning was quite elevated.

Finally, Gu Can said, “Li Baoping, you should see Chen Ping’an sooner than I will. When you do, tell him that Gu Can is in Baidi City, cultivating the Dao!” 

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 769: Young Zhu Lian

Outside Clear Wind City, on a small hill in a desolate area, beneath a solitary wild peach tree, two figures stared at each other, eyes wide open.

Liu Chicheng glared fiercely, not wasting any time to wipe the blood off his face.

The pink robe he wore was as vibrant as the peach blossoms. 

The Yuan Ying wild cultivator, who had been captured and brought here, revealed his true appearance—a short “youth” with hair as white as snow, his face showing signs of age.

What was peculiar, however, was the long string of ancient jade pendants and small bottles hanging from the white jade belt adorned with a dragon pattern around his waist.

This man swayed precariously, still doing his utmost to maintain his stance, fearing that with a mere tilt of his head, the man in the pink robe in front of him would slap him to death.

At this moment, he felt like a person about to indulge in a feast of rich dishes when suddenly the table was overturned, leaving him with no chopsticks and a head full of bumps from the falling table.

Until now, he still couldn't comprehend how he had fallen from the peak of the Yuan Ying realm to the pitiful state of just finishing his Golden Core stage.

What puzzled him even more was the remarkable skills of the man before him, who seemed to be injured as well. But the question lingered—had he even struck first?

He had once been a formidable figure, a hidden emperor behind several small nations, known for seeking treasures while concealing his identity. His reputation was not small throughout the entire Baoping Continent. He had clashed with Li Tuanjing from Thunder Garden, taking a few strikes yet miraculously surviving, and was pursued for miles by an old immortal from the Divine Scripture Sect without meeting his end. In his early years, he had been both an enemy and a friend to Liu Laocheng at Book Scroll Lake, having explored the secret realms of the ancient Shu Kingdom together, where he had suffered greatly due to an unequal division of spoils, almost losing half his life to Liu Laocheng. Even after Liu Laocheng ascended in status, he had still managed to ambush and kill several direct disciples of the Palace of Willow Island who had ventured out, leaving Liu Laocheng unable to find him, leading to his eventual retreat.

His life had been filled with excitement and bizarre experiences, but nothing could compare to the utter confusion he felt today. Who was this person? How had he attacked? Why had he come here? Would he die here today...?

Liu Chicheng shook off the blood on his hands and smiled, “Thank you.”

The “youth,” a wild cultivator of the mountains and rivers, seeing Liu Chicheng as a Daoist immortal, respectfully bowed and said softly, “I am Chai Bofu, with the Dao name Longbo. I believe you have heard of me.”

“An extraordinary figure, known for his assassination skills and escape techniques, who is also proficient in water techniques,” he thought. It was rumored that he had once fought with Liu Zhimao of Book Scroll Lake over a heavenly secret manual, their battle so fierce it nearly turned their brains to mush.

Liu Chicheng gritted his teeth and replied, “I’ve heard of your grand uncle. I am Liu Chicheng, a person of the White Water Kingdom. Have you heard of me?”

Chai Bofu braced himself and said, “I am but a shallow person; I have not heard of your esteemed name.”

Liu Chicheng fell back against the peach tree, his expression despondent. “Finding chicken droppings in a crevice and digging up dog feces next to rotten mud—after struggling to accumulate a bit of cultivation, I get slapped and it’s all gone! I don’t want to live anymore. Just kill me!”

Chai Bofu remained completely still, not pretending to be frightened, nor would he utter any heartfelt words. When dealing with high-level cultivators who were also reclusive, the most unwise thing to do was to act clever and overstep boundaries.

Liu Chicheng began to close his eyes to rest, repeatedly bumping his head against the peach tree, muttering, “Cut down the peach tree, spoil the scenery.”

Then, Liu Chicheng suddenly slapped himself hard across the face, as if waking up. His face broke into a smile. “I should be happy! Who in this world can survive such a calamity as I have? There must be blessings ahead, surely great fortune awaits!”

Liu Chicheng stood up, transforming from listlessness to vigor in an instant, straightening his back, shaking his sleeves, and producing three incense sticks. He then looked at the foolishly standing wild cultivator and glared, “Why aren’t you leaving? You’re wasting my time to burn incense and pray to the immortals!”

Liu Chicheng took a deep breath. “No, no, I must be kind to others, treat people with courtesy, and uphold the principles of a scholar.”

Chai Bofu stepped back, daring to stand firm only when he was a good twenty feet away.

There was no sense of grievance here; a wild cultivator from the mountains who could reach Chai Bofu’s level certainly had some cunning.

Li Tuanjing from Thunder Garden had once laughed, saying the deepest cultivators in the world were not the renowned immortal masters, but the wild cultivators, who had no choice but to resort to unconventional methods, otherwise, the Dao would be within reach.

Liu Chicheng gathered his thoughts, dispelled distractions, began to chant, and then rubbed the incense head slowly until it caught fire, seemingly performing three bows to heaven and earth.

In reality, the first bow was to the ancestors of the White Emperor City who had imparted teachings unto him.

The second bow was to the scholar in green robes from the ancient temple who had once presented a sword, his swordsmanship exceptional and his righteous aura unparalleled.

The third bow was to that imposing “middle-aged Daoist.”

Gu Can, cautious and meticulous, while riding the wind, noticed Liu Chicheng’s presence, which he had not deliberately concealed. He landed near the wild peach tree, and only after Liu Chicheng finished his three bows did he say, “What if? Why bother?”

Liu Chicheng remained silent, waiting until the incense had nearly burned out before he resumed his usual demeanor, smiling broadly. “Alright, alright, don’t rub salt into my wounds! My heart aches at the moment.”

Gu Can didn’t even spare a glance at the wild cultivator, but his next words revealed his true feelings, “What’s he keeping around for?”

Liu Chicheng asked with a grin, “Gu Can, do you wish to be my junior brother or my nephew?”

Gu Can replied, “It’s not for me to choose. Why ask?”

In these years, if a stranger met Gu Can for the first time, they would find him a gentle, courteous scholar, a well-mannered young man.

However, after traveling together with Liu Chicheng on their northern journey, they both knew each other's true nature very well.

When Gu Can said he bore no grudge for today, it was an insult to Liu Chicheng.

Gu Can spoke bluntly, “You once said that Mr. Qi had greatly benefited you, imparting you a piece of golden advice that cleared your path and broke down barriers, allowing you to smoothly ascend to the fifth realm. You have made a promise to Mr. Qi that when Chen Ping’an visits White Emperor City, you will owe him a favor, so you must act with kindness. Now weigh the consequences of your actions. What you did today is nothing but ungratefulness and creating enmity with me. Liu Chicheng, you truly live up to the reputation of a high figure from White Emperor City, acting as you please. I am increasingly looking forward to White Emperor City; this might be the only right thing you did today.”

Gu Can didn’t use secret words to communicate with Liu Chicheng.

Liu Chicheng glanced at the wild cultivator Chai Bofu, then withdrew his gaze, helplessly saying, “Is it that you want Brother Longbo to die so badly?”

Gu Can remained silent.

Liu Chicheng, patient, explained, “First, yesterday’s matters belong to yesterday, and tomorrow’s matters belong to tomorrow. For example, if Chen Ping’an wants to argue with me later, I’ll bring up my senior brother, and Chen Ping’an will die. Then I’ll use Mr. Qi’s kindness as leverage, essentially saving Chen Ping’an’s life and thus repaying a favor.”

“Second, regardless of current outcomes, my initial thought was simple: creating enmity with you, compared to helping my senior brother find another path of ascension, Gu Can, think for yourself, if you were me, what would you choose?”

“Lastly, I respect and fear my senior brother, but I cherish and long for White Emperor City. I don’t want it to merely be a stepping stone. Someone needs to appear to provide my senior brother with a reason to convince himself.”

Gu Can understood everything Liu Chicheng said, except for that last sentence.

No matter how twisted or convoluted Liu Chicheng’s reasoning seemed to Gu Can, it was evident that Liu Chicheng genuinely believed in his reasoning, speaking from the heart.

Gu Can could choose not to agree, but he had to present his own “reason,” whether through fists, Dao methods, or words.

Ultimately, Liu Chicheng always looked down upon Gu Can, his thoughts and vision reaching the highest point of White Emperor City, to the seniors, as well as to others of the same generation.

Liu Chicheng wished to take on disciples on behalf of his master, but his greatest enemies, or obstacles, were those same peers.

Chai Bofu felt a chill run down his spine; in the path of cultivation, after experiencing numerous hardships, he felt despair for the first time in his life.

The three words “White Emperor City” pressed down on him like a mountain, suffocating him.

In the world of nine continents, among countless wild cultivators, there was only one sacred ground in their hearts—the White Emperor City of the Central Region, presided over by the universally recognized foremost figure of the demonic path.

Yet here was this pink-robed Daoist, conversing with a young man, each sentence filled with references to White Emperor City, senior brothers, and junior brothers.

So, when the two fell silent, Chai Bofu finally spoke, “Senior Liu, Gu Can, how can I avoid death?”

The one truly asking was the youth with a low cultivation level.

Since Liu Chicheng had detained him here, his life was at least secure. However, Gu Can had enmity with him, both old and new.

Chai Bofu had heard of Gu Can primarily because of Liu Zhimao, the River Crossing True Lord. It was rumored that a few years back, Gu Can, as Liu Zhimao’s direct disciple, had a Yuan Ying water dragon, wreaking havoc at Book Scroll Lake. Then for reasons unknown, he suddenly went silent, losing both the water dragon and himself. Afterward, the entire Book Scroll Lake was occupied by foreign cultivators, becoming a territory of the Yuguizong of Tongyezhou. Those who were bold had likely been fed to the True Realm Sect, realizing the trend, as if taking a divine bath in Book Scroll Lake, washing away all the dirt of wild cultivators, transforming into proper disciples of sects.

Chai Bofu felt that his luck had hit rock bottom.

How had he encountered this little demon? How had Gu Can gotten tangled up with a river-crossing dragon like Liu Chicheng, connected to White Emperor City?

Liu Chicheng pointed at Gu Can. “For matters of life and death, ask my future little junior brother.”

The higher Gu Can’s Dao achievements, the smoother Liu Chicheng’s return to White Emperor City would be.

Gu Can said, “If you die, then you needn’t worry about dying.”

Liu Chicheng let out an incredulous laugh.

That statement was quite novel.

Chai Bofu spoke somberly, “Gu Can, why are you being so aggressive? Are you intent on killing me? Even if I have past grievances with your master, you are a wild cultivator, and so am I. This grudge means nothing.”

Liu Chicheng playfully asked, “Brother Longbo, what about you and Liu Zhimao?”

Chai Bofu replied, “It was over a secret text regarding the River Crossing…”

At this point, Chai Bofu suddenly realized, “Gu Can, could it be that Liu Zhimao truly regards you as someone to inherit his legacy? Has he learned that text and fears that my presence will disrupt your fortune?”

Chai Bofu muttered to himself, “Liu Zhimao is the most petty and narrow-minded; he would gladly eliminate all fellow cultivators in the world. How could he be willing to pass on the fundamental method of the Dao to you?”

Gu Can naturally would not expose the truth; Liu Zhimao had had little control over breaking through during his seclusion and could very well meet his end. Otherwise, why would he have passed the water technique to Gu Can, who would then attract the genuine owner of the technique, Liu Chicheng?

After being schemed against by Cui Chen, Liu Chicheng had once taken in a named disciple, a boy who had been a disciple of the old demon Mi, named Yuan Tiandi. Unfortunately, Liu Chicheng had invested some effort but had not achieved satisfactory results and felt embarrassed to keep him by his side. He left him on a small hill, allowing the boy to fend for himself, accompanied only by a little fox spirit. When Liu Chicheng parted from them, he didn’t give any aid to his named disciple, but instead, he gifted that little fox spirit a cultivation method and two protective artifacts. However, it was likely that her future cultivation would be lacking in diligence, and as for whether Yuan Tiandi could learn anything from her or what enmities might arise between them, Liu Chicheng cared little. The path of cultivation ultimately depended on destiny.

Liu Chicheng didn’t mind being the wild man of beautiful women but was unwilling to become anyone’s wild father. His past assistance to that little fox spirit wasn’t out of pity for her circumstances but rather a reflection of his own compassion.

After parting with Yuan Tiandi, Liu Chicheng wandered alone, not expecting that his River Crossing secret text would end up in the hands of wild cultivator Liu Zhimao, who had made quite a name for himself, earning the title of River Crossing True Lord.

In life, there were always times when one sowed flowers and got no blooms, while one could inadvertently plant willows to create a shade.

Gu Can glanced at Chai Bofu, suddenly smiling. “Forget it. In the future, let’s walk the Dao together and exchange techniques.”

Since Liu Chicheng didn’t want to kill anyone, and Gu Can was uncertain of his own abilities, he might as well keep Chai Bofu around.

Liu Chicheng didn’t think much of Chai Bofu’s level. Even if he returned to the Yuan Ying realm, what would it matter? Even if he became Liu Chicheng’s servant in White Emperor City, what significance would it hold? The cultivation in White Emperor City was not like what one would find in ordinary sects, where they depended on mutual support and ties.

The real reason Liu Chicheng spared this person was that he hoped his senior brother could exploit the relationship between Chai Bofu and Li Baoping to his advantage, helping his senior brother strategize against that “middle-aged Daoist.” Even if White Emperor City gained just a sliver of a chance to win, it would be a tremendous boon.

Liu Chicheng believed his little scheme had probably already been calculated by that “middle-aged Daoist.” No worries; when the time came, it would all be a headache for his senior brother.

Junior brothers had their duties, and senior brothers had their strategies.

The three of them then walked towards Clear Wind City without using wind for travel.

Liu Chicheng casually remarked, “Brother Longbo, your six life-bound items are rather flamboyant. Two of them are merely ranked as spiritual artifacts. What’s going on?”

Chai Bofu smiled bitterly. “For wild cultivators, starting out is the hardest. Among the wild cultivators of the lower five realms, having even one or two spiritual artifacts successfully refined as life-bound items is already a great fortune. Once my realm is sufficient and I have enough magical treasures, then I might consider forcibly replacing these deeply rooted life-bound items that are tied to my life. It can be done, but it’s too risky, especially if my enemies learn of it. Such seclusion isn’t just courting death. Even if I survive, if those gluttonous sect disciples catch wind, secretly coming at me, breaking my retreat, it would be a heavy loss.”

Chai Bofu sighed. “Before forming the Golden Core, if I provoke a low-level enemy, replacing life-bound items wouldn’t be a problem. Unfortunately, wild cultivators can only form a core after attracting the attention of some Golden Core peers and some sect disciples who cry out for help after being beaten. Sometimes, when I look around, I truly feel surrounded by troubles and enemies.”

When immortal sects “visit,” whether seeking revenge or visiting relatives, it’s not like being a common folk traveling a hundred miles away; no matter how vast the continent, once it comes to discussing establishing a sect, it feels small. In places with a bit better aura, there are local tyrants everywhere, and the mountains and rivers, deep waters and lakes—who isn’t occupied and managed by an immortal sect? Not to mention the sects of the immortal world, or the mountain gods and river deities. The reason wild cultivators find it hard to gain a foothold is that they lack advantages in timing, geography, and support.

Liu Chicheng nodded, indicating understanding.

Gu Can smiled slightly.

Chai Bofu, lost in thought, was suddenly seized by Liu Chicheng, his head pressed down, as the Golden Core was casually shattered. He collapsed to the ground, covered in blood, convulsing.

Earlier, when he fell from the Yuan Ying realm to the Golden Core, it was too abstract, and Chai Bofu hadn’t suffered too much. This time, falling from the Golden Core to the Dragon Gate realm was a genuine trial by fire.

Liu Chicheng grinned. “Alright, now you can safely replace your life-bound items, or else you’ll find it hard to break through that Yuan Ying bottleneck. Brother Longbo, don’t thank me.”

Liu Chicheng spun a finger, casually forming a formation to help Chai Bofu conceal his aura.

The techniques transmitted from White Emperor City were eclectic. Liu Chicheng once had a talented senior sister who had vowed to learn all twelve kinds of Dao techniques before she would stop.

However, every century, her complexion would grow worse, and eventually, she became the most irritable person in White Emperor City.

Chai Bofu sat cross-legged, his inner world in chaos. Today, with the Yuan Ying and Golden Core disappearing and shattering one after another, there was no need to discuss the damage to the foundations of the Dao; he needed to survive first before worrying about anything else.

Gu Can squatted beside Chai Bofu and asked, “I’m curious, why didn’t you pretend to be Xu Hun? Don’t you have any thoughts of framing him? How does one become a wild cultivator? What’s the hidden story here?”

Gu Can pressed down on Chai Bofu’s head. “You practice water techniques, and I happen to have the River Crossing secret text. If I take this opportunity to intercept your life-bound essence and water fortune, and refine your Golden Core fragments, it would be a perfect boon for my cultivation. Now, speak! What shady connections do you have with Clear Wind City or the Fox Kingdom that made you attempt murder and treasure theft so brazenly?”

The youthful Chai Bofu’s face turned pale as he recalled his once white hair, which, although aged, had been shining with vitality, a sign of life. Now, most of his hair showed signs of withering. With just Gu Can pressing down on his head, strands of hair fell away, turning to ashes before they even touched the ground.

Gu Can increased the force he was applying, using one of the foundational techniques of the River Crossing secret text to begin forcefully extracting Chai Bofu’s water fortune. Chai Bofu's inner world, already in disarray, was like a flood pouring in; Gu Can’s methods were like drilling a large hole in a collapsing dam, taking only the water fortune while letting the flood rush in, collecting it in his own pocket. As for whether that flood would burst through all the defenses, ruining Chai Bofu’s path of cultivation and whether he would have any chance to return to the Golden Core or Yuan Ying realms, Gu Can didn’t care in the slightest.

Chai Bofu immediately began to spill the beans. “I was once a fellow disciple of Xu Hun’s wife, back when we were both in the same sect! So, I wanted to deal a heavy blow to Xu Hun, the lord of the city, while not wanting to put Clear Wind City in danger, leaving Xu Hun without a chance to plead his case. If that young girl suffers here, Xu Hun, as the lord of the city, would be at fault for not offering protection and would bear the brunt of the blame. However, if I were to impersonate Xu Hun and steal treasures, then intentionally leave behind either the young girl or half of Wei Benyuan’s life, it would ruin the great prospects of the Xu family’s heir in Clear Wind City. I didn’t wish for my senior sister’s efforts to go to waste…”

When mentioning that senior sister, Chai Bofu’s emotions became complex, his expression reflecting a deep sense of regret.

Liu Chicheng chuckled. “Love-struck, indeed! I like it; no wonder I hit it off with Brother Longbo at first sight, not wanting to kill you.”

Gu Can pondered for a moment, then asked with a smile, “What about Xu Hun’s son?”

Chai Bofu snapped, “Xu Hun isn’t an idiot; why would he help me raise a son? My relationship with my senior sister is entirely innocent. Don’t you dare slander me!”

Only then did Gu Can withdraw his hand, saying, “What a shame.”

Gu Can suddenly extended his hand again, continuing to intercept water fortune and extract Golden Core fragments, and asked, “Do you not consider Xu Hun an idiot but think of me as a fool? Tell me, is your senior sister at a higher realm than you, or does she hold some leverage over you? Otherwise, with your genuine feelings, it doesn’t add up. Wild cultivators have their reasons for breaking the mold; since that child isn’t your son, your justification is lacking. Love between men and women? If you truly care, with Clear Wind City facing disaster, as it collapses, if Xu Hun were to seize your senior sister, would you not steal his wife and child? Could you really not do that?”

Chai Bofu opened his eyes, seemingly trying to see the young man’s face more clearly, smiling bitterly. “Although I’m a wild cultivator, I’ve never thought of myself as a naturally born wild cultivator. Gu Can, you’re quite the character!”

Chai Bofu paused for a moment. “My senior sister has always been deeply calculating. After we joined forces to kill our master, before she married into the Xu family of Clear Wind City, I only knew she had another sect’s inheritance, which was extremely obscure. I always feared her and never dared to provoke her.”

Gu Can turned to look at Liu Chicheng and smiled. “I have a low realm; it doesn’t matter if I’m seen as a fool. What about you? Do you still think this Brother Longbo is love-struck?”

Liu Chicheng chuckled. “It’s fine; I’m just a fool.”

Only then did Gu Can withdraw his hand and stand up, gazing toward Clear Wind City, which held great potential to become a major sect.

Chai Bofu felt his heart turn to ash. After being toyed with by Gu Can, he was now struggling even to maintain his current state in the Dragon Gate realm.

Gu Can said, “Let’s not go to Clear Wind City. We’ll head straight back to the small town.”

Liu Chicheng laughed. “As you wish.”

Gu Can added, “When we get to my hometown, I suggest you tread carefully.”

Liu Chicheng’s expression darkened.

Back then, Chen Ping’an, Qi Jingchun, and today, Li Baoping and Li Xisheng. 

Along with the person beside him, who was so eager to conceal his murderous thoughts, Gu Can was said to have teamed up with Ma Ku Xuan of Zhenwu Mountain and the young feudal lord Song Mu of Dali…

They all hailed from that small place.

Liu Chicheng immediately changed his mind, saying, “Let’s head north first. Brother Longbo and I will wait for you at the border of Lijuzhou. We won’t accompany you to the small town.”

Gu Can chuckled. “As long as you keep it low-key, there’s really no need to be so cautious.”

Liu Chicheng spoke heavily, “What if? Why bother?”

Gu Can asked, “What if Li Baoping were to go to the Fox Kingdom?”

Liu Chicheng laughed. “That girl is not as simple as you think. Just based on her own abilities, in the small Fox Kingdom, who dares to stretch out a hand? They would lose their tails.”

Gu Can’s expression turned gloomy. “Liu Chicheng, although I’m unclear about why you changed your mind earlier, don’t forget this trip is homecoming for me. Don’t let me walk to the Li family ancestral home on Fulu Street.”

Liu Chicheng smiled. “Oh you, your habit of refusing to acknowledge faces is terrifying.”

As soon as this topic came up, Liu Chicheng looked down at Chai Bofu, who was still sitting on the ground, and raised a foot to step on the “youth’s” Yuan Ying head, applying a little more pressure, pressing him into the ground, leaving just half his head exposed. Chai Bofu dared not move. Liu Chicheng crouched down, his large pink robe sleeves spreading out on the ground like an exceptionally vibrant peony opening up. Liu Chicheng impatiently said, “I’ll give you a stick of incense at most. If you still can’t stabilize your little Dragon Gate realm by then, I won’t protect you.”

Gu Can suddenly asked, “Have you been to the Suspended Mountain?”

Liu Chicheng didn’t lift his head and spoke without reservation, “Unless accompanied by my senior brother, I wouldn’t dare to go there at all.”

It wasn’t just a matter of cultivation level; the key was Liu Chicheng’s identity and roots, which made it unwise for him to approach the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Gu Can asked, “What about Liu Chicheng?”

Liu Chicheng replied, “Once we reach White Emperor City, I will return this skin suit to him. If luck is on his side, he might have the chance to become your fellow disciple.”

Over at the thatched cottage, Li Baoping and Wei Benyuan were also setting off toward the Fox Kingdom, which was allied with Clear Wind City.

Wei Benyuan naturally felt that his alchemical place was too dangerous; going to the Xu family of Clear Wind City would at least provide the girl with an extra talisman for protection.

Wei Benyuan summoned a symbol boat, elegant and refined. As he rode the wind, flowers of jade-green lotus appeared around the boat, suddenly sprouting and standing tall, then slowly dissipating, creating the illusion of a small boat parting a waterway through a lotus pond.

When Li Baoping boarded the small boat, taking advantage of Wei grandfather boarding first, with his back to her, she leaped onto the boat.

This long-lost playful move showed that her mood was quite good.

Seeing her older brother and ensuring the safety of Wei grandfather’s place of cultivation, she would also have the chance to meet her little master uncle again.

Once Wei Benyuan settled at one end of the small boat, Li Baoping stood ready, not sitting down. The scenic view was too beautiful to pass up; riding a horse while traveling gives a different perspective from being airborne.

Wei Benyuan chatted with Li Baoping about some hearsay, but the truth of the matter was likely unknown even to the Xu family’s younger generation.

That Fox Kingdom, home to tens of thousands of fox spirits, had a seven-tailed fox that had long hidden away. Seven hundred years ago, it split into three factions—one hoped to integrate with Clear Wind City and Baoping Continent, one sought a secluded little world, and the most extreme faction even wanted to completely sever ties with the Xu family of Clear Wind City. Eventually, under the leadership of the current patriarch Xu Hun, it transformed into a standoff situation. The third faction was hunted down, killed, and imprisoned, thus clearing the way for the continuous supply of foxskin talismans from Clear Wind City.

Moreover, after a woman took charge of affairs, she skillfully opened sources and generated wealth, steadily increasing the overall number of fox spirits. She had signed several secret contracts with Clear Wind City, one of which was a half-public secret: the Xu family had always leaned toward the Fox Kingdom for cultivation materials, but every fox spirit that failed to break through had to maintain its fox skin intact as repayment to Clear Wind City. Additionally, Clear Wind City had built many residences within the Fox Kingdom for tourists to enjoy, so that wandering sect disciples, pure martial artists, and cultured scholars wouldn’t need to spend their own money, all for the sake of winning the hearts of the fox spirits.

The Fox Kingdom had been meticulously crafted by the Xu family into a picturesque tourist destination, with calligraphy masters’ inscriptions on cliffs, poems from literati inscribed on walls, and the ancient residences of learned immortals, countless in number.

Wei Benyuan smiled. “The Xu family has a great knack for making money, but their reputation isn’t too good.”

Li Baoping had previously purchased some novels about scholarly fox immortals in Clear Wind City, beautifully printed, nearly rivaling the volumes of secular dynasties. However, she didn’t intend to read them and planned to gift them to Pei Qian later. As for the tales of the Jianghu and mountain spirits, Li Baoping had little longing for them now, far less than Pei Qian and Li Huai.

In these years, aside from studying at the academy, Li Baoping hadn’t been idle. She had inquired about some cultivation matters with Lin Shouyi and Xie Xie, and discussed some boxing techniques with Yu Lu. 

These three naturally shared everything they knew with Li Baoping.

Occasionally, when she ran into Li Huai on the road, it was just casual chatting.

The Fox Kingdom was located in a fragmented cave paradise, with vague historical records and a lot of hearsay that couldn’t be taken seriously.

Upon arriving at an entrance, Wei Benyuan disembarked the symbol boat at a wooden pavilion with a plaque reading “Branches of the Same Tree.” The couplets on either side had mostly faded, but the lower couplet was intact: “In this world, there are many passionate seeds.” The upper couplet’s ending read “Gentle Town,” which also had a backstory, said to have been cut down by a passing immortal with a sword. Some said it was Li Tuanjing of Thunder Garden, while others attributed it to Wei Jin of the Snow Temple. As for the accuracy of the dates, it was all for fun; who would bother to verify?

At the pavilion, many people milled about, mostly men, with scholars notably numerous, as the Fox Kingdom had one temple and one mountain that were said to be filled with literary inspiration. Pilgrims visiting to pray and burn incense found great success, hoping to achieve well in examinations. As for some penniless scholars purposely taking detours to the examination, hoping to earn some travel expenses, there were those too. The beauties of the Fox Kingdom were famously fond of scholars, and many downtrodden scholars willingly lived and died in this gentle town, often enjoying long lives. The fox spirits’ infatuation was no mere rumor; whenever the beloved man passed away, they sought not to be born in the same year and month but to die together.

To travel through the Fox Kingdom, there were interesting rules; one had to offer poetry or prose for passage. Poems, songs, essays, and even examination papers could suffice. As long as the talent was high, even a couplet would do. But if one wrote something that the discerning fox spirits found unsightly, then they would have to turn back. As for whether someone else wrote it on their behalf, it didn’t matter.

If one couldn’t produce decent writing, they would have to spend their heavenly money.

Li Baoping glanced at the magnificent building not far from the pavilion and frowned. Were the Xu family of Clear Wind City and the Fox Kingdom accumulating literary fortune through this? Accumulating little by little, what were they trying to accomplish? 

What could they actually do?

The Xu family of Clear Wind City had lowered their stature, marrying the legitimate daughter to a commoner, just to ally with the great Wei family of Dali. Was it that the Xu family had some ulterior motives regarding the future of the Dali court? Did they wish to position a capable Xu family descendant, one who could bear the literary fortune, to secure a place, step by step rising to the status of a minister, ultimately influencing some part of the Dali court and becoming the next great family?

Li Baoping began to recall the small-town journey with the Xu family mother and son. No, she had to ask her grandfather. Aside from that ugly armor, had the Xu family mother and son used any tricks to hide their true schemes back then?

There was one thing her little master uncle had always been indifferent to, but Li Baoping had always felt a small knot in her heart.

That was regarding the Mountain-Relocating Monkey and that little girl, who had borrowed shelter at the Li family in Fulu Street back in the small town.

If that were the only case, it would be fine. What she feared were the schemes and deceptions of those mountain people, twisting and turning for thousands of miles.

The Zhu River’s Zhu Lu father and daughter, her second brother Li Baozhen—two matters already. No more than three.

Wei Benyuan took out two pieces of snowflake money and led Li Baoping into the Fox Kingdom.

At the building, a woman lounged lazily over a writing desk, suddenly lifting her head, her spirit soaring as she immediately sent a flying sword message to the Xu family’s sword chamber in Clear Wind City.

Soon, a flying sword returned, providing a rough dossier. The wording at the end of the secret letter was not subtle, warning her not to have any unrealistic thoughts. The disciple of the Cliff of Immortals was also the direct granddaughter of the Li family’s Yuan Ying. She shouldn’t provoke her, as Clear Wind City was already a candidate for the sect and must avoid unnecessary complications. This made the woman unhappy, and with her long-fingered hand adorned with exquisite rings, she tore the confidential letter into shreds. Although unwilling in her heart, she still didn’t dare to defy the decision of Clear Wind City and could only lazily return to the desk.

That peach bud was cultivating near a waterfall in the Fox Kingdom. What Wei Benyuan referred to as opportunity was when the peach bud unintentionally passed by the waterfall, and unexpectedly, a ribbon of rainbow light floated on the water’s surface. Soon, a Golden Core fox spirit rushed over, eager to seize the opportunity, only to be struck by that ribbon, leaving it wounded and nearly pulled into the deep pool. Once that panicked fox spirit escaped, the ribbon floated back to the surface, gently nudging ashore, as if it had chosen its master, becoming this Wei family maid's colorful waist ribbon. Moreover, under its guidance, the peach bud picked up an inconspicuous dry peach branch in a deep mountain, which, after refining, became a hidden treasure.

Overnight, the peach bud became the luckiest individual in the Fox Kingdom in hundreds of years.

Within the Fox Kingdom, flying with the wind or taking a ferry was forbidden; one could only walk. Fortunately, there were three entrances to the Fox Kingdom. Wei Benyuan chose the one closest to the peach bud, hiring a horse carriage and renting a steed for the girl. One drove the carriage, while the other rode, all the while enjoying the scenery, making the journey far from dull.

Upon reaching the waterfall at the halfway point, the now lively peach bud felt a bit self-conscious when she saw Li Baoping.

After the three of them had tea, Li Baoping finished reminiscing and prepared to take her leave, saying she would head north to the capital of Dali to visit a friend. As for the horse left by the stream at the bottom of the mountain, it would rest now, having accompanied her over mountains and rivers.

Wei Benyuan was both amused and exasperated, while the peach bud was caught off guard.

Wei Benyuan asked, “Are you switching to the horse at the foot of the mountain?”

Li Baoping slapped her forehead, laughing, “I forgot to tell Wei grandfather; I’m now a Qi Refinement cultivator. My realm isn’t high, but I can ride the wind!”

Li Baoping added, “I can also ride a sword, though I prefer not to in general; the wind is strong up there, and it makes my cheeks hurt when I talk.”

The old man and peach bud exchanged glances.

Li Baoping thought for a moment and didn’t wish to hide, “I have some paper, and the words on them are dear to me; they can barely be turned into a symbol boat. But Mr. Mao hopes I don’t take it out easily.”

Wei Benyuan asked helplessly, “Is that all?”

Li Baoping shook her head. “Nothing more. I’ve just learned some boxing techniques from friends. I’m not a pure martial artist, so I can’t rely solely on my physique to travel far.”

Wei Benyuan rose. “Then let the peach bud escort you out of the Fox Kingdom. Otherwise, Wei grandfather will truly be uneasy.”

Though the peach bud’s cultivation might not surpass that of the elder at the moment, her two life-bound items were too mysterious, defensively and offensively balanced, and could already be regarded as the cultivation level of a Golden Core cultivator.

Li Baoping smiled. “Forget it, I won’t hold back Sister Peach Bud’s cultivation.”

She winked at Sister Peach Bud.

Peach Bud understood and blushed slightly, puzzled about how Little Baoping could tell she had someone she liked.

If she didn’t have someone she liked, why would a solitary woman, living in seclusion, apply rouge?

As for the elder, while he would be extremely concerned about Peach Bud’s cultivation, he wouldn’t care about such details.

Li Baoping said her goodbyes and left.

From south to north, she crossed mountains and rivers, passing through the Fox Kingdom, when suddenly a heavy snow began to fall. A young woman in a red cotton coat stood beside a cliffside path, breathing out mist.

The woman’s narrow blade and sword-raising gourd suited the heavy snow.

At that moment, it seemed the world was filled with only two colors: the pure white of the snow and the woman’s exquisite beauty.

In the Lotus Root Blessed Land of Nanyuan Kingdom’s capital, a young girl stood up, heading to the courtyard, striking a fist stance, then telling the little girl perched on the railing with her chin resting on her hands, “Little Rice Grain, I’m about to throw a punch. You go wander around in Scholar’s Alley and buy some sunflower seeds while you’re at it.”

The girl in black hesitated, “I’ll just take a look and won’t say a word; I still have some sunflower seeds in my pocket.”

In truth, it was her duty; as the right protector of the Fallen Mountain, she also served as the deputy leader of the branch. In such times, how could she not help Pei Qian guard the formation?

The young girl glared. “Once I throw this punch, I won’t hold back; is that okay?! Martial fortune doesn’t have eyes; it’ll flock around like rain falling from the sky. How big of a bowl of pickled fish will I eat tonight?”

Zhou Mili hurriedly jumped down from the railing, took a small shoulder pole and walking stick, and ran far away, suddenly stopping and turning her head to ask, “How many pounds of sunflower seeds should I buy?! I heard Sister Nuan Tree say that buying more is cheaper, while buying less won’t get a discount.”

Pei Qian replied helplessly, “Whatever you want.”

Zhou Mili frowned, lifting her small shoulder pole high in the air. “Then I’ll carry a sack on one end of the shoulder pole?”

The little girl felt she was being exceptionally clever.

Pei Qian nodded, though in reality, she was already speechless.

Zhou Mili glanced at Pei Qian, knowing the weight of the situation, then lightly stepped off and leaped over the courtyard wall.

After Little Rice Grain left, Pei Qian stepped out, stomping heavily, causing the entire Nanyuan Kingdom’s capital to tremble. Such an occurrence could not possibly be caused by a mere fifth realm martial artist; it was more due to the influence of her fist intent, causing the mountains and rivers to resonate, even the dragon vein of Nanyuan Kingdom was not spared.

Pei Qian twisted her arms into a strange posture, pausing briefly before lightly thrusting out her fist in a drumming motion.

Moments later, Pei Qian’s entire being seemed to move with her punch, pulled by the intent of her fist, as if her fist was propelled by her heart, aiming to deliver the final blow at the highest point. The girl’s figure soared, stepping into the air, then rushing toward the heavens, her speed like lightning. Ultimately, she arrived at the heavens above the Lotus Root Blessed Land, where the sun hung high, and Pei Qian finally delivered her final punch.

After that punch, beneath her feet lay a vast golden sea of clouds illuminated by the great sun, exploding into a scattering of brilliance.

Almost all the Qi Refiners who had embarked on the path of cultivation and had initially reached the middle five realms in the Lotus Root Blessed Land instinctively looked up at a certain spot in the sky.

Even the spirits and phantoms born from this new blessed land gazed up in confusion at the heavens.

At the same time, the Great Li Martial Temple, the Baoping Continent’s Martial Temple, and several other great martial temples across the other eight continents sensed the change.

Eight streams of martial fortunes surged toward Baoping Continent, ultimately converging with the martial fortune of Baoping Continent, crashing into the Tongye Umbrella held by the Mountain Lord Wei Ban.

In all the major martial temples of Dali, especially the one closest to the Fallen Mountain, the divine beings actively manifested, bowing and clasping their fists toward the Fallen Mountain.

Wei Ban, in his snow-white robe, struggled to maintain his stance, his feet rooted to the ground as he directly activated the power of the mountains and rivers, connecting himself with the entire Piyun Mountain. He had initially intended to help conceal his aura, but at this moment, he didn’t have the luxury to hide; merely standing firm while holding the Tongye Umbrella was already a strain on him. This great mountain lord of an entire continent had previously been perplexed by Zhu Lian’s insistence on holding the Tongye of the Tongye Continent, now both angry and amused, he exclaimed, “Zhu Lian! I’ll f*** your grandpa!”

Regardless of how many night tours he hosted, in terms of reputation, the Mountain Lord was simply exceptional; countless female deities, spirits, and fairies fell for him at first sight.

As for the old steward of the Fallen Mountain, it was best to forget about him; no one could remember his appearance well, at most only recalling his identity.

Zhu Lian stood at the cliff of a bamboo building, hands clasped behind his back, as the martial fortunes surged through the heavens and earth, rushing towards the Fallen Mountain. Despite the protective fist intent surrounding him, his long robe was still shredded by the dense and countless flying martial fortunes. Over time, the mask that had covered Zhu Lian’s face for many years also began to peel away, revealing his true visage.

Zhu Lian extended two fingers, pinching a strand of hair at his temple, squinting and smiling.

The young Zhu Lian, with such features, could captivate the hearts of beauties.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 770: No One at the Top

Pei Qian opened the courtyard door to find Zhou Mili standing there, a hiking staff in hand and a small shoulder pole balanced on her shoulder. One end of the pole carried a sack full of melon seeds. The little girl in black was chatting away with the stone lion at the entrance—a lively chatter from her, and a stoic silence from the lion, a perfect match.

Upon hearing the creaking door, Zhou Mili quickly turned to Pei Qian, about to ask something. However, Pei Qian gestured for her to stay quiet and then turned her gaze towards a distant rooftop.

There, a middle-aged martial arts master stood proudly atop a grand building with a sloping roof. Now that he had been discovered, he intended to leave and report back to the palace about the situation. In truth, he knew little; the young emperor was merely wary of the girl who had punched her way through the clouds, hastily ordering him to investigate. He had arrived too late; he saw the girl return to the earth, as swift and silent as an arrow, contrasting sharply with the earlier tremors that had shaken the capital. It was a silence that sent a chill through the master, a display of peak mastery, truly a transformation.

After the demise of the dark lord Ding Ying, Yu Zhenyi, who had turned to cultivating immortality, had vanished without a trace, rumored to have ascended to the heavens. Others like Chun Chao Palace’s Zhou Fei and the National Teacher Zhong Qiu had also gone on distant journeys. Top masters like the newly emerged Lu Tai, who had unified the demonic sects and was set to duel Yu Zhenyi, had faded into obscurity. Since then, there had been no top-tier martial artist appearing in the world of Jianghu for many years.

Was this “girl” not a legendary figure, a transcendent being with the ability to maintain her youth?

Was she an immortal who had descended from the heavens to roam this realm?

As the atmosphere of the Jianghu grew thin, the aura of the mountains thickened, filled with the strange and the bizarre.

Unexpectedly, the girl took just a few steps, leapt over the wall, and zipped across the rooftop, arriving effortlessly at the opposite roof facing the middle-aged master. They faced off, with Pei Qian standing slightly lower. The girl withdrew her fists, clasped her hands in greeting, and spoke in the refined dialect of the South Garden Kingdom: “I am Pei Qian, a disciple of the Falling Star Mountain. May I know what guidance you seek?”

The middle-aged martial artist, with a knife hung at his waist, reined in his awkwardness and returned the greeting. “I am Dong Zhongxia. I am currently a servant of the Wei family, the instructor for the Imperial Forest Army’s martial arts.”

Dong Zhongxia smiled and said, “No need for guidance; I am merely here on a patrol mission. Since it is indeed Miss Pei cultivating here, I can return to report without concern.”

The emperor had issued a secret decree that wherever a disciple of Falling Star Mountain was encountered, they must be respected.

The former emperor, Wei Liang, had unexpectedly abdicated in favor of his eldest son. After the new emperor, Wei Yan, took the throne, he initiated the imperial examinations, granting amnesty to various commoners and allowing their offspring to participate. He also established military examinations, permitting sons of soldiers and Jianghu disciples with three generations of clear lineage to compete. The edict specifically stated that these military examinations aimed to promote trusted individuals for national service. Additionally, shrines and temples were being constructed, with the Ministry of Rites tasked to sift through local records to commemorate loyal officials, hoping to honor their spirits for continued protection of the land. Furthermore, the Wei family began secretly supporting and courting practitioners of the Dao to help suppress the emerging demons and spirits, preventing them from causing harm, as the martial artists of various Jianghu sects, despite their prowess, were often at a loss against these unfamiliar entities.

However, Dong Zhongxia was among the newly emerging elite masters of Jianghu. At an age of enlightenment, he had recently broken through his martial arts bottleneck. After traveling abroad, he had suppressed several notorious demons, gaining fame, and was chosen by the new emperor to serve as one of the martial advisors of the South Garden Kingdom. Yet, he now realized that the emperor was the true master of martial arts, with profound cultivation.

Pei Qian smiled and asked, “So, Dong senior, are you not a native of the South Garden Kingdom?”

Otherwise, he would have recognized the peak fist style she had deliberately displayed, which originated from the former national master, Zhong Fuzi.

However, this indicated that Dong Zhongxia might not truly be the emperor's trusted confidant.

Dong Zhongxia nodded. “I hail from the Pine Whisper Kingdom and have only just arrived in the South Garden Kingdom.”

Pei Qian turned her gaze elsewhere, frowning slightly. Was there something he was hiding? Earlier, her punch had caused quite a stir, attracting the attention of a high-ranking figure from the South Garden Kingdom, fulfilling his duty as a court official. She treated him with respect, but the person accompanying Dong Zhongxia, upon seeing her emerge, mistakenly thought she hadn’t noticed and not only failed to withdraw but also audaciously employed a technique to eavesdrop, manifesting tiny droplets of water around Pei Qian and Dong Zhongxia to listen in.

Pei Qian bid farewell to Dong Zhongxia.

Dong Zhongxia was slightly surprised, realizing she truly wasn’t an immortal from a greater realm.

Pei Qian’s surroundings were still and silent, yet the dust on the roof suddenly scattered, and in the blink of an eye, Dong Zhongxia found himself unable to see Pei Qian’s figure.

Pei Qian had already crouched next to the eaves of a distant rooftop, staring at a young man who sat cross-legged, hands forming a seal, wearing a robe that was still scarce in the Lotus Root Blessed Land, topped with a jade crown, and a white jade short sword tucked at his waist.

The young man stood up with a smile. “I am Wang Guangjing, a guest from the Prince’s Mansion. I have the pleasure of meeting Miss Pei.”

Pei Qian inquired, “Are you not the Master Wang from the Prince’s Mansion? Weren’t you and the other two enlightened beings ordered to leave the capital and reopen the Longtan Water Cave?”

Currently, the capital of the South Garden Kingdom was a mix of dragons and fish, with many self-proclaimed masters, but true practitioners of the Dao were rare. Most were either quickly establishing their sects in beautiful locations or were aligning themselves with the monarchs of the three kingdoms to take advantage of their resources, which were as new as they were valuable. Falling Star Mountain had meticulously documented these events, and Nuan Shu would regularly transcribe them and send them to the ancestral hall of Jisefeng for archiving, with the original manuscripts stored with the old chef. Falling Star Mountain had secretly established two channels for collecting information in the Lotus Root Blessed Land: one personally crafted by Zhong Fuzi, well-known to both the old emperor Wei Liang and the new emperor Wei Yan, being one of the clauses of their contract with Falling Star Mountain; the other, run by Zhu Lian, deep within the Pine Whisper Kingdom.

Pei Qian did not fully understand these court affairs but was aware of the underlying tensions between the old and new emperors. Otherwise, the old emperor would not have been so close to his second son Wei Yun, nor would the new emperor Wei Yan have allowed his younger brother Wei Yun to hold the position of governor of the capital, especially not appointing a senior official who had favored the younger prince to serve as the national treasurer. If it had not been for the young emperor’s trusted aide, the Minister of Rites, who would later oversee the mountain and water deities, Pei Qian would have thought the old emperor was still in control.

Wang Guangjing, slightly taken aback, with an apologetic expression, said, “Before leaving, I was in a hurry to break through and made a significant error in my cultivation, necessitating a period of recovery in the capital.”

As Dong Zhongxia departed, he glanced back, a heavy heart.

That Prince Wei Yun was certainly not to be underestimated, especially with the retired emperor's backing, having gathered a considerable number of practitioners.

If Pei Qian, a martial artist, became entangled with the Prince’s Mansion, would that not incite further turmoil in the capital of the South Garden Kingdom?

Dong Zhongxia hurriedly returned to a hidden residence near the palace, once a place of cultivation for the National Teacher Zhong Qiu. There, he encountered a man in plain clothes who was secretly visiting, and his heart skipped a beat. He quickly lowered his stance and clasped his hands, softly saying, “Your Majesty.”

Emperor Wei Yan listened attentively to Dong Zhongxia’s words, smiling. “A mere snake and rat dares to speak of attracting attention in front of a dragon?”

How could a small pond in Prince Wei Yun’s residence possibly provide for a dragon accustomed to rivers? And what kind of hospitality could be expected?

Beside Wei Yan stood a graceful and charming woman, his sister Wei Zhen.

Wei Zhen softly asked, “Since that girl is from Falling Star Mountain, what is her connection to that Chen Jianxian? Brother, why not ask her?”

Wei Yan cautioned, “Such matters of state are not to be trifled with.”

Wei Zhen felt somewhat disappointed.

Now half a practitioner herself, she was deeply interested in the realm of Falling Star Mountain. Over the years, her explorations of the palace’s secret archives had only fueled her admiration.

On Pei Qian’s side, after listening to Wang Guangjing’s convoluted words, she maintained her usual expression but found it rather amusing.

Though she had previously suppressed her mind and body to appear younger, a mere girl from a small town, if one spoke of the human heart, even at the time she had just left the Lotus Root Blessed Land, Pei Qian was not a naïve child. Otherwise, those two seasoned constables from a small border town of the Daqing Dynasty would not have been so easily fooled by her fabrications, escorting her back to the inn of the Ninth Lady with respect. Even Li Huai and two other academy friends still regarded her as the “princess who fell into hardship.”

Pei Qian declined Wang Guangjing’s invitation, intending to return to the house and meet Zhou Mili.

Unexpectedly, Wang Guangjing remained persistent, bringing up Prince Wei Yun, claiming the prince greatly valued virtuous individuals, especially martial artists. Even if Pei Qian was unwilling to stroll over to the prince’s mansion, the prince could come to visit personally. If Pei Qian only nodded, the prince would surely find time to come.

Pei Qian felt a headache coming on. His words were full of empty threats or overly formal phrases. What kind of foolish guest was this Wang Guangjing? Was he helping the prince recruit people or drive them away?

Pei Qian then thought, despite Wang Guangjing’s falsehoods, his closed-door retreat was not an error; he had successfully advanced to the cave dwelling stage, making him one of the early fifth-stage Qi cultivators of the Lotus Root Blessed Land. In fact, he could be considered half an immortal. In this blessed land, the spiritual energy was growing denser, and more people were climbing the mountains to cultivate, yet those who could reach the fifth stage were still few and far between, each precious. The key was to progress quickly; the most gifted Qi cultivators would soon face the bottleneck of the Lotus Root Blessed Land.

Regarding when the Lotus Root Blessed Land could ascend to a higher tier, the old chef had once remarked that even if they could muster the funds for the “Grain Rain,” they should not rush, especially since Falling Star Mountain truly did not have that money.

At that moment, in the courtyard, all eyes were on Wei Bo, the Mountain Lord. 

Zheng Dafeng joked, “Slowly speak, but earn money quickly.”

Wei Bo smiled, “If you keep this up, I’ll flip the board.”

Suddenly, Pei Qian recalled the old chef’s reminder before departing: Do not imitate your master in every way; you have your own Jianghu to traverse. If you resemble your master too closely, he will always worry about you, seeing you as a child needing his support.

Pei Qian raised an eyebrow, feeling it made sense. Glancing at Wang Guangjing, she transformed her demeanor, no longer holding back as she had with Dong Zhongxia, and stated directly, “Stop trying to tug at Falling Star Mountain’s strings. I won’t meddle in the Wei family’s affairs. As for you, guest of the prince’s mansion, leave quickly and focus on your own cultivation. Remember my words: if others speak sweetly, listen well. Should you harbor ulterior motives and attempt to test me with tricks…”

Pei Qian raised her fist, lightly shaking it. “If I throw this punch, you may not catch it.”

Wang Guangjing feigned helplessness, “I’ve heard that Chen Jianxian is most reasonable. Miss Pei, as someone from my hometown and half an immortal…”

“My master said that using lofty ideals to harm good people is not much different from bullying with power.”

With a sudden push off the ground, Pei Qian appeared in front of Wang Guangjing in an instant. He barely had time to react before the girl’s fist was almost touching his forehead, barely an inch away.

“Still not leaving? Do you enjoy being carried away while lying down?”

Wang Guangjing’s white jade short sword, which resembled a paperweight, glimmered ominously.

Pei Qian didn’t even glance at it. “Do you know how many sword cultivators and sword immortals I’ve encountered?!”

Wang Guangjing stepped back, smiling. “Since Miss Pei does not wish to accept the prince’s good intentions, then let it be. The mountains are high and the waters are deep; we are all cultivators, and perhaps there will be opportunities to become friends in the future.”

Pei Qian retracted her fist, glancing at Wang Guangjing’s heart’s landscape, her demeanor shifting. She spoke in a deep tone, “Elder Cui once said, if a martial artist strikes, they should shatter the villain's malice and diminish their courage; one must strike decisively.”

Wang Guangjing chuckled wryly. “Why must Miss Pei be so aggressive? Do you want me to kneel and apologize? Have I shown any disrespect from beginning to end?”

Pei Qian felt conflicted, concerned that she might have misread the situation. She had misjudged the weight of her punch and acted rashly. 

Her embarrassment mirrored the awkwardness she felt before the Temple of the Water God of the Jade Liquid River.

Instead, she thought, it would have been more straightforward had Chen Lingjun handled it.

Suddenly, Pei Qian looked up.

A figure in a gray long robe arrived on the wind, floating down and pressing Wang Guangjing’s head, twisting his wrist and sending him spinning into the street.

Zhu Lian turned his back to the street, raised a hand, and casually waved, sending the unsteady Wang Guangjing flying ten feet down the street, his eyes rolling back as he fainted on the spot.

Zhu Lian chuckled, “There’s no such thing as being too cautious; you never know when a rat might spoil the pot.”

Zhu Lian leaned slightly back, glancing elsewhere. He noticed hidden practitioners lurking, preparing to rescue Wang Guangjing, and asked, “Does everyone from the Prince’s Mansion enjoy bringing home rat droppings?”

That Prince Wei Yun had been too restless for quite some time.

As for the retired emperor Wei Liang, his royal disposition remained unchanged. Even if he was keen on the Dao, he had never truly seen the grandeur of the world. Now a retired emperor, having shed his dragon robe, he had yet to fully achieve enlightenment and was up to his usual tricks. Of course, he might also have thoughts about bargaining with Falling Star Mountain.

If the current emperor Wei Yan hadn’t been reasonably benevolent, the Lotus Root Blessed Land would soon be in turmoil, and the ones suffering the most would be Fuzi Zhong Qiu and Cao Qinglang.

Pei Qian focused, puzzled. “Old chef, why do you suddenly have a different demeanor?”

Zhu Lian sighed. “The mountain winds are strong; it blew away my old face.”

Zhu Lian turned to look at the young immortal sleeping on the street, silently observing.

Pei Qian suddenly asked, “Old chef, is there a lack of freedom in Falling Star Mountain?”

Zhu Lian reflected, “You’ve grown up to ask such questions. I initially thought only the young master would ask me this upon returning home.”

Pei Qian laughed, “I just mentioned it casually; you can tell my master the answer later.”

Zhu Lian replied slowly, “The freedom to strike may not be great. But in life, the freedom of expression, the freedom to cook, the freedom to earn and spend money, the freedom to read and appreciate the scenery, the freedom to play chess with friends without seeking victory, and the freedom to watch younger generations grow day by day—aren’t all of these freedoms?”

Pei Qian found it uncomfortable not to hear the old chef’s familiar voice, so she quickly changed the subject. “What about that pretender Wang Guangjing?”

Zhu Lian said, “Yu Lu and Xie Xie have already taken leave from the academy and will be traveling together in the Lotus Root Blessed Land for the next two years. I’ll borrow someone from Wei Yun, and Wang Guangjing can guide them. With Yu Lu around, cultivating the heart won’t be a problem.”

Pei Qian was curious. “Did Li Huai not join in this excitement?”

Zhu Lian shook his head. “According to Brother Dafeng, if Li Huai were to step in, the practitioners of the Lotus Root Blessed Land wouldn’t have any significant opportunities.”

Pei Qian had an idea but didn’t dare voice it.

Zhu Lian asked, “Were you thinking of going to Lion Peak in Beiju Lu Zhou to find Li Huai’s father?”

Pei Qian nodded. “Although Senior Gu is no longer in the world, Uncle Li’s martial arts are still excellent, and he taught my master. I just want to practice my fists there. Coincidentally, Li Huai also wants to visit his parents and sister.”

Zhu Lian contemplated. “That’s doable.”

Pei Qian sat at the edge of the roof, feeling a bit lost. “But such matters should be approved by my master.”

Zhu Lian crouched nearby, softly comforting her. “If the young master were here, he would surely agree.”

On the street, a little girl carrying two bags of melon seeds approached, and Zhu Lian couldn’t help but chuckle. “Do you plan to eat melon seeds as your main meal?”

Pei Qian leapt forward, landing on the street.

As Zhou Mili made her way over, she carefully skirted around the unconscious Wang Guangjing. She kept her back turned to him, thinking, You don’t see me, I don’t see you; we’re all wandering in Jianghu, keeping our distances. Once past the sleeping man, Zhou Mili quickened her pace, balancing the two small bags, before stopping to steady them. She whispered, “Old chef, I saw Pei Qian chatting with someone from afar. What happened? You attacked sneakily? That’s not polite; next time, at least let me know before you hit someone. It wouldn’t sound good if it got out in Jianghu. I’ll crack some melon seeds to summon him awake, and you can come back?”

Zhu Lian nodded, imitating the little girl’s speech. “Sure, I like this.”

Since Zhu Lian had struck with great care, Wang Guangjing, in fact, had already awakened when Zhou Mili passed by. He was now acutely listening to the girl’s seemingly righteous but entirely unreasonable words, nearly brought to tears as the young immortal, both a guest and a behind-the-scenes strategist in the Prince’s Mansion, almost lost his composure.

Pei Qian pinched Zhou Mili’s cheek, and with a tug, the girl tilted her head and stood on her toes, gently tapping Pei Qian’s fingers, mumbling, “There’s no need for this; really no need.”

Zhu Lian stamped his foot.

Wang Guangjing’s entire body jolted up, no longer daring to pretend to be asleep. He stood, trembling slightly, “I pay my respects to the immortal.”

Zhu Lian nodded, his expression kind, and gave a light pat.

The strike sent Wang Guangjing flying straight to the end of the street.

Zhu Lian laughed, “This punch should make your courage shrink.”

Zhu Lian looked around, muttering to himself, “It’s a pity that when I first met Ding Ying, he was still a child. By the time I returned, he was gone. Otherwise, I could have taught him how to treat his juniors.”

He wasn’t just talking nonsense.

In fact, Ding Ying’s later actions followed Zhu Lian’s old path closely. Zhu Lian had previously single-handedly fought against nine others during the Jiazi agreement, wiping out more than half of the renowned masters on the list. The only reason Zhu Lian hadn’t killed Ding Ying was that he deemed the hope of ascension too slim, feeling that the meaning of ascension seemed trivial at that moment. He purposely gifted Ding Ying a rather appealing head, along with the corresponding martial fortune. It could be said that Ding Ying’s subsequent achievements, both in martial arts and character development, owed much to Zhu Lian.

During Zhu Lian’s time on earth, this world had first rank in literature and second in martial arts.

Pei Qian asked, “Shall we head back?”

Zhu Lian nodded, “Let’s finish a bag of melon seeds first, or Nuan Shu will surely scold you for buying too much.”

Upon returning to the residence, Pei Qian inquired about breaking through the sixth stage bottleneck, as well as how to deal with martial fortune in Beiju Lu Zhou. Zhou Mili reminded her to ask about the seventh and eighth-stage bottlenecks as well.

Pei Qian shot her a glare. “Does being anxious help you eat hot tofu?”

Zhou Mili looked puzzled. Isn’t even the hottest tofu a one-bite affair?

Zhu Lian still shared some precautions with Pei Qian.

Afterward, Zhu Lian quickly returned to Falling Star Mountain.

Pei Qian mentioned she had a few matters to attend to, stopping by Cao Qinglang’s ancestral home to help tidy up with Zhou Mili. Then, they went to Baihe Temple’s night market and indulged in the spicy, numbing delicacies the master had mentioned, ordering two servings of hot pot. After satisfying their appetites, they glanced at the imperial family’s library, which was much shorter than the Zhilian Tower back in Nuan Shu’s hometown.

Later, Pei Qian also visited a peer who had transformed into a young woman some years earlier. She had married a scholar who had successfully passed the imperial examinations and was now on a prosperous career path.

When that woman’s family set out in a carriage to a temple in the capital to offer prayers, Pei Qian followed from a distance, keeping herself hidden.

In the end, Pei Qian helped her master by visiting the Scholar’s Alley, where a once poor scholar had a story with a wandering woman holding a pipa. The lovers had never become a couple.

Asking the local shopkeeper, Pei Qian learned that the scholar had failed his examinations twice and had cried deeply, seemingly giving up entirely, returning home to start a school.

Who knows if that student would ever encounter a charming girl again in his life?

On the last day before leaving the South Garden Kingdom, Pei Qian quietly climbed to the rooftop at night.

Zhou Mili followed suit.

The slender girl and the not-so-small girl lay on the roof, gazing at the round moon.

Zhou Mili cracked some melon seeds and casually asked, “Why is it that the more one practices martial arts, the less one dares to strike?”

Pei Qian replied, “My master treats the lives of others as if they were fragile porcelain. He never explicitly says this, but I’ve always seen it.”

Zhou Mili nodded vigorously, “That’s quite right! So, there’s no need to rush into striking, Pei Qian, let’s not rush.”

Pei Qian smiled, “What do you mean by ‘we’? You’re not even practicing martial arts. Not practicing martial arts is tough enough. Look, my master once said not to start too early with martial arts. The only time I didn’t listen to my master, I faced a major setback. So, you see, you must listen to your master.”

Zhou Mili stealthily moved her hand with the melon seeds farther away, pretending to say something heart-wrenching. When Pei Qian reached for her, she missed, and the little girl burst into laughter, quickly pulling her hand back.

Pei Qian looked up at the sky, chuckling, scratching her head. She had thought that reaching the highest point would allow her to see Elder Cui again.

Zhou Mili whispered, “Pei Qian, when you go to Beiju Lu Zhou, remember to take a look at the Mute Lake for me.”

Pei Qian asked, “Don’t you want to go together?”

Zhou Mili shook her head. “I won’t have any friends there.”

Pei Qian ruffled Zhou Mili’s hair. “You silly head, getting confused over small matters but so clever with major issues.”

Zhou Mili sighed out of nowhere.

Pei Qian asked, “What’s wrong? Got something on your mind?”

Zhou Mili shook her head, her expression serious, “I don’t have any worries, so I’m troubled.”

Pei Qian delivered a light knock on her head.

Zhou Mili pretended to be in pain, rolling around on the rooftop, thoroughly enjoying herself.

Pei Qian lay quietly beside her, gently punching the sky, murmuring, “I guess I need to reach higher.”

Gu Can and Liu Chicheng traveled north with the recently demoted Chai Bofu.

Liu Chicheng indeed halted at the border between the two states.

Gu Can continued alone.

Liu Chicheng and Long Bo strolled leisurely in a bustling city of Chizhou. Liu Chicheng was there to admire the beauties of the mountains below, while the white-haired Chai Bofu was too busy healing from his injuries. He had previously misspoken and received a slap from Liu Chicheng, nearly losing his footing, compounded by the ever-watchful Gu Can, who seemed ready to dig a hole for him. The once formidable Yuanying master, who had wrestled with many prominent figures atop the mountains of Baoping Prefecture, now felt like he had regressed to his bleak days as a fifth-stage practitioner.

When Liu Chicheng and Chai Bofu returned to the immortal’s inn, Liu Chicheng walked with an air of confidence, only to be struck by lightning.

He ordered Chai Bofu to keep his distance.

Chai Bofu, filled with words, immediately went out to stroll by himself, not daring to stay at the inn.

Liu Chicheng directly put away his pink robe, daring only to show his original scholarly appearance, and lightly knocked on the door.

Inside, two people were engaged in a chess match, ignoring him completely.

Liu Chicheng mustered his courage to push open the door, silently approaching a man in white and observing him closely. 

The man in white was playing chess with a solemn-faced scholar in green.

The white-clad man smiled. “Cui Zhan, this move isn’t bad. If Gu Can were to become my disciple, I wouldn’t hold it against you for rescuing a waste of effort. If he becomes my junior apprentice, I’ll agree to your request.”

Cui Zhan nodded. “Then it’s a deal.”

Cui Zhan poised his piece but didn’t place it on the board, so the board remained empty.

Liu Chicheng held his breath.

The man in white, not looking at the board, smiled. “You’ve found a good seedling for Baidi City, and you’ve even brought this person to play chess. How should I thank you? No wonder my master once told me that the reason he chose you as a disciple was due to your knack for stirring up hives, ensuring that I, as your senior brother, wouldn’t be so bored.”

Liu Chicheng felt parched, his expression stiff.

The man in white stood up. “Let’s not play anymore. This game is a mess created by your own choosing; don’t think to drag me down with you. The Great Li Dynasty can’t bear the consequences.”

Cui Zhan sighed, returning the pieces to the box, and stood up. “Then I won’t see you off.”

The man in white nodded and vanished.

Liu Chicheng wiped the sweat off his forehead.

Cui Zhan collected the chessboard and box, glancing at Liu Chicheng with a smile. “Your ability to court death exceeds even mine.”

Liu Chicheng forced a smile. “Who would have thought I’d encounter so many ‘what ifs’ in a row?”

Cui Zhan chuckled. “Not many; just three.”

Liu Chicheng felt utterly helpless.

Cui Zhan casually remarked, “If you die, there’s no need to worry about dying anymore.”

Liu Chicheng bowed. “Congratulations, National Teacher, on breaking through.”

Cui Zhan replied, “Wishing a 99-year-old old-timer longevity is also courting death.”

Liu Chicheng began to play coy. “As long as my senior brother is around, I fear nothing.”

Cui Zhan said, “Letting your senior brother kill you is as simple as one phrase from me.”

Liu Chicheng immediately bowed again, looking pitiful. “I implore the National Teacher to share some scholarly wisdom; that’s what I wish to hear most now.”

Cui Zhan said, “Then heed my advice: when Gu Can arrives in Baidi City, regardless of what happens, just protect him from dying; don’t do anything unnecessary.”

Liu Chicheng wanted to ask this genuine master about heavenly secrets, but Cui Zhan had already vanished.

Liu Chicheng sighed heavily.

In the once-busy area of the old Shanyan Academy in the Great Li capital, it had been sealed off for years, now desolate, overgrown with weeds, with wild rabbits and foxes roaming.

A streak of white light descended from the sky, bright and unashamed, completely ignoring the grand formation of the Great Li capital, as if even the Confucian sage overseeing the heavens was not worth his attention.

After the man in white appeared, he glanced at the restless imitation of the White Jade Capital. There, it seemed they had received a secret decree, and the activated White Jade Capital quickly quieted down.

This man, who actually disliked leaving Baidi City, walked slowly, lamenting, “Spend a grain to remove weeds, but this is just evil grass.”

Before Gu Can returned home, four individuals, two pairs of master and servant, were essentially returning home.

In the mud-bottle alley, the Great Li prince Song Jixin and his maid Zhi Gui.

In the apricot blossom alley, Ma Kuxuan.

As for Ma Kuxuan’s maid, “Shu Dian,” she felt rather superfluous on this journey.

Song Jixin, who was being escorted by Ma Kuxuan under the pretense of protection, found it utterly repulsive.

The ferry docked at Niujiao Mountain.

Ma Kuxuan took Shu Dian to the River God Temple of Longxu River.

Song Jixin and Zhi Gui headed to the mud-bottle alley.

However, Zhi Gui, under the cover of night, left the house alone, glancing at the clean courtyard next door, with spring couplets and blessings, she stepped out of the alley.

After Zhi Gui left the small alley, deep in the night, Song Jixin carried a small stool into the courtyard, merely standing there and not sitting down, gazing towards the neighbor’s yard, which seemed to shrink increasingly.

Zhi Gui first went to the Iron Lock Well, scooped a handful of water, weighed it, and poured it back into the well.

Then she walked out of the town, nearby Li Huai’s house, looking at the small hill named Pearl Mountain, her brows tightly knit.

Buried there was the true dragon’s body, refined and suppressed by the three sects’ sage.

Pearl Mountain.

“Pearl” refers to Wang Zhu. The true pearl is indeed Wang Zhu’s true form.

As for Wang Zhu's current body, it was merely a transformation of the true dragon Li Zhu, not her true form. She still needed someone to “dot the dragon’s eye” to reclaim her true form legitimately.

Only then could she restore her complete true dragon identity, at which point all the grand fortunes of the world’s dragons would coalesce in her alone! Helping her break through the Yuan Ying stage bottleneck would be nothing, and breaking through the Yu Pu stage bottleneck wouldn’t be difficult either. Once she stabilized her immortal state, her combat power could rival half of the ascended beings.

The scribe, the one who helps with the “dotting,” was the mud-legged boy who had signed a contract with her years ago, Chen Ping An, the first person she saw during the harsh winter after leaving the Iron Lock Well.

However, at that time, Chen Ping An’s spirit was too weak, and his fortune was so thin it was appalling; she didn’t want to be dragged down by him, so she chose to recognize the neighboring Great Li prince Song Jixin as her “master.”

The four-legged snake that Song Jixin had tossed into the neighboring yard would run back on its own; why was it so despised yet unwilling to stay at Chen Ping An’s home?

Similarly, as one of the five opportunities of the great Dao, when Chen Ping An gifted that little mud loach to Gu Can, Gu Can not only accepted it but also managed to receive it without any issues.

Logically speaking, after Song Jixin tossed it several times, it should have counted as Chen Ping An’s opportunity.

But how could that little snake with horns on its forehead dare to sit on par with Wang Zhu?! Recognizing Chen Ping An as its master like Wang Zhu?!

Wang Zhu had established a master-servant relationship with the neighboring Song Jixin; however, that was merely a trick of Wang Zhu. Later, it was renamed Zhi Gui by Song Jixin, which was quite meaningful.

The name “Zhi Gui” originally belonged to the overseer Song Yuzhang, but it was actually given by Cui Zhan to Song Yuzhang, then “coincidentally” caught Song Jixin’s eye. He remembered it unknowingly, always resonating within him, leading to an unshakeable recollection, ultimately helping Wang Zhu to be named Zhi Gui.

The two characters “Zhi Gui” are also rooted in the tale of “borrowing light from a wall.”

The plaque hanging in the main hall of the mud-bottle alley reads “Huiyuan Hall,” hand-painted by the late Great Li emperor.

Everything has its significance.

Thus, during those years, Zhi Gui could slowly absorb the dragon energy of the Great Li Dynasty.

As a result, Song Jixin missed the dragon throne, merely becoming a prince and not an emperor; there were reasons for this.

In the grand scheme of things, fate and destiny had their own arrangements.

And when Zhi Gui initially met Lu Chen, who had specifically come to find her, she instinctively mentioned Chen Ping An to deflect disaster, not Song Jixin.

Zhi Gui stood still, gazing at Pearl Mountain, silent for a long time.

Song Jixin approached her.

Zhi Gui conveyed these inner thoughts silently.

Delaying further held little significance; perhaps it could lead to enmity with Song Jixin.

Unexpectedly, Song Jixin smiled. “I don’t mind.”

Wang Zhu blinked. “I don’t mind either.”

Song Jixin was taken aback, his heart aching slightly.

#### The Fifth Realm

The old scholar stood above the sea of clouds, gazing at the magnificent mountains and rivers, exclaiming, “A poor scholar moves house, moving books is like moving mountains; only with books can one be considered wealthy.”

Beside him stood a scholar empty-handed, without a long sword, because in the far distance, a sword light held up the heavens.

The scholar said, “This beautiful land will soon be filled with slaughter.”

The old scholar laughed, “Sages do not harm things; those who do not harm cannot be harmed.”

The scholar shook his head. “There are so few sages like that.”

The old scholar also shook his head. “I see sages everywhere; thus, it’s clear that if you’re skilled in fighting, your vision and realm should be lower.”

The scholar was left speechless. Now, in this world, there were only the two of them, and this boasting was not unfounded; the old scholar was indeed one to seize every opportunity.

This was what the old scholar himself said, not slander from the world.

The old scholar fell silent for a moment, suddenly invigorated. “Since we have nothing to do, let me tell you about my closed-door disciple.”

The scholar inhaled deeply. Here we go again; it wasn’t that he lacked patience, but even the best patience couldn’t withstand the old scholar’s incessant rambling. He turned his head, helplessly saying, “Can we not talk about this?”

The old scholar lamented, “What a regret in life!”

The scholar sighed in relief. 

It was less exhausting to hear the old scholar chatter than to engage in swordplay.

The old scholar suddenly said, “If I don’t speak, will you? That’s a refreshing thought!” 

*(End of Chapter)*
